Report on the results of the parallel checks carried out in 2005 on the administration of value added tax between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Introductory word
The submitted material informs about the progress and results of the parallel checks carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Najvyšší kontrolní úradom Slovenskej republiky, which focused on the area of value added tax administration and the use of the information system VIES (Value Added Tax Information Exchange System).
In May 2004, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic joined the European Union, so the revenue from value added tax affects not only the national budgets of both countries, but also the budget of the European Union as a whole.
The parallel control actions were mainly aimed at checking the procedure of tax authorities in examining the amount of value added tax paid in commercial transactions between individual Member States of the European Union.
The introduction of VIES has enabled the electronic exchange of information on the registration of VAT payers in individual Member States of the European Union and on the commercial transactions carried out by them.
The discrepancy between the VIES data and the data in the VAT return submitted by the taxpayer should alert the tax authorities to suspicious cases and allow the detection of tax evasion or fraud.
The benefit of the parallel checks carried out was not only the exchange of information on the procedure of the tax or tax authorities in the administration of value added tax, but in particular the examination of the use of the VIES system in the control of the application of the right to exemption from value added tax in intra-Community transactions.
The lessons learned from the implementation of parallel controls will contribute to the development of mutual cooperation and will be used in the implementation of further parallel controls in cooperation with the control institutions of the Member States of the European Union.
Report on the results of parallel checks on the administration of value added tax for the period 1 May 2004 to 30 June 2005
Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 05 / 19 (SK) 22 / 2005
Subject of the audit: (CZ) Value Added Tax Administration, (SK) Control of the procedure of the tax authorities in the administration, control and enforcement of value added tax and the performance of VIES tasks for the exchange of information between EU Member States
The Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as "SAO, Czech Republic") and the Najvyššší kontrolný úrad Slovenskej republiky (hereinafter referred to as "SAO SR") concluded a contract on cooperation in audit activities on 12 September 2005.
The subject of the contract was cooperation in the implementation of the parallel audit actions "Administration of Value Added Tax," included in the plan of audit activities of the SAO, the Czech Republic for 2005 under No 05 / 19 and "Control of the procedure of tax authorities in the administration, control and enforcement of taxes on added value and fulfilment of tasks within the VIES system on the list of informants among the member landscapes of the EÚ," included in the plan of audit activities of the SAO SR under No 22 / 2005.
The control actions carried out in parallel were in the nature of coordinated control.
The result of the joint coordinated control was processed within the meaning of the European Enforcement Regulation No 31 for the INTOSAI control standards.
The cooperation consisted in the exchange of information to the extent provided for by the contract concluded and the preparation of a joint final report on the outcome of the parallel checks.
The purpose of the coordinated inspection was to verify selected cases of supplies and acquisitions of goods in suspicious commercial transactions between value added tax payers from the Czech Republic ("the Czech Republic") and the Slovak Republic ("the Slovak Republic").
Both parties have contractually agreed to provide each other with information from public sources, from the electronic system VIES (Value Added Tax Information Exchange System) and data on received and sent requests for the examination of business transactions between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
The checks were carried out in parallel between June and December 2005.
On the territory of the Czech Republic, the inspection was carried out by the State Budget Department and the regional unions of Central Bohemia, Northwest Bohemia, South Bohemia, South Moravia, Central Moravia and Northern Moravia.
The audited entities were the Ministry of Finance and 12 tax offices: The tax office in Mladá Boleslav, the tax office in Cologne, the tax office in Teplice, the tax office in Karlovy Vary, the tax office in Tábor, the tax office in Brno III, the tax office in Znojmo, the tax office in Zlín, the tax office in Šumperk, the tax office in Ostrava I, the tax office for Prague 7 and the tax office for Prague 9.
The audit on the territory of the Slovak Republic was carried out by the Financial and Tax Section of the Slovak SAO in cooperation with the expositions of the Slovak SAO Banská Bystrica and Košice at 9 selected tax offices: The Bratislava I Tax Office, the Komárno Tax Office, the Trenčín Tax Office, the Prievidza Tax Office, the Zvolen Tax Office, the Dolný Kubín Tax Office, the Košice II Tax Office, the Košice V Tax Office and Michalovce Tax Office.
Objective of the checks:
The aim of the parallel control actions was to examine the procedure of the tax and tax authorities in the administration of value added tax (hereinafter referred to as "VAT") following the integration of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic into the single internal market of the European Union (hereinafter referred to as "the EU") and to examine the use of the VIES electronic information system, in particular when checking the application of the VAT exemption.
The audited period of coordinated control was from 1 May 2004 to 30 June 2005.
Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions An electronic VIES system is in place in EU Member States that allows tax authorities to check whether the supplier was entitled to exempt the taxable transaction from VAT and allows the country of destination to check whether the acquirer has correctly declared and taxed the acquired goods.
The VIES system is not centralised within the EU; each Member State develops its own system.
The audit found differences between the national VIES systems in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in the following areas:
Recapitulative statements show the value of supplies of goods to other EU Member States, and the value of services provided is not included in recapitulative statements.
Data from recapitulative statements submitted by Czech payers are processed in the Czech Republic at the level of the tax authorities, where they are compared with data on supplies of goods to other EU Member States included in the VAT returns.
The tax authorities transmit the data from the recapitulative statements to the Ministry of Finance (CLO), which sends them to other EU Member States.
In the Slovak Republic, data from summary reports submitted by Slovak taxpayers at tax offices are only converted into electronic form and processed centrally at the Tax Directorate of the Slovak Republic (CLO).
In the Czech Republic, payers report the value of supplies of goods and the value of supplies of services to other EU Member States on separate lines of VAT returns, which makes it possible to compare the values reported in the recapitulative statements with the values of supplies of goods according to VAT returns and to identify any differences between them.
In the Slovak Republic, the values of goods and services supplied to other EU Member States are reported cumulatively on the common line of VAT returns.
As a result, in the Slovak Republic, the system does not allow the automatic identification of differences between the values of supplies of goods according to VAT returns and recapitulative statements.
Separate reporting of the value of supplies of goods in VAT returns makes it possible to use the results of data comparisons to check the VAT exemption for supplies of goods to the EU.
The data received from recapitulative statements submitted by payers in other EU Member States are processed into CLOs and compared with the value of the acquisition of goods stated by payers from the Czech Republic and Slovakia respectively in VAT returns.
In the Slovak Republic, these data are sent to the tax authorities and the tax authorities themselves decide which cases of differences to examine.
In the Czech Republic, the Ministry of Finance (CLO) will determine which quantified differences between the values of supplies and acquisitions of goods must be examined by the tax authorities and will send a list of these cases to the local tax authorities.
This ensures that, for the most significant variations, it will be examined whether the VAT on the acquisition of goods has been declared at the correct level.
The audit also highlighted some problems in the VAT administration system due to the complications caused by the different reporting of intra-community transactions (i.e. supplies and acquisitions of goods made by payers from different EU Member States):
Recapitulative statements are made in the EU for each calendar quarter and the maximum time limit for processing and sending data to other EU Member States is set at 3 months from the end of the relevant quarter.
Shortening the reporting period to one month, together with shortening the processing period, would allow earlier access to VIES data.
This would allow tax authorities to check more effectively whether VAT on intra-Community purchases has been declared at the correct level.
At the same time, the submission of VAT returns and recapitulative statements for the same tax year (month) would allow faster verification of whether the payer has declared identical values of supplies of goods to the EU in both the recapitulative statement and the VAT return.
The differences between the values of delivery of goods reported by EU payers and the values of acquisition of goods reported by Czech and Slovak payers were due, among other things, to the different reporting of data on intra-community delivery and acquisition in individual EU Member States.
These included, for example, the inclusion of received advances in recapitulative statements, or the reporting of intra-community supplies in the supplier's recapitulative statement in a quarter other than intra-community acquisitions in the customer's VAT return.
Harmonising the conditions for the reporting of these data within the EU would make the control activities of Member States' tax administrations more efficient.
The cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic was also focused on the examination of selected intra-community transactions between the two countries.
Together, a total of 40 cases of commercial transactions between 29 Czech and 32 Slovak tax entities were examined, where there were doubts about their implementation or suspicions of VAT evasion.
The SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO of Slovakia found, among other things, the following facts:
Tax entities have declared in their VAT returns, for the purpose of improperly obtaining an excess VAT deduction, the carrying out of intra-Community transactions which have not actually taken place;
Tax entities reported intra-community supplies in carousel transactions where there was a deliberate multiple reduction in the value of supplies in order to draw excess VAT deductions;
In their VAT returns and recapitulative statements, suppliers declared intra-Community supplies of goods exempt from VAT to purchasers who were so-called "lost companies" and did not declare the tax on the goods acquired;
The suppliers made intra-Community supplies of goods exempt from VAT to tax entities not registered for VAT in another Member State.
In such cases, the supply should not have been exempt from VAT and should have been subject to tax in the supplier's country;
Suppliers declared intra-Community supplies in their VAT returns at a higher value than those declared by purchasers of intra-Community acquisitions, in some cases where VAT was declared at an incorrect level.
The findings of the audit exercise showed that VIES provides tax authorities with the information necessary to check the correct application of VAT in intra-Community transactions.
Tax administrations should pay particular attention to the rigorous examination of differences between data reported by VAT payers and data in the VIES system and the use of all information in tax procedures.
The issue of value added tax after the accession of the Czech Republic and Slovakia to the EU
Value added tax
On 1 May 2004, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic became members of the EU.
After joining the EU, internal borders and border controls on the movement of goods within the EU have been abolished.
Until 30 April 2004, the tax authority was the competent tax authority, with the exception of the import of goods and occasional bus services in the country, where the tax authority was the customs office.
In connection with the adoption of the new Act No. 235 / 2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax (hereinafter "Act No. 235 / 2004 Coll.") and Act No. 222 / 2004 Z. z., on Value Added Tax (hereinafter "Act No. 222 / 2004 Z. z."), the administration of VAT on the acquisition of goods and services (previously imports) from other EU Member States passed from the customs authorities to the tax and tax authorities respectively.
The supply of goods in the Czech Republic under the provisions of Section 13 of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll. means the transfer of the right to dispose of goods as owner.
The supply of goods from the Czech Republic to another EU Member State is the supply of goods that have actually been dispatched or transported to another EU Member State.
Under the provisions of Section 64 of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll. it is an exempt taxable transaction with the right to deduct VAT if the goods are delivered to a person registered for VAT in another EU Member State.
In the Slovak Republic, according to the provisions of Section 8 of Act No 222 / 2004 Z. Z., the supply of tangible property in which the right of ownership is changed is considered to be a supply of goods.
The transfer of goods owned by a taxable person from the territory of the country to another Member State shall also be regarded as a supply of goods where those goods are dispatched or transported by that person or on his behalf to another Member State for the purposes of his business.
Under Section 43 of Act No 222 / 2004 Z. z., the supply of goods from the country to another Member State is exempt from VAT if the person acquiring the goods is a person identified for VAT in another Member State.
The acquisition of goods from another EU Member State in the Czech Republic under the provisions of Section 16 of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll. means the acquisition of the right to dispose as owner of goods which are dispatched or transported to the purchaser by a person registered for VAT in another EU Member State.
The Czech payer purchases goods at a price excluding VAT and is obliged to declare VAT in the Czech Republic according to the provisions of Section 25 of Act No. 235 / 2004 Coll., if the conditions set out in the provisions of Section 73 of this Act are met, he will be entitled to deduct VAT.
The acquisition of goods in the Czech Republic from another EU Member State in the Slovak Republic under the provisions of Section 11 of Act No 222 / 2004 Z. z. means the acquisition of the right to dispose, as owner, of movable tangible property dispatched or transported to the customer by or on behalf of the supplier or the customer to the Czech Republic from another Member State.
Tax liability in the Slovak Republic arises when the payer acquires goods in the Czech Republic from another Member State according to the provisions of Section 20 of Act No 222 / 2004 Z.Z.
The payer can deduct VAT under the provisions of Section 49 of Act No 222 / 2004 Z. Z. if the tax is charged by him on the acquisition of goods in the country from another Member State under the provisions of Sections 11 and 11a of this Act.
According to the provisions of Section 17 of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll., or Section 45 of Act No 222 / 2004 Z. z., trilateral trade is a trade concluded between three persons registered for VAT in three different EU Member States, where the object of the trade is the supply of the same goods between the three persons.
Intra-community transactions are supplies and acquisitions of goods between VAT payers from different EU Member States.
The total volumes of intra-community transactions between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic are shown in the table below.
Vies system
A VAT information exchange system has been set up within the EU to monitor the application of VAT exemptions for intra-Community supplies of goods.
It includes the VIES electronic system, which allows EU tax authorities to check whether the supplier was entitled to exempt the taxable transaction from VAT and vice versa, whether the acquirer duly declared and taxed the acquired goods.
The VIES information system is not centralised within the EU.
Each Member State develops its own VIES system.
National systems operate on a common principle and are interconnected through a common EU communication network, the CCN (Common Communication Network; see diagram below).
In the Czech Republic, the VIES system was connected to an automated tax information system ("ADIS"), in the Slovak Republic to the application software of the tax information system ("APV DIS").
These systems are used by the tax and tax authorities as technical support for executive and management activities in the administration of taxes and fees.
International administrative cooperation
Through international administrative cooperation, the tax administration of each EU Member State obtains information on tax entities that it would not have been able to obtain on its own without such cooperation.
The main objective of international administrative cooperation is the fight against tax evasion and losses.
Under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003, each Member State establishes, within the internal organisational structure, a central unit in the field of administrative cooperation between EU Member States in the management of VAT, known as the Central Liaison Office (CLO).
In the Czech Republic, the Ministry of Finance - the Central Financial and Tax Directorate, where the Department of International Cooperation in the Administration of VAT (hereinafter referred to as "MF CLO") has been established, performs tasks arising from international cooperation.
The function of CLO in the Slovak Republic is performed by the Tax Directorate of the Slovak Republic, the Department of International Administrative Cooperation ("DR CLO").
These departments communicate with EU foreign administrations mainly in the field of VIES information exchange, spontaneous information and information exchange at the request of EU tax administrations, coordination of multilateral (simultaneous) tax controls, verification of tax identification numbers (TIN) of persons registered for VAT in other EU Member States, and communicate with the European Commission.
In order to examine a particular intra-Community transaction or to obtain further information relating to a particular tax entity, the tax and tax authorities send requests for information to the EU via MF CLO and DR CLO respectively.
Through these requests, they obtain information from the requested Member States which they can use to correctly determine VAT.
Requests for information between EU Member States' CLOs are mostly sent in electronic form, using a standardised SCAC form.
Selected control findings when verifying business transactions
The cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic focused mainly on the examination of selected intra-community transactions carried out between the two states and on the level of use of information obtained in the form of international cooperation by the financial and tax authorities.
In 30 cases, the SAO, the Czech Republic requested the SAO to examine business transactions between 19 Czech and 25 Slovak tax entities.
The SAO asked the SAO, the Czech Republic to examine in 10 cases business transactions carried out between 7 Slovak and 10 Czech tax entities.
An examination of intra-community transactions revealed, among other things:
O
The SAO, the Czech Republic asked the SAO of the Slovak Republic to examine the procedure of the tax administration, to which a reply to a request for information was sent.
The Slovak Tax Office, using the SCAC form, requested verification of the supply of goods (footwear) in the third quarter of 2004 from a Slovak payer in the value of 2 847,000 Sk.
The tax office in the Czech Republic replied that the Czech payer only stated the purchase of goods with this value in an additional VAT return and delivered the same goods back to Slovak tax entities with a value of CZK 2,550,000 by the end of 2004.
On the basis of the international cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR, it was found that the locally competent tax office fully recognised the Slovak supplier's right to an excess deduction of VAT arising from, among other things, this supply.
This tax office did not provide information on the suspicion of re-export to the tax authorities of the locally relevant customers of goods imported back from the Czech payer.
This will provide an incentive for further investigation of business activities in relation to possible carousel fraud.
O
The Czech tax authority asked through the SCAC form for verification of the delivery of a technology line to SR worth CZK 4,850,000 in the second quarter of 2004.
The tax procedure carried out in SR showed that only part of the technology line was delivered, and components worth CZK 3,395,000 were not delivered.
In examining this case, the SAO SR found that the VAT on the taxable transaction carried out was declared by the Slovak tax entity on the amount of CZK 4,850,000 in the VAT return ("DAP") for the tax year 7 / 2004.
The SAO, Czech Republic also found that the Czech payer reported an excess VAT deduction of CZK 655,000 in his DAP for that quarter, which was due to the application of a VAT deduction on the purchase of this technology line from another domestic payer.
On the basis of the results of the investigation, the Czech tax office concluded that the Czech and Slovak tax entities created a business relationship for the purpose of illegally obtaining an excess VAT deduction, questioned the performance of the taxable transaction and did not recognise the Czech payer's part of the right to deduct the tax in the amount of CZK 647,000.
O
In 2004, the Slovak tax authority asked through the SCAC form for verification of the supply of goods (copying machines) to the Czech payer in the value of 24,246,000 Sk made in December 2002.
In November 2002, the Slovak payer bought these goods from another tax entity in Slovakia, worth 29,667,000 Sk, and then sold them to a Czech payer.
The Slovak tax entity has claimed an excess VAT deduction for the relevant tax year.
In a tax investigation carried out in the Czech Republic, it was found that the Czech tax entity did not cooperate with the tax administration and did not file a DAP for the fourth quarter of 2002 or the following period.
The SAO SR found that on the basis of the result of the tax audit, the Slovak tax administration did not recognise the right to an excess deduction of 5,541,000 Sk applied in the DAP for the month of 11 / 2002 and established the tax liability of 1,750,000 Sk.
At the same time, that taxpayer was not granted an exemption from VAT in respect of the export of goods in December 2002.
O
The Czech tax authority received an order from MF CLO to verify the value of the acquired goods for the third quarter of 2004.
According to data from VIES, the Czech payer was to purchase goods (diluent) worth CZK 3,767,000 from Slovakia.
This tax entity did not cooperate with the tax authority, it did not file a DAP and the VAT for the months 7 to 12 / 2004 was assessed ex officio in the amount of CZK 0.
The Czech tax authority asked through the SCAC form to check whether deliveries of goods from the Slovak Republic to the Czech Republic took place, in what quantity and price (according to invoices).
In reply, the Slovak local tax office sent a copy of the invoice, the consignment notes and a request for payment of the invoice.
The SAO SR found that the Slovak payer had been granted an exemption with the right to deduct VAT on this supply.
The SAO, Czech Republic found that the Czech tax authority assessed the response to the request for information received from the Slovak Republic as evidence showing that the company had purchased goods from another EU Member State.
On the basis of further investigation, the tax office in the Czech Republic will ask the superior authority for a review of the tax liability.
O
The Slovak company supplied goods (particle board products) to, among others, an American company, which stored these goods in the Czech Republic in a free zone.
The operator of this free zone was identified on the invoices as the consignee of the goods.
In 2004, for example, an American company purchased $57,600 worth of particle board from a Slovak payer (at a unit price of $100 per piece), which it placed in a free zone.
Subsequently, the company transferred ownership of the goods to a Swiss company, worth USD 14,400 (unit price of USD 25 / piece), and the goods were exported back to SR.
The goods were not unloaded in the Czech Republic but left the area of the free zone on the same means of transport.
The Slovak tax authority initiated tax inspections of individual tax years 2004 and 2005 at the supplier of goods on suspicion of carousel transactions.
The verification of the underlying transactions was requested from the Czech local tax authorities through several SCAC forms.
The individual responses gradually created a picture of the shops and confirmed the involvement of stakeholders from the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in the carousel shops.
The SAO, the Czech Republic, in cooperation with the SAO SR, found that in these business relations, there was a deliberate multiple decrease in the value of goods.
On the basis of the information gathered, the Tax Directorate of the Slovak Republic concluded that in this case of the carousel trade it is free price formation (i.e. the import of undervalued goods and their overvaluation by domestic companies located in the chain between the importer and the exporter), which is not a violation of the VAT Act in the Slovak Republic.
Under current legislation, the payment of excess VAT to export companies cannot be prevented as they meet all the conditions of the law to exempt supplies from VAT.
O
The Czech payer's VAT registration was cancelled on 12 July 2005.
On 27 October 2005, following a voluntary application for VAT registration, the company became a tax payer again.
For the month of 8 / 2005 (i.e. the period when he was not a VAT payer), the Czech tax entity entered into the DAP the value of the purchase of goods (printing press) from the Slovak Republic in the amount of CZK 1,174,000 and claimed the right to deduct VAT.
This value corresponded to a supply of goods from a Slovak payer in the amount of 1,530,000 Sk, which the Slovak payer stated in the DAP as a supply of goods to another EU Member State with the right to deduct VAT.
The Slovak tax authority requested to verify the said supply using the SCAC form because the Slovak supplier did not prove how he acquired the goods delivered to the Czech Republic.
The SAO, Czech Republic found that the Czech payer does not cooperate with the tax authority and does not reside at the address listed in the Commercial Register.
As part of the international exchange of information, a local investigation will be carried out in the Czech Republic by the locally competent tax authority in order to verify the data.
O
The Slovak payer included in the summary report for the third quarter of 2004 the delivery of goods worth 956,000 Sk to a tax entity from the Czech Republic.
The VAT number of the Czech entity was marked as incorrect by the VIES system.
Verification in the database of payers revealed that such TIN was never allocated in the Czech Republic.
According to the invoices issued by the Slovak payer, it was the execution of electrical assembly work on real estate in the Czech Republic, not the delivery of goods from the Slovak Republic to the Czech Republic, but the provision of services.
The services were invoiced without VAT, as the Czech entity informed the Slovak entity that it was registered as a VAT payer in the Czech Republic.
The Slovak tax authority requested to verify these facts by means of the SCAC form.
The SAO, the Czech Republic, by asking the local tax authority in the Czech Republic, found that the tax entity listed on invoices as a customer was never registered as a VAT payer in the Czech Republic, did not declare the tax on received services from the Slovak entity and did not declare the tax on the acquisition of goods.
Neither the local investigation nor the tax audit was carried out on the Czech entity, its current residence is unknown.
On the basis of an international exchange of information, the Czech tax authorities learned that the Czech tax entity had become a VAT payer by law by accepting the service.
The Slovak tax entity will be subject to a tax audit for the first to fourth quarters of 2004.
O
In the summary report for the third quarter of 2004, the Slovak payer declared the delivery of goods worth 1,055,000 Sk to the Czech payer.
According to invoices issued by the Slovak payer, it was the execution of electrical assembly works on real estate in the Czech Republic.
It was not a supply of goods from the Slovak Republic to the Czech Republic, but a supply of services.
The Slovak tax authority requested to verify these facts by means of the SCAC form.
The SAO, the Czech Republic, by asking the local tax authority in the Czech Republic, found that the Czech entity was a VAT payer at the time of the delivery and a local investigation was carried out to examine the acquisition of goods from other EU Member States in the third quarter of 2004.
On the basis of this local investigation, it was found that the present case was not really about the acquisition of goods, but about the acquisition of services, which the Czech entity also reported in the regular DAP.
The tax office also found that the Czech entity did not pay the correct amount of VAT for the tax year of the third quarter of 2004 as a result of a bad procedure in the calculation of VAT.
The taxpayer submits an additional DAP.
The SAO SR, when questioned by the local tax office, found that the Slovak payer had erroneously stated the provision of the service in a summary report and would be subject to a tax audit for the 1st to 4th quarters of 2004.
O
The Czech tax entity has voluntarily registered as a VAT payer since 10 March 2004.
For the first quarter of 2004, DAP reported a high turnover in both input and output.
The locally competent tax authority initiated tax proceedings, the entity did not cooperate with the tax authority, so due to suspicion of involvement in the carousel business, it was charged VAT of CZK 0.
No further DAP was submitted by the payer.
His VAT registration was cancelled on 4 January 2005 due to a failure to comply with his obligations under the law.
According to data from the VIES system, this entity was to purchase goods worth 7,846,000 Sk from the Slovak payer in the 3rd and 4th quarters of 2004.
In order to verify the execution of these transactions, the Czech tax authority sent two requests for information to the Slovak Republic.
The SAO SR, when questioned by the local tax office, found that the manager of the Czech company denied in a witness statement that the transactions examined had taken place and questioned the authenticity of his signature on invoices and other documents.
On the basis of the tax procedure carried out in the Slovak Republic, the intra-Community supply to the Czech Republic declared by the Slovak payer was questioned.
The payer will not be recognised as entitled to the VAT exemption and will be charged VAT on the above amount.
O
According to data from the VIES system, the Czech payer should have purchased goods (work clothes) from the Slovak Republic in the first quarter of 2005 with a total value of 39,970,000 Sk.
In this quarter, the Czech payer reported the purchase of goods from another EU Member State only in the DAP for the month of 3 / 2005, worth CZK 11,292,000.
The local tax authority carried out a local investigation with the entity to check the data in this DAP.
Since the company did not submit any documents or otherwise prove the performance of taxable transactions, on 9 June 2005 the tax authority charged it VAT in the amount of CZK 0.
In May 2005, the tax authority sent two requests for information to the Slovak Republic due to doubts about the acquisition of the goods.
According to the reply to the requests for information, the tax authority in SR had doubts about the execution of the business cases and about the execution of the payment.
The SAO SR was informed that the Slovak tax administration had sent DR CLO an initiative to carry out simultaneous checks with the tax administration of the Czech Republic, which will be carried out with the participating entities.
At the time of the coordinated inspection, the locally competent tax authority in the Czech Republic carried out further investigations concerning the Czech entity and at the same time an investigation by the Police of the Czech Republic was under way.
O
The following two cases involve companies suspected of being involved in carousel fraud.
Transactions in goods (work clothes) were carried out between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in the fourth quarter of 2004 and the first quarter of 2005.
Slovak payer No 1 supplied goods to Czech payer No 2.
In the Czech Republic, the goods were then sold to payer No 3, who delivered them back to SR payer No 4 (see diagram No 2).
(A)
Czech payer No. 2 was to purchase goods (work clothes) worth CZK 4,847,000 from Slovak payer No. 1 in the 4th quarter of 2004 and goods worth CZK 17,050,000 in the 1st quarter of 2005.
As the acquisition declared by the Czech payer in the DAP did not correspond to the data in the VIES system, the local tax authority sent a request for information to the Slovak Republic on 25 May 2005.
In reply, the Slovak tax authority expressed doubts about the execution of the business cases as well as the execution of the payment.
On 8 June 2005, a request for information was received at MF CLO from SR concerning goods worth 16,575,000 Sk, which were to be delivered by Slovak payer No 1 to Czech payer No 2 in December 2004.
The Slovak side demanded to check whether the Czech payer No. 2 actually received the goods, declared them in DAP and paid VAT.
An official record drawn up by the local tax authority in the Czech Republic shows that the Czech payer No 2 has not been based at an address registered in the Commercial Register for a long time.
Although he was a VAT payer with a monthly tax year, he submitted DAP for a quarterly tax year.
In view of this, the Czech tax authority was not able to assess VAT.
In view of the above, it was not possible to verify the performance of the taxable transaction between Slovak payer No 1 and Czech payer No 2 mentioned in the application for the amount of 16 575 thousand.
The Czech tax authority suspected the involvement of both entities in the carousel business for the purpose of drawing an excess VAT deduction.
(B)
Czech payer No. 3, who deals with the purchase and sale of passenger cars, filed a DAP for the tax period of months 1 and 2 / 2005, in which he declared the supply of goods (work clothes) to Slovak payer No. 4 for a total value of CZK 21,935,000.
These work clothes were to be purchased by the Czech payer No 3 from the Czech payer No 2 between December 2004 and January 2005.
The locally competent tax office sent a request for information to SR, which was mainly aimed at verifying whether Slovak payer No. 4 purchased goods worth CZK 1,025,000 from Czech payer No. 3 in December 2004 and CZK 21,935,000 in the first quarter of 2005.
The reply to this request for information received from SR showed that in the DAP for the month of 12 / 2004 the Slovak payer No 4 stated a zero value for the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State and in the DAP for the months of 1 and 2 / 2005 he stated a value for the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State of only 1,193,000 Sk.
Slovak payer No 4 did not respond to the invitation to submit tax documents for the tax period from 10 / 2004 to 3 / 2005.
A local investigation carried out in SR revealed that the company was not located at the address listed in the Commercial Register.
The reply further stated that this payer fulfils all the characteristics of a so-called "lost company" and therefore there is a reasonable suspicion of carousel fraud.
The SAO SR was informed that the Slovak tax administration had sent DR CLO an initiative to carry out simultaneous checks with the tax administration of the Czech Republic, which will be carried out on the participating tax entities.
In the course of the coordinated inspection, the Czech tax authority collected documents that would confirm or deny the existence of the goods.
VAT will be measured according to the outcome of the investigation.
The Police of the Czech Republic is also investigating the case.
Progress of control action
As part of the preparation of parallel audit events, a coordination meeting between representatives of the SAO, the Czech Republic and representatives of the SAO SR took place in the first half of July 2005.
The participants in this meeting were acquainted with the VAT legislation in both countries and the integration of the VIES electronic system into national databases.
The negotiations resulted in the specification of the scope of cooperation and the setting of conditions for the selection of control samples.
The two parties agreed that the cooperation will focus on the following areas: (A) verification of the validity and correctness of the VAT registration numbers of persons registered for VAT in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic for intra-community supplies; (b) verification of data on intra-community purchases listed in the DAP by payers in the Czech Republic using information from summary reports (hereinafter referred to as "SH") of payers from the Slovak Republic contained in the VIES system, and vice versa; (c) exchange of information between tax administrations in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic on business transactions carried out.
It was also agreed that the selection of tax entities for inspection would be carried out following the volume of intra-community deliveries between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic and according to the number of requests for international cooperation sent and received between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic via the SCAC form.
5.1 Intra-Community Transactions
The following diagram illustrates the process of processing information by the tax administrations of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic during the intra-Community supply and acquisition of goods.
5.1.1 Intra-Community Delivery
If the VAT payer carries out an intra-Community supply, he is obliged to submit an SH by the 25th day after the end of the calendar quarter.
The payer in the Czech Republic provides in the SH summary information about his supplies of goods to another EU Member State exempt from VAT for the previous calendar quarter.
The payer in the Slovak Republic is obliged to enter in the SH the value of goods that have been exempted and delivered from the Czech Republic to other EU Member States during the calendar quarter period.
Data on the value of the goods delivered are always presented in SH in Czech and Slovak currencies, broken down by individual tax entities, with an indication of their VAT number, under which they were registered in their country.
Data on services are not included in the SH.
If the payer in the Czech Republic finds that he has given incorrect data in the SH, he is obliged to submit a subsequent SH.
If the payer in SR finds that the information given in the SH was incomplete or incorrect, he will file a corrective SH before the deadline for submission of the SH, after which he is obliged to file an additional SH.
The VIES system allows for the exchange of information on the registration data of VAT registered payers in EU Member States.
Payers from the Czech Republic or the Slovak Republic can check whether the VAT number of the relevant customer is registered in the EU Member State.
The data from the submitted SH are grouped on MF CLO and DR CLO by VIES according to the individual VAT numbers of the purchasers.
The aggregate value of all deliveries for each customer's VAT number and the code of the method of fulfilment from all its Czech and Slovak suppliers, the so-called L1QD files, will be created.
Data from the L1QD files shall be sent to the relevant EU Member States no later than three months after the end of the quarter to which the data relate.
The total value of intra-community transactions between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic (from L1QD files) is shown in the table below.
If VIES in another Member State detects the wrong TIN of the customer in the L1QD files sent, it generates a so-called O _ MCTL message, which contains all the wrong TIN, indicating the type of error.
This message is then sent to MF CLO and DR CLO respectively.
The O _ MCTL report may contain 4 types of errors: Formally incorrect TIN, TIN is not registered in the country or has never been allocated, the customer with a particular TIN was not a VAT payer in the quarter, the customer's VAT registration was terminated during the quarter.
In the Czech Republic, MF CLO transmits data from the received O _ MCTL reports to the tax authorities.
If the wrong VAT number of an EU payer is used in one of the SH lines sent or subsequent SH lines, the so-called "VAT ID Doubt Notification" is generated by ADIS at the relevant tax office.
The tax office will check whether the delivery to a VAT-registered payer in another EU Member State has actually taken place and will record the result of the verification in the system.
In SR, DR CLO will process all O _ MCTL messages in the VIES system and send them electronically to the local tax authorities together with the identification of the taxpayers who have entered the wrong VAT number in their SH.
The tax authorities then invite the payer to submit an additional SH and state the valid TIN, or the tax office will check the delivery of the goods with the relevant payer when declaring the invalid TIN in the submitted SH.
Data on the number of erroneous VAT numbers relating to intra-community transactions between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic are given in the table below.
Out of a total of 41,728 VAT numbers of Czech payers listed in SH of Slovak payers in the period from the 2nd quarter of 2004 to the 1st quarter of 2005, 929 VAT numbers were incorrect, i.e. 2.23%.
Out of a total of 62,997 VAT numbers of Slovak payers, listed in the SH of Czech payers in the same period, 416 were incorrect VAT numbers, i.e. 0.66%.
When reporting intra-community transactions between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, Czech VAT payers reported on average fewer incorrect VAT numbers in their SH than Slovak taxpayers.
An examination of the activities of the tax and tax authorities found that the VIES system did not provide up-to-date information on the validity of VAT registrations of tax entities in all cases.
For example:
- although, when questioned by the tax administration in the Czech Republic, the VIES system confirmed the validity of the registration of the tax entity in the 4th quarter of 2004, the O _ MCTL report was subsequently generated due to the termination of the registration of the payer in this quarter.
The investigation revealed that the termination of the marketing authorisation did not take place until 1 January 2005;
- The SAO SR also found that 6 tax entities submitted SH, in which the wrong VAT number was mentioned, but the O _ MCTL reports did not contain these VAT numbers.
In SR, the submitted SH will be converted into electronic form at tax offices and the data from them will be sent to DR CLO.
Following the subsequent processing of these data in VIES, DR CLO will send to the relevant tax authorities the so-called breakdown of errors in SH submitted by tax entities for the relevant quarters.
The SAO SR compared data on the occurrence of erroneous data in the SH as of 26 July 2005 (i.e. data processed before the start of the audit) and as of 2 February 2006 (i.e. data processed after the end of the audit).
A comparison of the data is presented in the table below.
The above data show that the audit of the SAO SR had an impact not only on the reduction of the number of SH with an incorrect VAT number (by an average of 199 SH per quarter), but also on the reduction of the number of uncorrected errors in SH (by an average of 431 errors per quarter).
In the Czech Republic, the value of intra-community supplies given by the payer in the relevant DAP lines is compared with the value of intra-community supplies given by the payer in the quarterly SH.
The ADIS system automatically indicates the differences between these values.
The tax authority should examine the differences, remove any ambiguities and use the data collected to determine the tax liability.
The SAO, the Czech Republic found that the audited tax authorities did not verify these differences in 27 cases.
The total difference between the values given in SH and DAP in these cases was CZK 537,231,000.
Since the third quarter of 2004, the ADIS system has allowed the tax administration in the Czech Republic to consider the difference between the values listed in SH and DAP of up to 0.5% of the total value of intra-community supplies according to SH as a match and to set it in the ADIS system.
For payers with a large volume of intra-community supplies in one quarter, 0.5% of the value represents a not insignificant amount, so tax authorities should not set the SH and DAP match in these cases without explaining the causes of the differences.
For example, without verification, the tax authority set the match for a difference in values of CZK 1,561,000.
The examination of differences in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic was complicated by the fact that SH for each calendar quarter was submitted by payers within 25 days after the end of this quarter.
The tax authorities were not able to compare the values of intra-community supplies listed in these DAPs with the values according to SH for payers with the monthly tax year at the time of filing the DAP for the first two months of the calendar quarter.
In these cases, the tax authorities only became aware of any discrepancy between the data in DAP and SH when the tax liability or excess VAT was assessed or refunded.
5.1.2 Intra-Community acquisition
The VIES system provides, inter alia, information on the values of intra-community transactions within EU Member States.
Acquisition of goods in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, data received from SH submitted by payers from other EU Member States (delivered by L1QD) are processed by MF CLO.
During processing, the data are converted at the minimum and maximum daily exchange rates of the Czech National Bank for the relevant period and then compared with the value of the acquisition indicated by Czech payers in the DAP for the relevant quarter.
The value of acquisitions of goods reported by payers in the DAP should be in the range of the minimum and maximum converted value of L1QD (L1min and L1max).
If the value reported in the DAP is less than L1min, a "verification order" is generated for the payer with the most significant irregularities.
Orders to verify the acquisition of goods are a warning to problematic tax entities and are passed on to the local tax authorities, which must investigate the data transmitted.
The number of verification orders relating to the audited tax authorities in the Czech Republic is shown in the table below.
The SAO, Czech Republic found that in 33 cases the audited tax authorities did not check the irregularities in the values of the intra-Community acquisitions referred to in the verification orders received.
In these cases, the total difference between the values stated in the SH of payers from other EU Member States and the DAP of Czech payers was at least CZK 148,319,000.
The SAO, Czech Republic selected 533 files of tax entities for inspection, for which the audited tax authorities received a verification order from the Ministry of Finance.
The inspection found the following most common causes of differences between the values stated in the DAP of the customer and in the SH of the supplier: On the part of the customer (Czech payer) in 263 cases the customer did not declare the acquisition of goods in the regular DAP, in 93 cases the payer admitted the acquisition of goods in a different tax period than in which he was obliged to declare the tax, in 6 cases the customer stated the value of the purchased goods in the wrong DAP line, on the part of the supplier (EU payer) in 88 cases the EU payers included in their SH the values of the services provided to the Czech payer, of which 54 were Slovak payers, in 39 cases the suppliers included in the SH the supply of goods in a different tax period than the Czech purchasers in their DAP, in 22 cases the suppliers stated in the SH the incorrect VAT number of the Czech payer, in 16 cases the suppliers stated in the SH the incorrect values of the supply of goods, in 12 cases the suppliers included in the SH the value of goods delivered to the Czech Republic before 1 May 2004, in 5 cases the suppliers included in the SH the value of the advances received.
On the part of Slovak payers, the value of the services provided was most often erroneously included in the SH.
54 such cases were found at the audited tax offices.
For example, when investigating the verification order, it was found that the difference in the value of CZK 10,974,000 was due to the fact that the Slovak payer introduced the provision of services (construction work and delivery of goods, including assembly in the territory of the Czech Republic) into SH for the first quarter of 2005.
Another reason for the differences was the inclusion of the values of received advances in the SH, for example 2 Slovak payers reported received advances from Czech payers in the SH, as a result of which an order was generated to verify the difference of CZK 3,580,000.
Orders to authenticate procured goods are generated only once per quarter.
In cases where there is subsequently a change in the data from the SH in the EU Member States, such as a change in the customer of goods in the Czech Republic or an increased value of delivery of goods to the Czech Republic, new verification orders are not generated.
Since the VIES system does not automatically draw attention to these changes, the locally competent tax authority of the purchaser of the goods may not, without any other initiative, know about the facts relevant to the correct determination of the tax liability on the acquired goods and there is a strong likelihood of VAT evasion.
An audit of the SAO, the Czech Republic found that this situation occurred, for example, in the following cases:
The Slovak payer stated in SH for the 2nd quarter of 2004 the value of the delivery of goods to the Czech payer in the amount of 1 504 thousand Sk.
On 1 February 2005, the tax office with local jurisdiction sent a request for information to the Czech payer in Slovakia, because the Czech payer only admitted the purchase of goods in the amount of CZK 425,000.
On the basis of the tax procedure, the Slovak payer filed an additional SH on 1 March 2005, in which he corrected the data on the delivery of goods to the Czech Republic by reducing the value of the delivery for the originally mentioned Czech payer to 538,000 Sk and increasing the value of the delivered goods for another Czech payer from 194,000 Sk to 1,160,000 Sk.
Four Slovak payers reported in their SH for the 2nd quarter of 2004 an intra-community delivery to payers from the Czech Republic totalling 10,240,000 Sk (i.e. 8,183,000 CZK).
However, Czech buyers did not report intra-Community acquisitions in the DAP.
On the basis of an international exchange of information, it was found that the goods were delivered in all cases to another Czech payer, who was not mentioned in the SH submitted by the Slovak payers.
During the first quarter of 2005, Slovak payers increased the value of intra-community deliveries for this Czech payer by a total of 10,240,000 Sk in the additional SH relating to the second quarter of 2004.
In view of the above, the local tax authority in the Czech Republic could not have doubts about the accuracy of the data submitted by the DAP for the second quarter of 2004, even though the actual acquirer did not comply with the obligation to declare intra-Community acquisitions for that quarter.
The SAO, Czech Republic found that based on the international exchange of information between tax administrations, the aforementioned Czech payer was additionally charged VAT for the tax years 5 and 6 / 2004 in the amount of CZK 3,640,000 and for the third quarter of 2004 in the amount of CZK 3,305,000 on purchased goods during these periods.
It can be seen from the above that tax authorities had to examine in tax proceedings not only differences arising from errors in the customer's DAP, but also differences due to different reporting of data on intra-Community supplies and acquisitions in different EU Member States.
Harmonising the conditions for the reporting of these data would make the control activities of the tax authorities more effective.
Acquisition of goods in Slovakia
In SR, the APV DIS system makes it possible to compare data on the value of purchased goods obtained through VIES from other EU Member States with data contained in the DAP of Slovak purchasers.
The method by which data are compared is called the "min-max method."
This method is used to convert the delivery values of goods listed in the SH of payers from other EU Member States at the minimum and maximum exchange rates for the relevant quarter.
There will be a min-max interval, which is used for comparison with the values of the purchase of goods listed in the DAP of Slovak payers.
Dr CLO will send information to the tax authorities on the values of intra-Community acquisitions listed in the DAP and the values of EU supplies in the VIES.
The tax authorities will decide for which VAT-registered persons the difference will be checked, taking into account other risk analysis criteria.
On the basis of data provided by DR CLO, the SAO SR selected 57 files of Slovak purchasers of goods for inspection at the audited tax offices, of which 25 payers also purchased goods from the Czech Republic, where the highest differences were found between the acquisition values obtained from the VIES system and those declared in the DAP.
The audit carried out by the SAO SR confirmed the fact that the tax authorities did not rigorously check the differences obtained using the min-max method and thus did not check the accuracy of the data contained in the DAP of Slovak purchasers.
As part of the audit, the SAO asked the tax authorities to carry out 47 local investigations into specific tax entities.
During the audit of the Slovak SAO at the tax offices, 31 local investigations were completed.
For Slovak companies, where VIES showed significant differences in min-max values when acquiring goods from EU Member States, the following facts were found, inter alia:
In the DAP for the fourth quarter of 2004, the Slovak payer did not indicate the value of the acquisition of goods from the EU.
The tax office found that a company from the Czech Republic had erroneously declared the VAT number of this payer in SH for the 4th quarter of 2004, while goods worth CZK 19,184,000 were actually delivered to another Slovak payer.
According to the VIES system, in the fourth quarter of 2004 the Slovak company was to purchase goods from the Czech Republic, Poland, Hungary and Austria worth MIN 682,692,000 Sk and MAX 715,105,000 Sk.
The company filed a DAP for the periods in which it stated the value of the acquisition of goods from the EU at only 480 599 thousand Sk.
The tax authority carried out a local investigation and found that the tax entity had purchased electricity from the Czech Republic, Poland, Hungary and Austria.
Suppliers to SH and DAP did not list intra-Community deliveries according to the date of issue of invoices, but according to the date of delivery.
In view of further irregularities in the acquisition of goods from these EU countries, the tax authorities will request an examination of the value of the goods delivered using SCAC forms.
The acquisition of goods from EU Member States in Q4 2004 was not mentioned by the Slovak payer in the DAP.
According to the VIES system, this payer was to purchase goods worth MIN 11,286,000 Sk and MAX 11,845,000 Sk.
The Tax Office carried out a local investigation, which showed that the tax entity did not purchase any goods from EU Member States in the fourth quarter of 2004.
The SAO recommended that the tax office ask for verification of supplies of goods from EU member countries using the SCAC form.
The VIES system reported the delivery of goods to a Slovak customer worth MIN 557,000 Sk and MAX 565,000 Sk.
In the DAP, for the tax period from 10 to 12 / 2004, the payer did not declare any acquisition of goods.
A local investigation by the tax authority found that the tax entity received an invoice from a supplier in the Czech Republic on 10 December 2004 for the material consumed during the repair of the hydraulic loader.
The SAO recommended a tax audit of the payer.
During the audit of the SAO SR, in 16 cases, the tax authorities did not complete the local investigation.
In 10 cases, the SAO asked the tax authorities to carry out a tax audit of the tax entities.
Reports on the results of local investigations and tax audits will be submitted by the tax authorities after they have been carried out by the SAO SR.
Examples include:
The Slovak acquirer did not mention the acquisition of goods from EU Member States in the DAP for the 4th quarter of 2004 and did not declare any tax for the tax period from 10 to 12 / 2004 and claimed a refund of excess VAT for a total amount of 1 236 thousand Sk.
The tax authority carried out a local investigation, which showed that the tax entity had purchased goods from the Czech Republic worth 683,000 euro (approx. 27,080,000 Sk).
The goods were transported from the Czech Republic by a Czech supplier to the customs office in Čiernej nad Tisou, from where the transport continued to the Russian Federation.
The Slovak payer issued an invoice to customers in the Russian Federation for the amount of EUR 683,000, which he did not mention in the submitted DAP.
The tax authority carries out a tax audit of the tax entity.
The difference between the acquisition data reported in the Slovak payer's DAP for the third quarter of 2004 to the first quarter of 2005 and the supply data reported by payers from EU Member States in each quarter was a total of 4,800,000 Sk.
The tax office found that the tax entity purchased goods from suppliers in the Czech Republic and Belgium and then sold them to Ukraine.
The invoices were accompanied by the single export declaration.
The acquisition of goods in DAP was not mentioned by the tax entity, according to the company's manager, the goods in transit were transported directly from the Czech Republic to Ukraine.
The taxpayer did not submit any VAT records to the local investigation.
A tax audit has been initiated on the payer.
5.2 International exchange of information level L3
The exchange of information at L3 level is initiated by locally competent tax authorities, who send their requests for information (hereinafter referred to as "JOI") or spontaneous information (hereinafter referred to as "SPI") relating to a particular tax entity or transaction through MF CLO, respectively.
Dr CLO to another EU Member State. The aim of ŽOI is, for example, to prove the execution of a given transaction in the context of intra-community transactions, to check a certain VAT number, etc.
In the case of an SPI, it is a communication of information relevant to tax administrations in another EU Member State.
Cooperation in the field of information exchange is governed by Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003.
The maximum time limit for replying to an EOI was set at 3 months in Article 8 of this Regulation.
The conditions for the admissibility of applications are governed by a decision of the Commission of the European Communities of 15.11.2004, which stipulates that, unless otherwise agreed by the participating States, an EOI must relate to commercial transactions with a value of at least EUR 1 500, excluding VAT.
Where an EOI relates to a commercial transaction with a value of less than EUR 15 000 excluding VAT, the requested authority may refuse to respond in view of its workload.
The procedure for processing incoming ŽOI by the tax administration of the Czech Republic, including the indication of the internal time limits set for processing at each organisational level, is illustrated in the following diagram.
In the Slovak Republic, the deadline for processing ŽOI by the tax authorities was set internally at 2 months in order to comply with the three-month deadline under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003.
MF CLO received a total of 29 ŽOI and 3 SPI from Slovakia from 1 May 2004 to 30 June 2005.
Of the 29 IOUs received, 26 (89.7%) were discharged within the stipulated time limit of 3 months and 3 (10.3%) were discharged after that time limit.
During the same period, DR CLO from the Czech Republic received a total of 71 ŽOI and 7 SPI.
Of the 71 received by the JOI, 64 (i.e. 90.1%) were dealt with within the stipulated time limit of 3 months, 5 (i.e. 7.0%) were dealt with after this time limit (for the remaining 2 cases it was not possible to determine the time limit from the submitted material).
The following graph contains more detailed data on the processing time of IOUs received by MF CLO and DR CLO, respectively.
The reasons given on the SCAC forms for sending a JOI are set out in the table below.
Conclusion
On the basis of international cooperation, compliance with Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of VAT has been examined, as well as the use of VIES to exchange information between EU Member States, in particular when monitoring the exercise of the right to exemption from VAT.
International cooperation has made it possible to examine selected intra-Community transactions between VAT payers from the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
An examination of the selected transactions revealed that, based on an international exchange of information, the tax administrations of both countries detected cases of companies carrying out fictitious intra-Community business transactions in order to obtain excess VAT deductions, as well as cases where the purchasers did not declare VAT on the received supplies of goods at the correct level.
The audit also revealed differences in the processing and use of VIES data by the tax administrations of the two countries.
The audit also highlighted problems caused by the different reporting of data on intra-community supplies and purchases of goods in different EU Member States.
Harmonising the conditions for the reporting of these data within the EU would make the control activities of Member States' tax administrations more efficient.
An examination of the procedure of the tax and tax authorities in the administration of VAT and the use of the VIES system revealed that the tax and tax authorities did not make sufficient use of all the possibilities of the VIES system and the relevant legal powers.
In addition, it was found that VIES did not provide up-to-date information on the supply of goods and the validity of the VAT registration of tax entities in all cases.
The SAO SR compared the data on the occurrence of erroneous data in the SH, processed before the start of the audit, with data processed after the end of the audit.
Comparing these figures, it was clear that the audit of the SAO SR had an impact not only on the reduction of the number of SH with misstated VAT numbers, but also on the reduction of the number of uncorrected errors in SH.
In the event of irregularities in the reported data, the SAO asked the tax authorities to carry out local investigations or to carry out tax audits.
The SAO, the Czech Republic did not have such an option under the current legislation in the Czech Republic.
The findings of the audit exercise showed that VIES provided tax authorities with the basic information necessary to check the correct application of VAT in intra-Community transactions.
As there is still scope for tax evasion in this area, there is a need to pay close attention to intra-community transactions when managing VAT.
Communiqué
This report was drawn up in Czech, English and Slovak and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Chairman of the Najvyšššššie Audit Office of the Slovak Republic.
Parallel control of the administration of value added tax and excise duties between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Introductory word
This information material gives an overview of the progress and results of the parallel control actions carried out by the Supreme Audit Office and the Najvyšší kontrolní úradom Sloven-skej republiky, which were focused on the area of value added administration and excise duties.
Cooperation between the supreme audit authorities of the two countries was carried out on the basis of a cooperation agreement on control activities concluded in February 2004.
The topic of parallel control actions was chosen in view of the fact that indirect taxes make a significant contribution to the revenue of the national budgets of both countries.
The design of value added tax, which allows for the refund of excess deductions, provides scope for tax fraud or evasion.
High rates of excise duties, especially on tobacco and tobacco products, alcohol and mineral oils, mean high profits for those who escape taxation by illegally selling these goods.
Tax fraud is a problem not only in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, but also in other countries of the European Union.
In view of the need to address this issue comprehensively across the European Union, the VAT Working Group has been set up by the supreme audit institutions of the Member States of the European Union, in which the highest audit offices of both countries are actively involved.
The greatest benefit of the control actions carried out can be seen not only in the exchange of experience, but in particular in the joint effort to identify problem areas of indirect tax administration in order to reduce the scope for tax evasion.
The experience and knowledge gained will be used in the framework of the planned indirect tax controls, aimed in particular at involving the tax authorities of both countries in the VIES system, which allows the movement of goods between the Member States of the European Union to be controlled.
Report on the results of the audit of the administration of value added tax and excise duties for the years 2002 and 2003
1. Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 04 / 07 (SK) 18 / 2004
Subject of inspection:
(CZ) Value added tax and excise duties
(SK) Control of the procedure of the tax authorities in the administration, control and enforcement of value added tax and excise duties
On 11.2. 2004, a contract for cooperation in audit activities was concluded between the Supreme Audit Office (hereinafter referred to as "SAO") and the Najvyššší kontrolní úrady Slovenskej republiky (hereinafter referred to as "SAO SR"). The object of the contract was cooperation in the parallel audit actions "Value Added Tax and Excise Tax," included in the SAO's audit activity plan for 2004 under No 04 / 07 and "Control of the procedure of the tax administration, control and enforcement of taxes on added value and spot taxes," included in the SAO SR's audit activity plan under No 18 / 2004.
The cooperation consisted in the exchange of information to the extent provided for in the contract concluded and the preparation of a joint final report on the outcome of the inspections.
In the contract, the two parties undertook to provide each other with information from public sources, from the database of the customs administration and from the files of tax entities kept by the tax authorities in the Czech Republic and the tax authorities in the Slovak Republic, which the contracting parties could not obtain when checking the application of value added tax and excise duties on imports and exports from sources in the territory of the respective state.
The checks were carried out in parallel between January and August 2004.
In the territory of the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as "the Czech Republic"), the inspection was carried out by the State Budget Department and the regional unions of South Bohemia, North-East Bohemia, South Moravia, Central Moravia and Northern Moravia.
The audited persons were the General Directorate of Customs and 12 selected tax offices: The Financial Office for Prague 1, the Financial Office for Prague 3, the Financial Office in České Budějovice, the Financial Office in Frýdek-Místek, the Financial Office in Hodonín, the Financial Office in Jihlava, the Financial Office in Kostelec nad Orlicí, the Financial Office in Kroměříž, the Financial Office in Písek, the Financial Office in Rožnov pod Radhostem, the Financial Office in Ústí nad Orlicí, the Financial Office in Velke Meziříčí.
The audit on the territory of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as "SR") was carried out by the Tax and Customs Administration Section of the SAO SR in cooperation with the expositions of the SAO SR Banská Bystrica and Košice at 10 selected tax offices:
Bratislava Tax Office for selected tax entities, Bratislava III Tax Office, Trnava Tax Office, Pú-chov Tax Office, Banská Bystrica I Tax Office, Liptovský Mikuláš Tax Office, Žilina I Tax Office, Žilina II Tax Office, Košice I Tax Office and Košice IV Tax Office.
Objective of control
The aim of the control actions was to verify the fulfilment of the obligations of the tax and customs authorities in the administration of value added tax and excise duties, with a focus on the collection of these taxes on the import and export of goods and services.
The aim of the international cooperation was to verify imports and exports of selected commodities between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in the customs database of the Czech Republic and the customs database of the Slovak Republic and their subsequent verification in tax returns at the respective tax and tax offices.
The audited period covered the years 2002 and 2003.
2. Recap of inspection results
2.1. General evaluation of control activities
In the framework of international cooperation, the SAO handed over 22,206 items of single customs declarations (hereinafter referred to as "JCDs") on imports and exports of goods between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic from the Czech Republic's customs database, while the SAO handed over 30,221 items of JCDs from the Slovak Republic's customs database.
A comparison was made between the designated JCD items from the Customs Database of the Czech Republic and the Customs Database of the Slovak Republic.
Of the 5,883 selected JCD items from the Customs Database of the Czech Republic, a total of 43% of the related JCD items were assigned.
Out of the 12,343 selected JCD entries from the SR customs database, a total of 26% of the related JCD entries were allocated.
On the basis of the non-allocated items of the JCD, a selection of the files of tax entities was carried out at the tax and tax offices, for which the declared imports and exports were further verified in cooperation with the customs administrations of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
On the basis of the exchange of information from the documents of the customs administrations of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic and the financial and tax authorities, the implementation of reported imports and exports between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic was verified in the territory of the second state.
The SAO and the SAO SR carried out a joint pilot inspection at the border customs crossing point Starý Hrozenkov - Drietoma, in which the two parties worked closely together to verify the accuracy of data on the movement of goods between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
The audit did not find shortcomings in the registration of selected cases of imports and exports of goods carried out in 2002.
International cooperation has made it possible to examine trade transactions between trading partners from both countries and has highlighted shortcomings in the registration of imports and exports.
Summary of the results of the inspection
In the area of international cooperation, the audit of the SAO and the SAO of the Slovak Republic focused on imports and exports of alcohol and spirits, tobacco and tobacco products, computers and computer components, mobile phones and their components, and possibly other types of goods.
Based on the audit of the files of tax entities at selected financial and tax offices, the SAO asked for verification of the implementation of exports of goods declared at 40 JCDs with a total statistical value of 15,301,093 CZK and the SAO asked the Slovak Republic for verification of exports with a statistical value of 56,989 Sk.
The SAO and SAO SR found, among other things, the following facts:
- trade transactions were not declared in the same way on both sides, which made it difficult to identify the corresponding imports and exports in the Czech customs database and the Slovak customs database,
- an error in entering data into customs databases made it impossible to identify certain imports or exports;
- for some exports from the Czech Republic, corresponding imports to the Slovak Republic have not been demonstrated.
In such cases, there are reasonable grounds to suspect fictitious exports of goods for the purpose of improperly claiming deductions of value added tax;
- tax entities have failed to comply with certain statutory obligations when declaring imports and exports in value added tax returns;
- weaknesses have been identified in the activities of the tax and tax authorities in the administration of value added tax and excise duties and in their cooperation with the customs authorities.
In the area of value added tax and excise duties, attention will continue to be paid to international trade in order to effectively minimise tax evasion.
In particular, it is important to improve the activities of tax administrations in the administration of value added tax.
Effective control of excise duties is based on the control of the circulation of documents, systematic physical control of goods and mutual exchange of information on the import and export of goods.
3. Description of the situation in the field of value added tax and excise duties
Value added tax
Value added tax ("VAT") was levied by the tax or tax authorities on taxable transactions carried out within the territory of the country and by the customs authorities on the importation of goods.
The tax revenue for the tax authorities was due to the difference between the collected own tax liability and the refunded excess VAT deductions.
VAT revenue at the customs offices was determined by the amount of tax collected by them.
In accordance with the basic principles of the VAT mechanism, the tax collected by the customs authorities was reflected in the tax deductions applied to the tax authorities or tax authorities.
For most tax and tax authorities, excess VAT deductions exceeded the tax liability.
VAT is one of the key taxes in terms of state budget revenue, as it accounted for about 31% of the tax revenue of the state budget of the Czech Republic in 2003 and about 42% of the tax revenue of the state budget of the Slovak Republic.
The total VAT collection in the Czech Republic amounted to CZK 162.9 billion in 2003.
The tax and customs authorities collected a total of CZK 394.3 billion in VAT in 2003 and the excess VAT deductions returned amounted to a total of CZK 231.4 billion.
The total collection of VAT in the Slovak Republic amounted to CZK 83.8 billion in 2003.
In 2003, the tax and customs authorities collected Sk 187.0 billion in VAT and the excess VAT deductions recovered totalled Sk 103.2 billion.
Excise duties
The collection of excise duties (hereinafter referred to as "SPD") was carried out by the relevant tax and tax authorities and, on imports of products subject to SPD, by the customs authorities.
The share of the SPD in the tax revenue of the state budget in the Czech Republic was about 16% in 2003 and about 19% in the Slovak Republic.
The total collection of SPD collected in the Czech Republic by the tax and customs authorities in 2003 amounted to CZK 85.6 billion and in the Slovak Republic it amounted to CZK 38.0 billion.
4. Progress of the control action
Cooperation between the SAO and the SAO of the Slovak Republic took place in two stages.
In the first stage, a comparison was made between imports and exports of selected commodities from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic; in the second stage, the results of this comparison were used in the mutual verification of the implementation of selected commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic and in the checks carried out on the territory of both countries.
4.1.
Preparation of the control action
The first proposal for cooperation in parallel VAT and SPD checks was presented at a working meeting of representatives of the SAO and the SAO of the Slovak Republic in April 2003.
A coordination meeting took place in November 2003 at which, among other things, the selection of commodities - types of goods which posed a significant risk in compliance with customs and tax legislation was agreed: - ethyl alcohol and spirits, tariff headings 2207 and 2208, - tobacco and tobacco products, tariff headings 2401, 2402 and 2403, - computers and computer components, tariff headings 8471 and 8473 30, - mobile phones and their accessories, tariff headings 8525 20 91, 8525 20 99, 8529 90 40.
