Both parties agreed that the selection of tax entities for inspection will be carried out: (A) from non-allocated items found by comparing exports and imports of selected commodities between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, (b) from entities carrying out imports and exports on a regular or one-off basis in large volumes, (c) on the basis of findings from inspections carried out by selected tax and tax authorities.
4.2. Comparison of customs databases of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
In the first stage, the mechanism for cross-referencing JCD items registered in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic was tested on a sample of imports and exports of selected commodities for the month of October 2002.
Subsequently, part of the exports from the Czech Republic were compared with imports into the Slovak Republic for 2002 and vice versa for selected commodities according to the customs tariff:
- 2207 undenatured ethyl alcohol of an alcoholic strength by volume of 80% vol or more; ethyl alcohol and other spirits, denatured, of any strength,
- 2208 undenatured ethyl alcohol of an alcoholic strength by volume of less than 80% vol; spirits, liqueurs and other spirituous beverages;
- 2401 Unprocessed tobacco; tobacco waste;
- 2402 Cigars (whether or not with the ends cut off), cigarillos and cigarettes of tobacco or tobacco substitutes,
- 2403 Other tobacco products and tobacco substitutes; homogenised or reconstituted tobacco; tobacco extracts and essences;
- 8525 20 91 Transmission apparatus containing reception equipment: For the cellular network (mobile phones),
- 8525 20 99 Transmission apparatus containing reception apparatus:
- 8529 90 40 Parts suitable for use solely or principally with the apparatus of headings 8525 to 8528.
Other: Parts of apparatus falling in subheadings 8525 10 50, 8525 20 91, 8525 20 99, 8525 40 11 and 8527 90 92.
JCD items from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia were assigned to each other on the basis of the conformity of the individual paragraphs of the JCD (e.g. invoiced price, quantity, weight, registration number of the vehicle carrying the cargo, date of crossing of the national border, tariff item, etc.).
The results of the comparison are presented in the following tables and graphs.
The fact that trade transactions were not declared in the same way on both sides made it difficult, among other things, to match imports and exports.
For example, exports from the Czech Republic, declared on one export JCD, were declared on several import JCDs in the territory of the Slovak Republic, or the export JCD had a different number of items from the import JCD.
Other factors that had an impact on the success of the assignment were the different composition of data in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, as well as the time difference between the registration of exports in the customs database of one country and the registration of corresponding imports in the customs database of another country.
The results of the comparison were used in the selection of control samples at the audited tax and tax offices respectively.
Priority was given to certain tax entities that carried out imports or exports between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, which could not be identified in both databases.
In addition, some tax entities were selected for the verification of business transactions reported in VAT returns, where data on imports or exports between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic were found in both databases.
4.3. Pilot check at the Starý Hrozenkov-Drietoma border crossing point
The border customs crossing point for the performance of the pilot inspection was selected on the basis of a joint analysis of non-allocated JCD items in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
On the basis of a bilateral agreement between the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, the use of control sheets has been introduced at border customs crossing points between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic since 1 June 1998.
The aim of this measure was to eliminate as far as possible customs and tax evasion, to provide an overview of the movement of means of transport carrying goods of a commercial nature in the customs area and to create the conditions for comparing customs records with each other.
The joint pilot inspection was carried out between 8.3.2004 and 26.3.2004 and was aimed at examining this system of customs control.
Procedure for the use of checklists at the Starý Hrozenkov-Drietoma border crossing point:
1) Weighing the vehicle, issuing a checklist and handing it over to the driver.
2) Putting the vehicle in the designated sector in the parking lot.
Customs discussion in the check-in hall of the Police of the Czech Republic, Police of the Slovak Republic, Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, Customs Administration of the Slovak Republic.
The completion of the check-in process was confirmed by the individual files by stamping on the checklist.
(3) Landing the vehicle in the area where the physical inspection is carried out.
Presentation of the checklist, JCD or other documents to the customs official - check that all prescribed acts and documents have been carried out.
Carrying out a physical check by the relevant services.
Release of the vehicle from the customs area.
When importing goods into the Czech Republic, the weighing of vehicles was carried out directly by the staff of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
When the goods were imported into the Slovak Republic, the weighing of the vehicles was carried out by the staff of an authorised legal entity.
After consideration, the vehicles were registered in a computerised register.

Exports from the Czech Republic to Slovakia

When exported from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic, the control sheets were issued and registered by the Customs Administration of the Slovak Republic.

Of the 453 JCD items, the SAO SR found 256 cases of imports into the Slovak Republic according to data from the customs database of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic. The remaining 44 cases were identified in their records by the staff of the Drietoma border customs crossing and the export of goods from the Slovak Republic to the Czech Republic was confirmed.
The audit of the SAO and the SAO of the Slovak Republic did not find shortcomings in the registration of selected cases of imports and exports of goods in 2002 at the Starý Hrozenkov-Drietoma border crossing point.
4.4. Selected control findings in the verification of commercial transactions
In the framework of international cooperation, the implementation of imports and exports between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic was verified on the basis of documents from customs administrations and financial and tax authorities in the territory of the other country.
For the selected tax entities, the following were verified:
- whether the submitted JCDs were registered in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia,
- the fulfilment of the legal conditions for the application of the VAT deduction on importation, the refund of excess VAT and the application of the VAT exemption on exportation.
The verification of the commercial transactions revealed:
1. The SAO asked the Slovak Republic to verify the implementation of the export of alcohol with a statistical value of 56 989 Sk.
The SAO identified the corresponding imports in the Czech customs database with a statistical value of CZK 42,624.
2. The company involved in the import and export of photographic equipment and accessories claimed an excess VAT deduction of CZK 3,740,664 in the VAT return for December 2002.
In order to check the reported exports from the Czech Republic, the SAO selected 3 JCDs (16 items) with a statistical value of CZK 1,274,822.
The SAO SR identified 3 corresponding import JCDs (17 items) with a statistical value of 1,724,321 Sk.
VAT was paid to the competent customs office in Slovakia.
3. The company, whose business was mainly trading in optical equipment, claimed in 2002 a total excess VAT deduction of CZK 4,1,36,000 higher than the tax liability.
The SAO selected an export JCD (32 items) with a statistical value of CZK 7,154,124 for the verification of the reported business activities.
The SAO SR found that this JCD corresponds to an import JCD (12 items) with a statistical value of 9 653 827 Sk.
VAT was paid to the competent customs office in Slovakia.
4. The company involved, inter alia, in the purchase of goods for resale and sale, did not declare any exports of goods in the VAT returns submitted in 2002 and 2003.
According to the Customs Database of the Czech Republic, the statistical value of exports of goods in 2002 totalled CZK 3,439,888.
Based on these facts, the SAO selected 5 export JCDs (5 items) with a total statistical value of CZK 669,839 for verification.
The SAO SR identified 5 corresponding import JCDs (5 items) with a statistical value of 1 012 656 Sk.
An audit by the SAO of the Slovak Republic at the relevant tax office showed that the declared imports had been carried out and VAT paid.
5. The company, whose business was, among other things, the purchase of goods for resale and sale, production, installation and repair of electrical machinery and equipment, reported exports of goods worth CZK 12,966,706 in VAT returns in 2002.
According to the Customs Database of the Czech Republic, the total value of exports in 2002 was 14,474,381 CZK.
The SAO presented 17 export JCDs (59 items) with a total statistical value of CZK 2,975,122.
The SAO SR identified 13 JCDs (50 items) in the SR customs database with a statistical value of 3 621 370 Sk.
The SR customs database failed to identify the corresponding import JCDs for 4 export JCDs (9 items) with a total statistical value of 399,776 CZK.
The competent tax office in Slovakia verified these imports with the tax entity.
The tax entity, listed on the JCD as an importer to the Slovak Republic, stated in the minutes of the local investigation that it did not carry out the imports declared on the Czech export JCDs.
The SAO of the Slovak Republic therefore asked the local competent tax office to carry out a tax audit of VAT and corporate tax for the tax years 2002 and 2003.
According to the Customs Database of the Czech Republic, the company involved in the import and sale of cigarettes exported tobacco stickers with a statistical value of 7,338,199 CZK in 2002 and 12,228,545 CZK in 2003.
The company did not declare any exports in its VAT returns in 2002 and 2003.
The SAO selected 5 export JCDs (5 items) for verification, with a total statistical value of CZK 2,471,598.
In addition to the 4 export JCDs (4 items) with a total statistical value of CZK 2,246,860, the SAO SR identified 7 JCDs (7 items) with a statistical value of CZK 2,919,514 in the SR customs database.
The corresponding imports could not be attributed to the export JCD (1 item) with a statistical value of CZK 224,738 in the SR customs database.
The software company did not declare exports of goods in its VAT returns for 2002 and 2003.
According to the Customs Database of the Czech Republic, the statistical value of exports of goods in 2002 and 2003 totalled CZK 1,630,198.
The SAO selected 9 JCDs (9 items) for verification in the Slovak Republic with a total statistical value of 755,588 CZK.
In the SR customs database, the SAO SR identified 8 JCDs (8 items) with a statistical value of 915 601 Sk.
The corresponding imports could not be attributed to the export JCD (1 item) with a statistical value of CZK 68,286 in the SR customs database.
In these cases, it was not possible to identify in the SR customs database the corresponding imports to 6 JCDs with a statistical value of 692,800 CZK.
Of which:
- for the 2 export JCDs from the Czech customs database with a statistical value of 293,024 CZK, the corresponding import JCDs could not be identified in the Slovak customs database (see paragraphs 6 and 7).
Due to a certain error rate in entering data into the customs database, it was not possible to identify some registered imports, e.g. in cases where the name of the importer was missing or there was an error in the tax identification number ("TIN").
It is therefore not possible to conclude with certainty that those exports were not made.
- 4 export JCDs from the customs database of the Czech Republic did not show imports corresponding to exports from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic with a statistical value of 399,776 CZK (see paragraph 5).
In such cases, there are reasonable grounds to suspect the fictitious export of goods for the purpose of improperly claiming the VAT deduction.
5. Control of imports and exports of goods and services as part of the control of selected tax and tax authorities
5.1. Control sample
In order to verify the fulfilment of the obligations of tax entities in respect of imports and exports of goods and services and to evaluate the level of cooperation between the tax and customs authorities, the files of tax entities were selected at the audited tax and tax offices according to the following criteria:
1. tax entities were selected from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic: (A) with the highest volume of imports, (b) with the highest amount of VAT charged, (c) with the highest volume of exports,
(A) the VAT deductions applied on importation, (b) the excess VAT deductions applied, (c) the right to a refund of the SPD, (d) the VAT exemption applied on exportation,
3. tax entities that have been subject to a tax audit.
The sampling was carried out irrespective of the country of destination, with a focus on risky commodities.
5.2. Control findings in the Czech Republic
An overview of imports into the Czech Republic and exports from the Czech Republic for risky commodities in 2002 and 2003 is shown in the following table:
5.2.1. Control of the selected sample at tax offices
At the audited tax offices, the SAO focused mainly on:
- the procedure followed by the tax authorities to verify the accuracy of the VAT declared;
- cooperation between the tax authorities and the customs administration;
- comparing data from the customs database with the JCD database at the tax offices, focusing on comparing the declared value, applying the correct VAT rate following the customs classification of goods or services, or comparing data on the JCD and accompanying invoices with data in the customs database;
- comparing data from VAT returns on transactions carried out and received from abroad with data in the JCD database at tax offices or in the customs database;
- the method of verifying entitlement to VAT exemption on the export of goods or services abroad,
- a comparison of the volume of exports of goods or services declared in VAT returns with data from the customs database.
The JCD database at the tax offices contained only records of those imports and exports for which tax entities were required to declare imports or exports on the tax return.
The audited tax offices examined the files of tax entities, which reported imports totalling CZK 60,396,379,000 and corresponding VAT totalling CZK 12,644,052,000 in VAT returns in 2002 and 2003.
In addition, the files of tax entities reporting exports worth a total of CZK 47,323,111,000 in tax returns for 2002 and 2003 were checked.
According to the Customs Database of the Czech Republic, in 2002 and 2003, the tax entities for which imports and exports between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic were examined carried out imports into the Czech Republic from the Slovak Republic with a total VAT base of CZK 3,759,352,000, VAT of CZK 767,607,000 and exports from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic with a total statistical value of CZK 1,989,090,000.
The observed differences between the records in the JCD database at the tax offices and in the customs database of the Czech Republic were examined as follows:
- JCD items that were missing from the Czech customs database were requested directly from the General Directorate of Customs of the Czech Republic,
- JCD items that were missing from the tax authorities' database were checked for cancelled documents;
- for JCD items, which were found to have different values between the customs database of the Czech Republic and the database of the tax authorities, the relevant JCD was requested from the General Directorate of Customs of the Czech Republic in written form, including the attached invoices.
The investigation revealed that the JCD database at the tax offices did not contain, for example, records of import JCDs with a total value of VAT of CZK 3,622,000 and records of export JCDs with a total statistical value of CZK 9,359,000.
5.2.1.1. Differences identified
A comparison of the JCD database at the tax offices and the cumulative tax liability for 2002 and 2003 in the VAT returns of a selected sample of tax entities revealed the following differences:
The differences in values were mainly due to:
- The time lag between the realisation of imports and the exercise of the right to deduct the VAT charged on the importation of goods.
The taxable person could exercise the right to deduct on importation of the goods within 3 years of the end of the tax year in which the goods were placed under the relevant procedure or, in the case of the temporary importation procedure, within 3 years of the end of the tax year in which the procedure ended.
- The time lag between the realisation of the export and the moment when the taxpayer received the JCD.
The taxpayer was obliged to enter data on realised exports exempt from the obligation to apply output tax in the VAT return at the earliest for the tax year in which the goods left the country, if he also had a tax document, which was a JCD.
- Failure to comply with the obligations of tax entities when declaring imports and exports in VAT returns.
In some cases, tax entities did not provide correct data on imports and exports in their VAT returns.
As tax entities did not have to attach JCD lists to the VAT returns submitted, the control of the right to deduct VAT or the exemption from VAT by the tax authorities was made more difficult.
5.2.2. Cooperation between financial and customs authorities
During the audited period, import or export duties and VAT were repaid or remitted on the basis of decisions taken by the customs authorities.
The tax entities were required by law to reduce the previously exercised right to deduct VAT by the amount of tax returned by the customs office in the tax return for the period in which the tax was refunded.
No legislation provided for information on changes in the level of customs duties and VAT to be sent from customs offices to tax offices.
Some of the audited tax offices received this information, but irregularly or with considerable delays, and only from some customs offices.
One audited tax office did not receive this information at all.
If the tax office did not receive information about changes in the amount of customs duties and VAT directly from the customs office, it did not have the data necessary to check compliance with the legal obligation of tax entities.
In 2002 the customs authorities returned VAT in the amount of more than CZK 319 million and in 2003 in the amount of more than CZK 398 million.
The results of the audit revealed persistent shortcomings in the activities of the tax authorities, some systemic errors in the cooperation of the tax authorities with the customs authorities and the failure to comply with certain obligations of taxpayers submitting VAT returns and the SPD.
Weaknesses were identified in the VAT and SPD administration, in particular in the following areas:
(A) when VAT registrations are cancelled, the fulfilment of the obligation of the payers to pay VAT on the business property registered or which should have been registered on the date of the deregistration, for which the payer claimed the deduction, was only rarely verified;
(B) the tax authorities have not consistently used the possibility to carry out a tax audit or a local investigation.
This has in some cases led to a lack of verification of the right to deduct VAT;
(C) the official records and minutes of the oral hearing do not contain all the necessary information to prove the validity of the excess VAT deductions claimed;
(D) the tax authorities have not sufficiently verified the imports and exports declared in the VAT returns.
5.3. Control findings in SR
5.3.1. Control of the selected sample at tax offices
For the selected sample, the SAO audited or the tax office carried out a tax audit for the tax years 2002 and 2003.
After analysing the submitted tax returns and requests for tax refunds from selected tax entities, the SAO asked the tax office to secure the relevant JCDs showing imports and exports, invoices and proof of payment of the tax.
Subsequently, the SAO SR checked whether the submitted JCDs were registered in the customs database of imports and exports and the fulfilment of the decisive facts and legal conditions for the application of the deduction of input tax in respect of imports, for the refund of excess VAT, for the application of the export tax exemption and for the reimbursement of SPD.
At the 10 tax offices audited, the SAO of the Slovak Republic verified selected cases of imports and exports of goods between the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in a structure according to the honour of JCD items and the sum of statistical values shown in the table below.
In total, imports with a statistical value of CZK 856.2 million were checked, which represents 5.11% of the total value of imports of selected commodities from the Czech Republic to SROV.
Exports of selected commodities were checked for a total statistical value of 176 million SK, which represents 6.87% of the total value of exports of selected commodities from the Slovak Republic to the Czech Republic.
In addition, 618 cases of imports of other goods and services (mainly white technology, packaging technology and software) from EU countries to the Slovak Republic were checked for a total statistical value of 532.8 million SK.
5.3.2. Cooperation between tax and customs authorities
The SAO of the Slovak Republic's audit at the tax offices found discrepancies between the data registered in the Slovak customs database and the data reported in specific VAT returns, e.g.:
- 2 tax entities (natural persons) declared imports of goods with a total value of Sk 1 589 261 in their tax returns, on the basis of which they claimed a refund of excess VAT deductions.
In local investigations carried out at the initiative of the SAO SR, tax entities were not able to prove to the tax office that the application of the input tax was justified by the relevant documents on the realisation of imports and the payment of VAT,
- in the tax return for the tax year January 2003, the tax entity (s. r. o.) declared the taxable transaction received in the value of 77 167 576 Sk, the export of goods in the value of 18 006 041 Sk and claimed an excess VAT deduction of 17 157 101 Sk.
According to the VAT returns submitted for 2003, the difference between the volume of purchases and exports of Sk 59 161 535, which arose in January 2003, was not made up during the whole of 2003.
In the cases mentioned above, the SAO asked the relevant tax authorities to carry out a tax audit of the excess VAT deductions applied.
- in another case, the tax entity (s. r. o.) for the tax period January to June 2002 stated in the VAT returns the export of goods with a total value of 87 199 Sk.
A verification in the SR customs database revealed that the tax entity had made exports with a statistical value of SKK 296 747 during the period.
The Tax Office carried out a number of local inquiries at the company's head office, finding that the manager of the company (a UK citizen) had travelled and the company had left the rented premises without terminating the lease in August 2002.
At the time of the audit of the SAO SR, the tax administration filed a complaint with the law enforcement authorities on suspicion of the crime of non-payment of tax.
Based on the results of the audit at the selected tax offices, the SAO SR notes that the biggest problems in the performance of the administration and control of VAT and SPD occurred mainly in the following areas:
- not making use of the possibility to carry out VAT checks on problematic tax entities, in particular in cases where the high value of excess VAT deductions is applied;
- the tax inspection reports did not contain an inventory of the audited documents
- JCDs for the import and export of goods;
- insufficient verification of declared imports and exports of goods in tax returns;
- lengthy procedures for tax administrations to issue decisions, in particular in the context of the assessment procedure, with the consequence that the right to impose penalties ceases to exist;
- failure to comply with legal conditions when granting tax deferrals;
- failure to compensate for VAT arrears by the deadline for the refund of excess VAT;
- under-utilisation of all forms of security and recovery of tax arrears.
On the basis of the findings of the audit, the SAO asked the relevant tax authorities to carry out a tax audit of VAT, focusing on the legitimacy of the claimed excess VAT deductions for 14 tax entities.
At all audited tax offices, measures have been taken to remedy the shortcomings identified by the audit, the implementation of which will be monitored and audited by the SAO.
6. Conclusion
International cooperation has made it possible to examine trade transactions between trading partners from both countries and has highlighted shortcomings in the registration of imports and exports.
The inspections also resulted in the identification of persistent deficiencies in the performance of VAT and SPD obligations, in the activities of the tax and tax authorities, in the system of cooperation and exchange of information between tax and customs authorities, which ultimately reduced the efficiency and effectiveness of tax controls.
The findings also showed that the tax authorities in the Czech Republic have basic data on imports and exports from the customs database of the Czech Republic as part of the tax information system. In the Slovak Republic, there is no similar system for transmitting information on imports and exports of goods between the customs and tax administration.
The procedure for verifying the performance of the VAT administration and the SPD was not the same, due to the different legislation and conditions in the territory of the two states.
The SAO verified the necessary data from information obtained at the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic and from documents available at the audited tax offices. The SAO of the Slovak Republic verified the execution of business transactions from documents of tax entities requested through the tax authorities.
If irregularities were found, he asked the tax authorities to carry out tax checks.
The parallel VAT and SPD checks carried out assessed the state of the administration of these taxes in the period before accession to the European Union and pointed to the need for further cooperation in this area.
Mutual cooperation will be further enhanced in the monitoring of the activities of the tax and tax authorities in the context of the adoption of the new VAT law.
One of the new obligations related to the delivery of goods to other Member States of the European Union is the submission of a so-called summary report.
This declaration must be made by all VAT payers who have made a supply of goods to another Member State to a person registered for VAT in another Member State.
Tax administrations are required to enter data from recapitulative statements into the VAT Information Exchange System (VIES), which is accessible to tax administrations from Member States of the European Union.
The tax and tax authorities then have the opportunity to compare these data with the data contained in the VAT returns submitted.
This system is also used to verify the validity of the VAT registration number of persons registered for VAT, to verify the validity of the VAT exemption applied when goods are delivered to another Member State and to check the proper taxation of goods.
The implementation of parallel audit actions has shown the possibilities of cooperation between the SAO and the SAO of the Slovak Republic.
The results of these control actions will be confronted with the results of the planned control actions, which will focus, among other things, on the examination of the VIES system, which is designed to prevent tax evasion in so-called "intra-community supplies."
Given the importance of VAT and SPD for budgetary revenue, control activities need to focus primarily on monitoring and identifying risk areas in order to reduce the scope for tax evasion in indirect taxes.
Communiqué
This report was drawn up in Czech, English and Slovak and signed by the Vice-President of the Supreme Audit Office and the Chairman of the Najvyššššie Audit Office of the Slovak Republic.
Report on the results of checks at asylum facilities in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
State property and funds intended to secure the activities of the Refugee Facilities Administration of the Ministry of the Interior
Control Action No 04 / 23 "State property and funds intended to ensure the activities of the Refugee Facilities Administration of the Ministry of the Interior"
Control action No 15 / 2004 "Control of the economy with staff and financial resources for the provision of asylum and temporary refuge in the Slovak Republic"
1. Introduction
Population migration is one of the global phenomena that has become an inseparable part of the current development phase of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
This is mainly due to the flight of citizens from their country of origin or last permanent residence from persecution, in particular for reasons of race, religion, nationality, politics, as well as the consequences of military conflicts and ethnic cleansing.
Their aim is to gain asylum and integration into society, especially in one of the advanced democratic countries of Europe.
A large group is also made up of foreigners, whose migration is due to unfavourable economic and living conditions.
Migration is not a new phenomenon.
The adoption of the 1951 Geneva Agreement and the 1967 New York Protocol on the Status of Refugees, the acceptance of which the governments of the signatory countries undertook to apply in their foreign policy orientation, has already resulted in the establishment of specific principles for refugee assistance.
The Czech and Slovak Federal Republics ratified the New York Protocol in 1991 and the Geneva Agreement in 1992.
After the separation in 1993, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic declared their position on the refugee issue by continuing to comply with accepted international documents and confirmed their binding force under national legislation by a legal act.
Both Republics have also enshrined the granting of asylum in their constitutional laws.
Parallel checks carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Najvyššší kontrolný úradom Slovenskej republiky, the results of which are contained in the joint final report, focused on the asylum process and related issues.
The cooperation between the supreme audit authorities of the two countries was carried out on the basis of the "Treaty on Cooperation in Control Activities" (hereinafter referred to as "the Treaty") concluded in April 2004.
In the Treaty, the two Parties undertook to provide each other with information on the legislation governing the asylum procedure in the State of the other Party, selected statistics on the number of asylum seekers and the results of the asylum process, as well as information on asylum facilities.
The aim of the parallel control action was to identify the same problem areas and to highlight the consequences for the area of population migration.
The cooperation consisted in the unification of the programme of control actions, the exchange of information to the extent provided for by the Treaty and the preparation of a joint final report on the outcome of the checks.
The first joint meeting, which took place from 5.4 to 7.4.2004, set out the same areas of control issues and control procedures for the preparation of control actions.
At the second meeting, which took place from 28.6 to 30.6. 2004, the common items for the programme of the control action were specified.
During the third joint meeting, which took place during the inspection mission from 8.11 to 10.11.2004, there was an exchange of experience on the ongoing inspections.
The modalities of the outcome of the checks have been specified and the structure and content of the joint final report, which was drawn up from 14.2. to 17.2.2005 at the last joint meeting, has been provisionally established.
The checks were carried out in parallel between September 2004 and January 2005.
In the Czech Republic, the inspection was carried out by inspectors of the Department of Defence and Security and selected territorial departments.
The audited persons were the Ministry of the Interior ("MV") and the Administration of Refugee Facilities of the Ministry of the Interior ("SUZ").
In the Slovak Republic, it carried out inspections of the defence section, vnútra and štátnych úradov.
The audited entity was the Migračný úrad Ministerstvo vnútra SR ("MÚ").
The audited period covered the years 2001, 2002 and 2003 (the audited period).
In some cases, statistical data over a longer period of time are also used in the joint report.
2. Recap of inspection results
2.1. Evaluation of control activities
The subject of parallel checks was: - the asylum process, - asylum facilities, - the management of state funds and assets, - the internal control system.
The mutual exchange of experience between the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Najvyššší kontrolní úradom Slovenskej republiky took place at the stage of preparation and implementation of the control actions.
This exchange allowed for a more thorough evaluation of the submitted supporting documents, an analysis of the causes of the identified differences in the security of the asylum process.
In this way, it was possible to focus on the critical problems affecting the activities of asylum facilities.
In the end, this had a positive effect on the quality of the control work carried out.
2.2 Summary of control results
The harmonisation of the asylum laws of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic with European Union (EU) documents was the subject of evaluation reports by the European Commission on the readiness of both countries to join the EU.
The adoption of legislation in this area continues after the accession of the two countries to the EU with a view to further harmonisation with EU law.
The number of asylum seekers in the Czech Republic increased significantly in 2001.
In the Slovak Republic, the number of applicants has been on a steadily increasing trend, with a significant increase in applicants in 2001.
Within the meaning of international agreements, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic provide financial and material security for asylum seekers.
The national budgets of both countries allocate the necessary funds for this purpose.
The amount of expenditure drawn from the state budget of both countries is mainly influenced by the number of applicants, the duration of the asylum procedure until asylum is granted or not granted, as well as the state of health of the applicants.
Some of the doses collected are comparable in both countries.
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic have set up asylum facilities in which they have gradually created suitable conditions for the stay of participants in asylum procedures.
During their stay, asylum seekers are provided with accommodation, meals, health care and basic material and hygiene equipment.
At the same time, courses are organised as part of leisure activities and the conditions for cultural and sporting activities are created for applicants.
Asylum facilities include reception centres and residential centres as well as integration centres in the Czech Republic.
The cost per day of stay depends on the occupancy and equipment of the centre and is comparable in both countries.
In the Czech Republic, the capacity of asylum facilities is basically stable.
In the Slovak Republic, it is expected to increase by almost 1 000 jobs in the next two years.
The aim is to create the conditions for applicants, an increasing number of whom are expected to continue in the coming years in the context of the application of the Dublin Convention.
In the Czech Republic, the highest part of the approved budget expenditure was spent on the provision of services. The decisive expenditure of this item was expenditure on accommodation and meals for applicants in asylum facilities operated under contract, expenditure on health care provided to asylum seekers and the cost of a permanent security service ensuring the protection of asylum facilities.
Expenditure on salaries, payments for work carried out and insurance premiums also accounted for a significant share of total expenditure.
In the Slovak Republic, the budgetary management of the security of migration policy and the asylum process was marked by a number of budgetary measures addressing legitimate demands related to the increase in the number of asylum seekers.
Expenditure on wages, salaries and insurance premiums, expenditure on materials and services and expenditure on security services were a decisive factor in the absorption of current expenditure.
The results of the audit in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic highlighted some similar shortcomings which did not have a major impact on the financial management and management of the state's assets.
These were mainly shortcomings in the use of state budget funds, contrary to the purpose for which they were determined by the State Budget Act, when current expenditure was used to cover actions in the nature of technical evaluation of fixed tangible assets.
The Act on Accounting in the Field of Inventory and Non-Compliance with the Accounting Curriculum was also violated.
In the Czech Republic, minor deficiencies were also found in the disposal of state property when it was transferred to another person without a contract.
Failure to comply with the deadline for reporting changes in land registry data violated the Land Registry Act and the Waste Act was violated by leaving waste for disposal to a person who was not a person authorised for waste management.
In the Slovak Republic, deficiencies were also found in the provision of excessively high advances for the collection of electricity and natural gas, deficiencies in the award of public contracts and in the management of the state's assets, when its records were not sufficiently secured and the method of liquidating unnecessary assets was not demonstrated.
The internal control system has been ensured in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic within the meaning of the generally binding legislation in force governing the way financial control is carried out.
No deficiencies were found in the written documentation submitted.
Despite some shortcomings identified, the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Najvyšší kontrolný úrad Slovenské republiky are positive about the progress of SUZ and MÚ in providing services for asylum seekers.
Based on the lessons learned during the inspection, the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Najvyššší kontrolný úrad Slovenské republiky note that despite a significant increase in the number of asylum seekers in recent years, the respective organisational units of both countries have managed the tasks related to the care of asylum seekers at an appropriate level.
The evaluation shows that the system is functional and stable.
The results of the inspection were discussed with the interested statutory representatives of the relevant organisational units of the state on both the Czech and Slovak sides.
Based on the results of the inspection, we recommend that the positive methodological experience of the inspection be used in other joint control actions within the framework of international cooperation between supreme audit institutions.
3. Legislative framework
In both the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, asylum law is based on the 1951 Geneva Convention (the Convention relating to the Status of Refugees and the subsequent 1967 New York Protocol).
The first legislation was implemented by Act No 498 / 1990 Coll., on Refugees.
In the Czech Republic, Act No. 325 / 1999 Coll., on Asylum and amending Act No. 83 / 1991 Coll., on the Police of the Czech Republic, has been in force since 1 January 2000.
This law has been amended five times (Act No. 2 / 2002 Coll., Act No. 217 / 2002 Coll., Act No. 320 / 2002 Coll., Act No. 519 / 2002 Coll., and Act No. 222 / 2003 Coll.).
Two other amendments to Act No.325 / 1999 Coll., on Asylum, are currently in the legislative process and the adoption of further amendments will be linked to European legislation.
At the time of the creation of Act No.325 / 1999 Coll., on Asylum, the area of asylum was part of the 3rd pillar of the EU and asylum documents were political documents in terms of binding force.
Even as part of the adoption of this law, efforts were made to make it as compatible as possible with EU law.
A major change for asylum policy within the EU was the transfer of asylum issues from the 3rd to the 1st pillar, when asylum law became part of Community law from 1.5.1999 on the basis of the Amsterdam Treaty.
This shift has led to the need to create appropriate legislation, i.e. to create legal instruments that are legally binding.
The compatibility of Czech asylum law with EU documents has been the subject of regular evaluation reports by the European Commission.
Key Community regulations in the field of asylum were adopted shortly before or after the Czech Republic joined the EU and their transposition period at the time of the inspection by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic has not yet expired.
Once they have been implemented in the Czech legal order, the Czech Republic will be obliged to notify the European Commission of how it has implemented the transposition.
In the Slovak Republic, the procedure of the state authorities in the procedure for granting refugee status and determining the obligations of foreigners who have applied for refugee status or who have been granted temporary refuge in the territory of the Slovak Republic was laid down with effect from 1.1.1996 by the Act of the National Council of the Slovak Republic No 283 / 1995 Z. z., on refugees.
Since 2003, the Refugee Act has been replaced by Act No 480 / 2002 Z. z "on asylum and amending and supplementing certain laws, which incorporated the harmonisation of the legislation of the Slovak Republic with Council of Europe Directive 2001 / 55 / EC of 20.7.2001 on minimum standards for the provision of temporary protection in the event of a mass influx of displaced persons and on measures to promote a balance of efforts between Member States in receiving such persons and bearing the consequences thereof.
After two amendments to Act No.480 / 2002 Z. z., on Asylum, in 2003 and 2004, a third amendment was approved at the beginning of 2005, which means further harmonisation of the law of the Slovak Republic with the EU legislation on migration and asylum.
Its important elements are, for example, the establishment of an obligation for asylum seekers to attend a course on the basics of the Slovak language during their stay at the integration centre, the appointment of a guardian by the courts for underage foreigners if they are staying in the territory of the Slovak Republic without a legal representative, the possibility for applicants to enter into an employment relationship in certain circumstances, as specified in the amendment to the law.
The harmonisation of the law of the Slovak Republic with EU law in the area of migration and the asylum process has been evaluated in the European Commission's regular reports on preparedness for the Slovak Republic's accession to the EU.
In 2002, the report highlighted the lack of staffing in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, which did not correspond to the increased number of asylum seekers.
4. The asylum process
In the Czech Republic, refugee issues have been the responsibility of the Ministry of Justice since 1990.
With effect from 1 January 1996, the Ministry established the organisational arm of the state of SUZ. This was due to the separation of the administration's performance in the field of asylum procedure, which is carried out through the Department of Asylum and Migration Policy of the Ministry of Agriculture, from the provision of services to asylum seekers.
The task of the SUZ is to provide accommodation, catering, health and other services to participants in asylum procedures and asylum seekers.
In the Slovak Republic, the Ministry performs decisive tasks in the area of the asylum process, in particular from the point of view of the financial and material-technical security of the asylum process, to the extent defined by specific regulations.
Priority tasks are issues related to the decision on applications for asylum by foreigners in the first stage of the administrative procedure and the complex operation of asylum facilities in the areas of accommodation, meals, health, financial and material security of asylum seekers.
In addition, it is preparing concepts for the migration policy of the state.
The results achieved in the development of the asylum system in the Slovak Republic in recent years have been significantly influenced by the cooperation and support provided by the Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees (UNHCR).
A particular benefit was his financial contribution to the reconstruction of the housing stock for asylum seekers.
UNHCR has also co-funded social, cultural and sporting activities for applicants.
4.1 Evolution in the number of asylum seekers and the results of the asylum process
The development of the number of asylum seekers in the Czech Republic is shown in the graph.
There was a significant increase in 2001 due to the Kosovo crisis and in 2003 there was an increase in the number of refugees from Chechnya.
An overview of the results of the asylum procedure in the Czech Republic can be found in Table 1.
A total of 394 cases were granted asylum during the period under review, including 83 in 2001, 103 in 2002 and 208 in 2003.
A total of 22,731 asylum cases were not granted during the period under review and 22,636 asylum procedures were discontinued.
The number of parties to the proceedings at 1.1. includes both those to whom the decision has not yet been issued and those to whom the decision has not been transmitted.
It also includes people who have been excused from missing the deadline for lodging an appeal, or whose previous decision has been overturned and a new one has not yet been issued.
In the Slovak Republic, the number of asylum seekers is on a steadily increasing trend.
If 96 applicants were registered in 1993, in 2003 it was already 10,358.
There was a significant increase in the number of applicants in 2001, when 8,131 applicants were registered, an increase of 423% compared to 2000, when 1,556 people applied for asylum.
Data on the results of the asylum procedure in the Slovak Republic during the audited period are presented in Table 2.
A total of 49 asylum applications were granted during the audited period and the number did not exceed 0.22% of the registered number of applicants per year.
Asylum was not granted in 860 cases.
A total of 23,088 asylum procedures have been closed.
The majority of applicants, by staying outside the asylum facility without permission, voluntarily left the asylum procedure before it was completed.
In 2002 it accounted for more than 82% of the total number of registered applicants, and in 2003 it was already more than 94%.
The duration of one applicant's stay in an asylum facility, converted into an average number of days, was 13 days in 2001, 18 days in 2002 and 19 days in 2003.
The findings of the Ministry also show that most applicants entering the asylum process in the Slovak Republic are seeking better living conditions, i.e. so-called economic migration, which has no basis in documents adopted by the international community, to which the Slovak Republic has also signed up.
In such cases, the asylum system is used for a purpose by applicants.
An application for asylum based on economic reasons, such as seeking employment or better living conditions, does not qualify for asylum.
According to the provisions of Section 12 (1) (a) of Act No 480 / 2002 Z. z., on asylum, such an application should be considered manifestly unfounded and decided upon within 30 days.
Internationally recognised principles to identify economic migrants are not yet in place to distinguish them from those persecuted in their country of origin and to speed up the asylum process.
In view of the above, it can be concluded that the Slovak Republic is a transit country from the point of view of international migration and the destination countries for migration were and remain Western European countries.
After joining the EU, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic acceded to the Agreement designating the State responsible for examining asylum applications lodged in one of the Member States of the European Communities (Dublin Convention).
The Convention prevents multiple asylum applications from being made in more than one EU country.
Applicants shall return to the country of first registration after positive identification in EURODAC.
The Slovak Republic is part of the external borders of EU countries, so the application of the Dublin Convention may in the next period result in an increase in the number of applicants who will need to create the conditions to stay in the Slovak Republic until a decision is taken on whether or not to grant asylum.
4.2 Execution of funds
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic are obliged to provide financial and material security to asylum seekers within the meaning of the international agreements and the national legislation based on them.
The national budgets of both countries allocate the necessary funds for this purpose.
The amount of expenditure drawn from the state budget is mainly influenced by the number of applicants, the duration of the asylum procedure until the final decision on the granting of asylum and their state of health.
The increasing number of people entering the asylum process has a direct impact on the higher uptake of statutory benefits for applicants, such as food, pocket money, expenditure on basic material equipment, other material equipment and other social contributions.
Some of the doses collected are comparable in both countries.
In the Czech Republic, during the audited period, the meal allowance was CZK 58 per person per day, the allowance was CZK 12 per person per day and CZK 6 per child under the age of 15.
The cost per asylum seeker per day was on average CZK 351 in 2001, CZK 383 in 2002 and CZK 345 in 2003.
In addition to the allowance, asylum seekers accommodated in residential centres with separate cooking and those accommodated in private outside asylum facilities can be granted a contribution up to the minimum subsistence level.
Act No 325 / 1999 Coll., on Asylum, as amended, inter alia grants municipalities the right to a contribution to cover the costs incurred in connection with an asylum facility on its territory, in Section 84.
The amount of the allowance was determined annually by government resolutions and during the audited period it was CZK 7 per person per day of stay.
At the same time, municipalities are entitled to an allowance to cover the non-investment costs of primary schools attended by asylum seekers.
The amount of the allowance was CZK 120 per pupil per month during the audited period, on condition that the person attended school for a minimum of 10 days in that month.
In the Slovak Republic, during the audited period, the meals were 70 Sk per person per day, the allowance was 12 Sk per person per day and 8 Sk per child under 15 years of age.
The cost per asylum seeker per day of stay averaged 442 Sk in 2001, 447 Sk in 2002 and 445 Sk in 2003.
In accordance with Act No 480 / 2002 Z. z., on Asylum, municipalities in whose territory there is an asylum facility are granted a contribution towards the partial reimbursement of expenses incurred by the municipality in connection with the establishment and operation of the asylum facility.
So far, municipalities have only partially used the possibility to apply for the allowance, which is set at 1,500 Sk per bed per calendar year.
National legislation in both countries provides for a 90-day period from the start of the asylum procedure for issuing asylum decisions, while allowing for an extension of this period in justified cases.
The most common reason for extending the asylum procedure, which affects the level of state budget expenditure, is to appeal against the decision not to grant asylum.
In the Czech Republic, the highest number of final decisions was issued between 90 and 180 days (31.54%).
The second highest number was within 90 days of the date of the asylum application (17.61%).
In total, 73% of asylum procedures initiated in 2001-2003 were finally decided within one year of their start.
Within two years of the start of the asylum procedure, 92% of asylum applications were finally decided.
In the Slovak Republic, according to MÚ data, up to 90% of applicants who have not been granted asylum use the legal option of extending the deadline by lodging an appeal with a court.
In some cases it was an extension of more than a year and at the time of the inspection the court proceedings had not been completed.
Some benefit in shortening the asylum procedure is expected from the establishment of the joint offices of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Úrad hraničnej a cudzineckej polície Policajný zboru in the reception centres in Adamová-Gbeloch, Opatovskej Novej Vsi and Liptovský Vlachoch, which took place at the time of the inspection from 1 October 2004.
This is intended to simplify procedures and shorten the time limits for procedures between the two components of the asylum process.
5. Asylum facilities
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic have established asylum facilities in which they have gradually created suitable conditions for the provision of services to participants in asylum procedures.
During their stay, asylum seekers are provided with accommodation, meals, health care, pocket money and basic material and hygiene supplies.
At the same time, courses are organised as part of leisure activities and the conditions for cultural and sporting activities are created for applicants.
5.1 Asylum facilities in the Czech Republic
Suz manages and operates asylum facilities and is responsible for managing state property in the premises of the reception centre Vyšní Lhota, the reception and residence centre Červený Újezd, the residential centres Bělá-Jezová, Zastávka u Brna, Kostelec nad Orlicí, Havířov and in the premises of the integration asylum centres Jaroměř and Zastávka u Brna.
At the beginning of 2002, a reception centre was established in the transit area of Prague-Ruzyně airport.
Suz also operates asylum facilities in Stráž pod Ralskem, Seč, Bruntále, Zbýšov and Kašava, which are operated by a legal person on the basis of Section 80 (3) of Act No 325 / 1999 Coll., on Asylum.
The total accommodation capacity of the reception centres is 747 seats and the total accommodation capacity of the accommodation centres is 1,977 seats.
Reception centres are closed facilities which asylum seekers are not allowed to leave until the prescribed medical examinations and basic reception procedures referred to in Act No 325 / 1999 Coll., on Asylum have been carried out.
A breach of the obligation to stay in a reception centre is classified as an offence.
The accommodation centres to which asylum seekers come from reception centres are used to house asylum seekers until the decision on their application for asylum or non-asylum becomes final.
Subject to certain conditions, asylum seekers have the option of leaving or staying in private.
Asylum seekers have the right to free accommodation, food, other services and pocket money in reception and accommodation centres where they are declared to be staying, provided that they have taken the necessary steps to establish their financial and financial situation, and these conditions are such that they cannot be fairly required to pay even part of the said services.
Integration asylum centres are used for the temporary accommodation of people who have been granted asylum.
Clients are accommodated in the centre on the basis of an accommodation contract, which is usually concluded for 6 months, with the possibility of an extension until adequate housing can be provided for them, or they can arrange it themselves as part of the state integration programme.
At the integration centre, clients pay for all accommodation costs and eat individually.
Persons granted refugee status have the same rights and obligations as Czech citizens and have the same access to social security.
5.1.1 Cost of asylum facilities
For the comparison of asylum facilities, it was chosen as the best indicator of the cost per physical day of stay.
It is based on the actual number of persons who have actually been provided with services provided by the asylum facility each day.
In Table 3 and in the graph, the facilities operated by the SUZ are designated as own and those operated by legal persons under Section 80 of Act No. 325 / 1999 Coll., on Asylum, as contractual.
The cost of a single day's stay in the SUZ's own asylum facility is decreasing with the increasing fulfillment of these facilities. This is due to the fact that the fixed costs of operating the facilities are allocated to more asylum seekers.
The total cost of providing services for asylum seekers is increasing in direct proportion to the growing number of asylum seekers.
In 2001 and 2003, applicants were accommodated in their own asylum facilities in a crisis capacity.
In part of 2003, extra accommodation capacity in residential containers (320 beds in total) was even used to deal with the capacity crisis in asylum facilities caused by the mass arrival of asylum seekers of Chechen nationality from Poland.
This capacity was provided by renting 80 residential and 6 sanitary containers.
Expenditure per applicant per day of stay was then lower in those years.
However, it is not possible to maintain a high level of fulfillment of these devices in the long term.
The risks of an unexpected influx of refugees and the associated demand for higher accommodation capacity should be taken into account.
At the same time, it is not possible to carry out certain repairs, maintenance and investments with fully occupied accommodation capacity.
The form of the asylum facilities operated under contract allows for the adoption of operational solutions in the area of the capacities of the asylum facilities, where necessary.
5.2 Asylum facilities in the Slovak Republic
The asylum facilities are reception centres and residential centres.
The Ministry has in its administration the reception centres Adamov-Gbely, Rohovce, Opatovská Nová Ves and the residential centre Brezová pod Bradlom.
The total capacity of the reception centres is 470 seats and the accommodation centre 100 seats.
An increasing number of asylum seekers were dealt with by the Ministry by setting up a residential centre in Gabčíkov in the rented premises of the Slovenskej Technickej University Bratislava with a flexible available capacity of between 250 and 940 seats.
According to the contract concluded, the lessee also ensures the provision of services related to the operation of the centre.
In this form, the Ministry addressed the lack of its own staff.
The residential centre was also temporarily set up in 2002 and 2003 in rented premises in Jazierciach with a capacity of 160 seats.
Reception centres had an average occupancy rate of 57% to 62% in the audited period, while residential centres had an average occupancy rate of 33% to 50%.
The occupancy rate varied according to the season and was highest in the last months of the year, when many more applicants applied for asylum compared to other months of the year.
A further increase in accommodation capacity of about 450 seats will be possible after the reconstruction of the centres in Opatovskej Novej Vsi and Vlachoch.
Following the completion of the centre in Humennom in 2006, the number of seats will increase by a further 550 people.
5.2.1 Cost of asylum facilities
Data on the cost of operating asylum facilities are presented in Table 4.
Their analysis shows that the operation of an asylum facility by another body, which will provide premises and ensure the running of the facility, including related activities, is one of the options to ensure, at reasonable cost, the tasks arising from the stay of asylum seekers in the Slovak Republic.
6. Management of state funds and assets
6.1 Economic analysis
In the Czech Republic, in 2001, the approved budgeted expenditure of SUZ was increased by CZK 103,077,000 by 13 budget measures.
Of these, 89,979,000 CZK (87.29%) were earmarked funds. Most of it was intended to deal with the consequences of the Kosovo crisis (44,538,000 CZK) and to provide health care to asylum seekers (38,870,000 CZK).
In 2002, the SUZ's expenditure was increased by CZK 88,362,000 by twenty budget measures.
Of these, 62,282,000 CZK (70.48%) were earmarked funds, the bulk of which (53,200,000 CZK) was intended for health care provided to asylum seekers.
In 2003, SUZ's expenditure was increased by a total of CZK 88,078,000 by 14 budget measures.
Of this, CZK 82,000 (93.09%) was earmarked funds released from the General Treasury Administration.
The amount of CZK 51,000,000 was intended for medical care provided to asylum seekers, CZK 24,000,000 for dealing with the influx of Chechen refugees and CZK 7,000,000 for the humanitarian evacuation programme for disabled people in the Republic of Iraq.
An overview of the implementation of the SUZ's selected expenditure in the audited period is given in Table 5.
It is clear from the above overview that the highest part of the expenditure was spent on the provision of services.
Expenditure on purchasing services ranged from 37.07% to 38.23% of total expenditure.
The worsening expenditure under this heading was expenditure on accommodation and meals for applicants in asylum facilities operated under contract, expenditure on medical care provided to asylum seekers and the cost of a permanent security service providing security at individual asylum facilities.
Expenditure on salaries, payments for work done and insurance premiums (23.99% - 24.97%) accounted for a significant share of the total expenditure of the SUZ.
Last but not least, purchases of materials accounted for a significant share of SUZ's total expenditure (around 14%), with food purchases accounting for the highest share of this expenditure (7.61%? 9.83% of total expenditure).
In the Slovak Republic, the budgetary management of the Ministry for the security of migration policy and the asylum process was marked by more budgetary measures, which dealt with legitimate demands related to the increase in the number of asylum seekers.
In particular, in 2001 and 2002, the draft and breakdown of the budget in the expenditure section was characterised by an imbalance between the requirements of the Ministry, which were based on an increase in the number of asylum seekers and the need to finance their legal entitlements, and the resources provided mainly in the main category of current expenditure.
The budget chapter manager addressed the disproportion with a number of budgetary measures during the year, increasing the current expenditure limit by 41.8% in 2001 and by up to 71.7% in 2002.
An overview of the implementation of the selected expenditure of the Ministry during the audited period is given in Table 6.
Expenditure on wages, salaries and insurance premiums in the range of 24.47% to 30.51% and expenditure on materials and services in the range of 21.04% to 38.82% of total expenditure accounted for the bulk of current expenditure.
More than 10% was spent on security services and between 3.92% and 7.20% was spent on food purchases.
Another significant part was spending on accommodation and catering services, with a share ranging from 10.82% to 26.96%.
Capital expenditure accounted for a relatively low share in the range of 1.03% to 6.25%.
6.2 Deficiencies identified
The results of the audit in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic pointed to some similar shortcomings which did not have a major impact on the management of the state's funds and assets.
These were mainly shortcomings in the following areas: (A) the use of state budget funds contrary to the purpose for which they were intended by the State Budget Act, when current expenditure was used to cover actions having the character of a technical evaluation of fixed tangible assets; (b) the violation of the Accounting Act in the field of inventories and the failure to comply with the indicative chart of accounts.
In the Czech Republic, minor deficiencies were also found in the management of state property, where it was left for use by another person without a proper contract; failure to comply with the deadline for reporting changes to land registry data violated the Land Registry Act; leaving waste for disposal to a person who was not a person entitled to waste management violated the Waste Act.
In addition, in the Slovak Republic, deficiencies were found in the provision of excessively high advances for the collection of electricity and natural gas, deficiencies in the award of public contracts and in the management of the state's assets, when its records were not sufficiently secured and the method of liquidating unnecessary assets was not demonstrated.
7. Internal control system
In the Czech Republic, an internal control system within the meaning of the provisions of Act No. 320 / 2001 Coll., on Financial Control, was introduced at SUZ as of 1.7. 2002, setting out the competencies of individual employees responsible for carrying out preliminary, ongoing and follow-up checks.
At the same time, an internal audit system was put in place and an internal auditor of the SUZ was appointed.
Every year, the SUZ is issued with a plan of financial, social and operational technical checks, the aim of which is a comprehensive verification of the management of state funds and assets in individual asylum facilities managed by the SUZ.
In 2002, 42 management checks were carried out and in 2003 54 were carried out.
In the Slovak Republic, the Office of the Control of the Minister ensures the direct exercise of control activities in the departments and organisations of the Ministry of the Interior of the Slovak Republic with regard to compliance with generally binding legislation and internal regulations.
During the audited period, the performance of tasks in the field of asylum policy was not checked.
The internal control system of the Ministry of Finance is mainly focused on the implementation of preliminary and ongoing financial control under Act No 502 / 2001 Z. z., on financial control and vnútornom audit.
The exercise of financial control is also governed by the internal rules of the Director of the Ministry of Finance.
The substantive orientations of the control activities as part of the management of the various departments were set out in the framework of the annual plan of the Ministry of Finance.
The directors of the trade unions have been designated as responsible for exercising control in this area.
According to the written documentation submitted, no deficiencies were identified.
Since the entry into force of Decree No 28 of 23 April 2004 of the Ministry of the Interior of the Slovak Republic, the Ministry of the Interior has been obliged to handle and investigate complaints under the Complaints Act.
The organisational security of this task will need to be resolved in the near future.
Communiqué
This report was drawn up in Czech, English and Slovak and signed by the Vice-President of the Supreme Audit Office and the Chairman of the Najvyššššie Audit Office of the Slovak Republic.
Joint Report on Parallel Controls of Expenditure on Construction of the Prague-Dresden Motorway
Introductory word
Without trans-European transport networks, it would be difficult to imagine a modern, dynamic and, above all, united Europe.
High-quality transport networks are a prerequisite for maintaining and raising the standard of living of Europeans.
Creating the conditions for fast, safe, reliable and cheap transport of passengers and freight is an important task for the state administration.
It is a very demanding task, both in organisational and technical terms and in financial terms.
European efforts at sustainable mobility often find it difficult to compromise with Europe's interest in maintaining a healthy and human-friendly environment.
The construction of transport infrastructure, even with the necessary measures for the benefit of the environment, is expensive.
The considered procedures and decisions of the state administration in the preparation and acquisition of transport works can bring significant savings in public financial resources, which can be used differently for the benefit of citizens.
One of the tasks of audit institutions is to actively look for deficiencies that have led to lower than achievable economy, efficiency and effectiveness of expenditure on the construction of transport infrastructure.
The audit institutions should not only draw the attention of the state administration to the shortcomings identified, but recommend measures to improve the situation, for the benefit of the citizens, for the benefit of Europe.
Short summary
In 2005 and 2006, the two highest audit institutions of the Federal Republic of Germany and the Czech Republic (Germany and the Czech Republic), the Bundesrechnungshof (BRH) and the Supreme Audit Office (SAO), carried out parallel checks on expenditure on the construction of the Prague-Dresden motorway (D 8 motorway in the Czech Republic and A 17 motorway in Germany).
The motorways are connected by a border bridge, which is co-financed by both countries.
Thanks to the cooperation with the SAO, BRH was able to carry out a thorough audit of the effectiveness of the funds spent on the construction of the border bridge.
On the basis of close cooperation with BRH, the SAO obtained the necessary data on the amount of German costs for bridges and tunnels for comparative purposes.
In 2000, the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany concluded a contract for the construction of a border bridge.
According to the construction process, the completion date was finally scheduled for the end of 2006.
However, in the course of the award of the contract, the Road and Motorway Directorate of the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as "the SDD") made mistakes which led to an extension of the competition period and a reduction in the construction period.
As a result, the contract with the contractor was signed later than expected.
The contractor agreed to build the bridge in a shorter period of time and to ensure its completion in 2006.
As a result, however, the SDD had to accept a significant increase in the price of the bridge.
As part of the joint inspection work, the prices of bridges on the D 8 and A 17 motorways were compared on the basis of the per m2 area of the bridge structure.
Statistical analysis of prices has made it possible to identify bridges with high costs per square metre of area.
The analysis revealed that the border bridge was the most expensive bridge in a group of large bridges with a length of more than 100 metres.
The price increase could also be attributed to a delay in the procurement process.
When analysing the cost of building the tunnels, the auditors found that the prices of the tunnels on the D 8 motorway were significantly higher than the prices of comparable tunnels in Germany.
BRH and the SAO now have a database on the prices of bridges and tunnels, which they will be able to rely on for future checks on the effectiveness of the funds used for transport infrastructure.
For the construction of bridges, both control institutions recommend: Standardization of bridge construction and use of coupled steel concrete and special structures only in cases where pre-stressed reinforced concrete bridges are not adequate.
One of the main features of cooperation was its team spirit and informality.
In the course of the parallel inspection, the inspectors shared their specific knowledge and skills.
Introduction
This report reports on the progress and results of parallel checks on the funds spent on the construction of the motorway connecting Dresden and Prague (D 8 in the Czech Republic and A 17 in Germany).
The controls focused on the economy, efficiency and effectiveness of the expenditure incurred.
Parallel inspections were carried out by BRH in Germany and the SAO in the Czech Republic.
Parallel checks were carried out in 2005 and 2006.
The SAO audited the economy, efficiency and effectiveness of expenditure amounting to approximately CZK 20 billion, including VAT (approximately €690 million) on the border section of the D 8 motorway, which has the number 0807.
Of this amount, €64 million was planned to be used from European funds (ISPA).
In addition to a parallel audit carried out jointly with the SAO, BRH audited the preparation and construction of the A17 motorway in 2003 and 2005.
The funds spent on the construction of all three sections of the A17 motorway amounted to around €670 million, of which €277 million will be co-financed by European funds (ERDF).
The motorway from Prague to Dresden is part of the Trans-European Transport Corridor IV Dresden - the central and southern parts of Eastern Europe - Istanbul.
The D8 motorway runs from Prague through Ústí nad Labem to the state border.
The A17 motorway runs from the state border of the Czech Republic / Germany to Dresden.
At the time of the inspection, the border sections of the two motorways were under construction.
These sections became operational on 21 December 2006.
On the German side, the motorway is thus completed all the way to Dresden, while on the Czech side of the D 8 motorway it is not completed, as section 0805 of 16.4 km through the Bohemian Central Mountains between Řehlovice and Lovosice is still in the preparatory phase.
According to the plan, section 0805 between Prague and Ústí nad Labem is to pass through the protected landscape area of the Czech Central Mountains.
According to forecasts made in the Czech Republic in 2001, the traffic intensity on the border section 0807 of the D 8 motorway should be 22,940 vehicles per day in 2008.
According to German forecasts, the traffic intensity at the Czech border will total about 25,000 vehicles per day in 2010.
In 2000, Germany and the Czech Republic concluded an agreement between the Federal Republic of Germany and the Czech Republic on the interconnection of the German motorway A 17 and the Czech motorway D 8 on the common state border by the construction of a border bridge.
Both states are involved in the construction of the bridge, so the control of the construction of the bridge was an important aspect of the parallel checks carried out by the two control institutions.
Cooperation between BRH and the SAO
Since mid-2005, the two supreme audit institutions have been discussing close cooperation in the control of the construction of the motorway connecting Prague and Dresden.
There were serious reasons for both parties to cooperate:
1.
Germany is financially involved in the construction of the border bridge.
Its planning and construction is based on the SDD.
Therefore, BRH itself did not have the opportunity to carry out an inspection of the construction project.
2.
The SAO did not have the comparative database needed to assess whether the funds were used economically in terms of the overall level of costs of bridges and tunnels on D 8.
3.
The SAO needed to ascertain the effectiveness of the expenditure, taking into account the main technical parameters of the motorway, especially the arrangement of bridges and tunnels, which should allow the same quality of travel on both sides of the border.
Following preparatory negotiations, the Agreement on the coordinated control of the D 8 / A 17 motorway was signed on 4 January 2006 by the presidents of the two supreme audit institutions.
The joint working meetings between the auditors of BRH and the SAO took place over the whole of 2006 at an interval of approximately six to eight weeks.
The meetings addressed current problems and challenges, in particular the preparation of a uniform methodology for controlling the prices of bridges and tunnels, the exchange of findings from the inspection of the construction of the border bridge and the preparation of joint reports.
The continuous exchange of information was an important feature of the cooperation.
While BRH carried out most of the work on comparing the technical parameters of bridges and tunnels and the tender procedure, the SAO largely prepared a methodology for controlling the prices of bridges and tunnels.
The applicable legal standards for control in the civil service differ in the way control actions are concluded in both countries.
For these reasons, the two supreme audit institutions have drawn up their own audit conclusions on their findings during their inspections.
This report reflects the results achieved by the parallel controls.
The cooperation will end with the signing of the final communiqué in the first half of 2007.
Construction of the border bridge
In a 2000 agreement, the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany agreed on a date for the completion of the construction of the border bridge, as far as possible, in 2005.
The two sides then agreed to postpone this deadline until the end of 2006.
The SDD acted as an investor.
Germany has a 42.13% financial stake in the construction of the bridge.
In the period up to 1999, the SDD proposed that the border bridge should have a prestressed reinforced concrete structure.
In 1999, in agreement with its partners in Germany, the SDD agreed to a coupled steel and concrete structure.
This decision was justified by the reduction of the number of double pillars from seven to five and the consequent environmental benefits of such a solution for the valley.
In addition, the comparative calculations carried out by the SDD stated that the coupled steel concrete structure should be a less expensive option.
But there was an error in the calculations.
They stated that the new jointed steel concrete structure would be only 397 m long.
In fact, it's 5% longer.
In the course of awarding the contract for the border bridge, the SDD made serious errors.
It did not prepare contract documents that adequately described the assessment criteria and the sub-criteria for the comparison of tenders.
