Joint FINAL REPORT on the results of parallel checks on the administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic
Joint Final Report
May 2017
Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic
Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic
Introductory word
The present joint report reports on the progress and outcome of international cooperation in parallel inspections carried out by the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic, focusing on the administration of excise duties in 2012-2015.
Cooperation between the highest audit institutions of both countries was carried out on the basis of a cooperation agreement between the SAO of the Slovak Republic and the SAO of the Czech Republic in the performance of parallel audits focused on the administration of excise duties, which was concluded in August 2015.
The topic of parallel checks was chosen on the basis of the fact that the two EU Member States are based on common European legislation in order to find out how it is applied at national level, how the excise tax administration system is set up and how the systems in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic are different.
The greatest benefits of the control actions carried out were the exchange of experience, identification of differences and identification of good practice.
Last but not least, it was beneficial to note that the international comparability of data on the performance and efficiency of excise administration is very limited without parallel controls.
Miloslav Kala,
Karol Mitrik,
The President
The President
Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic
Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic
On the results of parallel inspections of the SPD administration in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic
Summary and evaluation
The regulation of excise duties in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic and their administration is in line with EU legislation and significantly exceeds EU requirements.
Differences have been found between the adjustment of excise duties in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic; in the Czech Republic, verification of the economic stability of applicants for permits and mandatory marking and colouring of selected mineral oils and certain other oils contribute to the effective administration of excise duties; in the Slovak Republic, the distribution of control stamps is easier than in the Czech Republic and less burdensome for tax authorities.
In the fight against evasion of excise duties, the supervision of the movement of raw tobacco or tobacco raw material, the implementation of the institute of fuel distributors and the registration of sellers of consumer packaging of alcohol have proven to be good practice in both countries.
Revenues from excise duties in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic are growing more slowly than other tax revenues.
The EU's goals of reducing taxes on labour, introducing eco-saving measures and reducing dependence on tobacco and alcohol have not yet been met in the Czech Republic and Slovakia, not least because indexation of excise duty rates is not introduced in both countries.
This has the effect of reducing the importance of excise duties on overall tax revenue and, as a result of increasing purchasing power, reducing the tax burden on consumption taxes in real terms.
The introduction of environmental measures has long been financially supported by the state, but these measures have a negative impact on revenues from excise duties, which in the future will have to be replaced by other revenues or a reduction in state expenditure.
Administrative expenses incurred in administering excise duties in both the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic have been increasing over the long term, mainly due to wage increases, and their efficiency is decreasing.
In the Slovak Republic, this efficiency is also negatively affected by expenditure on the computerisation of the administration of excise duties (IT expenditure) and expenditure on the salaries of employees performing permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses for alcohol.
The computerisation of excise administration in the Slovak Republic has not had a significant impact on the reduction in the number of tax administrations.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic recommend that the Slovak Ministry reassess the validity of the exercise of permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses for ethyl alcohol.
In the Czech Republic, the efficiency of administrative expenditure was influenced by the fact that the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic did not apply procedures during the audited period that would have led to a reduction in the personnel requirements of the excise administration.
The number of comparable administrative tasks of tax administrations was similar in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in the different years of the audited period, while the number of comparable tax entities in the Slovak Republic is about a third lower than in the Czech Republic.
Tax authorities in the Slovak Republic carry out administrative tasks mainly in the form of the physical exercise of tax supervision, while tax authorities in the Czech Republic place emphasis on remote supervision and risk analysis.
The administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic is more administratively demanding than in the Czech Republic and more expensive due to the ratio of the number of tax acts to the number of entities.
The computerisation of the administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic took place in different areas.
In the Slovak Republic, the administration of tax returns for excise duties is fully computerised; in the Czech Republic, documents proving the taxation of selected products in free tax circulation are electronically transmitted.
Both methods of electronisation support the effective management of excise duties, which is why the SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic recommend that they be applied not only in both countries.
The total expenditure for EMCS deployment could not be compared, as the SR DG provided data on expenditure only for system upgrades in the period 2011-2015, but expenditure was also incurred before this period.
The expenditure incurred in that period only for the upgrade of EMCS in the Slovak Republic was about 20% higher than the expenditure incurred in the Czech Republic both for the introduction of EMCS and for the upgrade of this system in more than ten years.
Excise tax administrations in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic did not achieve comparable values of quality indicators when spending comparable expenses.
The level of supervision is comparable in both countries, but in the Slovak Republic the management of excise duties is significantly more resource-intensive.
The introduction of the electronic system for monitoring the movement of products subject to excise duty (EMCS) has made the administration of excise duties more efficient, but to a lower extent in the Slovak Republic, as significantly higher expenditure has been spent on the introduction and modernisation of the system than in the Czech Republic.
Basic information
The cooperation between the two audit institutions took place on the basis of the Cooperation Treaty on the implementation of parallel controls aimed at the administration of excise duties of 18.8.2015.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic have agreed to carry out parallel checks, which will primarily focus on the issue of the administration of excise duties and whose results will allow analysis, comparison and evaluation of the established facts.
Common audit issues were agreed on which the parallel controls were based.
Characteristics of the subject matter and objective of the parallel control:
The aim of the parallel checks was to compare the performance of the excise administrations, taking into account qualitative and quantitative indicators, and to identify weaknesses in the excise administration process.
In particular, the following main audit questions were to be answered:
Did the excise tax authorities in the Czech Republic and Slovakia achieve comparable values of quality indicators when spending comparable expenses?
Has the introduction of the Excise Movement and Control System (EMCS) made the administration of excise duties more efficient and has the cost of implementing it been spent effectively?
The parallel checks carried out were intended to identify the causes of significant differences affecting the efficiency and effectiveness of the tax administration in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, especially in the area of regulation and in the setting up of the organisational structure.
ThissegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The Directorate-General for Customs (GŘC) and the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic (SR) have joined the joint declaration on mutual cooperation between the Visegrad Four countries, the objectives of this declaration include, among other things, the fight against fraud, exploring the possibility of harmonising legislation and seeking harmonised interpretations on the rules of selected problems, exploring the possibility of joint activities to increase efficiency in the detection of fraud and sharing experiences and best practices.
1 EMCS is operated under Decision No 1152 / 2003 / EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 on the introduction of an electronic system for the movement and monitoring of products subject to excise duty.
Identification of the audit carried out by the Czech SAO
Control number: 15 / 33
Subject of inspection: Administration of excise duties
Objective of the audit: The aim of the audit of the SAO of the Czech Republic was to examine the procedure of the customs authorities in the administration of excise duties, in particular when monitoring transport in the system of conditional exemption from excise duties and when securing the tax (customs debts); to check whether the system of administration of excise duties is set up in such a way as to ensure the efficiency of the collection of revenue from the state budget.
Audited period: 2012-2015 and, in the case of factual context, the period before and after
Person audited: Directorate General of Customs
Identification of the audit carried out by the SAO SR
Control number: KA-023 / 2016 / 1050
Subject of inspection: Administration of excise duties
Objective of the inspection: The aim of the inspection was an independent and objective examination of whether the SR CCP and the Customs Offices (Customs Offices) operate economically, efficiently and effectively in the administration of excise duties in accordance with generally binding legislation.
Audited period: 2012-2015
Audited person: Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic
Legislation on excise duties in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Legislation on the administration of excise duties is divided into the level of EU legislation (see Annex 1) and the level of national legislation (see Annex 2).
Council Directive 2008 / 118 / EC concerning the general arrangements for excise duties and repealing Directive 92 / 12 / EEC defines excise duty and lays down the basic rules for the administration of taxes and the handling of energy products and electricity, tobacco products, alcohol and alcoholic beverages.
This directive allows taxes on consumption to be imposed on other products.
In particular, EU legislation regulates the minimum conditions for: The level of tax rates for the different types of products selected, the production, storage, processing and holding of taxable products, chargeability, exemptions and refunds, supervision of the transport of selected products between EU Member States, international cooperation and the keeping of registers on economic operators and tax warehouses.
EU legislation allows control procedures and institutes to be set up at national level, provided they do not distort competition.
Legislation on excise duties in the Czech Republic
Definition of legislation in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, the legislation on excise duties is concentrated in the Excise Tax Act (Act No. 353 / 2003 Coll.), which regulates the administration of the tax on mineral oils, the tax on alcohol, the tax on tobacco products, the tax on beer, the tax on wine and intermediate products and the tax on raw tobacco.
This law defines the forms of treatment of products subject to excise duties, the taxpayer, the authorisation procedure, the conditions for the transport of products, the declaration of tax and penalties for infringements.
The law and subsequent decrees also regulate certain other conditions for the handling of mineral oils (labelling of mineral oils), restrictions on the sale of spirits and tobacco products, monitoring the handling of special mineral oils and the storage of raw tobacco for purposes other than the production of tobacco products.
Taxes on other energy products (i.e. natural gas and certain other gases, solid fuels and electricity) are regulated in sections 45 to 47 of Act No. 261 / 2007 Coll., on the stabilization of public budgets.
In the Czech Republic, a number of provisions related to the administration of excise duties are also contained in special legislation. The Fuel Act No. 311 / 2006 Coll. and the implementing regulation regulate the conditions for the sale, supply, distribution of fuel and the keeping of records of fuel put into free circulation.
Act No 61 / 1997 Coll., on ethyl alcohol, and its implementing regulations define the conditions for production, storage, registration and control of the production and circulation of ethyl alcohol.
Act No 307 / 2013 Coll., on mandatory labelling of ethyl alcohol, and the relevant implementing regulations provide for mandatory labelling of ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging, conditions for the handling of control tapes and conditions for the handling of ethyl alcohol (i.e. for the production, processing, sale or other transfer, transport, transport, storage, taking over, use, possession, import or export of alcohol).
The procedures for tax proceedings, which are not specified in special regulations, are regulated by Act No 280 / 2009 Coll., the Tax Code.
Penalties are imposed in accordance with the procedures laid down in Act No 500 / 2004 Coll., the Administrative Code.
The conditions for the issue of a trade licence (concession) for the operation of the trade "production and processing of fuels and lubricants and distribution of fuels" and "production, preparation and sale of fermentation alcohol, drinking alcohol and spirits" are regulated by Act No 455 / 1991 Coll., on Trade Licensing (Trade Licensing Act).
The Czech Republic has used the power to introduce control procedures and institutes to control the transport of selected products in free tax circulation and to monitor compliance with the legislation in the handling of selected products for which excise duty has not been paid, as well as in the handling of selected products for which tax has already been paid.
These include monitoring the handling of specific mineral oils and raw tobacco, the labelling of certain other mineral oils, the labelling of tobacco products and alcohol in consumer packaging.
The Czech Republic has used the right to apply excise duty to other products and has introduced excise duty on raw tobacco as one of the measures against tax fraud.
Structure of changes in legislation for different types of excise duties in relation to the subject of control in the Czech Republic
On the basis of the resolution of the Government of the Czech Republic of 3 October 2012 No 735, the implementation of the "zero tolerance plan for the black market in spirits," major legislative changes were made in the Czech Republic in 2012-2015, introducing a number of measures against tax fraud on excise duty on alcohol.
During the same period, there were also major changes in the legislation on the tax on mineral oils, the tax on tobacco products and the criminalisation of the preparation of tax cuts.
Protection of tax revenue through criminal law
With effect from 1 July 2016, the criminalisation of the preparation of the crime "tax reduction, fee reduction and similar compulsory payment" is introduced. The modification made should allow police authorities to take more effective and timely measures to reduce tax fraud, e.g. the use of operational means of search.
General provisions of the excise duty administration
With effect from 1 January 2015, the issue of a permit for the handling of products subject to excise duty under the Excise Duty Act is subject to: Reliability; indebtedness; economic stability; the right to operate a business allowing the exercise of an activity related to the permit; a situation in which the applicant is not in liquidation or bankruptcy.
In particular, the aim of the legislation was to address the issue of the creation of tax arrears by reducing entities authorised to handle products subject to excise duty.
The condition of economic stability now allows the tax authorities to take into account the financial situation of tax entities both in the authorisation procedure and after the authorisation.
The purpose of this measure is to prevent those who do not have sufficient financial income to properly comply with their tax obligations from handling selected products.
To assess the economic stability of the proposer, indicators (profitability, liquidity, financial stability, activity, labour productivity) have been established on the basis of which a financial analysis is carried out.
In addition to these indicators, it also depends on the administrative discretion of the tax authorities with regard to the individual conditions of the procedure.
The law provides for a frequency of verification of compliance with the condition of economic stability due to the topicality of the data - the verification takes place once a year following the deadline for submitting income tax returns.
The tax authority also has the option of laying down other conditions necessary for the administration of the tax.
If the permit holder does not comply with the conditions, the tax authority is entitled to revoke the permit or to revoke it with a delay.
Out of a total of 2,609 entities for which the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic examined the condition of economic stability, 18.6% were found to be economically unstable with a high risk of incurring arrears if the tax liability exceeds the amount of security of the tax (e.g. repeat beneficiary).
The permit was revoked for ten entities, the other applicants increased the security of the tax, capitalized their contribution to the company or provided up-to-date accounting data, according to which they already fulfilled all the conditions for the permit.
In addition to the applicant, the conditions of reliability and indebtedness must also be met by a natural person who is a statutory body or a member of it, or by a natural person who, although not a statutory body of the applicant or a member of it, carries out this activity (chain of legal persons in the capacity of a statutory body or its member, so-called linked entities).
By the end of 2016, more than 30,000 connected entities had been examined.
The records kept under the Excise Tax Act (Sections 37 to 40 and 60 of Act No 353 / 2003 Coll.) contain information on:
The type, name, code and quantity of goods produced, taken over, issued or dispatched, broken down by type of tax treatment (conditional exemption scheme, import, re-entry into conditional exemption scheme, export, free circulation, own consumption, loss);
The SEED ID of the recipient or supplier of the selected products, the declarant, the date of the event and the registration;
Transport of selected products (e.g. means of transport, carrier, transport number);
The registration numbers of the related documents;
Notification of the release for free circulation of ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging marked with a control tape and details of its distribution.
A record of receipt after transport must be made immediately after it has been completed.
In the case of records kept electronically, the records must be kept or allow output in xls, xlsx, ods format.
Alcohol
After 2012, the Czech Republic introduced a complex of measures aimed at ensuring a detailed overview of the activities of the operators (see Annex 3, Schedule A), from the production of raw alcohol to the marking with a control tape to its distribution to the final seller or authorised user of the exempt alcohol.
In the Czech Republic, the production facility for the production of alcohol, which is not in operation, is also subject to supervision by customs authorities.
The aim of the new legislation was to increase the overview of the processing of alcohol and the production of spirits and to identify persons handling alcohol in consumer packaging, to reduce the handling of alcohol to financially stable and reliable persons and to ensure constant supervision of the production and labelling of spirits.
The most important measures are: Records of the production, receipt, stocks and dispensing of alcohol contain information on the quantity of alcohol according to the stages of production and processing of alcohol, including document numbers.
Limit the volume of consumer packaging, packaging material and limit the number of packages with broken control tape at the point of final sale or issue to the consumer.
Consumer packaging means a container or other container with a capacity of up to one litre and three litres, respectively, if it is a container made of glass.
Spirits in larger packages shall be regarded as unmarked and shall not be disposed of.
At the point of final sale to a natural person for his or her personal consumption, there may be a maximum of one consumer package with a broken control tape, or three if it is fitted with a one-way valve.
Compulsory registration of a person who puts alcohol in consumer packaging products with at least 15% alcohol by volume into free circulation for tax purposes and is: An importer of alcohol, a producer of alcohol in the Czech Republic or an operator of a tax warehouse under a conditional exemption regime, provided that personal and technical conditions are met.
Personal conditions - reliability, integrity and failure to declare a disqualification - must be met by the applicant and a person in the position of a statutory body or a responsible representative.
The applicant must provide bail of 100,000 CZK to 5,000,000 CZK (i.e. approximately 3,700 €to 185,000 €), depending on the number of control tapes taken.
The technical conditions for registration are a suitable place for the marking of alcohol and the equipment of a marking point or tax warehouse with a camera tracking device with continuous operation and remote access by the tax authorities.
The registration markings of the control tape are introduced for the labelling of spirits with a capacity of more than 0.06 litres.
In the case of the transport of control tapes, the registration of the control tapes shall be indicated in the transport documents or the export declaration.
Until 30 November 2013, the control tape contained a 10-digit registration code, which included a four-digit registration sampling number, an application code for the allocation of control tapes and a classification code according to the level of ethanol concentration by volume.
As of 1 December 2013, the control tape now contains two types of identifiers and the quantity of alcohol in the immediate packaging expressed in millilitres of ethanol at 20 ° C, rounded down to whole millilitres.
The register of control tapes for the marking of spirit drinks contains daily records of the various ways in which the control tapes are handled according to the registration codes, as well as the documents on the basis of which the registration took place.
When specific control tapes are destroyed, lost or stolen, the holder is obliged to electronically notify the tax authorities of the registration code of the control tapes in question and their number on the following working day after the decisive event.
Introducing a new offence and adjusting the level of penalties imposed for infringements in the handling of control tapes.
Penalties may be imposed up to or up to ten times the amount of excise duty (e.g. destruction or loss of control tapes in excess of 0.1% of the total quantity of individual control tape orders made, failure to return the control tape within the statutory time limit).
Restricting the handling of control tapes only to registered holders, who may not pass them on to another person, with the exception of providing them to a foreign supplier for the purpose of labelling spirits in consumer packaging produced outside the Czech Republic.
The exported control tapes must be placed on the consumer packaging and re-imported no later than nine months after receipt from the tax authorities.
Compulsory registration of the distributor of alcohol in consumer packaging, provided that similar personal conditions are met as for the person required to mark alcohol and with the obligation to post bail of up to CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. approx. €185,000).
Definition of persons for the sale or purchase of ethyl alcohol in immediate packaging.
Authorised persons are obliged to sell alcohol in consumer packaging to other registered persons or to final sellers, or to sell it as a final seller.
They may acquire ethyl alcohol from other registered persons, the insolvency practitioner, the administrative authority, organisational units of the state or unregistered persons in the execution of tax execution.
Notification of the release for free circulation of ethyl alcohol or sale in consumer packaging is required to be sent by holders and distributors of ethyl alcohol to the tax authority immediately the following day after the decisive event, through an information system maintained by the tax authority (ORO web client) or in accordance with the content in xml format.
The notification shall include the number of control tapes used, the volume and type of consumer packaging, the percentage by volume of ethyl alcohol, the European Goods Code (EAN), the identification of the distributor or the final seller, as well as the name of the product and the batch of production.
Tax entities sent about 10.5 million notifications in 2014 and 2015.
A compulsory concession (a specific form of business licence) not only for the production and preparation of ethyl alcohol, but also for the sale of ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging by an entrepreneur to a natural person for his personal use or to another legal or professional natural person for his own internal use.
Licensed trades can only be carried out after a decision has been taken by the Trade Licensing Office, subject to professional competence and other conditions.
No required professional competence is required for the sale of ethyl alcohol.
The tax authorities benefit from an overview of sellers and their establishments and restrictions
Trading on reliable entities.
In the Czech Republic, about 94,000 licences were registered in 2014 and about 104,000 in 2015 for a field including the production, treatment of fermentation alcohol, drinking alcohol, spirits and other alcoholic beverages and sales.
Checks on compliance with legislation on the handling of products subject to excise duties in the Czech Republic are also carried out in their activities outside the tax administration: Trade offices, the State Agricultural and Food Inspection Authority, the authorities of the Financial Administration of the Czech Republic, the authorities of the Czech Trade Inspectorate.
If it finds that there has been a breach of the obligation or a breach of the prohibition, it shall immediately inform the excise authorities.
Mineral oils
The Czech Republic has put in place a comprehensive system of supervision (see Annex 3, Schedule B) to which mineral oils subject to excise duty, but also selected mineral oils not subject to excise duty, which have been misused for tax evasion.
The system includes supervision from the production of mineral oil to the storage, transport, marking and colouring of selected mineral oils, the marking of certain other mineral oils to delivery to the final consumer or user and, in some cases, the consumption of mineral oils.
Customs supervision also includes the production and handling of markers for the marking and handling of mineral oils.
Mineral oils listed under Combined Nomenclature codes 2710 19 25 (other kerosene), 2710 19 29 (other medium oils not elsewhere specified) and heavy gas oils 2710 19 41, 2710 19 45 and 2710 19 49 shall be subject to the labelling and colouring of selected mineral oils, unless their labelling is prohibited.
For example, benzole, toluene, xylol and lubricating oils and other oils intended for purposes other than motor propulsion are subject to the labelling of certain other mineral oils.
It is only possible to mark and colour selected mineral oils and certain other mineral oils with a marker on the basis of the permission of the tax authorities.

ThissegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The most significant new measures since 2012:
Monitoring of the handling of special mineral oils, which are a group of mineral oils falling within Combined Nomenclature codes 2710 19 71 to 2710 19 99 (i.e. lubricating oils and other oils intended for purposes other than engine propulsion), the kinematic viscosity of which at 40 ° C is less than 12 mm2. s-1 inclusive and have at least one of the following characteristics: The flash point is less than 150 ° C, the distillation test distils at least 20 per cent by volume, including losses up to 350 ° C.
These mineral oils have been misused as an admixture to finished fuels, in particular diesel, or have been directly used or sold to power engines, as the physical characteristics are very similar.
Operators handling monitored mineral oils in bulk or in packs of more than 220 litres must register with the tax authorities.
The personal conditions of the applicant, the statutory body and the responsible representative must be fulfilled for the issue of the registration, which applies throughout the period 2 With the exception of beer, fruit wines, other wines and mead and fruit spirits obtained by burning.
No 2658 / 87 of 23 July 1987 on the tariff and statistical nomenclature and on the Common Customs Tariff.
4 For example, when mineral oil is used as a fuel (except when sailing on water, unless it is a private pleasure craft) or as a component for the production of fuel, if the marking is defective in its use.
Registration.
As of 30 November 2016, the register of persons handling special mineral oils contained 54 valid registrations, four registrations were cancelled at the request of the marketing authorisation holder.
The electronic register shall contain detailed information on the receipt, actual consumption and sale or transfer of mineral oil, including document numbers, purchase notification numbers to the tax authority, places of storage and consumption, the purpose of consumption, the place of storage and consumption or, at the time of sale, the place of supply and the customer registration number.
Notification of any acquisition of a specific mineral oil must be made to the tax authorities between 24 and 72 hours before receipt.
The identification of the trading partners, the name and nomenclature of the specific mineral oil, the quantity, the purpose of consumption or information on the sale or transfer shall be notified.
Notification of the expected quantity of mineral oil acquired, sold or consumed in the relevant year shall be submitted by the body together with the application for registration or by the end of January of the relevant calendar year.
Notifications of the purpose of use and labelling, the place of storage or consumption, the identification details of the person to whom the specific mineral oil is resold or transferred shall be transmitted before each change.
Notifications shall be made electronically via smart forms or via a PDFA data container.
In 2015, 630 notifications were made by people handling special mineral oils.
The seizure and confiscation of special mineral oils or means of transport must be declared by the tax authority in cases where it finds that special mineral oils are being handled without registration or where the registered person fails to comply with his obligation to notify.
As in the case of non-compliance with obligations in the transport of products subject to excise duties, these deficiencies cannot be remedied retrospectively.
The registration of a fuel distributor is compulsory for persons who sell or are authorised to sell fuel.
Only persons who meet the following criteria may be registered fuel distributors:
Compulsory licence of the Trade Licensing Office (a specific form of trade licence).
The opinion on the concession application and, where appropriate, on the appointment of a responsible representative shall be given by the customs office, which shall examine whether the applicant for the concession, the statutory body or the members of the statutory body of the applicant - a legal person and the appointed responsible representative fulfil the condition of reliability.
If these persons meet the condition of reliability, the customs office will issue a favourable opinion.
A reliable person is a person of impeccable character, from the point of view of criminal property, customs and tax law.
The award of the concession is subject to professional competence.
The indebtedness of the same class of persons as in the case of reliability.
A debt-free person is a person who provides sufficient guarantees that he will meet his payment obligations to the state in a proper and timely manner, i.e. he does not have arrears to the state budget and on general health insurance.
A fuel distributor may not be prohibited by a court or administrative authority from carrying out his activities.
The fuel distributor must not be wound up or bankrupt.
Deposit of a deposit (or bank guarantee) of CZK 20,000,000 (i.e. approx. €740,000), which can be reduced to CZK 10,000,000 (i.e. approx. €370,000) after three years of registration of the fuel distributor and fulfilment of other conditions.
The distributor is obliged to notify the customs office of the distribution of fuel within 20 days of the end of the calendar month.
The electronic notification shall include details of the individual purchase and sale of fuel.
The reported data are data on business partners, document numbers, selected product, quantity, price, carrier and transport, place of loading and unloading.
The right to reimbursement of the tax on mineral oils consumed in primary agricultural production was reintroduced at the end of 2014.
A refund of excise duty on mineral oils can only be claimed in respect of an activity which is clearly linked to an activity carried out on land.
In 2015, there were about 64,000 claims for tax refunds totalling 1,172,844,680 CZK (i.e. 43,401,720 €).
Since 2017, the government of the Czech Republic has also introduced refunds of excise duty on fuel to livestock farmers.
This entitlement will now be available to farmers or breeders who, for example, are involved in the rearing of cattle, pigs, poultry, sheep and goats.
Tobacco products
Restrictions on the sale of tobacco products at the old tax rate
In response to the long-term under-achievement of budgeted revenues from excise duty on tobacco products, the Czech Republic introduced restrictions on the sale of tobacco products with the old tax rate in the event of a change in the tax rate with effect from 1 December 2014.
Excise duty on tobacco products is paid by the use of tobacco stickers.
The use of a tobacco label means placing it on a unit packet (Section 116 of the Excise Duty Act).
The decisive factor for the application of the rate of excise duty is the manufacture of the tobacco product in the state intended for the final consumer, which does not have to be removed from storage, delivered, dispatched or sold, or sold to the final consumer.
The letter of the alphabet characterising the rate of excise duty appears on the tobacco label together with the price for the final consumer of cigarettes, and the label indicates the number of items in the package or the quantity of smoking tobacco in kilograms.
The tobacco label has no identifier.
The length of the transitional period for the sale of unit packets of ready-to-eat cigarettes labelled with the previous (old) rate of duty has been fixed until the end of the last day of the second calendar month following the entry into force of the new rate of excise duty.
The development of tobacco sticker collection in 2014 and the comparison with previous years show that tobacco manufacturers have significantly frontloaded tobacco products with the "old" tax rate each year, effectively shifting the effectiveness of the "new" tax rate by about one year.
Tax on raw tobacco
Due to the misuse of raw tobacco for the production of tobacco products without the authorisation of the tax authority and the non-payment of excise duty, a tax on raw tobacco and monitoring of the handling of raw tobacco have been introduced as a measure against tax fraud.
With effect from 1.7.2015, raw tobacco which has not been used or supplied for the manufacture of tobacco products, which has been delivered to another Member State or a third country, or for which the origin, purpose of use or person to whom the raw tobacco has been or is to be supplied has not been proved, shall be subject to excise duty.
Restrictions on the handling of raw tobacco
Measures such as supervision of the transport and manufacture of tobacco products, marking of unit packs with control tape and restrictions on sales at designated locations have been complemented by restrictions on the handling of raw tobacco.
Production facilities for the processing of tobacco raw material and the manufacture of tobacco products shall not be subject to customs supervision.
Only a registered person may store raw tobacco for a purpose other than the manufacture of tobacco products, but such tobacco may not be further processed or processed.
A registered person can only be a person who meets the personal conditions of the applicant, the statutory body and the responsible representative, which applies throughout the registration period.
The conditions for registration are: (A) the right to operate a business allowing the activity of a person storing raw tobacco to be carried out, (b) reliability, (c) indebtedness, (d) the fact that the person storing raw tobacco has not been banned from carrying out his activity, (e) the fact that the person storing raw tobacco is not in liquidation or bankruptcy, (f) the granting of a bond of CZK 20,000,000 (i.e. approximately €740,000).
The electronic register shall contain the date of receipt or delivery of the raw tobacco, the document number, the identification of the business partner, an indication of the quantity and type of raw tobacco.
Notification of any acquisition of raw tobacco by a registered person storing raw tobacco must be made to the tax authorities between 24 and 72 hours before it is received or dispatched.
The details of the business partner, the quantity of raw tobacco, the address of storage, the purpose of use and the carrier shall be notified.
The notification of the expected quantity of raw tobacco received or dispatched in the relevant year shall be submitted by the body together with the application for registration or by the end of January of the relevant calendar year.
Notifications shall be made electronically via a data container in PDFA format.
The transport of raw tobacco must be accompanied by a document with the required particulars.
Legislation on excise duties in the Slovak Republic
The legal framework regulating the area of excise duties in the Slovak Republic is based on EU legislation and thus co-creates its single tax system.
The various types of excise duties are exhaustively determined by the legislation of the Slovak Republic, which is similar to the legislation of the surrounding countries.
Definition of legislation in Slovakia
The legislation on excise duties is ensured by four laws according to the individual subject of the tax.
The harmonisation was achieved by the adoption of the following laws on excise duties: Act No 98 / 2004 Z. z., on excise duty on mineral oils, Act No 106 / 2004 Z. z., on excise duty on tobacco products, Act No 530 / 2011 Z. z., on excise duty on alcoholic beverages, Act No 609 / 2007 Z. z., on excise duty on electricity, coal and natural gas.
All laws on excise duties are regulations of substantive law and deal with the taxation of the subject of excise duties in the tax territory.
Act No 563 / 2009 Z. z., on Tax Administration (Tax Code), is a regulation of procedural law, regulating the administration of taxes, the rights and obligations of tax entities and other persons.
This legal framework has transposed the various provisions of Council Directive 2008 / 118 / EC of 16 December 2008 concerning the general arrangements for excise duties and repealing Directive 92 / 12 / EEC, as well as those of other European Community directives and legislation.
Structure of changes in legislation for different types of excise duties in relation to the subject of control in the Slovak Republic
Since 2011, the legislation on the administration of excise duties has undergone several major changes according to the structure of individual excise duties.
In EMCS, the monitoring of the transport of selected products subject to excise duties under the conditional exemption scheme has been changed from a paper accompanying administrative document to an exclusively electronic system, where these services are monitored in real time.
The EMCS e-system introduced in 2015 the concept of suspension of access to EMCS for tax entities.
ThissegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The customs office has the option of suspending access precisely because of a well-founded fear that the tax from previous tax years will not be due or determined and that it will not be enforceable.
This applies to the payment of the tax, as the transport of excise goods requires the deposit of a security, which is released by the end of the transport.
Excise duty on mineral oils
A major change in the administration of excise duty on mineral oils occurred in 2011, when the possibility of using so-called red diesel was abolished.
The designated gas oil, also commonly known as red diesel, was a mineral oil.
In the past, red diesel was used for specific statutory purposes, for example in agriculture, and its use was favoured by a lower rate of excise duty.
This change had a positive impact on the revenue part of the state budget.
The aim of the abolition of red diesel was to reduce the public deficit, to simplify the system of taxation of mineral oils and to reduce the administrative burden on the businesses concerned.
In 2012, a new type of tax entity was created, namely a fuel vendor.
The purpose of this legal amendment was to introduce an obligation to keep records for all service stations.
The clarification of the movement of taxed petrol and diesel is linked to the obligation to purchase petrol and diesel from a fuel distributor.
In 2014, new institutes of tax entities were introduced, namely the fuel distributor and the fuel consumer.
This amendment helped to eliminate tax evasion on petrol and diesel and clarified the movement of these fuels (see Annex 4, Schedule A).
As part of the fight against tax evasion, the legal provisions on the registration of tax entities trading in lubricating and base oils have been extended.
In SR, however, these mineral oils are not subject to the obligation to be labelled with an indicator substance.
Excise duty on tobacco products
As part of the fight against tax evasion and monitoring of tobacco raw material, the scope of the Tobacco Raw Materials Act has been extended and a new tax entity - the trader of tobacco raw material - has been introduced.
The tobacco raw material is not a harmonised tobacco product and its movement is not monitored within the EU.
In addition, an obligation to register technological installations for the production of tobacco products has been introduced.
The legislation introduced a new system for ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using control marks for the labelling of consumer packages of tobacco products.
Cigarettes, cigars, cigarillos and tobacco are marked with a check mark.
Under the new system, the purchaser of the control stamps must apply to the customs office for the issue of the control stamps electronically, through the information system for the collection of the control stamps.
In doing so, electronic communication between the taxpayer and the tax authority was introduced.
One state printer of control stamps has been set up - in the Kremnice Mint.
The exercise of fiscal supervision over the printing of control stamps has also been introduced.
The changes contributed significantly to the elimination of tax evasion.
The new stamp printing system strengthens the system for checking goods, as a unique identification number is generated on the stamp, which can be used to easily verify whether goods come from legal sources.
A unique 12-digit identification number (1st to 2nd place is the checksum; 3rd place determines whether the code belongs to a check mark or a group of packages; 4th place is the series identifier; 5th to 8th place is the alphanumeric part of the sequence; 9th to 12th place is the decimal part of the sequence) can also be applied in the form of a two-dimensional bar code.
In addition, the price of cigarettes, the indication of the validity of the excise duty rate, the number of cigarettes in the consumer pack and the length of the cigarettes must appear on the control mark intended for the labelling of cigarettes.
Excise duty on alcoholic beverages
The biggest legislative change affected alcohol, wine and beer, as the original three substantive laws were repealed and one common law on excise duty on alcoholic beverages was created.
The law was drafted mainly because of the need for a comprehensive solution to the issue of taxing alcoholic beverages, addressing their production, monitoring movement, ensuring the tax, as well as the need to improve the business environment in the area, to streamline the administration of the tax, to reduce the administrative burden for small and medium-sized enterprises.
A new way of addressing the issue of the taxation of different types of alcoholic beverages has introduced the application of a uniform rate of excise duty on alcoholic beverages and has taken into account the percentage by volume of actual alcohol content.
For non-sparkling wine, sparkling wine and fermented beverages, the percentage by volume of the actual alcoholic strength of the final product shall be taken into account.
The concentration of beer is also expressed as a percentage by volume of the actual alcohol content of the finished product.
A category of small producer of fermented beverages has been introduced, the essence of which is an exemption from excise duty for a natural person who produces a sparkling fermented beverage for his own consumption and for the consumption of his household up to a maximum of 1 000 litres per marketing year.
The legislation introduced a new system for ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using control marks for the labelling of consumer packaging of alcohol.
Under the new system, the purchaser of the control stamps must apply to the customs office for the issue of the control stamps electronically, through the information system for the collection of the control stamps.
In doing so, electronic communication between the taxpayer and the tax authority was introduced.
One state printer of control stamps has been set up - in the Kremnice Mint.
The exercise of fiscal supervision over the printing of control stamps has also been introduced.
The changes have contributed significantly to the elimination of tax evasion (see Annex 4, Schedule B) and the elimination of the falsification of control marks.
The new stamp printing system strengthens the system for checking goods, as a unique identification number is generated on the stamp, which can be used to easily verify whether goods come from legal sources.
A unique 12-digit identification number (1st to 2nd place is the checksum; 3rd place determines whether the code belongs to a check mark or a group of packages; 4th place is the series identifier; 5th to 8th place is the alphanumeric part of the sequence; 9th to 12th place is the decimal part of the sequence) can also be applied in the form of a two-dimensional bar code.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Excise duties on alcohol, mineral oils, tobacco products, beer, wine and intermediate products are regulated in the Czech Republic by one common law No. 353 / 2003 Coll.
The tax on solid fuels, the tax on natural gas and certain other gases and the tax on electricity are part of Act No 261 / 2007 Coll.
In the Slovak Republic, on the other hand, each excise duty is regulated by a special law, apart from the law on excise duty on alcoholic beverages, which contains a tax on alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products.
A special law regulates excise duties on electricity, coal and natural gas.
In the Czech Republic, from 1 January 2015, the issue of a permit for the handling of products subject to excise duty under the Excise Tax Act is subject, among other things, to proof of the economic stability of the applicants, which the customs authorities verify annually by carrying out a financial analysis.
In the Slovak Republic, a similar form of analysis is carried out only when deciding to waive or reduce the security of the tax.
FR SR carries out tax supervision in the form of the presence of an employee of the Finance Directorate over the handling of control stamps for the marking of alcohol and tobacco products, their disposal in the printing works and their sale to individual customers.
The law stipulates that the production of control stamps is carried out by the state-owned company Mincovna Kremnica.
The production of tobacco stickers and control tapes in the Czech Republic is not supervised by the customs authorities.
The tobacco stickers and control tapes will be taken over from the printer by the designated territorial office of the customs office in Kutná Hora.
The tobacco stickers are taken over by their customers at the local authority, and the alcohol control tapes are then distributed to the various local tax authorities according to the location of the markings.
The legislation of the Czech Republic does not define manufacturers of tobacco stickers and control tapes.
In the Slovak Republic there is an obligation to register technological equipment for the production of tobacco products or part of it, in the Czech Republic there is no such obligation.
In the Czech Republic, the tobacco sticker bears excise duty on tobacco products, which is paid when the tobacco stickers are collected from the authorised customs office.
In the Slovak Republic, on the other hand, the control mark does not contain excise duty on tobacco products.
In the Czech Republic, a refund of excise duty on mineral oils was introduced during the audited period in the case of their use for agricultural plant primary production, the so-called green diesel.
Since 2017, this tax refund has been extended to livestock production.
There is no such support for farmers in the Slovak Republic (it existed until 31 December 2010 as so-called red diesel).
In order to strengthen the fight against tax fraud, a deposit of CZK 20 million (i.e. €740,000) was introduced for fuel distributors in the Czech Republic.
As a result of the introduction of this measure, the number of fuel distributors decreased from 1 891 in 2013 to 174 in 2014 (i.e. a decrease of 1 717 tax entities).
A similar institute of fuel distributors is in place in the Slovak Republic, but without the deposit required to secure excise duty on mineral oils.
In the Slovak Republic, 303 distributors were registered in 2014 and 407 distributors were registered in 2015.
In the Slovak Republic, the institute of fuel sellers and fuel consumers is established, which is licensed by the local customs office.
There is no such institute in the Czech Republic.
In the Czech Republic, selected mineral oils and also some other mineral oils are subject to labelling; in the Slovak Republic, after the abolition of the so-called red diesel, the labelling of mineral oils is not applied.
In the Czech Republic, the control tape for the marking of alcohol contains an eight-digit individual code used to verify the origin of the alcohol and a 12-digit registration code indicating the spirituality of the spirit drink, according to which a record of the control tapes is kept.
The destruction, loss and return of the control tape shall be entered in the register on the following working day.
The holder of the tape is obliged to notify their use within the same period.
In SR, a control mark intended to mark ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging contains a unique 12-digit identification number, which, if used once a month, is communicated to the tax authorities and is used to verify the authenticity of the control mark.
The register shall contain the number of stamps collected, used and returned.
Both the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic have introduced the institute of compulsory registration or registration of alcohol distributors.
In the Slovak Republic, registration is conditional on the fulfilment of conditions relating, inter alia, to a storage area exceeding 200 m2; an annual turnover from the sale of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol of at least €100,000 or a paid-up capital of at least €100,000; a minimum number of 10 employees.
In the Czech Republic, obtaining registration is conditional, among other things, on the deposit of a bond of CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. €185,000) in favour of the tax authority for the entire period of validity of the registration.
ThissegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
In the Slovak Republic, the production of alcohol not only in consumer packaging requires the permanent presence of the tax authorities.
In the Czech Republic, the production of ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging requires a special form of registration of the person required to mark the ethyl alcohol, with the condition that a deposit be made in favour of the tax authority, ranging from 100,000 CZK (i.e. 3,700 €) up to 5,000,000 CZK (i.e. 185,000 €), depending on the number of control tapes taken and the installation of a tracking device with continuous access by the tax authority.
Evaluation
The legislation of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic goes far beyond the EU's minimum requirements for the subject matter and administration of excise duties and responds to identified risks from other Member States as well as those identified in tax territories.
The legislative changes adopted during the audited period allow tax administrations to prevent possible tax evasion to a greater extent.
In the Czech Republic and Slovakia, as part of the fight against tax evasion in the form of misuse of tobacco raw material (e.g. leaves), an excise duty on raw tobacco or tobacco raw material has been introduced in addition to EU legislation.
Although raw tobacco and tobacco raw material are not harmonised tobacco products, both the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic monitor their movements.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic can recommend that this measure be applied in other EU Member States.
In the Czech Republic, good practice has shown that the examination of economic stability of applicants for permits under the Excise Tax Act has proved successful because it reduces the risk of tax arrears.
For this reason, both audit institutions recommend that such checks also be applied in the conditions of the Slovak Republic.
The distribution of control stamps is more efficient in the Slovak Republic than in the Czech Republic because it does not burden the customs authorities with the costs related to transport between the printer and the purchaser of control tapes and tobacco stickers.
The financial administration of the Slovak Republic has a better overview of the existence and location of technological facilities for the production of tobacco products.
In the Czech Republic, however, it is more efficient to collect the tax on tobacco products, because the order of the tobacco sticker itself is a tax return followed by the payment of the tax.
Thanks to the introduction of the institutes "fuel sellers" and "fuel consumers," the tax administration in the Slovak Republic has a better overview of the points of sale of fuel.
The introduction of compulsory labelling of mineral oils in the Czech Republic makes it easier to control the misuse of mineral oils at a reduced rate of tax or exempt from tax.
In the Czech Republic (2013) and in the Slovak Republic (2014), a new control tape or a stamp containing an identification code was introduced.
The control tape in the Czech Republic also contains a registration code, while in the Slovak Republic the new legislation has abandoned its introduction.
It is not yet possible to assess the impacts due to the short effectiveness of the legislative changes.
The introduction of effective labelling of consumer packaging of alcohol with a check mark or tape is an effective measure in the fight against tax evasion.
The SAO of the Slovak Republic and the SAO of the Czech Republic can also recommend the introduction of this control measure in other Member States.
The SR's position on the conditions for the distribution of alcohol is characterised by a pro-client approach that does not block the funds of tax entities.
The Czech Republic's approach, on the other hand, is rather restrictive, as it introduces a bond that burdens the cash flow of tax entities, but it further reduces the risk of tax arrears.
Evolution of revenue from excise duties
Excise duty is an indirect tax introduced by the state to increase revenue for the state budget as well as to regulate the quantity of goods sold, the consumption of which is considered harmful to individuals and / or society (the regulatory function of the tax).
According to the Communication from the Commission: Europe 2020 - A strategy for smart, sustainable and inclusive growth of 3.3.2010 under the flagship initiative "Resource efficient Europe," the European Commission intends to improve the framework for the use of market-based instruments, including by revising energy taxation to reduce energy and resource consumption.
In order to fulfil the EC's intention, Member States should seek to shift the tax burden from labour to energy and environmental taxation, among other things, as part of a greater "greening" of tax systems.
The collection of tax revenue from excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia includes the collection of excise duties on mineral oils, tobacco products, alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products, as well as natural gas, solid fuels and electricity.
The Organisation for Economic Cooperation and Development (OECD), among others, monitors the share of excise duties in total tax revenues and the share of GDP.
The two supreme audit institutions used the following selection criteria to enter a query on the OECD website.
Collection of excise duties in relation to macroeconomic indicators in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, the share of excise duties in total tax revenues and the share of GDP decreased slightly, according to OECD data.
The ECB's European Central Bank rate was used to convert the amounts in CZK into €at 31 December of the relevant year.
The nominal exchange rate of CZK against €in 2013 decreased by 9.1% year-on-year compared to 2012 (from 25,140 to 27,425).
This was mainly due to the monetary policy decision of the CNB Bank Board of 7 November 20136.
The resulting values of collection of excise duties, rates of excise duties and per capita income in €decreased significantly due to the exchange rate difference.
The significant reduction in the share of excise duties in 2014 was due to a one-off shortfall in revenue from excise duty on tobacco products due to the impact of new legislation restricting the sale of tobacco products at the old tax rate.
The share of excise duties is also affected by the increase in the collection of income taxes, which has increased significantly as a result of the improved overall economic situation of the Czech Republic.
Excise duty on mineral oils accounts for the largest share of the total collection of excise duties (around 55.7% in 2015), but this has fallen compared to 2012, despite significant economic growth.
The collection of excise duties on mineral oils in 2013 and 2014 was significantly lower than in 2012 and 2015, although the registration of fuel distributors was introduced in 2013 as a measure against tax fraud.
The trend towards environmentally friendly vehicles and the promotion of biofuels have a negative impact on tax revenue.
Gas, solid fuel and electricity taxes account for a negligible share, which is due to the low tax rate, which is close to the minimum rates set by the EU, compared to neighbouring countries.
If rates are not increased, their share will decrease in the future due to the ever-decreasing energy performance of buildings and production processes.
The collection of excise duty on ethyl alcohol in 2013 and 2014 has been negatively affected by the repercussions of a large tax fraud case involving the putting into circulation of untaxed ethyl alcohol, ethyl alcohol containing methanol or insufficiently denatured ethyl alcohol in the form of spirits.
In 2015, following the adoption of a series of measures against such behaviour and the recovery of the spirits market, the collection of excise duty on alcohol exceeded the collection of 2012 by €4 million.
The share of the tax on tobacco products has increased as a result of rising rates.
The standard rates of excise duties changed between 2012 and 2015 for the tax on tobacco products, where the rate was increased mainly due to compliance with Council Directive 2011 / 64 / EU on the structure and rates of excise duty on tobacco products.
As a result of the CNB's monetary intervention, the real rate of excise duties in €, apart from the tax on tobacco products, has fallen significantly. For tobacco products, it has risen only slightly.
There is no indexation of the excise rate in relation to price growth, GDP or standard of living, so the function of excise duties to regulate socially problematic activities may not be fulfilled.
With the economic growth of the Czech Republic and the rise in living standards, real rates of excise duties are decreasing.
7 Indexation - the automatic adjustment of an economic quantity for inflation, this adjustment takes place on the basis of a law or a contract (for pensions paid by the state it is called indexation).
Collection of excise duties linked to macroeconomic indicators in the Slovak Republic
The current legislation on excise duties in the Slovak Republic does not address the indexation of the level of excise duty rates to the development of consumer prices, as they are fixed.
ThissegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
ThissegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
ThissegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
ThissegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Of all the excise duties introduced in Slovakia, excise duty on mineral oils accounts for the largest share of the state budget's annual tax revenue, while its share did not fall below 52% during the whole audited period.
Excise duty on tobacco products accounts for the second largest share.
On average, this tax accounts for around 32% of the total collection of excise duties.
Between 2012 and 2015, there was an increase in the collection of excise duty per capita in Slovakia.
This development is due to an increase in excise duty rates on tobacco products, higher purchasing capacity and higher consumption of the population in a given year.
The growth in the collection of excise duties per capita in the Slovak Republic is constant and corresponds to the development of excise duties on tobacco products, higher purchasing capacity and higher consumption of the population in a given year.
In the Czech Republic, the decrease in income in €per capita is influenced by the CNB's intervention on the exchange rate of the koruna against the euro.
The difference between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in the total collection from the SPD is mainly due to the collection of excise duty on mineral oils and tobacco products, which in the Czech Republic is about 2.7 and 2.8 times higher respectively, but per capita of the Czech Republic the collection of these selected products is only about 1 / 3 higher.
This is due to the lower price of these selected products in the Czech Republic due to lower rates of excise duties in the Czech Republic and the exchange rate of CZK to €for foreign consumers.
In the case of the tax on mineral oils, this is also due to greater transit through the Czech Republic and cross-border purchases.
In the case of the tax on tobacco products, increasing foreign tourism to the Czech Republic and cross-border purchases have a significant impact.
Evaluation Real rates of excise duties in the Czech Republic fell as a result of the CNB's interventions.
The share of energy taxes in the Czech Republic and Slovakia in total tax revenues is not increasing and there is no shift from labour taxation to taxation of the consumption of selected products subject to excise duties, which is not in line with EU strategies.
However, the share of excise duties achieved is consistently above the OECD average.
The overall collection of excise duties is mainly influenced by the change in excise duty rates, the development of the economic condition and the behaviour of the population.
Future shortfalls in the collection of excise duties due to environmental measures, which are subsidised by the state in various forms, will have to be compensated by other revenues or by a reduction in state expenditure.
The absence of indexation of excise duty rates in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic reduces their regulatory function and does not sufficiently support the EU's objectives of a Europe less dependent on environmentally unfriendly resources and reducing dependence on alcohol and tobacco.
The higher collection of excise duty per capita in the Czech Republic is reflected in the higher consumption of selected products by foreign consumers, which is influenced by the lower total price of selected products in €.
Administrative expenditure of excise duties
The efficiency of administrative costs reflects the correlation between expenditure and revenue related to the administration of excise duties, i.e. it expresses the amount of expenditure per 100 units of revenue (CZK, €).
The higher the resulting value, the worse the efficiency of the administrative costs.
The effectiveness of the tax administration in administering the tax affects the scope and organisational organisation of the tax administration, the management of the organisation, the legal environment and the level of computerisation of individual activities.
The calculation of the efficiency of the administrative costs of the administration of the tax using the conversion factor method is based on the number of employees involved in the administration of excise duties in a line-managed structure.
In the Czech Republic, the administration of excise duties is carried out, among other activities, by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, which is a separate organisational unit of the state and an accounting unit.
In the Slovak Republic, the tax administration is carried out by the Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic, while the customs authorities are an internal organisational unit, costs and revenues are included cumulatively for the whole organisational unit.
Therefore, with regard to the possibility of comparing the efficiency of the administration of excise duties, the expenses and revenues of the Financial Administration of the Czech Republic were included in the calculation of the efficiency of administrative costs.
Administrative costs of administration of excise duties in the Czech Republic
The administration of excise duties is a complex of administrative tasks carried out mainly by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
Some partial control tasks are carried out by other public authorities, but their importance is negligible.
Excise duties are mainly administered by the following departments:
Directorate-General for Customs
Department 23 Daňový
Section 231 - Tax Methodology monitors and proposes legislative measures, ensures the interpretation of legislation, methodically manages and coordinates: The implementation of tax administration agendas and related regulations, in particular tax management and related control and supervision activities, the administration of transport of selected products;
Division 232 - ELO and Search carries out searches and methodically manages transport controls for selected products and ensures international cooperation between ELO and EMCS;
Unit 233 - Tax Control methodically manages and coordinates the implementation of the tax control agenda at customs offices;
Section 30 LEGAL
Section 301 - Legal carries out methodological activities in the areas of administrative punishment, administrative procedure, tax inspection process, registration procedure, finding procedure, payment of taxes, fines for late claims of tax, penalties and interest;
Section 302 - Administrative activities carries out decision-making activities in cases where the legislation provides for the competence of the GŘC, e.g. deciding on the delegation of the local jurisdiction of the entity to another competent tax authority, deciding on the attraction, i.e. taking over the matter by the superior tax authority, appealing against decisions of the customs authorities and examining suggestions for inaction in tax and administrative proceedings;
Unit 303 - Revenue and Enforcement methodically manages, coordinates and performs tasks in the framework of international cooperation in the recovery of tax arrears and the performance of tasks in the field of insolvency proceedings;
Section 60 ANALYSIS AND INFORMATION SUPPORT
Department 601 - Risk and Criminal Analysis provides and performs risk analyses and is involved in managing executive risks and planning control activities and control actions;
Section 604 - Financial Analyses carries out financial analysis in the customs administration, in particular in the context of the authorisation procedure.
