Unit 02 - Analyses and information support, which carries out risk analysis, risk profile management and the collection and evaluation of information from all available information sources;
Section 1 LEGAL
Section 11 - Legal and administrative activities, which processes documents, opinions and submission reports for the Appellate Body, issues permit decisions in connection with the administration of excise and environmental taxes, the law on mandatory labelling of alcohol and the law on alcohol, decides on ensuring payment for tax not yet due or not yet determined;
Section 3 - TAňový
Department 31 - Tax, which carries out the following tasks: Tax supervision of tax entities, e.g. monitoring compliance with the conditions laid down in the permits issued, supervision of the functionality and accuracy of the production equipment for the production of alcohol and the determination of the quantity and concentration of alcohol produced, expert supervision of the denaturing of alcohol, physical checks in the field of excise administration; non-tax controls in the field of checks based on laws indirectly related to excise duties, in particular the control of the mandatory marking and colouring of selected mineral oils, control of the taxation of selected products, control of the marking of tobacco products, control of whether the seller or buyer is in breach of the law on prices and other price regulations, carry out acts in connection with the law on fuel, carry out acts in connection with the law on mandatory marking of alcohol and the law on alcohol, carry out acts in connection with the fulfilment of the obligation of a minimum quantity of biofuels for free circulation for transport purposes; registration of economic operators for taxes, registration of persons obliged to mark alcohol and distributors of alcohol and registration of fuel distributors; tax administration, in particular the conduct of tax proceedings in relation to the assessment and prescription of the tax, where appropriate, the enforcement of the tax;
Section 39 - Tobacco stickers and control tapes - is the organisational unit of the Customs Office for the Central Bohemian Region and carries out activities in the field of ordering, producing and distributing and disposing of tobacco stickers and control tapes.
At the disposal of returned / damaged tobacco stickers, representatives of the customs office and representatives of the GŘC are present, who supervise the liquidation process and draw up a record of the destruction.
In the case of alcohol control tapes, the director of the customs office, by an internal act of procedure, appoints a three-member committee for the disposal of discarded uncollected / returned shredded control tapes.
After the physical shredding of the control tapes has been carried out, the chairman of the liquidation committee shall ensure that the details of the destroyed control tapes are recorded;
Section 5 - CONTROL,
Section 52 - Tax Checks carries out tax checks;
Section 6 - SUPERVISION
Department 61 - Supervision of entities supervises entities at points of sale, such as control of sales of spirits and tobacco products;
Unit 62 - Mobile Supervision carries out checks on the transport of selected products on the road.
Administrative costs of administering excise duties in the Slovak Republic
Since 1 January 2012, the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic has undergone a difficult transformation process in accordance with the approved UNITAS programme.
The creation of the SR CCP was also reflected in the composition of the staff of the newly created departments of the merged customs and tax administration.
In the context of the exercise of the administration of excise duties, activities related to the administration of excise duties within the organisational structure of the CCP have been integrated into a number of different sections and related departments.
Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic Section of Customs and Tax Directorate of the Slovak Republic Department of Excise Duties (pan-Slovak jurisdiction):
Excise department - directs and coordinates activities in the field of excise administration; draws up expert opinions; submits proposals and comments on legislative amendments; issues decisions on the delegation of territorial jurisdiction to tax entities; allocates and repeals registration numbers;
Separation of the exercise of tax supervision - directs and coordinates activities in the field of the exercise of tax supervision and control; carries out tax supervision;
The ELO and SPD systems department - directs and coordinates administrative cooperation activities in the field of excise duties, including the exchange of information through SEED and ISA systems; provides management and updates in SysNed and EMCS application equipment;
Control Stamps Department - regulates printing and stamp handling activities; it supervises the tax handling and disposal of printing sheets and control stamps in the printing works.
Department of the Vice President of Financial Administration
Department of Appeals for Excise Duties and Duties (pan-Slovak jurisdiction):
Excise Appeals Unit - reviews decisions of customs offices on the basis of ordinary and extraordinary appeals; appeals procedure at the second stage of the decision-making process.
The section of customs offices was created in the course of 2012; it directly integrated the various customs offices (9 customs offices), which have territorial jurisdiction designated by the higher territorial units, with the exception of one customs office, which was set up, inter alia, to carry out tasks related to the external border of the Community.
Customs offices:
Excise Department - carrying out methodical activities in relation to branches of customs offices and stations of customs offices; in the case of selected entities, the tax administration performs direct tasks, namely deciding on registration (tax warehouse, authorised recipient repeated, registered consignor), the amount of security of the tax, determining and repaying the tax, exercising tax supervision and tax control; deciding to waive the composition of the security of the tax; deciding to waive the obligation to ensure the presence of a customs employee in the tax warehouse for alcohol;
Legal separation - decision-making activities in respect of tax offences; activities related to ordinary and extraordinary legal remedies; tax enforcement proceedings;
Branch of the customs office - decides on registration (with the exception of the tax warehouse, the authorised recipient for repeated receipt, the registered consignor), the amount of security of the tax; prescribes and refunds the tax; exercises tax supervision and tax control; decides on security and forfeiture of goods;
Customs office station - the exercise of fiscal supervision over the possession and movement of goods subject to excise duties; ensures the exercise of permanent fiscal supervision in a tax warehouse for alcohol; decides on the security and forfeiture of goods.
The expenditure of the financial administration of the Slovak Republic on the administration of excise duties is constantly increasing as, with the exception of wage increases, investment in effective tax administration and computerisation of financial administration is increasing.
Although revenue from excise duties increased, expenditure increased faster as a result of IT adjustments related to the UNITAS project.
Wage expenditure in the Slovak Republic is significantly influenced by the performance of permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses for alcohol, which is not applied by the Czech Republic.
The expenditure of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic on the administration of excise duties increased significantly between 2012 and 2015 in 2015, mainly due to the increase in wage expenditure and expenditure on technical support.
In the Czech Republic, revenues from excise duties grew at about the same rate.
Compared to the Slovak Republic, wage expenditure in the Czech Republic is positively influenced by the broader competences of the customs administration, such as weighing trucks, checking compliance with obligations related to tolls.
The efficiency of administrative costs in Slovakia shows a slightly worsening trend year on year.
The number of employees did not change significantly, but expenditure per employee increased.
In the Czech Republic, too, the number of employees did not change significantly, but expenditure per employee grew more slowly than in the Slovak Republic.
Evaluation
In the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, wage growth is an important factor in the deterioration in the efficiency of administrative expenditure, which can be assessed as a natural development.
In both countries, maintaining a significant administrative burden in the administration of excise duties appears to be a negative factor, as confirmed by the undecreasing number of employees in the field of excise administration.
In the Slovak Republic, however, the administration of excise duties with lower revenues is significantly more demanding in terms of staff capacity.
Performance indicators of excise tax administration
The management of excise duties is a set of activities aimed at correctly identifying, determining and securing the payment of the tax.
The main processes in the administration of excise duties are the assessment of taxes, the authorisation and registration of activities, the supervision of transport, the control and search of taxpayers.
The number of administrative tasks and entities managed is an indicator of the performance of the tax administration.
The correlation between the indicator monitored and the number of tax administrations reflects the efficiency of the tax administration's activities and defines the cost of a particular activity.
Authorisation and registration for the activity are essential prerequisites for the handling and transport of selected products for commercial purposes under a conditional exemption scheme.
The tax authority is obliged to carry out a continuous administration of entities authorised or registered, with a focus on supervising compliance with the legislation and conditions laid down by the tax authority, to which adequate staff resources must be allocated.
The indicator monitored was the number of valid permits or registrations to operate at 31 December of each year.
The number of permits or registrations issued is not the same as the number of tax entities.
Administrative acts are specific administrative acts in a matter.
The administrative tasks monitored are the most important tasks of the tax administration (claims of the tax, administration of transport in EMCS), or activities that are a sequence of acts ending in a report or decision.
Performance indicators in the Czech Republic
Authorisation and registration to operate in the Czech Republic
Tax warehouse:
Selected products may be produced, processed, stored, received or dispatched on the basis of a tax authority's authorisation to operate a tax warehouse.
If the operator of a tax warehouse has more than one warehouse, a permit is issued for each one separately, including the security of the tax.
The security of the tax is not required in the case of distilleries under the permanent tax supervision of the tax authority (i.e. the physical presence of a public official and the securing of the facilities by the tax authority's conclusions).
Permanent tax supervision does not apply in the Czech Republic.
The operator of the tax warehouse is also registered for tax under Section 125 of Act No 280 / 2009 Coll.
Authorisation to operate a tax warehouse is a condition for the transport of selected products conditionally exempt from tax from the place of import to a tax warehouse, to an authorised consignee in another Member State, to a place of export in another Member State or to a consignee in another Member State (replacing the status of registered consignor under Article 4 (10) of Council Directive 2008 / 118 / EC).
Tax warehouse statistics do not include permits for the acquisition of electricity, natural gas and solid fuels without tax, which are analogous to tax warehouse permits.
The producer brandy produces alcohol at a reduced rate of 50% tax (14,300 CZK / hl ethanol) - fruit spirits for growers. It is not a tax warehouse and the operating permit is issued by the Ministry of Agriculture.
The reduced tax rate can be applied to 30 litres of pure alcohol per household of the grower for personal consumption during the production period (July-June).
The register of crop burning, which is kept by the operators of the brandy and made available to the tax authorities, must contain information on the grower, the basic raw material, the distillate issued, the origin of the fruit and the production of the distillate.
The authorised recipient for the repeated receipt of selected products and the authorised recipient for the one-off receipt of selected products shall be entitled, subject to the authorisation of the tax authority and the conditions laid down, to receive or repeatedly receive selected products in a conditional system transported from another Member State.
The beneficiary is not the operator of the tax warehouse and is not allowed to store or dispatch the selected products under the conditional exemption scheme.
The user of the selected exempt products is a legal or natural person who receives and uses, or under Section 52a or Section 53 of Act No 353 / 2003 Coll. sells to another user the selected exempt products; users have the status of tax entities without the obligation to register for tax purposes.
The acceptance and use of selected products exempt from tax can only take place on the basis of a final authorisation, and only from the supplier specified in the authorisation.
On the basis of the authorisation, the exempt mineral oils may be sold to another holder of the authorisation for use or to a user who is entitled to use the mineral oils without authorisation.
It is possible to sell tax-free mineral oils without authorisation in statutory cases, such as:
Waste oils in quantities of less than 10 000 litres per calendar year, if produced by the user himself or in the course of his activities,
Exempted mineral oils collected in unit packs of a maximum capacity of 20 litres, intended for purposes other than engine propulsion or heat production and intended for sale to the final consumer.
It is possible to transport selected products exempt from tax with proof of exemption.
After compulsory registration with the tax authorities, the distributor of ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging is entitled to sell or otherwise transfer the ethyl alcohol put into free circulation.
The storer of raw tobacco is entitled to store raw tobacco for a purpose other than the manufacture of tobacco products, on the basis of registration with the tax authorities and the conditions laid down.
A person handling special mineral oils is entitled, on the basis of registration with the tax authorities and the conditions laid down, to acquire, sell or otherwise transfer special mineral oils which are in bulk or placed in packages of more than 220 litres.
The fuel distributor is entitled to sell fuel on the territory of the Czech Republic, with the exception of the sale of fuel from a service station, on the basis of the concession issued and the registration of the tax authority under the specified conditions.
PHM transport must be accompanied by a tax document, proof of sale or proof of transport, or a delivery plan and bottling tickets.
These documents may be replaced by electronic documents sent to the tax authorities prior to the start of the transport.
The service station operator is the owner of the fuel sold at the service station.
Petrol stations are places where the sale or delivery of PHM to a fuel tank is usually permitted on the basis of a permit from the building authority.
The Ministry of Industry and Trade records petrol stations and their operators in a breakdown into: Registered - normal sale or delivery of PHM usually to the fuel tanks of vehicles; with a defined approach - operation usually in different company premises (e.g. quarries, sawmills, agricultural farms, transport organisations, construction yards), sale there for the other side is limited on the basis of specific contractual relations; non-public - delivery points of fuel only for the operators' own consumption.
A service station is not a building or installation in the form of an operating tank located in operation (e.g. on a chassis) if the fuel is dispensed only for its own use.
Operating tanks are not subject to the permission of the tax authorities and are not registered.
Natural and legal persons may purchase, receive and sell liquefied petroleum gases put into free circulation for resale, subject to authorisation by the tax authorities.
They must also be authorised when they purchase or obtain liquefied petroleum gases for their own consumption exceeding 20 tonnes per calendar year.
Administrative tasks in the Czech Republic
Tax control is a set of actions. The subject of tax control is tax obligations, claims by the tax entity or other circumstances relevant to the correct determination and determination of the tax relating to a single tax procedure.
A tax audit may be carried out jointly for several tax procedures of a single tax entity.
A repeat tax inspection can only be carried out under the conditions and justification laid down by law at the start of the inspection.
The tax audit is carried out within the deadline for determining the tax, which is three years, with the deadline being extended by one year under the conditions laid down by law (e.g. submission of additional tax proceedings, initiation of criminal proceedings in relation to the tax in question) or suspended (court proceedings, international cooperation).
The period for determining the tax shall end no later than 10 years after the expiry of the period for making a proper tax claim.
There is no obligation on the tax authorities to carry out a tax audit on each tax entity.
The start of the tax audit suspends the deadlines for the possibility of submitting an additional tax return or an additional statement by the tax entity (Section 141 of Act No 280 / 2009 Coll.) and restarts the period for determining the tax (Section 148 of Act No 280 / 2009 Coll.).
On the basis of its result, the tax can be assessed ex officio.
A local investigation is an individual time-limited act (one day) in which the tax authority searches for evidence and inspects premises, goods, documents, records, means of transport and transport packaging from tax entities and other persons involved in the tax administration, in a place outside the premises of the tax authority (e.g. at the tax entity, at the point of sale, on the way to transport).
The tax authority is entitled to borrow documents and items, take samples and, if necessary, secure them.
Based on the outcome of the local investigation, the tax cannot be assessed separately, but the taxpayer can be asked to submit an additional tax return (Section 145 (2) of Act No 280 / 2009 Coll.).
The EMCS traffic data check is not a local survey.
The order for alcohol marking control tapes can only be submitted to the tax authority at the local marking point by a registered person obliged to mark alcohol and is carried out by means of intelligent forms, which are automatically imported into the application of the alcohol marking register.
The tax authority will process the order, evaluate the adequacy of the quantity of control tapes ordered and order the production.
It does not supervise the production of control tapes.
The production is carried out by the State Printing House of Cenin, a state-owned company.
The purchaser of the control tapes takes over the control tapes from the tax authority of the local marking point.
Ordering tobacco stickers to mark cigarettes, cigarillos, cigars and smoking tobacco serves as a tax return.
The value of the tobacco label corresponds to the amount of the tax liability, with the purchaser of the tobacco stickers obliged to pay their value within 60 days from the date of their removal from the tax authority.
The customer is obliged to calculate the value corresponding to the amount of tax liability of the ordered tobacco stickers in the order.
This period shall apply only if the value of the tobacco stickers is ensured.
The order for tobacco stickers is submitted on a form specified by the Ministry of Finance in writing or through a data container with the possibility of using intelligent forms.
The production of tobacco stickers is carried out by the State Printing House of Cenin, a state-owned company.
The authorised tax authority, which is the Customs Office for the Central Bohemian Region (Kutná Hora Regional Office), ensures the purchase and transport of tobacco stickers to the tax authority, which distributes them and further examines their transport, storage and use with customers.
Tax claims include regular tax returns, additional and corrective tax returns, including orders for tobacco stickers, filed by tax entities.
The following are not included: Mineral oils used for the production of heat, other petrol used in the course of business other than for the production of heat or the propulsion of engines, mineral oils used for primary agricultural production.
The fines imposed include administrative proceedings to deal with identified infringements, which are a set of successive administrative acts. The international exchange of information on tax entities (ELO) within the meaning of Council Regulation (EU) No 389 / 2012 takes the form of: Requests for administrative cooperation, replies to requests for administrative cooperation, spontaneous information, occurrence reports, inspection reports.
Transport taking place under a conditional exemption regime between the Czech Republic and EU Member States - the Czech customs office is the tax authority of the receiving or sending tax warehouse or the authorised consignee.
Performance indicators in the Slovak Republic
Authorisation and registration to operate in Slovakia
The administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic is mainly carried out by the customs authorities and the excise department of the Customs and Tax Department of the Slovak Republic, whose procedure for the administration of excise duties is governed by individual laws on excise duties and the tax code.
These laws lay down not only the scope of the authorisation for the CÚ and the CCP in the administration of excise duties, but also the rights and obligations of tax entities in connection with the registration or payment of excise duty.
The largest year-on-year increase in tax entities (by 234%) was recorded in 2012 and 2013, which was due to an increase in permits issued within tax warehouses, an increase in the registration of the authorised recipient for re-admission and the registration of a large number of user enterprises.
The legislation clarified the transport of certain bulk mineral oils, as well as the obligation to notify when they are transported in bulk or in packaging containing more than 150 litres and 230 litres respectively, and also extended the list of mineral oils subject to control and transport procedures to include other goods, such as anti-knock products, oxidation inhibitors, bituminous inhibitors, viscosity enhancers, anti-corrosion products.
For lubricating oils, a mandatory indication of their kinematic viscosity has been introduced.
An approximation of the registration process for selected tax entities within the meaning of national legislation in the Slovak Republic can be found in the following parts of the document.
Tax warehouse operator
Under the national legislation of the Slovak Republic, when registering the operator of a tax warehouse within all excise items, a person who wants to operate a tax warehouse must also apply for registration and authorisation to operate a tax warehouse at the same time.
The final decision in the registration process is the certificate of registration for the relevant excise duty, by which the operator of the tax warehouse acquires legal personality for all tax warehouses.
At the same time, the CÚ will issue a permit for the operation of a tax warehouse, which entitles the operator of a tax warehouse in that tax warehouse to produce, process, store, receive or dispatch selected products under a conditional exemption scheme.
Where the operator of a tax warehouse has tax warehouses in several locations, the tax authority will issue a separate permit for each tax warehouse to operate a tax warehouse.
The movement of excise goods under suspension of duty shall be monitored electronically through the EMCS.
A unique reference code is generated for each shipment, known as
Arc code under which the traffic can be tracked online and thus in real time.
If the operator of the tax warehouse is also a person authorised to distribute ethyl alcohol, he is obliged to electronically notify the CÚ of the trade name of the consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol, the volume and volume concentration of ethyl alcohol in the consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol and the EAN bar code for each new type of consumer packaging which he puts into free circulation for tax purposes, at the latest on the date of its introduction.
Registered consignor
A registered consignor is a special type of tax entity which cannot be simultaneously registered as a tax warehouse operator even if it consigns an excise item under a duty suspension arrangement after it has been released for free circulation.
Under the national legislation of the Slovak Republic, when registering a registered consignor under all excise items, a person who wishes to send an excise item under the conditional exemption procedure after it has been placed under the "free circulation" customs procedure must also apply to the CÚ at the same time for registration and authorisation to send an excise item under that procedure.
The CÚ issues a certificate of registration for the relevant excise duty and at the same time also issues an authorisation to dispatch an excise object under a suspensive procedure after it has been placed under the customs procedure "free circulation."
Growing spirit
The basic task for the operation of the growing brandy is to obtain a permit for the production of alcohol in the distillery plant from the Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Development of the Slovak Republic.
However, the authorisation from the Ministry itself does not entitle the holder of the licence to operate the growing brandy.
In order to be able to operate a growing brandy, a person must submit an application to the CÚ for registration and the issue of a registration certificate for the operator of the growing brandy.
The CÚ issues a certificate of registration for the relevant excise duty, which at the same time entitles the operator of the growing brandy to produce alcohol in the growing brandy.
The purpose of growing brandy is to provide a service to growers.
Growing spirit cannot be a tax warehouse.
The legislator allows a reduced tax rate of 50% of the standard rate of tax, i.e. €540 / hl a, to be applied to ethyl alcohol produced in brandy.
The reduced tax rate shall apply to ethyl alcohol produced in a growing brandy in a quantity not exceeding 43 l a. per grower and per household per production period in the tax territory.
The production period runs from 1 July of the current year to 30 June of the following year.
The production period is not the same as the calendar year and it is therefore possible to apply a reduced tax rate to the alcohol produced more than once in one calendar year because the alcohol is produced in two production periods.
It concerns the production of ethyl alcohol outside the conditional exemption scheme, which in practice means that the alcohol produced is in free circulation for tax purposes.
The grower pays not only excise duty and value added tax on the alcohol produced, but also the price of the services provided.
The grower's brandy issues the grower with a removal certificate, which serves not only as proof of the origin and method of obtaining the alcohol, but also as proof of payment of excise duty.
The transport of alcohol produced in this way is not subject to monitoring by the tax authorities.
Importer of immediate packaging
National legislation allows persons who intend to import consumer packaging of alcohol or cigarettes from the territory of a third country in the course of their business and to put it into free circulation for tax purposes in the tax territory to apply to the CÚ for inclusion in the register of importers of consumer packaging.
The importer of consumer packaging does not register for the relevant excise duty, but the CA issues him with a certificate of inclusion in the register of importers of consumer packaging.
That certificate entitles the importer to import consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol or consumer packaging of cigarettes from the territory of a third country.
At the same time, before issuing the control stamps, he must lodge a tax guarantee equal to the amount of tax due on the quantity of alcohol or cigarettes he wishes to put into free circulation for tax purposes.
The importer of consumer packaging is required to put into free circulation for tax purposes only consumer packaging bearing a control mark.
For this reason, they must submit to the customs office of export the number and identification number of the control marks exported to the territory of the third country.
On importation, the importer is required to have the number of control marks imported back from the territory of a third country confirmed by the customs office of import.
When importing consumer packaging, the importer proceeds within the meaning of customs legislation, where the amount of excise duty is also included in the customs debt.
In the event of the release for free circulation of consumer packaging, the tax guarantee lodged shall be returned to the importer or may be used to pay the customs debt.
The importer of consumer packaging is not a tax warehouse.
If the importer of the consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol is also the person authorised to distribute the ethyl alcohol, he is obliged to electronically notify the CÚ of the commercial name of the consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol, the volume and volume concentration of ethyl alcohol in the consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol and the EAN bar code for each new type of consumer packaging which he puts into free circulation for tax purposes, no later than the date of its introduction.
Seller of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol in free circulation
In order to monitor the movement of alcohol in free tax circulation and eliminate tax evasion, the legislator introduced a new tax institute for the seller of consumer packaging of alcohol.
A person who wants to hold a permit for sale must apply to the CÚ for a permit and meet the legal conditions (business license for commercial activities; good repute in relation to intentional economic crimes; no permit for sale has been withdrawn for ten years; he is not in liquidation or bankruptcy).
As it is a consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol in free circulation for tax purposes, no accompanying document is required for the transport of these goods.
For example, an invoice, which also contains the number of the holder of the distribution authorisation, is sufficient to prove the way in which the consumer packaging of alcohol is purchased.
For each establishment, the authorisation holder shall keep a record per calendar month of the number of consumer packages of ethyl alcohol received, the number of consumer packages of ethyl alcohol issued, the stock of ethyl alcohol in the consumer packages of ethyl alcohol as at the last day of the month and a record of the shortfall or surplus in the number of consumer packages of ethyl alcohol received and issued.
The holder of the authorisation is obliged to purchase or otherwise purchase ethyl alcohol in the course of business only from the person authorised to distribute it.
Distributor of immediate packaging of alcohol
In order to monitor the movement of alcohol in free tax circulation and to eliminate tax evasion, the legislator introduced a new tax institute for the distributor of consumer packaging of alcohol.
A person who wishes to hold a distribution licence must apply to the CA for a distribution licence.
The applicant must meet the legal conditions (business licence for a commercial trade; storage area exceeds 200 m2; annual turnover from the sale of consumer packaging of alcohol of at least €100,000 or paid-up equity of at least €100,000; minimum number of 10 employees; no arrears to the customs office; no arrears in compulsory contributions; good repute in relation to intentional economic crimes; no permit to sell has been withdrawn for 10 years; no liquidation or bankruptcy).
As it is a consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol in free circulation for tax purposes, no accompanying document is required for the transport of these goods.
For example, an invoice, which also contains the number of the holder of the distribution authorisation, is sufficient to prove the way in which the consumer packaging of alcohol is purchased.
For each establishment, the holder of a distribution authorisation shall keep a record per calendar month of the number of units of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol received, the number of units of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol issued, the stock of ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol as at the last day of the month and a record of the shortfall or surplus in the number of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol received and issued.
The holder of the distribution authorisation is obliged to purchase the alcohol in the immediate packaging only from another person authorised for distribution.
The data for each calendar month shall be communicated electronically by the person authorised to distribute by the 25th day of the following calendar month.
Fuel dealer
A new type of tax entity, namely the fuel seller, has been introduced to monitor fuel in free circulation and to eliminate tax evasion.
There is no specific regulation governing service stations in the Slovak Republic.
That is why petrol stations are incorporated in the national legislation of the Slovak Republic as fuel sellers.
A person who wishes to sell petrol, diesel or LPG for final consumption in free circulation for tax purposes in the course of a business activity in the tax territory is required to apply to the CÚ for a permit to sell before the sale begins and to provide proof that the storage facility is verified and equipped with suitable verified measuring equipment allowing the quantity of mineral oil to be measured at the time of receipt and delivery, and the tank must comply with technical standards.
If the seller of fuel is a tax warehouse operator, an authorised consignee or a registered consignor, the CÚ will also automatically issue a permit for the sale of fuel to registered persons.
The seller of fuel is obliged, among other legal obligations, to keep records of petrol, diesel or LPG purchased and sold per calendar month and is also obliged to notify the CA of the new supplier (distributor) of fuel.
The seller of fuel is legally obliged to purchase or otherwise purchase fuel only from the distributor of fuel or from a registered person.
As the fuel is in free circulation for tax purposes, no accompanying document is required for the transport of the goods.
However, when the fuel is delivered via a car tanker, the distributor prints a so-called bottler from a measuring device built into the car tank when the fuel is pumped out.
That document shall include, in addition to the quantity data, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the car assigned by the transport inspectorate.
For example, an invoice, which also contains the number of the fuel distributor assigned by the tax authority, is sufficient to prove how the fuel was purchased.
The tax authority in the territory of the Slovak Republic records tax evasion related to the transport of this type of goods in the exercise of tax supervision of mineral oils.
In particular, it is an effort to avoid roadside checks during transport, which is why hauliers use secondary roads, circumventing the toll collection system due to the difficulty of monitoring actual traffic.
The transport of mineral oils in converted double-bottomed tanks is also carried out.
It happens many times that illegal traffic is accompanied by a vehicle, which carriers report possible mobile patrols in order to change the route and avoid roadside checks.
The fuel is also mixed with light fuel oils or waste oils.
Fuel Distributor
A new type of tax entity, the fuel distributor, has been introduced in order to monitor fuel in free circulation and to eliminate tax evasion.
A person intending to distribute petrol, diesel or LPG in free circulation for tax purposes in the tax territory as part of a business activity shall, before distribution begins, apply to the customs office for a distribution permit and provide proof that the storage facility is verified and equipped with appropriate verified measuring equipment, as well as a list of suppliers and customers.
The fuel distributor is obliged, among other legal obligations, to keep separate records of petrol, diesel or LPG purchased and sold per calendar month for each establishment.
A fuel distributor is required by law to purchase or otherwise purchase fuel only from a fuel distributor or a registered person.
A fuel distributor may only sell to a fuel distributor, a registered person or a fuel consumer in the tax territory.
However, when the fuel is delivered via a car tanker, the distributor prints a so-called bottler from a measuring device built into the car tank when the fuel is pumped out by the fuel sellers or the fuel consumer.
That document shall include, in addition to the quantity data, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the car assigned by the transport inspectorate.
As the fuel is in free circulation for tax purposes, no accompanying document is required for the transport of these goods.
For example, an invoice, which also contains the number of the fuel distributor or registered person assigned by the tax authority, is sufficient to prove how the fuel was purchased.
Fuel consumer
The consumer of fuel has a special position in national legislation.
A person who purchases petrol, diesel or LPG in free circulation for his own consumption in the tax territory and stores that mineral oil in a storage facility with a capacity of 15 000 litres or more shall notify the customs office at the latest before the first placing in the storage facility.
Consumers of fuel shall be registered by the customs office.
In addition to the legal facts, he is obliged to give the address of the location of the storage facility.
In practice, these are large transport companies, cooperatives, bus companies, road construction companies and other entities.
The storage facility shall be verified and equipped with a measuring device enabling the quantity of propellants to be measured at the time of reception and delivery (stop sign, measuring rod).
The tank must comply with technical standards.
The fuel consumer must only purchase fuel from the fuel distributor or from a registered person.
As the fuel is in free circulation for tax purposes, no accompanying document is required for the transport.
However, when the fuel is delivered via a car tanker, the distributor prints a so-called bottler from a measuring device built into the car tank when the fuel is pumped to the consumer.
That document shall contain, in addition to the data relating to the quantity, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the car assigned by the transport inspectorate.
For example, an invoice, which also contains the number of the fuel distributor assigned by the tax authority, is sufficient to prove how the fuel was purchased.
The tax authority in the territory of the Slovak Republic records tax evasion related to the transport of this type of goods in the exercise of tax supervision of mineral oils.
Small independent brewery
The operator of a small independent brewery is a person who produces beer in the course of his business and meets the legal conditions.
Subject to the conditions laid down by law, a small independent brewery can apply a reduced rate of tax, i.e. €2,652 per hl / percentage of the actual alcoholic strength.
Annual beer production is limited to up to 200 000 hectolitres of beer.
As it concerns the production of beer outside the conditional exemption scheme, there is no need for an accompanying document for transport as it is in free circulation.
A small independent brewery cannot be a tax warehouse.
In practice, they are small family businesses, which also operate restaurants or saloons in which they offer their own beer for sale.
Administrative tasks in Slovakia
This sub-chapter approximates the exercise of tax supervision by the administration of excise duties on selected tax entities within the meaning of national legislation in the Slovak Republic.
The largest year-on-year increase in administrative tasks (by 5.3%) was recorded between 2012 and 2013, which was due to more EMCS shipments.
In contrast, the biggest year-on-year decrease was recorded in 2014, by up to 4.3%, which was due to fewer completed tax checks and fewer filed tax returns.
This decrease related to legislative changes.
Tax controls
By carrying out a tax audit, the CÚ ascertains or examines the facts relevant to the correct determination of the tax.
When carrying out a tax audit, the employees of the CÚ are shown a mandate to carry out a tax audit, which includes, among other things, the purpose and subject matter of the audit and the scope of the audited tax years.
In practice, this means that the audited tax period can be one month, but also more than one tax year.
The scope of the audited tax years is determined by the CA.
The tax audit begins with the drawing up of a report on the start of the tax audit.
The CA will confirm receipt of the documents.
The loaned documents are to be returned to the CÚ within 30 days of the completion of the tax inspection.
The CA staff member draws up a report from the tax inspection.
If the tax audit reveals a difference in the sum to be paid, declared or claimed by the audited taxpayer, the CÚ, together with the protocol, will also send the audited taxpayer an invitation to comment on the findings set out in the report.
The tax inspection shall be completed on the date of receipt of the report.
The time limit for carrying out a tax audit shall be no more than one year from the date of its initiation.
The tax inspection of registered persons and selected registered persons shall be carried out as necessary, but at least once before the date of expiry of the right to determine the tax, which is 5 years.
The FR SR issued an internal management act which adjusted the above deadlines due to the uniform procedure of the tax administration in the territory of the Slovak Republic.
Local investigation
A local investigation is the activity of the tax authority, in which it searches for evidence, examines and ascertains facts that are necessary for the purposes of tax administration.
A member of the CA staff draws up a report on the local investigation and submits a copy to the tax entity.
When carrying out a local investigation, a CA employee has the right to unlimited access to land, operational buildings, rooms and places, including means of transport, transport packaging and accounting documents.
The settlement of the quantity of alcohol produced shall be determined by means of a local investigation.
The facts established are the basis for the exercise of the tax control.
Also in the performance of the local investigation, the CÚ is entitled to take samples as well as to secure the case.
The FR SR issued an internal management act regulating the exercise of tax supervision and local investigations for individual excise items in order to harmonise the procedures of the tax administration.
Permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses for alcohol
With the accession of the Slovak Republic to the European Union on 1 May 2004, there was also a change in the area of the administration of excise duties.
The need for more efficient spending of state budget funds in the management of excise duty on alcohol, the improvement of the business environment in the area and the introduction of legislative instruments for more effective suppression of the grey economy in the area resulted in the adoption of new laws in 2004 in relation to the administration of excise duties.
One of the measures brought about by the new legislative amendment was not only the transfer of the excise tax administration from the tax authorities to the customs authorities, but also the introduction of the need for the tax administration to be present in the tax warehouse for alcohol.
In the territory of the Slovak Republic, national legislation exhaustively defines that it is only possible to receive, supply, produce or process alcohol in a tax warehouse in the presence of a CA employee.
This does not apply to a tax warehouse which receives, stores or dispatches alcohol only in the immediate packaging of alcohol.
At the same time, the CÚ is obliged to provide for employees in the tax warehouse so as not to restrict the income, supply, production or processing of alcohol.
The operator of the tax warehouse is obliged to ensure the conditions of the working environment for the employees of the CA.
On the basis of a contract concluded with the Ministry of Finance for the premises provided, the Ministry of Finance pays the operator of the tax warehouse the rental costs on a monthly basis.
In the tax warehouse for the production, processing or storage of ethyl alcohol, the production facility for the storage of ethyl alcohol must be adapted so that the quantities of ethyl alcohol produced, processed ethyl alcohol, stored ethyl alcohol, including the stocks of ethyl alcohol and alcohol contained therein, can be ascertained at any time.
ThissegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Where ethyl alcohol is not accepted, issued, produced or processed in a tax warehouse, the customs office may waive the obligation to ensure the presence of an employee of the customs office, which it is obliged to secure by closing the customs office.
In practice, however, this option is not used very often, as tax warehouse operators use the continuous presence of a customs employee to their advantage.
Some operators of the tax warehouse use a legal option within the meaning of Act No 467 / 2002 Z. z., on the production and marketing of ethyl alcohol, and use production facilities for the production of ethyl alcohol in the distillery for the production of the distillery and also for the purposes of the distillery, which must be a tax warehouse.
Around 250 customs officers provide permanent tax supervision in alcohol tax warehouses.
Issue of vouchers for the collection of alcohol control stamps
The basic act for the collection of control stamps is to send an application to the customs office for the allocation of a registration sampling number and to issue a voucher for the collection of control stamps for alcohol.
Alcoholic beverages, which are ethyl alcohol, are goods of Combined Nomenclature 2207 and 2208 with an actual alcoholic strength by volume of more than 1,2%.
The control mark is intended for the labelling of the consumer packaging of alcohol.
A sealed container filled with alcohol intended for direct human consumption is considered to be a consumer packaging of alcohol.
Consumer packaging of Combined Nomenclature codes 2207 and 2208 may be put into free circulation for tax purposes in the tax territory only if it is marked with a control mark.
Only the operator of the tax warehouse, the authorised consignee and the importer of the consumer packaging, who will put it into free circulation for tax purposes, may mark the consumer packaging of alcohol with a control mark.
The control mark contains, among other things, an identification number consisting of a 14-digit numerical character. The identification number contains the registration sampling number (1-6 instead of the numerical character), the volume of alcohol (7-11 instead of the numerical character) and the volume concentration of alcohol in the immediate packaging (12-14 instead of the numerical character).
Original model of the ethyl alcohol control mark:
The registration number will be assigned separately by the CÚ to each customer of the control mark.
Only a control mark, the identification number of which corresponds to the volume of the immediate packaging, the volume concentration of alcohol in the immediate packaging and the customer's control mark, may be used to mark the immediate packaging of alcohol.
At the end of 2014, national legislation brought about the introduction of a new information system for control marks.
The aim of the new information system for control marks was to simplify and computerise the system for ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using control marks for the labelling of consumer packaging of alcohol.
Only the operator of the tax warehouse, the authorised consignee, the importer of the consumer packaging and the consignee (purchaser) of the alcohol can mark the consumer packaging of the alcohol.
A purchaser of control stamps who wishes to collect control marks under the "new system" must apply to the customs office for the issue of control marks electronically.
Through the electronic system, the purchaser of control stamps is obliged to request their issue, to report data resulting from the national legislation of the Slovak Republic and to keep a register of control marks.
The number of pieces of stamps ordered shall not be less than 500 pieces or a multiple thereof.
The tax authority also communicates with customers of control stamps through an electronic system of control stamps, in particular when announcing the number of control marks that the customer of control stamps can remove or when determining the date of receipt of control marks by the customer of control stamps in the printer.
Before accepting the stamps, the purchaser of the stamps is obliged to deposit into the account of the tax authority funds corresponding to the price of the stamps, which he can withdraw and the quantity of which is notified to him by the customs office.
The price of the stamp takes into account the amount of refunds to the printer, but it does not take into account the amount of excise duty.
The state-owned company Mincovna Kremnice is entitled to print the stamps.
FR SR carries out tax supervision of the handling of control stamps and their liquidation in the printing works.
Fr SR is obliged to ensure the presence of an employee of the financial directorate in the printing works when handling the control stamps.
FR SR ensures the sale of control stamps to the purchaser of control stamps in the printer.
Check marks can only be taken from a member of staff of the Financial Directorate at the printer.
Issue of vouchers for the collection of control stamps for tobacco products
The purchaser of the control mark must ask the CA to assign a registration number and issue a voucher for the collection of the control mark.
Consumer packaging of cigarettes can only be put into free circulation for tax purposes if it is marked with a control mark.
It is only possible to mark the consumer packaging of cigarettes with a control mark in a company which produces cigarettes.
Only the operator of a tax warehouse, an authorised consignee or an importer of tobacco products who wishes to put tobacco products into free circulation for tax purposes in the tax territory can be a purchaser of the stamps.
Only a control mark may be used to indicate the consumer packaging of cigarettes, the details of which correspond to the relevant price of the cigarettes, the number of cigarettes in the package, the length of the cigarettes, the validity of the tax rate and the registration number.
The consumer packaging of cigarettes can only be sold for final consumption at the price indicated on the control mark.
At the end of 2014, national legislation brought about the introduction of a new information system for control marks.
The aim of the new information system for control marks was to simplify and computerise the system for ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using control marks for the labelling of consumer packaging of tobacco, cigars, cigarillos and cigarettes.
A purchaser of control stamps who wishes to collect control marks under the "new system" must apply to the customs office for the issue of control marks electronically.
Through the electronic system, the purchaser of control stamps is obliged to request their issue, to report data resulting from the national legislation of the Slovak Republic and to keep a register of control marks.
The state-owned company Mincovna Kremnice is entitled to print the stamps.
FR SR carries out tax supervision of the handling of control stamps and their liquidation in the printing works.
Fr SR is obliged to ensure the presence of an employee of the financial directorate in the printing works when handling the control stamps.
FR SR ensures the sale of control stamps to the purchaser of control stamps in the printer.
Check marks can only be taken from a member of staff of the Financial Directorate at the printer.
The operator of the tax warehouse or the importer of tobacco products may mark the consumer packaging of tobacco with a control mark.
The operator of the tax warehouse, the importer of tobacco products or the authorised consignee may mark the consumer packaging of cigars or cigarillos with a control mark.
To mark the packaging of tobacco, cigars or cigarillos for consumption, only a control mark shall be used, the particulars of which correspond to the mark for the validity of the rate of excise duty.
It is only possible to mark the consumer packaging of cigarettes with a control mark in the company that produced them.
The number of pieces of stamps ordered shall not be less than 500 pieces or a multiple thereof.
Within three working days at the latest, the CÚ will electronically notify the purchaser of the control marks of the number of control marks that it can withdraw, the price of the control marks and the account number of the CPP SR.
The CÚ may reduce the number of pieces of control stamps ordered if there are circumstances on the basis of which it can reasonably be assumed that there may be an infringement of tax rules.
Fr SR will set a date for the acceptance of the control marks by the purchaser of the control marks, but no later than 10 days.
The date of receipt of the control marks will be announced by the Slovak Ministry via the electronic system of control marks to the purchaser of the control marks.
The stamps are issued by the Finance Directorate exclusively in the printing works, but only after the receipt of the funds corresponding to their price into the relevant account indicated in the electronic notification to the customs office.
The purchaser of the control marks is required to keep a separate register of the control marks in the electronic system of control marks, broken down for cigarettes, cigars, cigarillos and tobacco.
Administrative cooperation between EU Member States (ELO)
Within the meaning of Council Regulation (EU) No 389 / 2012, the ELO and SPD Systems Unit of the Excise Duty Department of the CCP is responsible for ensuring the exchange of information following a request for administrative cooperation between EU Member States and the relevant financial authorities.
These include, in particular, requests for verification of entities within the excise administration, requests for information relating to the excise administration, as well as requests for confirmation of information from the SEED database.
The exchange of applications shall take place in electronic form within the framework of the EMCS.
The following actions are included in administrative cooperation between EU Member States: Requests for administrative cooperation (request for verification, request for information on excise administration, request for confirmation of registration in SEED); response to request for administrative cooperation; spontaneous information; event report; inspection report.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Authorisation and registration
In the Slovak Republic, permanent tax supervision is applied to tax warehouses for alcohol; in the Czech Republic, this supervision is replaced by continuous supervision by the tax administration through a monitoring device.
In the Czech Republic, small independent breweries are a tax warehouse; in the Slovak Republic, they are only registered by the tax authority.
The institute of registered consignor, which is included among tax warehouses in the Czech Republic, is established in the Slovak Republic.
In the Slovak Republic, it is possible to burn 43 litres a at a reduced rate of excise duty on ethyl alcohol in the case of crop burning.
In the Czech Republic, on the other hand, the reduced rate of alcohol tax can only be applied to 30 l a.
Cultivation brandy in the Slovak Republic must be authorised not only by the Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Development of the Slovak Republic, but also by the tax authorities.
In the Czech Republic, only the Ministry of Agriculture allows the production of brandy.
In SR, in addition to the operator of the tax warehouse, the import of consumer packaging of alcohol is also carried out by the importer of consumer packaging of alcohol.
The importer's authorisation is subject to the registration of the applicant with the excise authority.
In the Czech Republic, no special permission from the tax authority is required for the import of consumer packaging of alcohol.
In the Slovak Republic, the sale of consumer packaging of alcohol is subject to the issue of a permit by the tax authority for the seller.
The seller of consumer packaging of alcohol has a statutory obligation to keep records of, among other things, purchases and sales.
In the Czech Republic, the tax authority does not issue any permit for the final sellers of consumer packaging of alcohol, it is sufficient to issue a concession for the sale of alcohol by the trade office; the final seller does not keep any special records.
In SR, the seller of fuel must have permission from the tax authorities to sell it.
National legislation in the Slovak Republic does not provide for any special regulation of petrol stations, all activities relating to petrol stations are regulated only in the law on excise duty on mineral oils.
In the Czech Republic, petrol stations are regulated by a special law on fuel, but the tax authority does not issue any permit for the sale of fuel.
Service stations are registered and their list is published by the Ministry of Industry and Trade.
In the Slovak Republic, it is not technically possible to obtain a list of petrol stations from the financial management system.
There has been a significant increase in the number of selected permits or registrations of tax entities in the Slovak Republic since 2012.
This increase was due to a legislative change in that period.
In the Czech Republic, on the other hand, the number of selected permits decreased significantly in 2013 due to the introduction of bail for fuel distributors.
Administrative tasks
In the Slovak Republic, the substantive legislation provides for the obligation to carry out tax checks on selected tax entities.
This issue is further specified in the internal management act issued by the SR CCP for the purpose of applying a uniform procedure for tax administrations in the territory of the Slovak Republic.
In the Czech Republic, the substantive legislation does not provide for the obligation to carry out a tax inspection; the procedural law only provides for the possibility of carrying out an inspection at the latest by the deadline for the assessment of the tax.
The reason for the large differences in the number of tax checks and local investigations carried out in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic is that the internal management act of the Slovak Republic stipulates in which cases and within what time limits the tax authority must carry out a tax check, while in the Czech Republic the accuracy of the amount of excise duty declared or its refund is verified mainly by a local investigation.
The number of comparable administrative tasks in the Czech Republic has increased since 2012 as a result of the increase in the number of shipments in the EMCS system and the increase in the number of tax returns submitted.
In the Slovak Republic, the number of administrative tasks had a slightly increasing trend between 2012 and 2015, which was influenced by the increasing number of shipments in the EMCS system as well as the decrease in the number of tax returns.
Evaluation
The large differences between the number of comparable permits and the registration of tax entities have been reflected in the different legislation.
The number of comparable administrative tasks of tax administrations was similar in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in the different years of the audited period.
In the Slovak Republic, the total number of comparable tax entities, which is about two-thirds of the number of tax entities in the Czech Republic, accounts for about the same number of administrative tasks.
From this it can be concluded that SR is more focused on the implementation of administrative tasks by tax administrations, e.g. the exercise of physical tax supervision.
In the Czech Republic, the emphasis is more on remote surveillance, e.g. tracking devices, immediate sending of data via a web interface and risk analysis.
Computerisation of administrative tasks
Computerization of administrative tasks in the Czech Republic
The tax return can be filed through a data container.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic has introduced so-called interactive tax return forms, which can no longer be processed in an automated way.
The data must also be transferred to the personal tax account of the taxpayer.
The benefit is a reduction in the error rate of filed tax returns (DAP), which saves the tax administration's actions related to the procedure for correcting erroneously filed DAP.
GŘC is working on a new application for electronic processing of DAP.
In addition, smart forms can: Submit tax applications or registration for activities and notification of changes in data, claim refunds, comply with reporting obligations for the handling of special mineral oils, the handling of raw tobacco and the fulfilment of biofuel obligations.
The handling of control tapes is recorded by tax entities in the information system ORO webclient, which is available for registered entities for registration by the tax authority of the specified data.
The transport of selected products in the Czech Republic under the conditional exemption regime must be carried out in the Czech Republic on the basis of an electronic accompanying document, which is implemented in the Czech Republic as a national functionality in the electronic system for monitoring the transport of selected products (EMCS).
The transport of selected products in free circulation in the tax territory of the Czech Republic can always be carried out with a document proving their taxation, proof of exemption from excise duty, a decision by the customs office to place selected products under a customs procedure, a simplified accompanying document or another decision on the assessment of excise duty.
The required content of the data is laid down by law.
In order to facilitate the fulfilment of these obligations, the Czech Republic has introduced a voluntary electronic system for issuing alternative documents (Sections 5 and 6 of Act No 353 / 2003 Coll.).
This allows the paper form of documents to be replaced or supplemented by electronically issued documents, which are sent via the web interface of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic to a data warehouse, where each such document is assigned a unique 12-digit identification code (JIK).
Jik is used for the purpose of control by customs authorities on the way and prevents repeated transport on the same document.
For the largest operator of a fuel tax warehouse in the Czech Republic, which puts about half of the volume of PHM into free tax circulation, CS ČR has online access to an electronic registration system in which the entity automatically stores the issued tax documents.
CS ČR is considering the introduction of e-VDO, i.e. an electronic system for recording and monitoring shipments of selected products carried out in free tax circulation.
This system should make use of 70% of the current EMCS functional specification.
The advantage will be a user-friendly environment for both declarants and customs officers.
It will also be linked to a system of global guarantees, a register of tax entities or a system of risk analysis.
The system should allow for an overview of shipments in free circulation between Member States, which so far operates on the basis of written documents without registration and the sharing of negotiating numbers through simplified accompanying documents.
The risks of the current procedure for recording shipments of selected products in free tax circulation can be seen mainly in the misuse of a simplified accompanying document, the repeated use of a single document or illegal transport without any document.
Computerisation of administrative tasks in Slovakia
In the administration of excise duties, the Slovak tax administration uses electronic communication to monitor the movement of goods in the EMCS system under the conditional exemption regime, check marks, submission of tax returns, as well as registration and registration of tax entities.
One-way electronic communication between tax entities and the tax administration was also introduced in 2014, which was extended to two-way communication in 2016.
In the context of electronic communication, the taxpayer has access to a personal internet zone, called an electronic personal mailbox, which is designed for communication with the tax administration.
Within this zone, the taxpayer has access to an electronic mailroom through which he submits applications, notifications, tax returns and other documents relating to the administration of excise duties.
However, electronic communication via a personal internet zone does not apply to all tax entities.
National legislation defines the tax entities that are required to communicate electronically with the tax authorities.
These are mainly value added tax payers, tax advisers representing the tax entity and lawyers representing the tax entity.
During the audit, the SAO SR also dealt with the issue of the scope of the computerization of the administration of excise duties.
These were only fully electronic acts, namely tax returns and electronic communications within the ELO.
Apart from the transport carried out in EMCS, there has been an increase in the computerisation of selected comparable administrative tasks, which is also a requirement for modern tax administration.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Fully computerised processing of the tax return is already in place in the Slovak Republic, from its filing to the registration of the tax liability.
Electronic processing of tax returns is not set up in the Czech Republic.
In the Czech Republic, the option is set up for tax entities to enter on the website compulsory documents for individual shipments in free tax circulation.
In the future, the declaration of transport in free tax circulation in the form and on the basis of EMCS is being prepared.
Evaluation
The system of reporting shipments in free tax circulation in the Czech Republic contributes to tax supervision, thus eliminating the transport of selected products for which excise duty has not been paid in violation of the legislation.
This can be recommended as good practice.
ThissegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Due to good practice in the Slovak Republic in the field of computerization of tax returns, the SAO of the Slovak Republic and the SAO of the Czech Republic recommend completing the computerization of the processing of tax returns in the Czech Republic.
Analysis of changes in organisational structure and staffing in the field of excise duties
The organisational arrangements of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic and the Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic have undergone fundamental changes.
Organization of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic
Since 1 January 2013, the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic has been composed of the General Directorate of Customs and Customs Offices, which are administrative offices and organisational units of the state.
The GŘC is an accounting unit for the entire customs administration.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic has been carrying out a comprehensive administration of excise duties since 2004 as one of the many competences it provides.
CS ČR continues to carry out:
(A) inspection:
In the field of road transport (weighing of trucks, payment of infrastructure charges, fulfilment of conditions for the transport of dangerous goods, professional supervision of the work of vehicle crews in international road freight transport and in matters of international passenger transport),
Management of waste and packaging material;
The safety of imported food,
In the field of consumer protection and the protection of intellectual property rights,
Employment of foreigners,
(B) customs administration - it is a complex application of customs legislation, commercial policy measures and formalities for the import and export of goods;
(C) the collection and recovery of pecuniary benefits imposed by other public authorities in the context of a split administration;
(D) the activities of the police authority (designated customs authorities) in proceedings concerning offences committed in breach of customs and related regulations and tax regulations, if the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic is the tax authority.
While the scope of competences (concurrence of control activities) increases the overall cost of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, there are economies of scale as the public administration does not have to spend on the status of a control group for each subject of control separately.
At the same time, there is a reduction in the administrative burden on the persons checked by repeated checks.
10 The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic also carries out from 1 December 2016 the task of verifying compliance with obligations in the registration of sales (Section 2 (2) of Act No. 112 / 2016 Coll., on the registration of sales) and from 1 January 2017 the supervision of compliance with the law and the conditions for the operation of gambling, including the imposition of sanctions (Section 116 of Act No. 186 / 2016 Coll., on gambling).
As part of the project Modernization of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic changed the three-stage structure to a two-stage structure with effect from 1 January 2013, with the abolition of the central article of the procedure (customs directorates).
GŘC spent approximately CZK 51 million on the project (i.e. approximately €2,031,000).
Since 1 January 2013, CS ČR has been made up of GŘC and regional customs offices, which are administrative offices and organisational units of the state.
The customs offices and their competences are laid down by law, the administration of excise duties is carried out by all customs offices through departments and territorial offices.
The territorial offices are the internal organisational units of the customs offices.
The Ministry of Finance is entitled by decree to set up and abolish territorial workplaces and to determine their material scope.
The legislation does not provide for any competence for the territorial office; the territorial office exercises the competence of the customs office on its behalf.
Organizational structure until 31 December 2012
Organisational structure as of 1 January 2013
Until 31 December 2012, the administration of excise duties was carried out by the GŘC, eight CŘ and 58 CÚ departments (including branches), i.e. a total of 67 departments and departments.
As of 1 January 2016, the administration of excise duties was carried out by the GŘC and 51 departments at the CÚ and their territorial offices, as well as eight offices of the legal department of the GŘC and the departments of the CÚ providing mobile supervision, i.e. about 60 places.
The costs of CS CR are most significantly influenced by wage expenditure.
As a result of the reorganisation of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, there have been no savings in personnel resources.
The performance of the main processes is carried out by customs officers in the service of the law on the service of members of the security forces.
The possibility of reducing the number of these members is very limited in the Czech Republic, as according to the provisions of Section 42 (1) of Act No 361 / 2003 Coll., on the service of members of the security forces, they can be dismissed from the service only in cases exhaustively defined.
The reduction of posts due to organisational changes in the security force is not a reason for dismissal and the employer is obliged to ensure that members are assigned adequate posts within the force, or to provide posts with another security force (e.g. the Police of the Czech Republic, the Prison Service of the Czech Republic), otherwise they will be transferred to a reserve for the temporarily non-attached, in which members of the security forces are entitled to 80% of the average service income according to the law.
ThissegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Organisation of excise administration in the Slovak Republic
In the framework of the programme statement for the years 2012 to 2016, the government of the Slovak Republic has set as one of its priorities the completion of the reform of the tax administration through the UNITAS programme, which will provide additional budgetary resources by unifying the collection of taxes, duties and levies and curbing tax evasion.
In this context, the tax reform was implemented at the central level, which resulted in the merger of the Tax Directorate of the Slovak Republic and the Customs Directorate of the Slovak Republic into the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic and the creation of a financial administration.
FR SR was established on 1 January 2012 by Act No. 333 / 2011 Z. z., on state administrative bodies in the field of taxation, fees and customs, as amended, as a budgetary organization, which is based in Banská Bystrica and is connected to the state budget through the budget chapter of the Ministry of Finance of the Slovak Republic.
Fr SR, CÚ and the Criminal Office of the Financial Administration within the meaning of Act No 199 / 2004 Z. z., the Customs Act and amending and supplementing certain laws, as amended, are customs authorities when they carry out tasks according to customs regulations.
Within the meaning of Act No. 333 / 2011 Z. z., on State Administration Bodies in the Field of Taxes, Fees and Customs, as amended, together with the tax authorities, they form a financial administration.
The new organisational structure of the financial administration as of 1 January 2012 consists of the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic, the Criminal Office of the Financial Administration, the Competence Centre for Financial Operations, tax offices, the Tax Office for Selected Tax Entities, branches of tax offices, contact points of tax offices, customs offices, branches of customs offices (branch of the Tax Office, branch of the Combined Tax Office, branch of the Customs Office) and customs offices.
The main mission of the SR CCP is the effective collection and administration of taxes and duties, i.e. also excise duties, to fulfil the revenue part of the state budget and to protect the economic interests of the state.
The statutory body of the Slovak Finance Ministry is the President of the Financial Administration, who is appointed and dismissed by the Minister of Finance of the Slovak Republic.
The president of the financial administration is responsible to him for the activities of the entire financial administration, and therefore also for the activities of the CCP, which he manages and represents in full.
The organisational structure of the Slovak CCP since 1 January 2012 in an abbreviated form
In addition to branches of customs offices (38 branches) and stations of customs offices (18 stations), excise departments (9 departments) and legal departments (9 departments) provide activities and processes in the field of excise administration within all customs offices in the territory of the Slovak Republic.
