Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Within the organisational structure of the financial administration of the Slovak Republic, 74 organisational units with a total of 1,300 employees were involved in the administration of excise duties in 2015, in addition to the Slovak Ministry of Finance; these units are managed by nearly 48,000 tax entities.
Within the organisational structure of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, in 2015 the administration of excise duties was handled by about 60 organisational units with a total of 1,011 employees, which are managed by about 114,000 tax entities.
In the Czech Republic, the performance of the various activities of the administration of excise duties is divided among several independent departments.
Their coordination and cooperation is dealt with through middle and top management.
In the Slovak Republic, the exercise of individual activities (registration, tax return, tax control) in the field of excise administration is divided between the excise department and the branch of the customs office, where the agenda is often dealt with by the same employees of the tax administration.
Evaluation
In the Slovak Republic, the number of tax entities is about a third of the total number of employees in the field of excise administration compared to the situation in the Czech Republic; the effect of the higher number of employees on the efficiency of the excise administration is not clear.
EMCS
According to the preamble to Decision No 1152 / 2003 / EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 on the introduction of an electronic system for the movement and monitoring of products subject to excise duty, the aim of the introduction of an electronic system for monitoring the transport of selected products was to enable real-time information on the movement and to carry out the prescribed checks, to facilitate the movement of goods within the Community under suspension of excise duty.
When implementing the system, Member States should have allowed economic operators, in particular SMEs active in the sector, to use these national elements at the lowest possible cost.
Article 3 of the EP and Council Decision allows for the inclusion in the EMCS of national specifications, national databases forming part of the system and such technical or software as the Member State considers necessary to ensure the full use of the system within its administration.
EMCS in Czech Republic
Development and functionalities of EMCS
In the Czech Republic, EMCS was preceded by a system of registration of selected products (EVV), which was operated from May 2004 to the end of March 2010.
The EMCS has been fully operational in the Czech Republic since 1 April 2010 and is continuously supplemented by European and national functionalities (see Annex 5).
A customs module and a declarant module have been introduced in the Czech Republic.
The customs module contains a number of national functionalities.
In addition to the Community system, in the Czech Republic, EMCS monitors shipments under the conditional exemption regime, both initiated and terminated in the Czech Republic.
After approval of the notification of receipt of a consignment intended for an authorised consignee for a single receipt, the system ensures that the information is automatically sent to the register of tax entities, with subsequent invalidation of the authorisation.
The system fully ensures the administration of received and sent requests for international cooperation and spontaneous information from the ELO, including the sending of replies with an annex in any format and providing translations.
It is also possible to receive a manual export termination message in the ECS (in the EU, only the transmission of an automatically created message is implemented).
Risk profiles for outgoing or incoming shipments are set according to the currently required criteria.
The EMCS will not allow the approval of an e-AD or an admission notification without the competent customs authority responding to the risk profile (the risk profile cannot be ignored).
The Declarant Module is available free of charge for tax entities, taking the form of a web application to which the user logs in with a username and password (coordinates), which are assigned to him after registration with CS ČR.
Any action against the EMCS Customs Module shall be accompanied by a valid electronic signature in the EMCS declarant module.
The Declarant Module allows tax entities to directly record data on commenced and completed shipments under the conditional exemption regime, so that tax entities do not have to spend money to acquire the system.
The national functionalities of the declarant module make it possible to load and store data offline (saving time on frequently used data), to fill in recipient data based on a SEED ID check and to require mandatory completion of data that is optional at EU level (maximum data for risk analysis).
The system also allows every consignment sent from the Czech Republic to be blocked in real time from securing excise duty at the corresponding amount of taxable transactions until the end of the transport.
The amount of collateral is calculated automatically by the EMCS.
Without a sufficient level of security, the EMCS declarant module is not allowed to send the e-AD proposal for approval to the CA of dispatch.
Each warranty has a unique number and includes the ARC of transportation (including the amount of security blocked) for which it was used.
The taxpayer can manage its guarantees directly in the EMCS declarant module, where it can see the current amount of the blocked and unblocked excise duty guarantee.
Expenditure on the implementation and use of EMCS
The development of EMCS was carried out on the basis of eight performance contracts from 2006 to 2017 totalling CZK 46,791,924.60 (i.e. €1,761,412.56) excluding VAT.
In accordance with the contracts concluded, the contractor issued invoices for a total amount of CZK 43,577,255.19 (i.e. €1,640,401.10) excluding VAT from 2006 to the end of 2015.
During the audited period, expenditure of CZK 14,545,454 excluding VAT (i.e. €547,438.99) was incurred for the upgrade of the EMCS.
The amount spent on upgrading EMCS in the audited period and converted into one transport contributed to EMCS is on average 16.49 CZK (i.e. 0.62 €), excluding national transport, this expenditure is 24.40 CZK (i.e. 0.92 €) per transport between the Czech Republic and the EU Member States.
The EMCS technical support was implemented on the basis of four performance contracts from 2011 to 2017.
By the end of 2015, the total amount of technical support was invoiced in the amount of CZK 7,499,675 (i.e. €281,389.77) including value added tax.
The average amount of technical support spent since 2011 per transport contributed to EMCS since 2010 is CZK 6.18 (i.e. €0.23).
The invoices for both development and technical support related to the national solution and developed the EVV application, which was already operated by GŘC before EMCS itself.
Invoices were paid as part of the programme funding from national sources.
Technical support is invoiced as part of the supply of services to other applications provided by the supplier for the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
EMCS in Slovakia
The EMCS is an electronic system operated by EU Member States to monitor the movement of excise goods between Member States under suspension of duty.
It replaced the accompanying administrative document - the SAD, which was used before the system came into effect, thereby ensuring better control and management of shipments.
It has been in place in the Slovak Republic since 1 April 2010 and has been continuously supplemented by requirements arising from EU legislation.
A unique reference code is generated for each transport, the so-called "
Arc code under which the traffic can be tracked online, i.e. in real time.
Development and functionalities of EMCS
The EMCS system ensures the receipt and dispatch of excise goods only by tax entities authorised to use the EMCS system, thus greatly reducing the risk of tax evasion.
The biggest development in functionalities occurred in 2011, when EMCS was fully operational (see Annex 6).
Expenditure on the implementation and use of EMCS
The introduction of EMCS has been implemented as an additional module of SysNeD application equipment and therefore it is not possible to determine the exact cost of its initial application on the Slovak side.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
The aim of EMCS was to replace a system based on paper-based transport administration.
The benefits of EMCS are a comprehensive overview of transport between Member States within the EU, from the announcement of the start of transport to the end of transport, with a significant reduction in administrative costs for tax administrations and tax entities for processing, handing over and archiving documents.
In the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, national functionality has been introduced into the EMCS system, allowing monitoring of traffic in a conditional system between two locations in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic respectively.
In addition, the automatic functionality of online monitoring and the provision of a guarantee for excise duty is applied in the Czech Republic.
National functionality is also introduced, which monitors the riskiness of the tax entity or transport, followed by a mandatory response from the tax authorities.
The Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic record a comparable number of intra-EU shipments in the EMCS system.
However, between 2012 and 2015, the expenditure incurred in the Slovak Republic to upgrade the system was €744,310.01 higher than in the Czech Republic.
The SAO of the Slovak Republic obtained data from the Slovak Ministry of Finance on the upgrade of the EMCS system only for the period from 2011, even though the system was introduced and operated earlier.
However, the costs incurred for upgrading the EMCS system in the Slovak Republic were €188,134.44 higher than the costs for the introduction and upgrade of the EMCS system in about ten years of operation in the Czech Republic.
Evaluation
During the audited period, the amount of expenditure related to the upgrade of the EMCS system in the Slovak Republic per shipment is 2.3 times higher than the expenditure of the same type in the Czech Republic.
Conclusion
The cooperation between the SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic has achieved its objectives.
Both audit institutions gained a deeper knowledge of the system of administration of excise duties in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
It was found that, despite the common basic legal framework, there are significant differences between the two tax systems which affect the efficiency of excise administration.
Parallel checks have identified examples of good practice that could contribute to reducing tax fraud, which will become increasingly important as tax rates rise.
Procedures to reduce the costs of administering excise duties have also been identified.
Mutual cooperation has revealed differences that significantly affect the efficiency of tax administration and limit international comparisons unless coordinated due diligence is carried out with the tax administration.
In this, the role of supreme audit institutions is indispensable.
Report on the results of a parallel audit of the VAT administration carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Introductory word
The 1977 Lima Declaration stresses that the Supreme Audit Institutions (SAIs) have the power to audit all public financial operations.
The declaration calls for tax revenues to be controlled as far as possible.
The European Organisation of Supreme Audit Institutions (EUROSAI) considers taxes to be one of the most important components of public revenue.
The VI. EUROSAI Congress held in Bonn in 2005 dealt with the audit of public revenue carried out by the SAI.
The development of a specific strategy for the audit of public revenue is an important step towards optimising SAI control activities.
This applies in particular to taxation as the bulkiest source of public revenue, which is the most vulnerable to large losses.
As national economies become increasingly interconnected and dependent, SAIs may to some extent be unable to carry out control activities without the cooperation of another state's SAI.
An example is the audit of internationally organised fraud, which causes significant income losses in many countries.
In order to combat this crime, the responsible authorities need to work together.
The Sai, which carry out checks in this area, must be willing to cooperate more closely with each other.
It was at the VI EUROSAI Congress in Bonn that the idea arose to carry out an audit of the administration of value added tax ("VAT") and the VIES system in the framework of cooperation between the Supreme Audit Office and the Federal Court of Auditors, the Bundesrechnungshof.
This was followed by careful preparation, where both parties first had to familiarise themselves with the legal environment and procedures for administering VAT in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany.
On the basis of an analysis of this information, a selection of control topics was carried out and included in the control programme.
Achieving an efficient and efficient VAT administration has been a long-standing challenge and individual states (especially European Union Member States) are looking for solutions to improve, simplify and make the collection of VAT more transparent.
We believe that the results of our inspection can serve not only to improve the work of tax authorities, but also as a basis for a proposal to improve the system of international exchange of information.
Report on the results of parallel checks on the administration of value added tax carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 06 / 27 (D) VIII 2 - 2005 - 1215
Subject of inspection:
(CZ) Administration of value added tax after the accession of the Czech Republic to the European Union
(D) Examination of administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003 and Commission Regulation (EC) No 1925 / 2004
Objective of the inspection:
(CZ) The aim of the audit operation in the Czech Republic was to examine the procedure of the tax authorities in the administration of value added tax following the integration of the Czech Republic into the single internal market of the European Union ("EU") linked to the free movement of goods and services and to examine the use of the VIES system, in particular when checking the application of the right to exemption from value added tax for intra-Community supplies.
(D) The aim of the audit was to examine the system for the control of intra-community value added tax, with a particular focus on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax under the aforementioned regulations.
The result should be a report on the weaknesses and recommendations for their elimination.
The system of exchange of information on value added tax The audit actions were carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as "the SAO") and the German Bundesrechnungshof (hereinafter referred to as "BRH") in mutual cooperation on the basis of a contract concluded between the two audit institutions on 8 June 2006.
The cooperation focused mainly on the examination of selected business transactions between payers from the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as "the Czech Republic") and the Federal Republic of Germany (hereinafter referred to as "Germany"), the use of information obtained in the form of international cooperation between tax administrations and the comparison of the VAT administration systems of the two countries.
The joint final report on the results of the control actions was prepared within the meaning of European Directive No 31 for the implementation of the INTOSAI audit standards.
The audited period covered the period from 1.5.2004 to 31.12.2005.
Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions
A parallel inspection in the area of VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany was carried out on the basis of a contract between the two SAIs.
Apart from the main point - exchanges of information based on Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003 and Commission Regulation (EC) No 1925 / 2004 - the audit covered other topics, such as the registration of payers, VAT returns and recapitulative statements, which are closely linked to the main point.
In addition, the inspection included the legal situation in the field of international bus passenger transport and a comparison of some statistical data.
A comparison of the VAT management systems of the two countries revealed differences in the following areas:
1) VAT registration.
While in Germany entrepreneurs are registered regardless of the amount of their turnover, in the Czech Republic the primary criterion (among others) for registration is exceeding the limit set in the VAT Act.
In the Czech Republic, payers are assigned only one tax identification number, which they also use in intra-community transactions.
In Germany, taxpayers are assigned a tax number when registering for VAT, which is used only for commercial transactions in the territory of Germany.
If the German payer intends to carry out intra-community transactions, he must apply for a special identification number, the so-called VAT ID.
As different registration methods cause problems, conditions should be balanced across the EU (see 4.1).
2) International passenger transport by bus.
In the Czech Republic, international bus passenger transport is exempt from VAT with the right to deduct VAT.
In Germany, the part of the transport which takes place on German territory is subject to VAT.
Efforts should be made at EU level to harmonise the situation within the meaning of Article 393 of Council Directive 2006 / 112 / EC on the common system of VAT (see 4.2).
(3) VAT returns.
While in the Czech Republic taxpayers only submit VAT returns for individual tax years (month or quarter), in Germany payers are obliged to submit so-called preliminary VAT returns (monthly or quarterly) and after the end of the calendar year they have to submit an annual VAT return.
Unlike the Czech Republic, payers in Germany are obliged to submit preliminary tax returns electronically.
The introduction of an obligation to submit VAT returns electronically in the Czech Republic would increase the efficiency of the Czech tax administration (see 4.3).
(4) Summary reports.
While in the Czech Republic payers file summary reports at tax offices, in Germany payers file summary reports at the CLO.
The tax authorities in the Czech Republic therefore have the data from the summary reports immediately after their submission.
The information from the recapitulative statements is only available to the German tax authorities after they have been processed into CLOs.
Combating VAT fraud requires up-to-date information on intra-Community transactions to be made available as soon as possible.
Monthly submission of recapitulative statements would reduce the time lag between the transaction date and the update of VIES data.
This, in turn, would allow for a timely examination of taxation in the Member State of the customer (see 4.4).
This would, however, require all Member States to adopt the same deadline for submitting a summary report.
5) International exchange of information in the field of VAT.
The Czech CLO monitors compliance with the three-month deadline for requests for information received.
The German CLO does not monitor the time elapsed.
As a result, the German tax authorities dealt with a significantly lower percentage of the applications received within the prescribed period.
Because of these problems, the BRH recommended that the German CLO carry out a permanent warning (see 4.6).
(6) Risk management system.
Each of the two Member States is developing its own risk management system (RMS), which has its own strengths and weaknesses.
The SAO and BRH point out that an effective RMS cannot be developed by just one Member State.
Successful RMS criteria, components and approaches must be exchanged and implemented in each EU Member State, otherwise fraudsters will choose the Member State with the weakest RMS (see 5).
As part of the cooperation, the two SAIs examined selected cases of intra-community transactions between tax entities from the Czech Republic and Germany.
Together, thirty-one cases of commercial transactions where there were doubts about their execution or suspicions of VAT evasion were examined using the CLO legislation.
It was found that:
In some cases, the tax authorities have used information obtained through international cooperation to assess the VAT liability of taxpayers.
In these cases, the payers either wrongly claimed exemption of the supply from VAT or did not declare the acquisition of the goods in the VAT return.
In some cases, the tax authorities could not use the information obtained because the information was either incomplete or unintelligible.
In other cases, the information could not be used due to different legal provisions in both Member States.
In some cases, the tax authorities of another Member State refused to respond to a request for information.
Cases have been identified where payers erroneously reported business transactions in recapitulative statements.
As a result, the VIES data was incorrect and tax administrations had to examine these cases (see 6.).
Progress of control action
Control event in the Czech Republic
The audit was carried out between June 2006 and March 2007 by Section II - the revenue department of the state budget and the regional unions of Central Bohemia, Northwest Bohemia, South Bohemia, South Moravia, Central Moravia and Northern Moravia.
The audited persons were: The Ministry of Finance (hereinafter "MF") and 10 tax offices - the Financial Office in Humpolec, the Financial Office in Jihlava, the Financial Office in Kadani, the Financial Office in Liberec, the Financial Office in Nymburk, the Financial Office in Otrokovice, the Financial Office for Prague 1, the Financial Office for Prague 4, the Financial Office in Sokolov and the Financial Office in Třinci.
The audit conclusion of this audit action was approved by the SAO College on 23 April 2007.
Progress of the control action in Germany
The audit was carried out between June 2006 and February 2007 by the control group for indirect taxes and by the staff of the designated regional control offices in Berlin, Frankfurt am Main and Munich.
The audit was part of the control plan for 2006 and was therefore notified to the Federal Ministry of Finance in 2006.
After the testing phase, the inspection started in the fourth quarter of 2006.
According to the cases selected by the BRH and later elected by the SAO, the BRH had to notify the audit to a number of federal states.
In addition to the interviews at the Federal Ministry of Finance and the CLO, the audit was carried out in the following federal states:
Baden-Württemberg, Bavaria, Hamburg, Lower Saxony, North Rhine-Westphalia, Rhineland-Palatinate and Saxony.
The tax files of the following tax authorities were included:
Bruchsal, Ettlingen, Freudenstadt, Karlsruhe-Stadt, Leonberg, Mühlacker, Singen, Tuttlingen, Cham, Fürstenfeldbruck, Munich - FÚ for Corporations / Legal Entities (München-Körperschaften), Munich II, IV and Munich V, Starnberg, Hamburg-Altona, Hamburg-Hansa, Hamburg-Centre (Hamburg-Mitte), Hamburg-North (Hamburg-Nord) and Hamburg for Large Enterprises (Hamburg für Großunternehmen), Hannover-Nord (Hannover-North), Winsen-Luhe, Bonn Centre (Bonn-Innenstadt), Cologne Centre (Köln-Mitte), Kolín-Porz (Köln-Porz), Cologne South (Köln-Süd), Sankt Augustin, Pirmasens, Budyshin (Bautzen), Chemnitz (South), Dresden II, Leipzig II and Dresden II.
In addition, discussions were held with the Tax Office of Augsburg-Stadt (Augsburg-Stadt), Aurich, Düsseldorf-Old Town (Düsseldorf Altstadt), Eisleben, Kelheim and Verden.
A report on the inspection findings was submitted to the Ministry of Finance in May 2007.
Cooperation between the two audit institutions
In preparation for the parallel control actions, several meetings of representatives of the two control institutions took place in the period prior to their launch.
The participants in these meetings were acquainted with the organisation of tax administrations, the legislation on VAT issues and the VAT administration system in both countries.
The topics of the test phase were agreed at a meeting held in May 2006.
The results of the test phase were evaluated at a further joint meeting in August 2006.
In the framework of this meeting, a timetable was agreed for the further progress of the work and the following topics of parallel controls were identified:
1. Registration of VAT payers.
2.
International bus passenger transport - legislation in the Czech Republic and Germany.
3. International exchange of information, in particular the procedure of the tax authorities when processing requests for information and examining selected problem cases mentioned in requests for information and spontaneous information transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany.
4. VAT returns.
5.
Summary reports.
6.
Statistics on the supply and acquisition of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany.
7. VAT risk management.
At the joint audit day of the SAO and BRH, which took place in December 2006, the two parties became acquainted with the progress of the audit in the Czech Republic and Germany and discussed the results of the parallel audit actions to date.
A report on the results of parallel checks of the VAT administration between the Czech Republic and Germany was prepared at a working meeting in July 2007.
4. Administration of Value Added Tax in the Czech Republic and Germany
Registration of payers in the Czech Republic
A) Plans who have their registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic
Under Act No 337 / 1992 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes and Fees (hereinafter "Act No 337 / 1992 Coll."), a taxpayer, a taxpayer and the legal successor of a natural or legal person, which is defined as a tax entity by law.
As of 31 December 2004, a total of 421 865 tax entities were registered for VAT in the Czech Republic.
As of 1 December 2005, the number of tax entities registered for VAT had increased to 457,590.
A taxable person who has his registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic, whose turnover exceeds CZK 1,000,000 (EUR 33,575) for the next 12 consecutive calendar months, becomes a payer from the first day of the third month following the month in which he exceeded the registration limit (Section 94 (1) of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax; hereinafter "Act No 235 / 2004 Coll.").
This person is required to submit an application for registration within 15 days of the end of the month in which he exceeded the registration limit.
The current legislation does not allow the registration of a taxable person so called retrospectively in cases where the reason for registration is to exceed the legal limit for registration.
A taxable person with a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic who carries out taxable transactions or transactions exempt from VAT with the right to deduct may become a taxable person, even if he does not exceed a turnover of 1,000,000 CZK (33,575 EUR), if he fulfils any of the other conditions set out in Act No 235 / 2004 Coll.
A taxable person with a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic who does not comply with any of the conditions laid down by law can apply for VAT registration on a voluntary basis.
The registration procedure under Act No 337 / 1992 Coll., is initiated by the delivery of the registration application to the local tax authority.
The voluntary VAT payer shall also indicate on the VAT registration application the date on which he applies to be registered as a VAT payer.
The tax authorities will check the information provided by the tax entity, i.e. the completed registration application with all annexes.
If it has doubts about the data, it shall ask the taxpayer to explain, supplement or substantiate the data.
After verifying that the tax entity meets the conditions for registration, the tax authority issues a decision in the form of a certificate stating that the tax entity is registered and has been assigned a tax identification number ("TIN").
On the certificate, the tax authority shall indicate the effective date of the VAT registration and the periodicity of the VAT tax year.
The tax year is the calendar quarter if the payer's turnover for the previous calendar year did not reach CZK 10,000,000 (EUR 335,750).
If the payer's turnover for the previous calendar year was CZK 10,000,000 (EUR 335,750), the tax year is the calendar month.
A payer whose turnover for the previous calendar year was CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) is entitled to choose a calendar month for the tax year and will notify the tax authorities of this change.
ThissegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The allocation of the TIN in the registration certificate is always constitutive and the tax entity is obliged to mention it in all cases of communication (including payments) with the tax authority and in cases where a special law so provides (e.g. Act No 235 / 2004 Coll. when issuing tax documents).
The TIN contains the code "CZ" and the generic part, which consists of a general identifier.
The general identifier for a natural person is the birth number or other general identifier, if provided for by a special law, and for a legal person the identification number (Section 33 (12) of Act No 337 / 1992 Coll.).
If the tax entity has not fulfilled its registration obligation even at the request of the tax authority, it will be registered by the local tax authority of its own motion without delay.
The result of the registration procedure is the issue of an ex officio registration certificate, which is served on the taxpayer.
In the Czech Republic, a tax entity that has obtained a business license is assigned a VAT number at the time of its first registration for any tax.
The same VAT number is used by the taxpayer even if it is registered as a VAT payer.
According to the wording of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll., which has been in force since 1 January 2005, in the event of failure to comply with the VAT registration obligation, the tax authority may order the taxable person to pay compensation of up to 10% of the total income or income for taxable transactions carried out by that person without tax for the period from the date on which he should have been a registered payer by law to the date on which he became a registered payer by decision of the tax authority (Section 98 (1) of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll.).
The payment of the amount thus determined is considered to be a payment of tax (Section 98 (3) of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll.), i.e. it is not a penalty.
The cancellation of the VAT payer's registration if the conditions laid down by law are met is possible for two reasons:
(1)
Cancellation of registration at the request of the payer, mainly due to the amount of turnover below the registration limit (Section 106 (1) of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll.).
The payer shall be entitled to apply for deregistration no earlier than 1 year after the effective date indicated on the registration certificate.
(2) Cancellation of registration "ex officio" (Section 106 (7) of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll.) if: (A) the payer has not carried out a transaction without notifying the tax authority of the reason for 12 consecutive months, (b) the payer has failed to fulfil his obligations under Act No 235 / 2004 Coll., (c) the payer ceases to be a taxable person.
(B) Plants who do not have a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic A person registered for tax in another Member State who does not have a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic, or a foreign taxable person who carries out a transaction with a place of supply in the Czech Republic and is liable to declare and pay tax on that transaction pursuant to Section 108 of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll. (The so-called "non-established payer"), becomes a payer on the date on which the transaction takes place.
This person is required to submit an application for registration to the Tax Office for Prague 1 no later than the date of performance.
She is required to include in her registration application all the VAT numbers she has been assigned in other Member States or in a third country.
If the "non-established" payer applies for registration later than the date of the first taxable transaction in the Czech Republic, the Tax Office for Prague 1 will register it retroactively because according to Act No. 235 / 2004 Coll. the tax entity became a VAT payer on the date of the first taxable transaction in the Czech Republic.
Upon retroactive registration, the Tax Office for Prague 1 requires tax entities to provide proof that the transaction has been carried out (invoices or explanatory letters).
If a "non-established" tax entity applies for registration in the Czech Republic before the first taxable transaction takes place, then the Tax Office for Prague 1 requests the submission of contracts that the transaction will take place.
As of 31 December 2004, 473 "non-established" payers were registered at the Tax Office for Prague 1, 124 of them from Germany, and as of 31 December 2005, 951 "non-established" payers were registered, 233 of them from Germany.
Under the provisions of Section 106 (9) of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll. the tax authority is entitled to cancel the registration of a "non-established" payer on 31 January of the following calendar year if that payer has not incurred any obligation to declare and pay the tax during the current calendar year.
An audit by the SAO found that if a "non-established" payer files a tax return abroad for postal transport on 25 January, i.e. in accordance with the legal regulations by the deadline for filing a tax return, it is often not yet available to the tax office on 31 January.
In cases where the facts relevant to the possibility of deregistration are known to the tax office later than 31 January, it is no longer possible in the Czech Republic to cancel the VAT registration of a "non-established" payer in a given calendar year.
Registration of payers in Germany
In view of the legal provisions of the German Tax Code (Paragraphs 137, 138 of the Abgabenordnung, "the AO"), anyone carrying on a business activity is required to inform the municipal / municipal authority or the competent tax authority.
The deadline for submitting information is one month after the start of the business.
This information is processed by the municipal / municipal tax office.
If the tax office identifies an enterprise that has started operations but has not registered, the competent tax office can register the payer ex officio - even retroactively.
Taxpayers who are both resident and non-resident taxpayers in Germany are required by law to register for VAT if they meet the criteria set out in Section 2 of the German VAT Act ("USTG").
That obligation does not depend on the amount of turnover they make.
There is no voluntary VAT registration in Germany.
There are special tax offices for entrepreneurs living abroad.
For example, for those based in the Czech Republic, the competent tax office is Chemnitz-Süd.
As of 30 April 2004, a total of 295 Czech entrepreneurs were registered at the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office; as of 1 March 2006, a total of 1050 Czech entrepreneurs were registered.
The BRH found that these special tax authorities often refused to register so-called semi-dependent independent workers based in the new eastern EU Member States.
As the work permits of employees from the ten new EU Member States are limited after their accession to the EU, these independent workers have tried to avoid these restrictions by starting a business.
These businesses do not meet the criteria for entrepreneurs set out in Section 2 of the USTG because they are usually dependent on a single employer to determine their working hours and the way in which they perform their work.
In order to register, the entrepreneur must complete a questionnaire from the relevant tax office, in which he must provide information about the company and the activities it carries out.
The questionnaire is a standard form that is binding on all tax authorities in Germany.
It is processed either by special departments of the tax authorities or by general departments, which are responsible for the assessment of taxpayers.
This form carries out a risk assessment of individual taxpayers before the tax office issues a tax number.
The structure of the tax number for domestic transactions is governed by certain rules:
The first three digits provide information about the relevant tax office, the next three (or four) provide information about the relevant department at the tax office, the next five (or four) are to distinguish the payers, the last being always the check-digit.
If a trader intends to engage in intra-Community trade, he needs a VAT identification number (VAT ID) in order to receive an exempt intra-Community supply.
Customs will assign a VAT ID at the request of the entrepreneur if the entrepreneur is registered in Germany and if he has a VAT number.
VAT ID is automatically allocated to businesses when payers declare intra-Community supplies in their VAT return.
The VAT ID structure is a country code (DE) followed by a series of nine digits.
The registration of an entrepreneur may be cancelled: 1. at his request (for example, if he has ceased his business activities), after all administrative work has been carried out (assessment for all business years) and 2. if the tax administration realises that he is no longer engaged in business activities.
The validity of a VAT identification number is usually linked to the validity of a VAT tax number.
In such cases, the tax authorities are obliged to inform the CLO of the cancellation of the tax number so that the CLO can terminate the VAT identification number.
Under the German VAT Act (Section 19 (1) of the USTG), tax residents in Germany are not required to pay VAT if 1. the turnover plus the relevant VAT of the previous calendar year does not exceed EUR 17 500 and 2. in the following year it is not likely to exceed EUR 50 000.
So-called small businesses ("Kleinunternehmer") are not entitled to invoice other businesses for VAT and do not have the right to deduct input tax.
Although they are not required to pay VAT, small businesses must be registered with the tax office and must submit an annual VAT return.
A small business may declare that it will not apply Paragraph 19 (1) of the USTG.
That declaration is binding on him for the next five years.
The trader can then invoice the VAT and deduct the input tax.
It is possible for non-residents to appoint tax representatives (Section 22a of the USTG).
It is a prerequisite that they carry out exclusively exempt commercial transactions and do not have the right to deduct input tax.
The function of a tax representative is to fulfil the tax obligations of a foreign entrepreneur, who does not have to register for VAT.
The invoices must include information on representation for tax purposes.
Comparison and evaluation
The situation is different in both countries.
While in Germany entrepreneurs are registered regardless of the amount of their turnover, in the Czech Republic the primary criterion (among others) for registration is exceeding the limit set in the VAT Act.
If the tax entity in the Czech Republic does not exceed the limit, it has the option to apply for VAT registration on a voluntary basis.
The registration process is standardized in Germany, but differences can occur as a result of different organizational models in federal states.
In the Czech Republic, the payer is assigned a VAT number at the time of his first registration for any tax.
If the payer registers for VAT, he also uses the same VAT number for intra-Community transactions.
In Germany, when registering for VAT, the payer is assigned a tax number, which is used only for commercial transactions in the territory of Germany.
If the German payer intends to carry out intra-community transactions, he must apply for a special identification number, the so-called VAT ID.
As the SAO and BRH have discovered, the German two-tier registration system can cause many misunderstandings in other Member States, such as the Czech Republic, which allocates a single identification number for national VAT registration and registration for intra-community transactions.
On the other hand, the two-tier system allows for retroactive (national) registration in cases where payers refuse to inform the municipality or the relevant tax authority about their business.
This retroactive registration allows the correct assessment of VAT for the previous tax year, in particular an accurate estimate of the VAT liability.
As different registration methods cause problems, conditions should be balanced across the EU.
The German Parliament recently decided to introduce a tax identification number (TIN).
The Federal Tax Office will allocate the TIN at the birth of a natural person.
This TIN will be valid for the entire life of a German resident.
If a natural person starts a business, the relevant tax office will apply for an economic TIN to be used as a VAT ID.
In the future, there should be no delay between the national registration of the payer and the allocation of VAT ID.
Work on the introduction of an IT resource to manage the TIN has not yet been completed.
International passenger transport by bus
Legislation in the Czech Republic
According to the provisions of Section 70 of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll. with effect from 1 May 2004, the transport of persons between individual Member States and also between Member States and third countries in the Czech Republic is exempt from VAT with the right to deduct.
Such transport is exempt from VAT even if it is carried out by a trader who is registered for tax in other Member States or by a foreign taxable person.
The return service is considered to be a separate service.
If "non-established" tax entities in the Czech Republic do not carry out any economic activity other than international bus passenger transport, they are not obliged to register as VAT payers in the Czech Republic.
International passenger transport was exempted from VAT in the Czech Republic under the Act of Accession of the Czech Republic, Annex V, Chapter 5, paragraph 1, point (b), which states:
"For the purposes of Article 28 (3) (b) of Directive 77 / 388 / EEC, the Czech Republic may continue the exemption from value added tax for international passenger transport referred to in point 17 of Annex F to the Directive until the condition laid down in Article 28 (4) of the Directive is met or the same exemption is applied by an existing Member State, whichever is the earlier."
Description of the legislation in Germany
According to Article 46 of Council Directive 2006 / 112 / EC of 28 November 2006, implemented in Section 3b (1) of the German VAT Act, the place of supply of passenger transport (i.e. transport services) is the route (i.e. the place) where the transport takes place.
Therefore, the German tax system does not distinguish between domestic and international cross-border passenger transport.
Only that part of the route which takes place in Germany constitutes a taxable supply of transport in Germany.
The German tax system also makes no distinction between residents and non-residents.
If a non-resident taxpayer transports passengers through Germany, the part of the route that takes place in Germany also constitutes a taxable supply of transport.
A non-resident taxpayer must declare his intention to provide passenger transport to the relevant tax office before performing his services in Germany.
The tax office registers this non-resident taxpayer for tax purposes (cf. 4.1.2) and issues a special certificate for any bus or coach that is mentioned in the taxpayer's notification.
The taxpayer is required to declare his taxable supplies of transport in the German VAT return.
As of 1 March 2006, the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office registered 741 Czech payers who were in the passenger transport business.
Where passenger transport is provided to a resident taxpayer who is liable for VAT, the non-resident taxpayer does not have to pay VAT to the tax office himself.
Instead, the entity liable to pay the VAT to the tax office and the net amount invoiced to the non-resident taxpayer is the resident taxpayer receiving the services, a process known as "reverse charge" and in accordance with Article 196 of Council Directive 2006 / 112 / EC.
In addition to the notification of the non-resident and his VAT return, the German tax authorities have several means of assessing the accuracy of the declared taxable supplies of passenger transport.
The customs office's mobile control groups audit the certification of buses licensed for foreign transport, which are used to transport passengers through Germany.
After each audit, the mobile control groups send an audit report to the relevant tax office.
If the bus driver does not have a valid certificate, the mobile control group is entitled to claim VAT from the bus driver before continuing with the next transport.
A non-resident taxpayer may deduct the VAT thus paid from the tax calculated in his VAT return.
If the tax office has doubts about the accuracy of the VAT return, it may announce its intention to carry out an audit, which must be carried out at the tax office, or it may use the means of administrative cooperation referred to in Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003 (see 4.6).
Even if a non-resident taxpayer refuses to pay the amount of VAT charged in accordance with its statutory rate, the tax office may request administrative cooperation under Council Directive 76 / 308 / EEC.
In order to carry out a review of the VAT return or the performance of the non-resident's tax obligations, BRH considers all these means of administrative cooperation to be too labour-intensive compared to the small amounts of VAT to be paid for taxable supplies of passenger transport.
In particular, auditing the accounts of a non-resident taxpayer generates disproportionate costs for both the taxpayer and the tax administration.
The tax administration must carry out an audit of foreign accounting, which means not only the need for knowledge of a foreign language, but also familiarity with foreign accounting standards.
An audit of this type is also likely to take more time than an audit of a tax resident, but this audit is limited to the provision of passenger transport that takes place in Germany.
On the other hand, a non-resident taxpayer does not only have to accept the right to carry out an inspection, which is the responsibility of his national tax administration, but also the right to have an audit carried out by other Member States in which he carries passengers.
In addition, in each Member State in which only one provision of passenger transport takes place, the taxpayer is obliged to fulfil all the tax obligations applicable to him in those Member States, in all the languages and on all the tax forms of those Member States.
The actual taxation of cross-border passenger transport therefore entails disproportionate bureaucratic costs.
Comparison and evaluation
The legal situation in the two countries is different.
In the Czech Republic, passenger transport between individual EU Member States or between Member States and third countries is exempt from VAT with the right to deduct under the Act of Accession of the Czech Republic.
In Germany, the part of the transport which takes place in Germany is a taxable transaction.
If this transport is provided for the first time in Germany by a non-established payer, he is obliged to notify the competent tax office in advance of the provision of the transport.
The tax office registers the payer and the payer is obliged to declare in Germany the taxable supplies of part of the transport in the tax return.
The implementation of the law is very time-consuming in Germany.
At least three of the four Czech payers registered with the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office are in the passenger transport business.
Compared to the effort, the tax revenue, if realised, is rather low.
Member States which collect VAT in accordance with Article 46 of Council Directive 2006 / 112 / EC of 28 November 2006 on the common system of VAT shall be subject to time-consuming obligations without a financially sensitive result.
In order to avoid disproportionate costs for charging VAT, the provision of cross-border passenger transport should be taxed in only one Member State.
This could be the state where the transport begins or where the provider is based.
Such taxation would require the adaptation of Council Directive 2006 / 112 / EC.
VAT returns
Filing and processing of VAT returns in the Czech Republic
The payer is obliged to submit a VAT return on a form prescribed by the Ministry of Finance within 25 days of the end of the tax year, even if he has not incurred tax liability, unless otherwise provided by law.
The actual tax liability is due within the deadline for filing the VAT return, with the exception of the tax charged in connection with the import of goods pursuant to Section 20 of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll., for which the tax is due according to the customs regulations.
If there is a refundable overpayment as a result of the over-deduction, the payer shall be returned without request within 30 days of the over-deduction.
The time limit does not apply in cases where the tax authority initiates tax proceedings concerning the taxpayer's tax liability.
In accordance with the provisions of Section 73 (11) of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll., the right to deduct may be exercised in the ordinary VAT return at the latest for the last tax year of the calendar year in which the right to deduct could be exercised.
After that period, the right to deduct may continue to be exercised within three years of the end of the tax year in which the right to deduct could have been exercised at the earliest.
However, this is only possible through the submission of an additional VAT return.
The amendment to Act No 235 / 2004 Coll., effective from 1 January 2005, allows the submission of an additional VAT return only for the period when the right to deduct could be exercised for the first time.
The payer is obliged to submit an additional VAT return if (a) by aggregating the corrections he increases the tax liability, (b) he makes a correction which does not change the last known tax liability, but only the data previously claimed by the taxpayer, (c) he makes a correction to the rate and amount of tax pursuant to Section 49 of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll.
The payer may submit an additional VAT return if, by aggregating the corrections, he reduces the tax liability.
The payer is required to submit an additional VAT return by the end of the month following the discovery of these facts.
The submission of VAT returns in electronic form can be made either via the Internet or on a technical data medium.
Internet submission can be made as a submission with a data message accompanied by an advanced electronic signature or as a submission with a data message not accompanied by an advanced electronic signature.
In the case of a submission with a data message not accompanied by a guaranteed electronic signature, a written submission is still required, i.e. the delivery of the computer report to the tax authorities (e-form).
The VAT return contains separate lines concerning the values of intra-Community supplies / acquisitions of goods.
The values of the acquisition of services are recorded on the separate lines of the VAT return.
Some lines are used for the purpose of the initial automated control within ADIS.
The values of supplies of goods to other Member States to taxable persons registered in other Member States shall be compared with the data contained in the recapitulative statements submitted by Czech taxpayers.
The values of acquisitions of goods from other Member States from taxable persons registered in other Member States shall be compared to those obtained through VIES from recapitulative statements of payers from other EU Member States.
The tax office is conducting a test of the credibility of VAT returns under the ADIS system.
This test is carried out automatically, as VAT returns cannot be assessed without a test.
The credibility test includes the calculation of credibility criteria and the evaluation of risk types of VAT returns.
According to the provisions of Section 37 (1) of Act No 337 / 1992 Coll. the tax office can repeatedly impose a fine of up to CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) on a person who fails to comply with an obligation of a non-pecuniary nature arising from this or a special tax law, or imposed by a decision pursuant to this law, within a specified period.
An automated tax information system used by the tax authorities to provide technical support to the tax administration.
The SAO audit found that the tax authorities mostly did not use the option to impose a fine on taxpayers for not filing a VAT return.
Submission and processing of VAT returns in Germany
In Germany, we distinguish between a preliminary monthly or quarterly VAT return and an annual VAT return.
Those taxpayers who are required to submit preliminary VAT returns must still submit an annual VAT return.
Even small businesses who are not required to pay VAT have to submit an annual tax return.
As a general rule, taxpayers are required to submit a quarterly VAT return by the 10th day of the month following the quarter in which VAT is incurred (Section 18 (2) USTG).
However, if the VAT liability exceeds EUR 6 136 in the previous calendar year, or if it is a newly created business, the trader concerned is required to submit a monthly VAT return by the 10th day of the following month.
A taxpayer may also choose to submit a monthly VAT return if there has been a refund in the past year that exceeds EUR 6 136 (Section 18 (2a) USTG).
VAT returns do not have to be submitted if the annual VAT does not exceed EUR 512.
The relevant amount of VAT must be paid by the 10th day of the month following the tax year in which the VAT was incurred.
The refund may lead to an even more detailed investigation by the FO.
There are no time limits (according to the law) for the processing of tax returns and the refund of excess VAT.
In order to obtain a timely refund, it is possible to offer security for the amount to be refunded.
The basic principle is to process the VAT returns and return the tax quickly.
The German VAT Act provides for the possibility of extending that period (Paragraph 18 (6) USTG).
Such an extension should be requested separately.
It allows you to submit a VAT return and pay the relevant VAT liability one month later, provided that a special advance is paid in the case of a monthly return.
This advance payment will be offset against the December VAT liability.
Whenever an error is detected, the trader must submit a corrective VAT return.
There is no additional VAT return.
Once the annual VAT return, which must be submitted by 31 May of the following calendar year, is registered with the tax office, the trader cannot correct the incorrect preliminary tax return, but only the annual VAT return.
A correction of the annual VAT return to the benefit or disadvantage of the payer is possible within the next 4 years after the year in which the first annual VAT return was submitted.
After these four years, the annual VAT return can normally be corrected only in cases of tax fraud or evasion.
Payers are required to submit their preliminary VAT returns electronically.
The tax authorities may apply exceptions to this rule to avoid excessive hardship.
The annual VAT return can be submitted on paper or via the Internet, with or without certification.
If it is carried out without certification, payers must submit a return once more on paper with personal signatures.
In the event that the taxpayer does not submit a VAT return, the tax administration is entitled to make a rough estimate of the taxpayer's turnover.
In the event of late submission, a penalty payment may be imposed on the payer (up to a maximum of 10% of the tax to be paid or EUR 25 000).
During a previous inspection, BRH found that the tax authorities often did not measure this standard fine.
In other cases where the tax authorities have imposed a fine, the amount has been assessed inconsistently and arbitrarily.
The standard fine therefore falls short of its objective of reducing the average delay, especially when filing an annual VAT return.
The VAT return contains separate lines relating to the values of intra-Community supplies / acquisitions of goods.
The values of the acquisition of services are recorded on the separate lines of the VAT return.
Non-taxable transactions must be reported on a separate line of the VAT return.
In the case of VAT returns which are submitted on paper, a copy must be made either through a scanner or by staff specifically authorised to do so.
The data from the VAT returns submitted electronically is immediately available to the tax office official.
Once all the data has been entered into the system, RMS staff will go through it and select cases that meet certain criteria.
The VAT returns collected must be checked by an official of the tax office on the basis of an inspection report prepared by the system.
(See section 5.2).
Although the tax administration has to make a rough estimate of the amount of VAT that the taxpayer has to pay, the estimated tax has to be as precise as possible.
Comparison and evaluation
In the Czech Republic, taxpayers submit VAT returns within 25 days of the end of the tax year.
The tax year is either a calendar quarter or a calendar month, depending on the amount of the payer's turnover.
In Germany, taxpayers submit preliminary VAT returns, depending on the tax liability in the previous year, either within 10 days of the end of the calendar quarter or month.
By 31 May of the following year, taxpayers are required to submit an annual tax return.
The obligation to submit an annual VAT return has its pros and cons:
+ at the end of the calendar year, the payer is able to correct errors in the (monthly provisional) tax returns by submitting a single annual VAT return;
- if the payer corrects the declared intra-Community transactions, the correction cannot be related to the reporting period;
- The Länder do not usually compare VIES data on intra-Community purchases by German payers before the annual VAT return is processed.
In accordance with the registration (see 4.1.3), German taxpayers are required to submit an annual VAT return, regardless of their turnover.
This obligation allows the German tax authority to examine the maximum turnover limit for small businesses.
In addition, the responsible tax office is able to compare annual VAT returns with direct tax returns and closing accounts.
In the Czech Republic, tax authorities are only able to determine the amount of the payer's turnover from filed income tax returns.
Unlike the Czech Republic, taxpayers in Germany are obliged to submit VAT returns in electronic form.
The introduction of an obligation to submit tax returns electronically in the Czech Republic would contribute to improving the efficiency of the Czech tax administration.
Summary reports
Submission and processing of summary reports in the Czech Republic
The recapitulative statement (hereinafter referred to as "SH") is submitted pursuant to the provisions of Section 102 of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll. by a payer who has made a supply of goods to another Member State to a taxable person registered in another Member State.
Data on the value of the goods delivered are always presented in Czech currency, broken down by individual tax entities, with their VAT ID, under which they are registered in their country.
Data on services provided are not included in the SH.
SH is submitted by payers with both monthly and quarterly tax periods for each calendar quarter within 25 days of the end of the period to the local tax office.
The correction of incorrect data shall be carried out in the subsequent SH within 15 days of the date of detection of the errors.
The incorrect information given in the SH is always replaced by the information given in the subsequent SH.
As well as tax returns, payers can also submit SH in electronic form.
In the event that the payer does not file an SH or subsequent SH and should have filed it under Act No 235 / 2004 Coll., the tax authority will invite him to file it and at the same time instruct him about the consequences in the event of failure to file an SH or subsequent SH, i.e. that the tax authority is entitled under Section 37 of Act No 337 / 1992 Coll. to repeatedly impose a fine of up to CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) for failure to fulfil obligations of a non-monetary nature.
The SAO audit found that the tax authorities mostly did not use the possibility to impose a fine on payers for failing to comply with their legal obligations.
In particular, in the case of filing an SH, tax entities do not have a sufficient incentive to fulfil their obligations, as the failure to file an SH does not affect the VAT liability.
Under Section 102 (5) of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll. the tax authority is obliged to check the data in the SH, or in the subsequent SH, to remove any ambiguities and to use the data to determine the tax liability.
In the event of a discrepancy between the data in the SH and the data in the relevant (payers with a monthly tax year) or relevant (payers with a quarterly tax year) VAT return, the tax authority should verify the accuracy of the declared tax liability in the VAT return.
Erroneous data in the SH is removed by the taxpayer himself by filing a subsequent SH, or he may be asked to do so.
The tax authority shall correct the data on supplies of goods to other Member States in the ADIS system in the event that:
- the payer fails to prove the information given in the SH (or subsequent SH) and corrects it by administering a subsequent SH;
- the tax authority has proved that the information provided by the payer in the SH or subsequent SH is not true.
By inserting a correction without submitting a subsequent SH, the tax authority does not replace the taxpayer's submission, it merely adjusts the data in the VIES database so that it is up-to-date, complete and accurate.
The SH data shall be sent to the Member States concerned.
They can only be sent and received by the national tax authority, designated for cooperation with other Member States in the field of VAT; this is the CLO (in the Czech Republic, this function is performed by the Ministry of Finance, the Department of International Cooperation in the Administration of VAT (CLO).
O _ MCTL is an automatic message that CLO receives from other Member States.
Contains all the wrong VAT IDs listed in the sent SH lines.
If the wrong VAT ID is used in one of the transmitted normal SH lines or the subsequent SH, an entry is made in the table of the wrong VAT ID.
The table contains the so-called "Notice of Doubt on VAT ID."
The tax authority checks the data and records the result of the verification in the system.
When acquiring goods from another Member State, the payer is required to declare the VAT and to indicate the values of the acquisition on separate lines of the VAT return.
Selected cases of irregularities in the value of purchased goods declared by the Czech payer in his VAT return and in the value of delivered goods, as declared by payers from other Member States in their SH, are sent from the CLO to the tax office for examination.
The tax authorities have a duty to investigate irregularities.
There may be three situations:
(A) The value declared by the Czech payer in the relevant lines of VAT returns is lower than the value of the supply declared by EU payers.
In this case, the tax authorities will verify the accuracy of the data.
(B) The difference is 0.
This situation can occur either by changing the data in the EU (the foreign supplier corrects its SH) or by changing the data in the VAT return (the Czech tax entity itself will submit an additional VAT return in the meantime).
In this case, it is at the discretion of the tax authorities whether, despite this, they will verify the accuracy of the data in the VAT return.
(C) The value of the acquisition of goods from other Member States, which the Czech taxpayer stated in the relevant lines of the VAT return, is higher than the value of the goods delivered declared by EU payers.
Here, too, it is at the discretion of the controller to verify the accuracy of the data.
After examining the difference and explaining the reasons for it, the tax authority will enter the result of the verification in the ADIS.
The results of the screening are transmitted back to the CLO.
The number of cases sent from the CLO to the tax authorities for examination for each quarter of 2005 is shown in Chart 1 (NB: MF).
Chart 1 above shows that the number of cases referred from CLO to the tax authorities decreased in the quarters of 2005.
There was a significant drop in the number in the fourth quarter of 2005. The duty increased the minimum threshold, including with regard to the possibility of sending requests for information to other EU Member States.
The discrepancy between VAT return data and EU data may not always be due to an error on the part of the domestic payer.
It may also be an error on the part of EU payers or an error due to the fact that in individual EU Member States some types of transactions may be entered in the SH in different ways.
The most common reasons for discrepancies in the values of reported transactions found at the audited tax offices are shown in Table 1.
Submission and processing of summary reports in Germany
Entrepreneurs who carry out intra-community deliveries from Germany to other EU Member States or engage in triangular transactions are required to submit quarterly SH, which lists intra-community deliveries by recipient (Section 18a (1) USTG).
Sh must be submitted by the 10th day of the month following the corresponding calendar quarter.
If an extension of this period is granted in the case of preliminary VAT returns, the same applies to SH.
Sh must be supplied by CLO.
From 1 January 2007, they must be submitted electronically.
Exemptions may be granted by the competent tax authorities to certain taxpayers in order to avoid undue hardship.
In cases where taxpayers are aware that incorrect information is included in the SH, they are required to submit a corrective report within one month.
In the event that taxpayers do not file an SH, the CLO will initiate proceedings to enforce the submission of such a report.
This procedure includes: - the first reminder - the second reminder linked to the threat of a fine / periodic penalty payment and - the imposition of a penalty payment.
Although the German Tax Code allows fines of up to EUR 25 000 to be imposed (Section 329 AO), the CLO imposes fines in three steps, amounting to EUR 125, 250 and 500.
In addition, Paragraph 26a (1) No 5 of the USTG provides that payers are to act unlawfully if, intentionally or negligently, they fail to properly file an SH, file it incomplete, file it on time, or if they fail to correct or correct it late at all.
This offence can be punishable by a fine of up to EUR 5 000.
Data on intra-Community supplies cannot be entered into VIES by the tax office, as processing SH is the exclusive task of the CLO.
Sh data is only stored in the CLO system.
The data from SH is therefore only visually available to the tax office after it has been processed into CLO.
The time limits for processing SH are laid down in Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003.
SH data must be stored within three months of the calendar quarter in question.
In case of incorrect VAT IDs in the SH of German payers, CLOs from another Member State will receive the O _ MCTL codes.
Customs will contact a specific trader and ask him for the correct information.
If the CLO fails to obtain the correct information, the case is referred to the relevant tax authorities.
It is then up to these tax authorities to ask for the correct data.
During the inspection, BRH found that most of the entrepreneurs had corrected the VAT ID at the request of CLO.
However, the challenge, the threat and the imposition of three additional fines takes up too much time in cases where the payer may be involved in cross-border carousel fraud.
These cases, which were eventually reported to the relevant tax authorities, were usually completed within one or two months.
In 73% of these cases, the Tax Office refused to exempt declared intra-Community supplies.
When the payer provided the correct VAT ID, the tax office asked him to file a corrected SH with the CLO, as the tax authorities could not correct the VIES data themselves.
BRH found that neither the tax authorities nor CLO had checked the submission of the corrected SH, so payers often did not comply with the request.
Due to the fact that the CLO does not have access to the VAT return data, the comparison of the supply data declared in the VAT return and in the SH will not take place before these data are submitted to the CLO of the other Member States.
This control can only be carried out by the tax authorities and is usually used in the preparation of the VAT control.
Data collected from other Member States are processed into CLOs.
Incorrect VAT IDs are selected and then submitted to the relevant Member States.
These data are used for the purposes of the control of acquisitions by the tax authorities.
Once they are entered into the system, the CLO checks them against data from previous calendar quarters.
If they meet certain criteria (see 5.2), control information is created and sent to the relevant tax authorities.
This procedure is applied on a permanent basis, while the compilation of data on the acquisition of goods or services for all VAT payers is produced at a later stage and submitted to the tax authorities.
The RMS installed for the purpose of the assessment procedure will then check these data with the data on the intra-Community acquisitions.
This system fully covers those businesses who do not have the full right to deduct VAT.
Comparison and evaluation
In the Czech Republic, payers who have made a supply of goods to another Member State to a person registered for tax in another Member State submit SH within 25 days of the end of the calendar quarter to the local tax office.
The tax authorities process the SH and transfer the data to the CLO.
The values of the supply of goods to another Member State, indicated by the payers in SH, are compared at the tax offices with the values of the supply of goods to another Member State, indicated by those payers in their VAT returns.
The results of the comparison are used in the assessment procedure.
In Germany, payers who have made intra-Community deliveries are required to submit quarterly SH by the 10th day of the following calendar quarter.
Sh payers submit to CLO, from 1 January 2007 in electronic form.
The tax authorities only have the information from SH after it has been processed into CLO.
Payers from the Czech Republic and Germany only mention the supply of goods in SH, the provision of services is not mentioned in SH.
Unlike the Czech tax authorities, the German tax authorities are not able to correct the wrong lines submitted by SH on their own.
As a result of this limited access to data from the German VIES system, the faulty VAT ID was not corrected, even though the payer provided the correct VAT ID to the FO.
The German tax authorities do not compare the data on intra-Community supplies contained in the VAT return of the German payer and his SH.
The differences between the data of these two statements are not usually detected before the German CLO provides data from VIES to other Member States.
In view of the BRH findings, it is clear that the comparison would increase the reliability of the data transmitted in VIES.
Data on the supply of goods to Czech payers, delivered from other Member States, are compared in the Czech Republic with data on the acquisition of goods from other Member States declared by Czech payers in their VAT returns.
The comparison is carried out by the CLO separately for each calendar quarter.
The most significant cases of irregularities are passed on to the tax authorities as a warning of possible errors in taxpayers' tax returns.
Unlike the Czech tax administration, the German tax administration does not normally control the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions.
Such a general check is carried out only for taxpayers who do not have the full right to deduct VAT.
In addition, the German tax authority controls the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions by other taxpayers only if the RMS produces a warning or if the payer is designated for inspection anyway.
This procedure relieves the tax authorities from having to explain the reasons for any difference.
On the other hand, detection of VAT fraud depends on the quality of the RMS.
The fight against carousel fraud requires continuously updated information on intra-Community acquisitions as soon as possible.
The current SH system, specifically VIES, provides financial authorities with information that can be up to six months old.
This delay can be reduced by up to four months if payers submit SH monthly.
Monthly filing would not be a significant increase in bureaucratic costs, as most taxpayers in the Czech Republic and Germany are required to submit monthly VAT returns - and SH does not require any additional information compared to the tax return.
In order to avoid bureaucratic costs, filing an SH may involve filing a VAT return.
However, an obligation to administer SH monthly would cause more time mismatches between the reporting of intra-community delivery and intra-community acquisition and could increase the flow of data between CLOs.
In 2006, the German Federal Government considered a general provision for monthly SH's.
Its implementation failed due to doubts from the federal states.
They were concerned that monthly submissions from VIES to other Member States' CLOs could lead to misunderstandings and confusion.
In fact, if the monthly SH submission obligation and the monthly data transmission were to be effective, a monthly update of VIES would require a European standard of monthly SH.
Statistics on the supply and acquisition of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany
In the context of foreign trade, Germany is the most important trading partner for the Czech Republic.
The total volumes of intra-community transactions in goods between the Czech Republic and Germany are shown in Table 2.
