These figures are set out in the following tables.
The data show significant differences.
These differences may be due to different bases for determining the number of O _ MCTL messages.
While the Czech CLO refers their numbers to the calendar quarter for which the SH was submitted, the German CLO refers their numbers to the calendar quarter in which the O _ MCTL report was received.
Level 3 international exchange of information
Implementation of international exchange of information in the Czech Republic
The international exchange of information allows tax administrations to obtain information from other Member States concerning intra-Community commercial transactions and the payers who have carried out such transactions.
Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing Regulation (EEC) No 218 / 92 distinguishes between two basic categories of exchange of information, namely the exchange of information upon request and the exchange of information without prior request.
The international exchange of information upon request takes the form of so-called "Requests for Information" (hereinafter referred to as "JOI"), using standardised SCAC forms.
The tax authorities from the Czech Republic send their ŽOI or replies to the received ŽOI via the financial directorates to the CLO, which ensures the translation of the information provided on the standardised SCAC forms into a foreign language and their dispatch to other Member States.
Customs also ensures the receipt of Rus from other Member States and replies to sent Rus, their translation into Czech and distribution to the local tax authorities for processing.
Article 8 of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003 sets a maximum time limit of 3 months from receipt of the application for the processing of an EOI.
All ŽOI submitted during the audited period between the Czech Republic and Germany were audited by the SAO.
Out of a total of 94 ŽOI received from Germany in the Czech Republic, 70 cases (i.e. 74.5%) were dealt with within the stipulated three-month period, another 23 cases (i.e. 24.5%) were dealt with after this period and the remaining 1 case had not received a reply to Germany by the time of the SAO audit.
Chart 2 contains more detailed information on the deadlines by which replies to the ŽOI received from Germany were sent from the Czech Republic.
Out of a total of 335 ŽOI sent from the Czech Republic to Germany, 136 cases (i.e. 40.6%) received a reply within the stipulated three-month deadline, another 179 (i.e. 53.4%) requests were answered after this deadline and 19 cases (i.e. 5.7%) had not received a reply from Germany by the time of the SAO audit (in the remaining 1 case, it was not possible to determine from the submitted data when the reply from Germany was received).
Graph 3 contains more detailed information on the deadlines within which the replies to the ŽOI sent to Germany were received in the Czech Republic.
The percentage of the values of intra-community transactions reported in ŽOI transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany is shown in Graph 4.
As can be seen from the graph above, the value of the commercial transactions examined through the JOI was most often in the range above EUR 60 000.
The international exchange of information without prior request takes the form of either automatic or structured automatic exchange of information or spontaneous exchange of information.
Tax administrations from other Member States are often provided with information without prior request which may be of interest to them in the management of VAT.
In the Czech Republic, all information is collected at the CLO.
The information shall be transmitted electronically between the Member States.
"Automatic exchange," according to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003, means the systematic communication of pre-determined information to other Member States, without prior request and at pre-established regular intervals.
"Structured automatic exchange" means the systematic communication of pre-determined information to other Member States, without prior request and as soon as the information is available.
The Czech Republic provides other Member States with information on the delivery of new means of transport in the form of automatic exchange.
This information is available to the tax authorities from the form Notification of the supply of a new means of transport pursuant to Section 19 of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll. and from a copy of the tax document issued.
When processing the above form, the tax authority fills in the necessary data in a specially created template and forwards it in turn to a contact officer at the tax directorate, where the data are collected and transmitted to the CLO for subsequent processing and transmission to other Member States within a specified deadline, i.e. no later than two months after the end of the quarter in which the information was available.
In addition, the Czech Republic provides other Member States with information on mail order sales, which are exempt from VAT in the Member State of origin, information on intra-EU transactions, which appears to be unjustified, and information on potential "missing traders."
That information shall be sent to other Member States by spontaneous exchange using the SCAC form.
Implementation of the international exchange of information in Germany
In Germany, both requests for information and the processing of spontaneous information are initiated by the local tax authority.
The tax authorities send the completed SCAC 2004 form directly to the German CLO, which forwards the SCAC forms to the foreign CLO.
The tax authorities have been instructed to write their requests for information or their own spontaneous information only in German; even the SCAC form used is not multilingual.
Half of the German requests for information, checked by the BRH, were sent in order to ensure the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions in another Member State, or to prove the exemption of intra-Community supplies from Germany to another Member State.
If the German CLO receives a request for information from another Member State, it will check the value of the supply of goods or services referred to in the request for a minimum limit of EUR 15 000.
If there is no reasonable reason for such a request, the German CLO will reject any request containing an amount below the limit.
In addition, the German CLO translates the free texts of the SCAC form [(B1-17) or (E)] if these texts are not in German or English.
In order to respond to a request for information, the CLO sends the request to the relevant tax office with a reference to the three-month deadline.
There are no further deadlines for processing applications at specific organisational levels of the tax administration.
Although the German CLO has the technical conditions to monitor past time limits, it lacks sufficient staffing capacity to alert the tax authorities when they respond to uncompleted requests for information.
The tax authorities obtain the necessary information by sending a letter to the taxpayer or by carrying out an audit.
Auditors usually choose between two different types of audit: A special VAT audit, which covers any taxable process over a period of several months, or a so-called VAT inspection, which can only relate to one business transaction that has been carried out recently.
This short and exportable type of audit does not require any notification to the taxpayer and has proven its usefulness in investigating individual taxable business transactions.
As part of the automatic exchange without prior request, the FRG provides other Member States with information - on VAT IDs allocated to payers resident in other Member States, - on input tax refunds to payers resident in other Member States.
In addition, the FRG undertook to provide the following information to other Member States through structured automatic exchange:
A. the supply of new means of transport to businesses without the use of their VAT ID, b. the sending or catalogue sale in other Member States which is not taxable in Germany, c. significant differences between intra-Community purchases declared by the payer and VIES data provided by other Member States, d. the intra-Community supply of goods which the German payer did not declare in SH because he treated the supplies as domestic transactions, e. a potential "missing trader" who carried out intra-Community transactions independently of the validity of their VAT ID, f. entrepreneurs who supplied goods to potential "missing traders" or to those recipients who misused their VAT ID.
Comparison and evaluation
The sending of ŽOI or spontaneous information is initiated both in the Czech Republic and in Germany by the local tax authorities, which send the completed SCAC form to the CLO.
While the Czech CLO uses the bilingual form SCAC (Czech - English) and translates the information sent into English and German respectively, the German tax authorities follow the instruction that they should write ŽOI or spontaneous information only in German on a monolingual form.
The German CLO does not provide for the translation of German texts.
An examination of the ŽOI submitted between 1 May 2004 and 31 December 2005 between the Czech Republic and Germany revealed that the Czech tax administration processed 74.5% of the received applications within the stipulated three-month period, while the ŽOI sent to Germany was processed by the German tax administration within the stipulated period in only 40.6% of cases.
Although the German CLO draws the attention of the tax authorities to the three-month period, it does not monitor the time periods that have elapsed.
The lack of warnings has resulted in a large number of delayed responses to the JOI.
Because of these problems, the BRH recommended that CLO be regularly alerted.
The situation has already improved.
According to the latest information from the German CLO, it is now alerting the tax authorities to respond to the incomplete answers to the JOI.
VAT risk management
Risk management in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, risk management in the area of VAT is handled by several departments at different organisational levels of the tax administration.
Within the Ministry of Finance, the following services deal with the issue of risk management and the fight against VAT fraud:
The Department of VAT Methodology and Performance and within it the report on VAT Risk Management, which, among other things, manages the selection of risks of possible tax evasion and evaluates trends of these risks at both domestic and Community level.
It coordinates the functioning of the role of credibility of VAT returns and the use of VIES data in terms of the risks of tax evasion in intra-Community transactions.
Based on data from the trade balance of the Czech Republic, it evaluates risky commodities, processes risk management in the area of VAT conceptually and cooperates in this area with the relevant EU institutions and with other Member States.
The Department of International Cooperation in the Administration of VAT, which, inter alia, ensures the exchange of information in the field of VAT, participates in the creation and maintenance of information databases, analyses data from other Member States contained in the VIES system, ensures public information and ensures other forms of international cooperation within the meaning of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003.
Both SAIs requested data on the number of erroneous TINs or VAT IDs contained in the O _ MCTL reports transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany for each quarter of the audited period.
These figures are set out in the following tables.
The data show significant differences.
These differences may be due to different bases for determining the number of O _ MCTL messages.
While the Czech CLO refers their numbers to the calendar quarter for which the SH was submitted, the German CLO refers their numbers to the calendar quarter in which the O _ MCTL report was received.
The Tax Control and Search Methodology Unit, which, among other things, carries out risk analysis in the framework of the methodological management of tax controls and, in accordance with the risk analysis, sets priorities for the targeting of tax controls in the plans of the financial directorates, carries out risk analyses in the context of the reduction of tax evasion, including the collection of lessons learned from tax administration and other sources, and proposes measures to reduce tax evasion.
In the financial directorates, search departments are set up to carry out, among other things, searches for tax entities and areas that are at risk from the occurrence of tax fraud (e.g. online shops, gold, pharmaceutical industry), searches for unregistered tax entities from the point of view of the risks of tax evasion (e.g. internet services, job matching, radio and print services, etc.), analysis of links between chain fraud and transmission of information to local and regional tax authorities.
Specialised control units are set up at the selected 12 tax offices.
They have a regional remit, they carry out tax checks outside the territorial remit of the tax authorities on the basis of a mandate.
The need to set up specialised tax inspection units has emerged as a result of increasing findings of new and improved forms of tax evasion, which occur mainly in entities linked to chains.
These departments focus on controlling tax entities according to the requirements of search departments, tax entities with a specific activity and multinational companies and tax entities with a large scale of activity in terms of turnover.
The following mechanisms have been integrated into ADIS to reduce VAT risks: - the role of Confidentiality of VAT returns, to assess the risk of tax returns submitted, - the role of Selection of tax entities for inspection, allowing the collection of payers for inspection on the basis of the chosen criteria, - the role of VIES, through which tax administrations have access to data provided from other EU Member States.
The role of VIES allows, inter alia: - to check the validity of VAT IDs of payers from other Member States, - to obtain from other Member States the values of goods delivered to the Czech payer, declared in SH by all its suppliers from other Member States, - to generate a set of payers who have not submitted SH, - to carry out a formal check of the data submitted by payers from the Czech Republic in SH before sending this data to other Member States, - to generate a set of payers for whom the data on supplies of goods to other Member States in VAT returns do not match the data in SH, - to generate a set of payers for whom the value of purchases of goods from other Member States in VAT returns does not match the data declared in SH by all its suppliers from other Member States.
As part of their activities to reduce the risks of tax evasion, tax authorities have access to registers of government bodies such as the Commercial Register, Land Registry, Motor Vehicle Register, Business Register, etc.
More detailed information can be found in chapter 4.4.1 Submission and processing of summary reports in the Czech Republic.
Risk management in Germany
Due to the federal (federal) structure of Germany, the federal tax administration (in particular CLO) and the tax administrations of the 16 federal states are involved in the development and operation of RMS.
Although there are joint development task forces, neither the CLO nor the federal tax administrations share a fully consistent database.
At CLO level, ST I 2 (hereinafter "Kuss" - the coordinating unit for special VAT audits and tax investigations) collects audit findings on tax fraud in a special database called the AACC.
Kuss, in cooperation with the tax authorities, has introduced a new database called Zauber, designed to transfer the names of tax evaders' "missing traders."
Kuss coordinates related cases of national and cross-border tax fraud.
The experience of Kuss is reflected in the development of RMS in working groups.
In addition, the specialists of several other departments of CLO and MF are entrusted with the duties and powers associated with RMS.
At CLO level, a formal check on the composition of VAT IDs of other Member States in SH submitted by German payers is in place.
This formal check is carried out before SH data is provided to other Member States, to improve the clarity and use of VIES data provided (see 4.4.2).
Verification of the validity of VAT IDs listed in the SH is carried out on the basis of O _ MCTL codes provided by other Member States (for the procedure for correcting invalid VAT IDs, see also 4.4.2).
In addition, the CLO RMS is based on VIES data transmitted by other Member States and produces several types of control reports based on several characteristics that typically feature in so-called carousel trading operations, in order to identify potential "missing traders."
Federal tax authorities are instructed to process these audit reports and, in some cases, to report the results of their CLO findings.
The findings of the BRH audit confirmed that it is necessary to take into account all available characteristics if a case of tax fraud (rather than focusing exclusively on the company's turnover) is to be assumed with sufficient probability.
BRH therefore proposed to the Ministry of Finance that different characteristics be taken into account in the processing of the reports.
The RMS should also sanction other facts, such as the taxpayer's payment behaviour (morality), industry (economic activities) or shareholder structure.
The second level of the RMS is processed in the tax administrations of the federal states and focuses on the processing of VAT returns.
For example, RMS generates a list of those taxpayers who have declared intra-Community supplies in their tax returns.
This list is sent to the CLO to monitor the full submission of SH.
In addition, this type of RMS compares intra-Community acquisitions reported in the payer's annual VAT return with VIES data.
Federal tax administrations try to avoid comparing quarterly data because such a comparison would reveal too much dissenting data that is attributed to reasons other than tax evasion or tax fraud; for example:
- the different duration of the intra-community transaction in the opinion of the supplier on the one hand and the beneficiary on the other;
- different accounting for sales discounts and sales promotions (incentives) and their different reporting in the tax return.
In addition to comparing VAT return and VIES data, many Länder have introduced RMS elements based on VAT return data and some other facts (such as company name structure, shareholder age, number of employees and taxpayer's payment behaviour / morale).
Bavaria has introduced a rules-based RMS that allows a team of tax fraud specialists ("risk managers") to program their own rules to single out potential tax evaders.
This RMS is applied when the tax authorities process the monthly VAT return.
The relevant tax authority will therefore receive a recommendation made by the RMS before VAT is determined.
As this RMS is not able to reflect current findings in its activities, risk managers have to adjust the relevant rules based on feedback from the tax authorities.
The administrative district of Mecklenburg-Western Pomerania has programmed an adaptive artificial neural network with data from tax files in which the inspection revealed tax evasion.
On the basis of these data, RMS is able to identify the characteristics of tax evasion.
Once a month, the RMS produces a list of tax files suspected of tax evasion.
This list is used by the relevant tax authorities as a basis for deciding on the audit of proposed taxpayers.
After the audit, the auditors have to report on their findings so that the results of the list can be reflected in the RMS.
The North Rhine-Westphalia administrative region uses an adaptive artificial neural network that is combined with a rules-based fuzzy system.
Based on a large number of data from assessed VAT returns and some other facts, this neuron-fuzzy system or system for collecting potentially useful information (the so-called data-mining system) calculates the probability that a particular taxpayer has committed tax fraud.
It then draws up a monthly list of potential fraudsters.
The local tax authorities use this list as a basis for selecting the relevant taxpayers to check and report the findings of the check to the Data Processing Centre.
The implementation of one of the three RMS in the other Länder is still ongoing.
Given that none of the three RMS are based on the same approach, a combination of all systems seems to be useful for tackling tax fraud.
It remains to be seen whether this system will deliver the expected results.
Comparison and evaluation
Although the specific criteria of the RMS in the Czech Republic and Germany cannot be discussed in this report, the SAO and BRH found that each Member State developed its own RMS.
As well as the different approaches in the three federal states of Germany, the RMS of each EU state has its strengths and weaknesses.
The tax authorities of the EU Member States are currently discussing new trends and new models of cross-border VAT fraud.
VAT fraud - particularly carousel fraud - is not proving to be a national problem, but rather a European problem.
Payers engage in fraudulent activities at the same time not only in one Member State, but in several States.
An effective RMS cannot be developed by just one Member State.
Successful RMS criteria, components and approaches must be exchanged and implemented in each EU Member State, otherwise fraudsters will choose the Member State with the weakest RMS.
The VAT loss caused by fraud in the EU may not affect the Member State of the instigator of the fraud.
Any Member State involved in fraudulent activities may be affected.
Therefore, there should be a European exchange and discussion on RMS.
Selected control findings when verifying business transactions
As part of their cooperation on the implementation of parallel audit actions, the SAO and BRH examined the quality and use of information on selected business transactions, which were the subject of an international exchange of information between the tax administrations of the Czech Republic and Germany.
In addition, the two audit institutions jointly examined the execution of several commercial transactions in respect of which there were doubts as to their execution or irregularities in the way in which payers from both countries declared these commercial transactions in their VAT and SH tax returns respectively.
At the request of BRH, the SAO examined a total of 8 cases concerning commercial transactions between 8 Czech and 8 German tax entities.
In addition, in 43 cases, the SAO examined the values of intra-community transactions with Germany reported by Czech taxpayers in their tax returns and by SH on the basis of BRH's warnings.
At the request of the SAO, BRH examined a total of 23 cases involving commercial transactions between 23 German and 21 Czech tax entities.
Important information was exchanged on the basis of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003 through official communication with the CLO.
An examination of the selected cases revealed, among other things, that the different registration methods in the EU Member States lead to the problems mentioned in Chapter 4.1:
1.
According to data in VIES, the Czech payer was to purchase goods worth EUR 60 500 from the German payer in the third quarter of 2004.
As the Czech payer only declared the purchase of goods with a value equivalent to EUR 29 869, the Czech tax authority sent a request to Germany to verify the value of the goods delivered.
In its reply to the JOI received from Germany, the German side stated that in the second quarter of 2004 the German payer delivered goods worth EUR 27 381 to the Czech payer, in the third quarter of 2004 it delivered goods worth EUR 31 997 and in the fourth quarter of 2004 it delivered goods worth EUR 10 276.
The reply also showed that the VAT ID of the German payer had only been valid since 28.9.2004, but in 2006 the German CLO retroactively issued the VAT ID certificate of validity from 1.5.2004, following an additional application by the German payer for a VAT ID certificate.
The German payer made a correction to SH.
On the basis of this information, the Czech payer was involved in the acquisition of goods.
When questioned by the local tax authority in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the Czech payer, based on an investigation by the tax authority, filed additional VAT returns for individual tax years in 2004, in which he increased the value of goods purchased from other Member States and at the same time exercised the right to deduct VAT on the acquisition of goods from other Member States.
However, from these additional VAT returns, the Czech tax authorities could not clearly determine whether the values of supplies from the aforementioned German supplier were also included.
Following a request from the SAO, BRH found that the German supplier had been registered for VAT in September 2003.
However, since he did not apply for a VAT ID when he registered, he was only given an identification number for transactions within Germany.
Although in Germany it is usually not possible to assign VAT ID to the payer retroactively, in this case the German tax official in 2006 allocated VAT ID to the aforementioned German payer retroactively as of 1.5.2004.
The German CLO allocates VAT ID retroactively if the German entrepreneur did not cause a delay in the assignment; for example, if the delay was caused by the CLO after the payer's request for VAT ID.
In this case, the CLO allocates VAT ID retroactively because the trader does not need his own valid VAT ID for intra-Community supplies under Section 6 of the German VAT Act.
On the other hand, the German recipient does not need a valid VAT ID of its supplier in order to be able to declare intra-Community acquisitions.
Due to these different procedures between Member States, the German CLO allocated the VAT ID retroactively in this particular case.
2.
As part of an international exchange of information, the Czech tax authority requested verification of the registration of the German taxpayer for VAT.
The VIES indicated the date of registration as 5.3.2005, with the date of 1.10.2004 on the German payer's registration certificate issued by the German tax office, which is locally competent.
In a reply received from Germany, the German side stated that the German tax entity had been registered since 1.10.2004, but that VAT ID had not been provided to it in Germany for organisational reasons until 16.2.2005.
When questioned by the local tax authority, the SAO found that the Czech tax authority had carried out a VAT audit on the Czech taxpayer for the tax period from the third quarter of 2004 to the second quarter 2005.
With this check, the tax office found that the Czech payer included in the VAT return services worth CZK 9,897 (EUR 314), provided to the German payer before his VAT registration (i.e. before 1 October 2004).
For the tax year of the third quarter of 2004, the tax office charged the tax entity VAT of CZK 1,880 (EUR 60).
As requested by the SAO, BRH found that the German payer was not allocated VAT ID until 16 February 2005 when he informed the tax office about his business, which he started in 2004.
In addition, the tax office registered it for VAT retrospectively on 1 October 200415 in order to monitor the submission of the annual VAT return for 2004.
In this tax return, the payer declared an intra-community acquisition from the Czech Republic worth 160 EUR (approx. 5,000 CZK).
The Czech payer declared a supply of goods worth 114,615 CZK (3,642 EUR) to the German payer in the VAT return for September 2004 and SH for the third quarter of 2004.
When verifying the registration of the German payer in the VIES system, the Czech tax authority found that his registration was valid from 11.11.2004, i.e. after the delivery of the goods by the Czech payer to Germany.
The Czech payer submitted an additional DAP for VAT, in which he declared the tax base on transactions carried out in the Czech Republic worth 114,615 CZK (3,642 EUR) and the VAT of 21,777 CZK (692 EUR), which he paid.
When questioned by the local tax office in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the Czech payer had subsequently submitted an application for a retrial of the additional VAT return and submitted as evidence a confirmation from the German tax administration that the German payer had been taxed since 1 January 2000.
Therefore, the Czech tax authority verified the validity of the registration of the German payer as part of an international exchange of information.
The reply received from Germany showed that the German payer was not allocated VAT ID until 11.11.2004, i.e. after the date of delivery of the goods.
For this reason, the tax authorities in the Czech Republic rejected the request for a retrial.
BRH found that the case was not an intra-Community acquisition of goods, as the German payer did not obtain VAT ID until 11.11.2004.
However, the German recipient declared the acquisition as an intra-Community acquisition and declared the VAT on that acquisition by claiming a refund of input tax of the same amount.
However, as there would have been no change in the value of the VAT that the German payer was obliged to pay, the tax authorities did not correct the data in Germany's VAT return.
BRH also found that the name of the German payer, mentioned in the JOI, had been changed during the processing of the reply in Germany, resulting in confusion between two German tax entities.
This change in the name of the German payer has also confused the Czech tax authorities.
4.
As part of the international exchange of information, the German tax authority verified the acquisition of goods by the Czech payer in the first quarter of 2005 worth EUR 22 686 from the German payer.
When questioned by the local tax authority in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the administrator had carried out a local investigation with the Czech payer, in which he verified that the delivery of the goods had taken place and that the Czech payer had booked and paid the invoice for the goods in question.
The Czech payer did not declare the acquisition of the goods in the VAT return because the German supplier did not mention his VAT ID on the tax document, but only the tax number intended for domestic transactions in Germany.
In the VIES application, the Czech tax authority found that the German payer was registered for VAT for intra-Community transactions only from 21 April 2005, i.e. after the delivery to the Czech payer.
At the same time, the Czech tax authority asked the German tax administration to send a copy of the German payer's registration certificate so that it could take steps to assess the tax if necessary.
The Czech tax office assessed the commercial transaction as the acquisition of goods from a non-payer from Germany and therefore did not charge the Czech payer additional tax on the commercial transaction.
BRH found that, under German law, a payer who supplies goods to other Member States does not have to be assigned a VAT ID in order for an intra-Community supply of goods to be exempt from VAT.
The supplier must only have the VAT ID of the person acquiring the goods from another Member State and must be able to prove that the goods have been transported to another Member State.
According to the German VAT Act, it was therefore an intra-community transaction and VAT should be charged in the Czech Republic.
In any event, it is important that the Czech tax authority noticed this transaction because the supply of the machine at the stated value was not the basic business of the German supplier.
As described in chapter 4.6.2, the German CLO refuses to reply to the Rus concerning intra-community transactions with a value of less than EUR 15 000: 5.
According to data from VIES, in the third quarter of 2004, the Czech payer was to purchase goods worth EUR 12,561 from the German payer.
The Czech tax authority carried out a tax audit of the tax entity for this tax year.
In the context of international administrative cooperation, he asked the German tax authorities to verify the supply of those goods by means of a SCAC form.
The Czech payer denied the acquisition of the goods, claiming that he had never done business with the German company and that the acquisition of the goods was not recorded in his accounts.
The German tax authorities rejected the request for evidence - contracts, orders, invoices and transport documents - on the grounds that the turnover did not exceed EUR 15 000 and no other explanatory reasons were given.
As the Czech tax authority did not obtain evidence for the assessment of the tax on the acquired goods, it terminated the tax inspection without finding and the tax liability remained assessed at the original amount.
At the request of the SAO, BRH found that the German payer acted as a so-called "fiscal representative" (§ 22a - e USTG).
The German payer declared those supplies in his annual VAT return and in SH.
He was recognised as entitled to exemption from the supply.
On the basis of the BRH notification, the German tax office will send to the Czech Republic the documents needed for the assessment of the tax on purchased goods in the Czech Republic.
As stated in chapter 4.6.1, the replies to the ŽOI sent from Germany to the Czech Republic exceeded the three-month deadline more often than the replies from the Czech Republic to Germany: 6.
The SAO's audit found that the Czech tax administration sent a request for information to Germany on 5 October 2005 regarding the examination of the value of the goods delivered for the fourth quarter of 2004.
The German payer declared a supply of goods to the Czech payer worth EUR 86 307 in the SH for this period, but the Czech payer only declared a purchase of goods worth EUR 35 314 in the VAT return for the same period.
In its reply to the ŽOI, delivered to the Czech Republic on 9 May 2006, i.e. after the expiry of the deadline for processing laid down in Article 8 of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003, the German side stated that the application could not be processed as the operation of the German firm was closed at the end of 2005.
As the German tax administration did not meet the deadline for processing ŽOI, the Czech tax administration did not have the necessary documents for the tax procedure in the Czech Republic.
In 2005, the Czech tax authority, using the SCAC form, requested verification of deliveries of cars worth EUR 1 265 554 to the German taxpayer, made in the third and fourth quarters of 2004, which showed signs of carousel fraud.
The SAO found that the ŽOI had not received a reply from Germany by the time of the audit.
The SAO also found, by asking the local tax authority, that the Czech payer did not include in the VAT return supplies of new means of transport for the German payer in the amount of CZK 11,816,103 (EUR 375,472).
The Czech tax authority corrected the data in the tax return and the Czech tax entity filed a subsequent SH.
Following a request from the SAO, BRH found that the German CLO did not, for technical reasons, submit the aforementioned ŽOI to the local tax office for examination.
Following BRH's warning, a check was carried out on the German purchaser in Germany, which found that the purchase of all the cars had been properly taxed and that the cars in question had been sold to another payer in Germany.
According to data from VIES, the Czech payer should have purchased a passenger car worth EUR 48 500 from the German payer in the fourth quarter of 2004.
The purchase of these goods was not admitted by the Czech payer.
When questioned by the local tax authority in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the Czech taxpayer had not filed VAT returns since August 2004.
The tax returns were not submitted by the Czech taxpayer even after calls from the tax authorities, so on 23 May 2005 the tax office charged him VAT of CZK 0 for the period October to December 2004.
On 2 June 2005, CLO drew attention to the abovementioned delivery from the German payer.
As the Czech payer did not cooperate with the tax authority, the tax authority sent ŽOI to Germany regarding the aforementioned supply.
Since the reply to ŽOI was not received in the Czech Republic until 7 February 2007, it was not known until the end of the SAO audit how the Czech tax administration used the information obtained in the international exchange.
The tax office cancelled the VAT registration of the Czech payer on 23 August 2005 due to a failure to comply with obligations under the VAT Act.
In some cases, only a partial reply was sent to ŽOI, because the audit carried out by the tax authorities on payers was not completed at the time of the audit of the SAO and BRH:
9.
In 2005, the Czech tax authority, using the SCAC form, requested an examination of the delivery of a car worth EUR 16 991 to a German payer, carried out in the third quarter of 2004, which showed signs of carousel fraud.
In its reply to ŽOI, the German tax authority stated that it only had an invoice issued by the Czech payer for a supply of EUR 16 335.
At the request of the SAO, BRH found that the audit carried out by the German tax office on the acquirer from Germany had not yet been completed.
The German acquirer declared the acquisition of goods worth EUR 16 335 twice, in the tax returns for August and September 2004.
10. In 2005, the Czech tax authority, using the SCAC form, requested verification of the delivery of cars to the German taxpayer worth EUR 198 167, carried out in the fourth quarter of 2004 and the first quarter of 2005, which showed signs of carousel fraud.
The German tax administration sent a partial reply to ŽOI to the Czech Republic, in which it confirmed the purchase of some cars by the German payer and further stated that the investigation in Germany had not been completed.

The SAO found that in order to verify the use of excess VAT deductions, the local tax office carried out several local investigations with the Czech supplier, during which it did not find that they had been improperly used.
BRH found that the German payer had declared in his VAT returns acquisitions of goods from other Member States for a total value of EUR 579 114 during that period and that the check carried out by the German tax office on the purchaser from Germany had not yet been completed.
Chapter 4.4.1 describes the reasons for the differences between the values of the intra-Community acquisition of goods declared by the recipient in the tax return and the values declared by the supplier in his SH.
The audited cases showed that the most common reasons for the differences were not the time lag or the indication of the incorrect value of the intra-community delivery of goods in SH:
11.
According to data from the VIES system, the Czech payer should have purchased goods worth EUR 35 716 from the German payer in the first quarter of 2005, but the Czech payer did not admit this acquisition.
As the Czech payer did not cooperate with the tax authority and did not carry out any activities at the company's headquarters, the Czech tax authority requested, as part of an international exchange of information, to verify how the German payer communicated with the Czech taxpayer.
The reply to the ŽOI received from Germany showed that, according to the findings of the German tax administration, the Czech tax entity was unknown at the address communicated and that the goods had been taken over by the agreed carrier.
The order was for a total amount of EUR 155 000, but the German payer delivered only EUR 21 659 worth of goods.
The Czech payer sent the German payer a false confirmation of the payment of EUR 155 153 in favour of the German payer.
Following the discovery of fraudulent behaviour on the part of the Czech acquirer, the German payer, with the help of his other Czech customers, managed to recover the supplied material, with the exception of one item worth EUR 7 916.
The SAO, by asking the local tax office in the Czech Republic, found that the tax authority, based on the information obtained, assessed the Czech VAT payer on the purchase of goods from other Member States in the amount of CZK 388,522 (EUR 13,044).
At the request of the SAO, BRH confirmed that the German supplier only declared the delivery of goods to the Czech payer in the amount of EUR 7 916 after repairs.
According to the German legal situation, the German payer reported the corrected values of the goods and a reduction in the taxable amount in the quarter in which the adjustment was made.
Thus, its SH contained the following delivery values in relation to the Czech payer:
12.
In the context of an international exchange of information, the German tax authority requested, using the SCAC form, to verify the supplies of goods and services carried out in the third quarter of 2005.
According to this ŽOI, during this period the Czech payer was to deliver goods worth a total of EUR 396 126 to the German payer and to provide services worth EUR 11 885.
The SAO found that the Czech tax authority carried out a local investigation with the Czech payer in order to verify this supply.
In reply to ŽOI, the Czech tax authority stated that the Czech payer had supplied the German payer with a production line, including assembly.
Individual parts of the production line were supplied by the Czech payer before the Czech Republic joined the EU and after 1 May 2004 the line was assembled on the basis of an order.
The German payer did not take over the assembled line because he claimed to have defects.
In the third quarter of 2005, the Czech payer issued invoices to the German payer for the amounts of EUR 107 100 for assembly and EUR 11 885 for services.
The German payer accepted the invoices issued, but did not accept them and did not pay them.
The SAO also found that all invoices are duly registered in the accounts of the Czech taxpayer by asking the local tax authority in the Czech Republic.
In the VAT returns for the third quarter of 2005, only the amounts which were documented by the Czech payer and which relate to invoicing after 1 May 2004 are mentioned.
BRH found that, on the basis of a reply from the Czech tax administration, the local tax office in Germany concluded that the transaction involved the supply of goods from a Czech payer to a German payer, including assembly services.
In this particular case, the place where the work was done is where the production line was assembled.
Under the German VAT Act, the German recipient of the service supplied is liable to pay VAT.
At the same time, the recipient may deduct VAT on the same amount.
As there would have been no change in the value of the VAT that the German payer was obliged to pay, the corrections in the VAT return were neglected by the German tax office.
According to VIES data, in February 2005, Czech payer A was to purchase a machine worth EUR 58 000 from German payer C.
The Czech tax authority has sent a request to Germany for verification of this supply.
In its reply to ŽOI, the German side stated that the machine had already been supplied in 2004 by the German payer C to the Czech payer B, who, however, was to return the machine to the German payer C in October 2004.
According to information from the German tax administration, the machine was not transported back to Germany, but was transported to the organisational unit of the German payer C in the Czech Republic.
It also emerged from a reply to a request for information that German payer C had sold the machine to Czech payer A in February 2005.
This payer took over the machine at the headquarters of the organisational unit of the German payer C in the Czech Republic.
As the delivery took place only within the Czech Republic, it was not an intra-community delivery of goods.
The SAO, by asking the tax authority of the local payer B, found that according to VIES data, the German payer C delivered goods (another machine) worth EUR 88 027 to the Czech payer B in the third quarter of 2004.
Payer B denied the acquisition of the goods, so the local tax authority from the Czech Republic sent ŽOI to Germany.
According to the reply to this request, the delivery of the machine took place.
A further investigation with payer B found that the machine, worth EUR 88 027, was not in the accounts of payer B and that it could be of the same type as that supplied by the organisational unit of German payer C to Czech payer A in February 2005.
The SAO also found that the Czech tax authority of the locally competent payer A carried out a local investigation of this payer.
The tax authority had at its disposal an invoice from German payer C dated 7.2.2005, on which payer A was listed as the purchaser of the machine.
The Czech tax authority found that payer A did not have this invoice included in the accounts.
Payer A had a lease agreement with another Czech company, where the object of the lease was a machine of the same type.
The transfer of the machine from the leasing company took place on 9 February 2005 and the transport of the machine was carried out by the leasing company.
The information contained in the reply to the request for information was not used by the Czech Tax Office to determine the tax liability of payer A.
BRH found that the German payer C did not deliver the machine worth EUR 88 027 to the Czech Republic, but to another German payer D.
It was therefore not an intra-Community supply of goods, but a taxable transaction in Germany.
For these reasons, the German tax authority did not grant the German taxpayer C an exemption from VAT and corrected the information in his tax return.
The German payer D supplied the machine to the Czech payer B.
According to German law, this supply was not taxable in Germany, but was subject to VAT in the Czech Republic.
In addition, BRH found that German payer C had declared in its SH for the first quarter of 2005 the delivery of a machine worth EUR 58 000 to Czech payer A.
That supply was not examined during the tax audit carried out by the German tax office.

14.
The SAO found during the audit of the received ŽOI that the Czech tax administration received a request for information from Germany on 4 October 2005, in which the German tax authority requested verification of an intra-community supply from a German payer worth EUR 879,680,625 to a Czech payer.
According to the German tax authority, there was a suspicion that this case was a fake intra-Community supply of goods.
It was also stated in the ŽOI that the German payer had not carried out any active commercial activity since 1999.
The SAO found that the Czech tax authority carried out a local investigation of the Czech taxpayer.
According to the manager of the Czech company, the above case was apparently a claim by a German payer against the German tax administration, which was filed by the Czech payer as a partner of a German company with the German tax office.
According to the information provided by the SAO, the Czech tax authority does not currently have any information that the German tax administration has dealt with the issue related to the Czech taxpayer.
According to the information available, it was not a supply of goods, yet the value is still included in the VIES system as an intra-community supply of goods to a Czech payer from Germany.
The main reason for the following irregularities was that the beneficiaries did not declare intra-Community acquisitions in their tax returns (see also Chapter 4.4.1):
15. According to data from VIES, the German payer delivered goods worth a total of EUR 33 205 to the Czech payer in the third quarter of 2004 to the first quarter of 2005. The Czech payer did not declare this acquisition.
ThissegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
As part of an international exchange of information, the Czech tax authority requested verification of the supply of goods from Germany.
In response to that request, the German tax authority stated that the German payer had sent part of the goods to the address of the Czech payer, while the remaining goods had been collected by the Czech payer himself.
When questioned by the local tax authority in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that even before receiving a reply to ŽOI, the Czech payer had submitted additional VAT returns for the periods mentioned.
Despite this submission, the differences in acquisition values have not been resolved, so the Czech tax administration recommended a tax audit of the Czech payer.
The inspection has not yet been carried out.
According to VIES data, the German payer delivered goods worth EUR 46 854 to the Czech payer in the third quarter of 2004.
For the same period, the Czech payer only awarded an intra-community purchase of the equivalent amount of EUR 14 856.
The Czech tax authority requested verification of the value of the supplies made as part of an international exchange of information.
The reply to the ŽOI, received from Germany, was accompanied by 3 invoices with a total stated delivery value of EUR 31 999, i.e. the value corresponding to the difference between the acquisition declared by the Czech payer and the data in the VIES system.
When questioned by the local tax authority in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that after receiving a reply from Germany, the Czech tax authority contacted the accountant of the Czech payer and agreed with him to discuss the submission of an additional VAT return for the third quarter of 2004 with the owner of the company after examining these invoices.
An additional VAT return has not yet been submitted.
The Czech tax authority told the SAO that it would proceed in such a way as to comply with the deadlines set for any additional assessment of VAT for the relevant tax year.
17.
In the fourth quarter of 2004, the German payer was to deliver to the Czech payer goods worth EUR 11 600.
As part of an international exchange of information, the German tax authority asked for confirmation of whether the Czech payer actually existed, because the alleged partner of the German payer had set up more fictitious companies in Germany.
During the examination of the commercial transaction, the Czech payer confirmed the acquisition of the goods to the tax office.
However, according to the Czech payer, the goods were not transported from Germany to the Czech Republic and were resold in Germany in 2005.
The Czech payer submitted evidence of the sale of the goods for January 2005.
The Czech payer was not registered as a VAT payer in Germany, he did not declare or pay the tax on the sale of the goods in question in the Czech Republic or in Germany.
All these facts suggested tax evasion on the territory of Germany and were communicated by the Czech tax authority to the German tax administration in response to the ŽOI.
When questioned by the local tax authority in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the Czech payer, on the basis of the investigations carried out, submitted an additional VAT return for the fourth quarter of 2004, in which he included the value of the acquisition of goods from, among others, the German payer and at the same time exercised the right to deduct the tax on the acquisition of goods from other Member States.
VAT on the sale of goods in Germany was not included in the Czech VAT return.
The Czech tax authority assessed the additional VAT return unchanged after a local investigation.
According to the Czech legislation, this case did not involve the acquisition of goods from other Member States, as the goods were not dispatched or transported from another Member State to the Czech Republic.
The Czech tax authority therefore made an incorrect conclusion of the local investigation.
BRH found that the German tax authority, immediately after receiving a reply to the JOI stating that the goods had not left Germany, corrected the tax return of the German taxpayer and demanded EUR 1 600 in VAT from him.
In addition, the relevant tax office has sent a warning to the tax office of the actual recipient of the goods to ensure that the resale of the goods is correctly taxed.
In the following cases, payers reported intra-community transactions that were unlikely to have actually taken place:
18.
The Czech tax authority received a request from the German tax administration for information on whether the Czech payer had purchased a passenger car worth EUR 47 400 from the German taxpayer in February 2005.
The application was accompanied by a copy of the certificate of registration of the Czech payer for VAT.
It was also accompanied by a copy of the passport of the person who, it was said, was to carry out the transport of the car.
An investigation by the Czech tax authority found that it was a stolen passport, the person mentioned in it did not import any vehicle into the Czech Republic and denied all contacts with the German tax entity.
The VAT registration certificate, a copy of which was sent by the German side, was never issued by the Czech tax authorities.
This information was provided by the Czech tax authority in its reply to ŽOI, along with a statement that it could not confirm the purchase of the goods - the car in question.
When questioned by the local tax authority in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the Czech payer was not based at the address listed in the Commercial Register and the manager of the company was non-contact.
After conducting a complaint procedure for the February 2005 tax year, the Czech tax authority charged the Czech taxpayer a tax liability of CZK 0.
A further investigation by the Czech tax authority found that the car in question had been sold to another Czech entity, which had bought it through an advertisement on the internet.
BRH found that, on the basis of the Czech reply to ŽOI, the competent German tax authority would not grant the German taxpayer the right to exemption from VAT on that supply.
During the inspection, the German tax office was unable to explain the difference of EUR 3 000 between the value of the goods acquired declared on the payer's tax return and the value provided from another Member State.
It was stated that the Czech payer was to deliver goods worth EUR 89 424 to the German payer during the fourth quarter of 2004 to the first quarter of 2005.
As the acquisition declared by the German payer did not correspond to the data in VIES, the German tax authority requested verification of the supplies and their payment in the context of an international exchange of information.
The Czech tax authority stated in its reply to ŽOI that the sole manager of the Czech company had been removed from the Commercial Register on 8 July 2005 and the new manager had not been registered.
The German recipient of the goods appeared to be related to a partner in a Czech company.
The Czech payer also submitted VAT returns to SH, which after the removal of the manager from the Commercial Register was signed by an unauthorized person - the stated partner of the company.
The accountant of the Czech taxpayer confirmed to the tax authority that the partner of the company deposited the cash paid for the invoiced goods in EUR into the company's account.
Cash receipts were not issued.
The SAO in the Czech Republic, when questioned by the local tax office, found that the tax authority had recognised the Czech taxpayer's entitlement to VAT exemption for the fourth quarter of 2004 on supplies of goods to another Member State worth CZK 1,326,307 (EUR 42,145) and for the first quarter of 2005 in the amount of CZK 1,416,180 (EUR 47,548).
BRH found that the tax authority in Germany had not corrected the VAT return of the German purchaser because a German judge had in the meantime confirmed the insolvency of the German payer.
As an earlier check did not reveal any signs of tax fraud, it will not be possible to recover the tax liability.
According to VIES data, in 2005 a German payer purchased goods from the Czech Republic worth €4,251,196 after purchasing goods worth €43,274 in the previous year.
Neither in the 2004 tax return nor in the 2005 tax return did the German payer declare an intra-Community acquisition.
In addition, it did not provide adequate supplies.
Due to these differences, the German tax office sent ŽOI for the fourth quarter of 2005 and the first quarter of 2006.
The Czech supplier reported intra-community delivery of goods to the German payer for a total value of 167,246,083 CZK (5,615,299 EUR) in SH for these two quarters.
On 6 September 2006, the ŽOI was received, in which the German side asked to check whether the Czech payer had made the declared intra-community deliveries.
In reply to this ŽOI, the Czech tax administration stated that the German party's request could not be met because the Czech payer had no manager.
According to the material provided by the SAO by the competent tax authority, on 30 March 2006 a report was drawn up with the manager of the Czech payer on the start of the VAT audit for the fourth quarter of 2004 and January-December 2005.
At the same time, the taxpayer was asked by the tax authorities to submit all accounting and tax documents for the above periods, but no documents were submitted.
According to the Commercial Register, the sole manager of the Czech payer ceased to hold office on 16 May 2006, and a new manager was not appointed.
Since April 2006, the Czech taxpayer has stopped submitting VAT returns.
As part of the audit, the SAO, in cooperation with BRH, examined, among other things, several cases of intra-community supplies made between the Czech Republic and Germany, which were not the subject of a previous exchange of information between the tax administrations of the two countries.
Information on the cases examined was transmitted by the two supreme audit institutions through the CLOs of both countries.
The Czech company (ECR), which is not resident in Germany, has informed the competent tax office (Chemnitz-Süd) that it intends to carry out a taxable transaction in Germany.
Because of this information, the company has been registered since June 2005 but has not received a German VAT ID.
(ECR) accepted an order from a Danish entrepreneur (EDK) for the production of several wind farms and for the delivery of these wind farms in the name, at risk and on behalf of a Danish customer to Austria.
Due to a lack of own capacity, the Czech company handed over part of the order to the German payer (eD), which is based in Germany.
The following diagram shows the contractual relationship and mode of transport of wind farms:
According to the German legal situation, the place where these transactions take place must be determined according to the following:
- A Danish entrepreneur (EDK) has sent wind farms to be assembled under his name, at his own risk and on his own account in Austria.
Since the assembly of this supply took place in Austria, the supply of wind turbines is taxable in Austria.
- Since the carrier was instructed by a Danish entrepreneur (EDK) and the transport was carried out under his name, at his risk and on his own account, the delivery of the German subcontractor (eD) took place where the transport started - in Germany.
Although the wind farms were shipped to another Member State and the recipient is a registered payer from another Member State, the supply of a German subcontractor (eD) could not be exempted because another Member State of destination is different from another Member State of the registered office of the Czech company.
This supply is therefore correctly taxed in Germany and the Czech company (ECZ) deducted the input tax in its tax returns.
The place of delivery to the Czech company (ECR) is also determined by the beginning of the transport.
The transport of some wind power plants started in the Czech Republic and others in Germany.
- The delivery of those wind power plants that are produced in the Czech Republic took place in the Czech Republic.
- The supply of other wind farms that are produced in Germany took place in Germany.
Thus, the Czech company (ECR) carried out both intra-community delivery from the Czech Republic to Austria and intra-community delivery from Germany to Austria.
BRH found that the Czech company (ECR) did not declare any intra-Community acquisitions in its VAT return in Germany, nor did it submit SH to the German CLO.
So it is possible that the Czech company reported all intra-community deliveries uniformly as intra-community deliveries from the Czech Republic.
The SAO found that (ECR) did not report any intra-community deliveries to Austria, but intra-community deliveries to Denmark.
An examination of the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions in Austria would require the cooperation of at least four tax administrations (Austrian, Czech, Danish and German), even though this case does not show any sign of tax fraud or evasion.
In addition, the SAO and BRH examined the transactions to point out the differences between the declaration in the tax return and the VIES data, which were due to the different VAT legislation in 2004.
The audited cases also demonstrate that changes in the legislation need time for the implementation of the new legislation by both payers and tax authorities:
In the SH for the second to fourth quarters of 2004, the Czech payer reported intra-community supplies to the German payer for a total value of 792 977 452 CZK (25 197 885 EUR).
During the same period, another Czech payer in SH reported an intra-community delivery to another German payer for a total value of 18,157,265 CZK (576,970 EUR).
According to the information provided by the SAO from BRH, both cases involved the supply of electricity.
Both Czech payers listed the above supplies in the SH in accordance with the text of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll., which was in force in 2004.
By further examining the above transactions, a group of auditors of the SAO found that in 2004 there were differences between the Czech Republic and Germany in the legal arrangements for the supply or purchase of electricity.
While in the Czech Republic the payers reported the supply of electricity in accordance with the current version of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll. as an intra-community supply of goods, from the point of view of the German legislation in force in 2004, it was not an intra-community acquisition, but a taxable transaction with the place of performance of the transaction in the territory of Germany.
The difference in legal regulations was eliminated in the Czech Republic by the adoption of Act No. 635 / 2004 Coll., which amends certain laws in connection with the adoption of the Act on Administrative Fees, effective from 1 January 2005.
In addition, when examining selected intra-community transactions in cooperation with BRH, it was found that the Czech payer reported in SH for the 1st to 4th quarters of 2005 intra-community delivery to the German payer for a total value of 240,411,163 CZK (8,071,823 EUR) and another Czech payer reported in SH for the same period intra-community delivery to the German payer for a total value of 263,470,776 CZK (8,846,050 EUR).
According to the information provided by the SAO from BRH, both cases involved the supply of electricity.
According to the wording of Act No 235 / 2004 Coll., effective from 1 January 2005, in the case of the supply of electricity, the place of supply is the place where the customer has his registered office, place of business or where he has an establishment for which the goods are supplied.
Therefore, Czech payers should not have declared the supply of electricity to SH in 2005.
The fact that the two payers mentioned above reported the intra-Community supply of electricity in SH distorted the data in VIES by a total of 503,881,939 CZK (16,917,873 EUR).
Conclusion
The cooperation met the objectives of BRH and the SAO.
Both SAIs have acquired a deeper knowledge of the VAT administration systems in the Czech Republic and Germany.
The cooperation revealed the differences between the two systems and showed that the legislation on VAT management differs.
During parallel checks, suspicious cases of intra-community transactions were identified.
It makes sense to examine some of them afterwards.
On the basis of the audit findings, both SAIs made recommendations on VAT administration.
The follow-up of these recommendations should also be part of the follow-up.
The new experience and knowledge gained through the cooperation of the two audit institutions is the basis for the successful implementation of the following controls on the VAT administration.
Communiqué
The report was written in Czech, English and German and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the President of the Bundesrechnungshof, the Federal Republic of Germany.
Report on the outcome of international cooperation in the control of excise administration between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in 2006
Introductory word
The submitted joint report reports on the progress and outcome of international cooperation in parallel inspections carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Najvyšší kontrolný úrad Slovenskej republiky, focused on the administration of excise duties in the period after the accession of the two countries to the European Union.
The cooperation was carried out on the basis of a contract for cooperation in control activities concluded in February 2006.
The topic of parallel checks was chosen in the light of a fundamental change in the system of collection of excise duties, which took place in connection with the integration of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic into the internal market of the European Union from 1 May 2004.
The functioning of the internal market of the European Union requires the free movement of goods, including excise goods.
The basic principle is to allow goods not subject to tax to circulate until the date of their delivery for final consumption.
In accordance with that principle, the new legislation adopted in both countries allows the movement of goods under tax supervision under a suspensive regime.
The system places great demands on the tax authorities and requires close cooperation between the competent administrative authorities of the Member States in the fight against tax fraud in this area.
Report on the outcome of international cooperation on controls of the administration of excise duties for the period from 1 May 2004 to 31 December 2005 1.
Introduction
Control number: (Czech Republic) 05 / 34 (SR) 48 / 11
Subject of inspection: (Czech Republic) Administration of Excise Duties (Slovak Republic) Procedure of the collegiate authorities in the administration of spotreble taxes
On 8 February 2006, the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (hereinafter "NKÚ-ČR") and the Najvyššší kontrolný úrad Slovenskej republiky (hereinafter "SAO SR") concluded a "Treaty on Cooperation in Audit Activities."
The subject of the contract was cooperation in parallel inspections of the "Administration of Excise Taxes," included in the NKÚ-ČR audit activity plan for 2005 under No 05 / 34, and "Control of the procedure of the collegiate authorities in the administration of spotreble taxes," included in the audit activity plan of the SAO SR for 2006 under No 48 / 11.
The parallel checks had the character of coordinated checks.
The cooperation consisted in the exchange of information that the contracting parties could not obtain during the inspection of the administration of excise duties on the territory of their state and in the preparation of a joint final report on the outcome of the inspections within the meaning of the European implementing directives for the implementation of the INTOSAI audit standards - Directive No 31.
In the territory of the Czech Republic, the inspection (hereinafter referred to as "the Czech Republic") was carried out by groups of auditors from the State Budget Department and from the territorial departments of Central Bohemia, South Bohemia, West Bohemia, Northwest Bohemia, Northeast Bohemia, South Moravia, Central Moravia and Northern Moravia between 7 February and 2 June 2006.
27 inspectors were involved in the inspection.
The audited entities were the Directorate-General for Customs (hereinafter referred to as "the GSC") and 11 tax offices.
Within the framework of the GŘC, 12 selected customs offices out of a total of 54 were inspected.
The audit on the territory of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as "SR") was carried out by the financial and tax section of the SAO SR in cooperation with the expositions of the SAO SR Banská Bystrica and Košice at 5 customs offices out of a total of 9 in the period from 13 February to 2 June 2006.
Eight inspectors were involved in the inspection.
The aim of the parallel checks was to examine the customs authorities' handling of excise duties and compliance with the relevant legislation in force in both countries and in the European Union.
International cooperation focused on the procedure of tax authorities in the exercise of supervision over the transport of goods subject to excise duties, in particular on the registration of initiated and completed shipments under the conditional exemption regime, and on the exchange of information in the framework of mutual administrative assistance between excise tax authorities of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
2. Administration of excise duties
The administration of excise duties in the Czech Republic was carried out by the tax authorities until 31 December 2003.
Since 1 January 2004, this agenda has been taken over by the customs authorities, which have so far only collected excise duty on imports.
In the Czech Republic, mineral oils, alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products and tobacco products are subject to excise duty.
The revenue of the state budget from excise duties in the Czech Republic amounted to a total of CZK 82.8 billion in 2004 and excise duties accounted for 19.5% of the revenue of the state budget from taxes and fees amounting to CZK 424.7 billion.
In 2005, the revenue of the state budget from excise duties amounted to CZK 103.6 billion and the share of the state budget revenue from taxes and fees of CZK 460.4 billion was 22.5%.
In 2004, the revenue from excise duty on mineral oils to the state budget amounted to 80% of the total revenue from this tax and in 2005 it amounted to 90.9%.
The difference from 100% in the amount of CZK 13 billion in 2004 and CZK 6.9 billion in 2005 was the income of the State Fund for Transport Infrastructure.
The administration of all excise duties in the Slovak Republic has been carried out by the customs authorities since 1 May 2004, with the exception of excise duty on mineral oil, the administration of which has been carried out since 1 January 2002.
Until then, excise duties had been administered by the tax authorities.
Mineral oil, alcohol, beer, wine and tobacco products are subject to excise duty in the Slovak Republic.
The revenue of the state budget from excise duties in the Slovak Republic amounted to a total of Sk 43.4 billion in 2004 and excise duties accounted for 20.7% of the total tax revenue of Sk 209.5 billion.
In 2005, the state budget revenue from excise duties was CZK 50 billion and excise duties accounted for 22.5% of the total tax revenue of CZK 222.6 billion.
Chart 1 - Comparison of revenues of the state budget of the Czech Republic from taxes and fees and tax revenues of the state budget of the Slovak Republic with revenues from excise taxes
- Council Directive 92 / 12 / EEC on the general arrangements for products subject to excise duty and on the holding, movement and monitoring of such products ("Directive 92 / 12 / EEC"), - Council Regulation (EC) No 2073 / 2004 on administrative cooperation in the field of excise duties ("Regulation No 2073 / 2004"), - Commission Regulation (EEC) No 2719 / 92 on the accompanying official document for the movement of products subject to excise duty under suspension of excise duty ("Regulation No 2719 / 92"), - Commission Regulation (EEC) No 3649 / 92 on a simplified accompanying document for the movement within the Community of products subject to excise duty which have been released for consumption in the Member State of dispatch ("Regulation No 3649 / 92").
The basic legislation governing the issue of excise duties in the Czech Republic is Act No 353 / 2003 Coll., on Excise Duties, as amended, (hereinafter "Act No 353 / 2003 Coll."), which took effect from 1 January 2004.
In the administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic, the customs authorities are, inter alia, bound by the following generally binding legislation: - Act No 98 / 2004 Z. Z. on the Spotrebnej Tax on Mineral Oil in the Zneší predpisov (hereinafter "Act No 98 / 2004 Z. z."), - Act No 104 / 2004 Z. on the Spotrebnej Tax on Wine in the Zneší predpisov (hereinafter "Act No 104 / 2004 Z. z."), - Act No 105 / 2004 Z. Z. on the Spotrebnej Tax on Lieh in the Zneší predpisov (hereinafter "Act No 105 / 2004 Z. z."), - Act No 106 / 2004 Z. on the Spotrebnej Tax on Tabak Products in the Zneší predpisov (hereinafter "Act No 106 / 2004 Z. z."), - Act No 107 / 2004 Z. Z. on the Spotrebnej Tax on Beer in the Zneh predpisov (hereinafter "Act No 107 / 2004 Z. z.").
2.1 Movement of excise goods under suspension of duty between Member States of the EU
The conditions governing the movement of excise goods under suspension of duty are governed by Directive 92 / 12 / EEC, in Title III - Movement of goods, Articles 15 to 20.
Under those provisions, the transport of those goods may be carried out only by an authorised warehousekeeper, who means a natural or legal person authorised by the competent authorities of a Member State to manufacture, process, store, receive and dispatch products subject to excise duty.
The consignee in another Member State may be an authorised warehousekeeper or an economic operator without the status of authorised warehousekeeper, who may not, however, store or dispatch such products under a suspensive arrangement.
Authorised warehousekeeper in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic means the operator of a tax warehouse, the economic operator is the authorised recipient for the repeated or one-off receipt of products subject to excise duty.
The movement of products subject to excise duty under suspension of duty is only possible under Directive 92 / 12 / EEC with an accompanying document.
The accompanying document shall be drawn up by the consignor in four copies before the start of the journey, unless further copies are required by the competent authorities of the Member State of dispatch.
2.2 Procedure for starting and ending the transport of goods under the conditional exemption regime between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Transport from the Czech Republic
The procedure for starting transport is governed by the provisions of Section 25 (3) of Act No 353 / 2003 Coll., which states, among other things:
"The operator of the tax warehouse shall inform the customs office, which is the local competent tax warehouse from which the transport is to begin, before the transport of the selected products begins;
The transport of the selected products can only start with the approval of this customs office.
The customs office shall give its consent to the transport of the selected products without delay after the condition of securing the tax has been met... "
The consignor in the Czech Republic can start the transport of all types of products subject to excise duty only with the consent of the locally competent customs office.
The customs office will only give its consent to the start of transport if security is provided for the amount of tax due on the goods transported.
The consignor is required to draw up the accompanying document in five copies before the start of the transport.
The customs office shall indicate on the accompanying document its agreement to the start of the transport.
Copy No 1 shall be kept by the consignor, copy No 2, 3 and copy No 4 shall be handed over by the consignor to the carrier and copy No 5 shall be kept by the customs office authorising the transport.
Under Slovak law, the consignee in SR keeps copy No 2 of the accompanying document. On copies No 3 and 4, he confirms receipt of the products and submits both copies to the local competent customs office.
Copy No 3, certified by the customs office, shall be sent to the consignor no later than the 15th day of the month following the calendar month in which he received the products.
Copy No 4 shall be kept by the customs office of the consignee.
The transport is terminated by the acceptance of the products by the recipient.
The release of the security of the tax will be decided by the customs office in the Czech Republic, which authorised the start of the transport, within 5 working days of the presentation of copy No 3 of the accompanying document, which is confirmed by the consignee and the Slovak customs office.
Chart 2 - Circulation of the accompanying document for transport started in the Czech Republic and ended in the Slovak Republic
Transport from Slovakia
Until 31 December 2005, the procedure for transporting alcohol and tobacco products from Slovakia to another Member State of the European Union was amended as follows:
Pursuant to Article 26 (4) of Law No 105 / 2004 Z. z.
"When transporting lieh from a tax warehouse in the tax territory to a tax warehouse, or to an authorised recipient, or to a tax beneficiary in an inom member's staff, the odosielatel" (the supplier ") is obliged to send the copy of the first diel of the preparatory document electronically or faxom to the Poprad Colný úrad on the day of the start of the transport; this copy is also required to be sent to the colný úrad by writing to the piatich of working days from the day of the start of the transport."
Pursuant to Article 22 (4) of Law No 106 / 2004 Z. z.
"When transporting tobacco products from a tax warehouse in the tax territory to a tax warehouse, or to an authorised recipient, or to a tax beneficiary in an inom member's staff, the odosielatel" (the supplier ") is obliged to send the code of the first diel of the sprievodní document electronically or fax to the Colný úrad Poprad on the day of the start of the transport; this code is also required to be sent to the colný úrad písomne najneskor in the piatich working days from the day of the start of the transport."
For the transport of other products subject to excise duty (mineral oil, wine and beer) during the period from 1 May 2004 to 31 December 2005 ("the audited period"), the taxpayer was not obliged to notify the Poprad Customs Office or the competent customs office of the start of the transport under suspension of duty.
The tax authority only became aware of the transport of these products during a local investigation or during a tax inspection from the accompanying documents and the accounting documents of the tax entity.
The consignor in SR is obliged to draw up the accompanying document in four copies before the start of the transport.
Copy No 1 shall be retained by the consignor (when transporting ethyl alcohol and tobacco products, he shall send a copy of copy No 1 electronically or by fax to the Poprad customs office and the competent customs office).
Copies Nos 2, 3 and 4 shall accompany the goods being transported.
