According to the Czech legislation, the consignee in the Czech Republic keeps copy No 2 of the accompanying document issued by the consignor in the Slovak Republic and confirms receipt of the products on copies No 3 and 4.
Certified copies Nos 3 and 4 will be sent no later than the first working day after the end of the transport to the local customs office in the Czech Republic.
Copy No 4 shall be retained by the customs office and copy No 3 shall be returned to the consignee to verify its accuracy and validity.
The consignee shall send the certified copy No 3 no later than the following working day after receipt to the consignor in SR.
Transport in the Slovak Republic is considered to have ended on the date of receipt of the products by the recipient.
The consignor proves the termination of the transport by producing copy No 3 of the accompanying document certified by the consignee and the tax authority in the Czech Republic.
Figure 3 - Circulation of the accompanying document for transport (alcohol and tobacco products) started in Slovakia and ended in the Czech Republic
In 2006, amendments to all laws on excise duties were gradually adopted in the Slovak Republic, according to which the consignor of goods under the conditional exemption procedure is obliged to send a copy of copy No 1 of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the customs office of the locally competent consignor before the start of transport.
The document proving the end of the transport of alcohol and tobacco products shall be copy No 3 of the accompanying document, certified by the consignee and his competent tax authority.
The document proving that the transport of mineral oils, wine and beer has ended is copy No 3, certified by the consignee.
Confirmation by the tax authorities of another Member State that the goods have been taken over by the consignee shall be required if the latter is required, under the legislation of the Member State concerned, to certify copy No 3 of the accompanying document.
2.3 Registry of initiated and completed shipments conducted by customs authorities in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
A single electronic system is not in place to monitor the movement of goods under suspension of duty between the Member States of the European Union.
Decision 1152 / 2003 / EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 on the introduction of an electronic system for the transport and monitoring of products subject to excise duty requires Member States and the European Commission to introduce, from 1 July 2009, an electronic system (Excise Movement and Control System) to enable excise authorities in each Member State to obtain real-time information on the movement of goods.
The system will allow the electronic transmission of accompanying documents, which are currently only used in paper form, and will contribute to simplifying the movement of goods under the conditional exemption regime and to ensuring more effective control of the movement of untaxed products across all Member States.
This system will include the national transport databases of the Member States.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic records all transport started and finished on the territory of the Czech Republic in the module Evidence of Selected Products ("EVV").
All customs authorities in the Czech Republic have online access to the system.
In the case of shipments carried out only on the territory of the Czech Republic, the tax authorities can obtain information about the start or end of the transport immediately after the registration of the accompanying document by the customs office in EVV.
The customs office shall release the security of the tax on the products transported provided by the consignor at the time of registration of the end of the transport by the customs office to the consignee responsible for the place.
Customs offices in the Slovak Republic use a database based on SysNed application software, which ensures the automation of their activities in the administration of excise duties and communication with European Union systems.
By registering a tax warehouse, tax warehouse operator or authorised recipient in SysNed's application software, this information is automatically transferred to the "System for Exchange of Excise Data" ("SEED") database.
3. Preparation and progress of cooperation
The first coordination meeting between representatives of the NKÚ-ČR and representatives of the SAO SR, at which the specific procedure for cooperation in the implementation of parallel controls in the field of excise duties was discussed, took place in January 2006.
The two sides got to know each other about the excise legislation and the organisation of the excise administration in both states.
Special attention was paid to the procedure of the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in authorising, respectively, the initiation and termination of the transport of products subject to excise duty under the conditional exemption regime and the exchange of information between the excise authorities of both countries.
At the meeting, it was agreed that the Czech and Slovak sides would: - process the total data on the quantities of products subject to excise duty transported from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic and vice versa, the transport of which started during the audited period, - compare the data on the transport of mineral oils - Combined Nomenclature codes 2710 and 2711 and ethyl alcohol - Combined Nomenclature codes 2207 and 2208 under the suspension regime started in the Czech Republic and ended in the Slovak Republic and vice versa in November 2004 and September 2005.
In the course of the checks, the periods examined were extended to include the months of October and November 2005, and the transport of tobacco products under the conditional exemption scheme was also subject to checks during those months.
Tables 1 and 2 show the total quantity of products subject to excise duty which were transported under the suspension arrangement between Czech and Slovak tax entities during the audited period.
4. Comparison of records of shipments of goods under suspension of duty
The NKÚ-ČR handed over to the Slovak side a database of shipments completed in the Czech Republic, which contained a total of 5,876 items listed on accompanying documents, of which 5,738 items related to mineral oils, 134 items of alcohol and 4 items of tobacco products.
The SAO SR handed over to the Czech side a database of shipments completed in the Slovak Republic, which contained a total of 3,319 items listed on accompanying documents, of which 696 items related to mineral oil, 2,066 items of alcohol and 557 items of tobacco products.
The NKÚ-ČR compared the data on shipments listed in the register of started shipments in the Czech Republic with the data on completed shipments registered in the Slovak Republic.
The results of the comparison are presented in Table 3.
Data on shipments in the months of November 2004 and September 2005 were compared by the NKÚ-ČR with the database of the Slovak customs administration, which was handed over to it by the SAO SR at the beginning of the audit.
The database did not contain data that could reliably agree individual traffic, and therefore only 63% of the traffic started could be attributed.
Individual shipments were assigned according to multiple data, e.g. sender, consignee, date of transport, quantity of products transported.
Data on shipments started in the Czech Republic and completed in the Slovak Republic in the months of October and November 2005 were compared by the NKÚ-ČR with a database of the Slovak customs administration, which contained all data according to accompanying documents, on the basis of which it was possible to clearly assign 93% of the shipments started.
In the database of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, data on the quantity of mineral oils were given in litres or tonnes, depending on the type of mineral oil.
In most cases, the quantity of alcohol was expressed in litres, which could, however, be converted into litres of absolute alcohol on the basis of the percentage of alcohol in the database.
The quantity of tobacco products was given in pieces, in thousands of pieces and kilograms by type of tobacco product.
For shipments initiated in the Czech Republic, the completion of which could not be reliably verified in the Slovak database or for which the quantity of products transported did not match, the accompanying documents were checked.
Documents accompanying 487 shipments of alcohol, mineral oils and tobacco products were checked.
The inspection of these documents was carried out at the customs offices where the NKÚ-ČR carried out the inspection.
For shipments authorised by other customs offices, the accompanying documents were requested through the GŘC.
The Czech side asked the Slovak side to verify the implementation of 141 shipments, for which the customs authorities in the Czech Republic did not provide certified copies No 3 of the accompanying document, or the quantity of products listed on the accompanying document did not agree with the quantity of products listed in the database.
In addition, data on shipments registered in the Slovak database were transmitted to the Slovak side, which, however, was not included in the database of shipments of the Czech customs administration.
The SAO SR found 95 shipments in the database of the Slovak Customs Administration.
He requested verification of the remaining 46 shipments from the local customs authorities, which proved their completion with copies of the accompanying documents.
The Slovak side forwarded to the Czech side copies of the accompanying documents, on the basis of which the transport was also identified in the Czech database, with the exception of the transport carried out by two Czech tax entities, which were not found in the Czech database of started transport.
An examination of these cases revealed:
- The Slovak transport database registered 11 shipments of alcohol in a total quantity of 276.7 litres of alcohol carried out by the Czech tax entity in 2004 and 20 shipments of alcohol in a total quantity of 404.66 litres of alcohol carried out in 2005.
The NKÚ-ČR found that it was the transport of taxed products, for which the sender does not need the approval of the tax authority to start.
The consignor informed the tax authorities in writing of the start of the transport. The transport was carried out on the basis of accompanying documents, which are used for the transport of products under the conditional exemption scheme;
- a total of 94 shipments of mineral oils, Combined Nomenclature code 2710 11 21, were registered in the Slovak Transport Database for a total volume of 173,000 litres carried out by the Czech tax entity between September 2004 and December 2005.
The NKÚ-ČR found that between May 2004 and June 2005, the tax entity carried out the transport of 102,000 litres of untaxed mineral oils without the appropriate authorisation.
The taxpayer was in possession of a special authorisation for the receipt and use of exempt products, under which it could only supply untaxed products to the holder of the same authorisation.
He did not notify the customs office in the Czech Republic of the start of the shipments and did not provide a tax guarantee of CZK 1,207,680 for the transported products.
Between July 2005 and December 2005, the tax entity delivered 71,000 litres of taxed mineral oils to the territory of SR. Even in these cases, it failed to comply with the legal obligation by not notifying the customs office of the start of the shipments.
The consignor in the Czech Republic can start the transport of products put into free circulation in the tax territory of the Czech Republic to another Member State without the consent of the customs office, but he is obliged to inform the customs office in writing before the start of the transport.
A taxpayer purchasing products put into free circulation for tax purposes in another Member State is required to declare the quantity and guarantee the tax before withdrawing them.
The goods may be transported only with a simplified accompanying document, the particulars of which are governed by Regulation No 3649 / 92.
This Regulation also allows the use of a movement document for transport under suspension of duty, but it must be clearly indicated that it is a "simplified accompanying document for tax control purposes (products subject to excise duty)."
The same rules on the transport and acceptance of products put into free circulation for tax purposes in another Member State apply in the Slovak Republic.
In those cases, the tax entities transported the products put into free circulation with an accompanying document for transport under a conditional exemption scheme, the 3rd and 4th copies of which were submitted by the recipient to the tax authorities in SR for verification.
The customs authorities in the Slovak Republic registered these shipments in the database of shipments under suspension of tax, as the accompanying documents did not state that it was a simplified accompanying document.
The SAO SR compared the transport database of the Czech customs administration with the transport database of the Slovak customs administration and found:
- in the databases, the quantity of products transported was reported inconsistently, e.g. mineral oil was given in litres, hectolitres or kilograms; alcohol was given in litres or litres of alcohol, making it more difficult to compare the quantity of goods transported;
- the quantity of alcohol transported indicated in the invoices did not match the quantity recorded in the databases,
- not all related invoices were listed in the databases;
- Two shipments of alcohol from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic were registered in the database of the Slovak customs administration in November 2004 for a total volume of 47,237 litres of alcohol, which were not found in the database of the Czech customs administration.
The Slovak side handed over copies of the accompanying documents to the Czech side.
5. International exchange of information between the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and Slovakia
Until 30 June 2005, Council Directive 77 / 799 / EEC on mutual assistance between the competent authorities of the Member States in the field of direct taxation, certain excise duties and taxes on insurance premiums laid down the conditions for cooperation between the administrative authorities of the Member States responsible for the administration of excise duties.
Regulation No 2073 / 2004 entered into force on 1 July 2005, laying down rules and procedures to enable the competent authorities of the Member States of the European Union to cooperate and exchange the information necessary for the correct assessment of excise duties.
Each Member State shall designate a central liaison office which shall liaise with other Member States in the field of excise administration and shall be responsible for exchanging information on the movement of excise goods.
In the Czech Republic, the "Excise Liaison Office" ("ELO ČR") was established at the GŘC to ensure the exchange of information in the field of excise duties between the Member States of the European Union.
With effect from 1 May 2004, ELO at the Poprad Customs Office carried out tasks related to the management of systems for the control of the movement of excise goods (SEED, ISA, EWSE) and the exchange of information in the framework of mutual administrative assistance between the Member States of the European Union and the Slovak Republic.
With effect from 1 July 2005, the tasks of ELO are carried out by the ELO department (based in Poprada) of the Excise Duty Department of the Customs Directorate of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as "ELO SR").
Under Article 3 (3) of Regulation No 2073 / 2004, the central liaison office is responsible, inter alia, for: - the exchange of data held in the SEED electronic register, - the Early Warning System Excise ("EWSE"), - requests for verification of the movement of excise goods sent to or received from other Member States by the Movement Verification System ("ISA").
The content, scope and functions of the SEED, EWSE and ISA systems are governed by Articles 22, 23 and 24 of Regulation No 2073 / 2004.
Seed - system for the exchange of information on tax entities trading in excise goods.
The system is made up of national registers of excise payers and allows tax authorities in the territory of the European Union to determine whether products subject to excise duty are traded by a person authorised to do so.
Each national register shall be made available to the competent authorities of the other Member States for excise purposes only.
The central liaison office of each Member State shall ensure that persons involved in the movement of excise goods within the territory of the European Union are able to obtain confirmation of the information held in that database.
In accordance with Section 41 of Act No 98 / 2004 Z. z., with Section 39 of Act No 104 / 2004 Z. z., with Section 46 of Act No 105 / 2004 Z. z., with Section 40 of Act No 106 / 2004 Z. z., and with Section 39 of Act No 107 / 2004 Z. z. ELO SR maintains an electronic database containing a register of tax warehouse operators, beneficiaries and tax warehouses - the SEED database.
Customs offices in SR contribute to the SEED database by registering a tax warehouse, a tax warehouse operator or an authorised recipient in the SysNed application software, which is automatically linked to the ELO SR.
For example, if a new tax warehouse operator, beneficiary or tax warehouse is registered in the SysNed database, the related data will automatically be transferred to the SEED database.
The SAO SR found that the exchange of SEED databases between the Customs Administration of the Slovak Republic and the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic usually took place once a month during the audited period, exceptionally more than once a month.
The SR Customs received 22 SEED files and sent 25 SEED files.
Data are transferred to the SEED database in the Czech Republic from the national register, which records all persons authorised to handle products subject to excise duty and issued authorisations to handle such products.
Individual customs offices in the Czech Republic do not have access to the international SEED database.
Requests from customs offices to provide information from the SEED database of other member countries are only obtained through ELO ČR.
EWSE - an early warning system aimed at controlling the transport of excise goods, through which the transport of risky consignments is announced.
On the one hand, the transport of certain products subject to excise duty in quantities exceeding the limits set by the European Commission regulation and, on the other hand, the transport, which is assessed as a risk by the tax authorities, is considered to be a risky consignment.
The exchange of information takes two forms:
- information - to be sent when the limits are exceeded,
- a warning message - is sent when the transport of goods is assessed as a risk.
When assessing the level of risk of a consignment, ELO SR uses the SEED database to send a warning message, on the basis of which it checks the data contained in the accompanying document.
If the data in the SEED database does not match the data in the accompanying document (for example, the registration number of the consignee of the goods or the registered office of the consignee does not match), ELO SR will draw up a warning message, which it will send to the ELO of the Member State of the consignee of the goods.
In drawing up the reports, the ELO follows the regulations of the Tax and Customs Commission CED 317 and CED 457, which, among other things, determine the type and quantity of goods in the appropriate units of measurement for the preparation of information and warning reports.
During the audited period, ELO SR sent one warning message to ELO CR.
In the Czech Republic, information about the start of shipments of products in quantities exceeding the specified limits is generated automatically when entering data from the accompanying document into the database when approving transport.
If, on the basis of its own analysis, the tax authority in the Czech Republic assesses the shipment as risky, it will prepare a so-called warning message, which it will send to the relevant Member State via ELO ČR.
In 2005, ELO ČR sent two warning messages to ELO SR.
The ISA - the system for controlling the movement of goods - makes it possible, through requests from the ISA, to control individual movements of products subject to excise duty as well as the control of a specified route of transport between the operators mentioned in the accompanying document.
The exchange of information is based on a request in which the ELO of the sending country specifies its requirements.
The system is used in particular in cases where the consignor receives certified copy No 3 of the accompanying document and requests, for example, a refund of excise duty, and in cases where the information contained in the accompanying document cannot be verified in the international SEED database.
During the audited period, ELO SR sent 33 requests to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs.
ELO ČR sent ELO SR 25 requests to the ISA.
The customs authorities in the Czech Republic most often checked the data contained in the accompanying documents, in particular the quantity of products received or dispatched, or whether the consignor of the products mentioned in the accompanying document is entitled to handle products subject to excise duty, unless this could be verified in the international database SEED.
The ISA applications received in both countries were forwarded to the customs authorities responsible for the consignee or consignor of the excise products.
The customs authorities examined the requested data and notified the result of the investigation via ELO to the other Member State.
6. Summary
The cooperation of the NKÚ-ČR and the SAO SR made it possible to compare the basic legislation governing the area of excise duties in both states, the procedure of the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic for the initiation and termination of the transport of products under the conditional exemption regime between the two states, the registration of these shipments, and to compare the exchange of information between customs authorities in the framework of international cooperation.
6.1 Comparison of legislation on excise duties in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic has revealed differences:
(A) the procedure followed by tax entities and tax administrations when commencing the transport of products under a conditional exemption scheme.
The transport of products under the conditional exemption regime can only be started by a tax entity in the Czech Republic with the approval of the tax authority, which will allow the start of transport on condition that the transported products have been provided with a tax guarantee equal to the amount of tax due to them.
The start of the transport of products under the conditional exemption regime in the Slovak Republic is not subject to the authorisation of the tax authorities.
During the audited period, the tax entity was obliged to notify the tax authority of the start of the transport of alcohol and tobacco products.
It was able to start the transport of mineral oils, beer and wine without informing the tax authorities.
In 2006, amendments to all laws on excise duties were gradually adopted in the Slovak Republic, according to which the consignor of goods under the conditional exemption procedure is obliged to send a copy of copy No 1 of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the customs office, which has local jurisdiction over the consignor, before the start of transport;
(B) within the time limits for dispatch of copy No 3 of the accompanying document.
The recipient in the Czech Republic is obliged to send copies 3 and 4 of the accompanying document to the tax authorities for verification no later than the next working day after the end of the transport.
Certified copy No 3 must be sent to the consignor no later than the following working day after receiving it from the tax authorities.
The consignee in SR is obliged to send to the consignor of the products copy No 3, certified by the tax authority and the consignee of the products, no later than the 15th day of the month following the month in which he received the goods.
6.2. Customs authorities in both the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic keep electronic records of shipments of products under the conditional exemption regime.
The content and method of keeping this register is not regulated by law in the Czech Republic or in the Slovak Republic.
The customs authorities in both countries record all the data from the accompanying documents on the basis of which the transport is carried out.
There is currently no single electronic system for monitoring the movement of goods under suspension of duty between Member States of the European Union, which would allow excise authorities in individual Member States to obtain real-time information on the movement of goods.
Decision 1152 / 2003 / EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 foresees the introduction of an electronic system for monitoring movements of products subject to excise duty from 1 July 2009.
On the basis of the agreement on cooperation in control activities, the Czech side handed over to the Slovak side a database of shipments of products under the conditional exemption regime started in the Slovak Republic and ended in the Czech Republic.
The database contained 5,876 items relating to transported mineral oils, ethyl alcohol and tobacco products.
The Slovak side handed over to the Czech side a database of shipments of products under the conditional exemption regime started in the Czech Republic and ended in the Slovak Republic.
The database contained 3,319 items relating to transported mineral oils, ethyl alcohol and tobacco products.
The Czech side compared the data on shipments listed in the register of shipments started in the Czech Republic with the register of shipments completed in the Slovak Republic.
The Slovak side compared data on shipments of goods under the conditional exemption regime started in the Slovak Republic and ended in the Czech Republic.
The comparison of data was made more difficult by the fact that the quantity of goods transported was not reported uniformly in the databases.
In cases where it was not possible to clearly attribute the data on individual shipments in the two registers, the accompanying documents were checked and no violations of the conditional exemption scheme or cases of tax evasion were found.
On the basis of the findings of the parallel checks, it can be concluded that Member States can obtain valuable information from the transport register in order to improve the management of excise duties.
The establishment of an electronic system for the movement and control of excise goods within the meaning of Decision No 1152 / 2003 / EC of the European Parliament and of the Council will allow for the electronic transmission of the accompanying document and more effective control of movements under suspension of duty within the territory of the European Union.
Communiqué
This report was drawn up in Czech, English and Slovak.
The report was signed by the Chairman of the Najvyššššie Audit Office of the Slovak Republic and the President of the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic.
Administration of Value Added Tax in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Report on the results of follow-up
Introductory word
Taxes are generally a key source of public revenue.
It goes without saying, therefore, that Supreme Audit Institutions (SAIs) should focus their attention in this area.
An example of this is value added tax (VAT) fraud.
In their case, a loss of EUR 100 billion is estimated each year in the European Union (EU).
As early as 2005, the participants of the VI EUROSAI Congress in Bonn agreed on the need for very close cooperation.
As part of this cooperation, SAIs can exchange control procedures, find the best solutions, etc.
VAT is a very suitable area for control cooperation, as it is the only tax harmonised within the EU.
The Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic ("SAO") and the Federal Court of Auditors (Bundesrechnungshof, "BRH") carried out the first parallel audit action in the field of VAT in 2006.
The report was published in 2008.
As VAT fraud is not confined to a single country but is widespread across the EU, close cooperation between SAIs is needed to ensure a comprehensive assessment of the steps being taken to address the problem.
The two SAIs therefore decided to further develop their cooperation in this area and carried out a parallel follow-up.
1. Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 09 / 11 (D) VIII 2 - 2009 - 0892
Subject of the audit: (CZ) Value Added Tax Administration (D) Bilateral audit with the SAO (follow-up)
Objective of the inspection:
(CZ) The aim of the audit operation was to examine the procedure of the tax authorities in the administration of VAT, in particular to verify the procedure for dealing with selected cases of commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany (hereinafter referred to as "Germany"), and to examine the procedures of the tax administrations of both countries in the framework of international cooperation.
(D) The audit action was designed to evaluate the measures taken by the tax administration to implement the recommendations issued by the SAO and BRH.
It was also intended to cover other areas related to VAT.
The resulting control findings were designed to compare with established best practice (if any).
The audited period covered the years 2006 to 2008 and, in the case of factual links, the periods before and after, until the end of the audit.
2. Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions
A subsequent audit of the VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany was carried out on the basis of an agreement between the two SAIs.
In the course of previous parallel checks, suspicious cases of intra-Community transactions were discovered.
Some of them required further examination.
On the basis of the audit findings, both SAIs formulated recommendations on the management of VAT.
The follow-up carried out was used to evaluate the measures taken in response to these recommendations and to examine selected suspected cases.
The audit also focused, for example, on selected cases of high-risk intra-community transactions, mutual assistance in the recovery of claims and the implementation of VAT controls on large tax entities.
When inspecting the VAT administration in selected areas in both countries, the auditors arrived at the following audit findings:
1. Recommendations from the previous review
* Recommendation 1: Conditions for registration of payers should be harmonised across the EU
In previous parallel checks, a comparison of VAT registration systems in the two countries revealed differences.
As different registration methods cause problems, both SAIs recommended harmonising the conditions for registration of payers within the EU.
This recommendation has been presented at EU level.
The proposal for an amendment to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing Regulation (EEC) No 218 / 92 ("Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003") called for the extension of existing databases within the EU, including the database of VAT payers' tax identification numbers.
It also amended common standards for the registration and deregistration of taxpayers.
Sai expected EU member states to agree on appropriate standards to support their decision to exclude unreliable traders from the VAT system as quickly as possible.
However, the latest version of the document, which was agreed by EU Member States in the framework of ECOFIN, does not contain the issue.
Both SAIs regret that the idea of common minimum standards has been abandoned.
However, they continue to see this as a relevant prevention tool in the fight against VAT fraud.
* Recommendation 2: Monthly submission of summary reports
In the framework of international cooperation, a previous control action recommended that all EU countries introduce a one-month deadline for submitting recapitulative statements to allow for a more timely examination of the values of intra-community transactions.
Council Directive 2008 / 117 / EC amending Directive 2006 / 112 / EC on the common system of value added tax to combat tax evasion linked to intra-Community transactions reduces the reporting period for intra-EU transactions to one month.
In the Czech Republic, this measure was implemented through the Value Added Tax Act with effect from 1 January 2010, and in Germany it was implemented from 1 July 2010.
In Germany, the obligation to submit recapitulative statements on a monthly basis was not introduced by the deadline in accordance with the applicable EU rules, while in the Czech Republic it was.
* Recommendation 3: Comparing data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements in Germany to make VIES data more reliable and considering linking the two systems for VAT returns and recapitulative statements
The German tax administration accepted the BRH's recommendations and set up a task force to explore possible solutions.
Work is still ongoing and the BRH will closely monitor further developments.
* Recommendation 4: Sharing the successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level Based on the results of the previous control action, both SAIs agreed that an effective risk management system cannot be developed by just one Member State.
Successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system need to be exchanged and implemented in individual EU Member States.
If this is not the case, fraudsters will choose the Member State with the weakest risk management system.
The audit found that our two Member States have different risk management systems, which have their strengths and weaknesses.
In this area, the SAO carried out an audit of the EUROCANET system, which allows the exchange of information within the EU, while BRH focused on German participation in the so-called risk management platform.
2. Follow-up of selected cases of intra-community transactions
In the course of the previous control action, commercial transactions where there were doubts about their execution or irregularities in the reporting of commercial transactions in tax returns or recapitulative statements by taxpayers from both countries were jointly examined.
Both SAIs selected nine cases for follow-up, which included the intra-community movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany.
The checks carried out by the tax authorities of the respective countries have not been completed by the date of completion of our previous joint control action.
The subsequent audit action verified that most of the tax procedures in relation to the selected cases of commercial transactions between payers from the Czech Republic and Germany had been concluded and that adequate measures had been taken by the tax administration of the Czech Republic or Germany (e.g. additional VAT assessments or avoidance of input tax refunds).
3. Control of selected cases of risky intra-community transactions
High-risk cases of intra-community transactions carried out by EU payers, which were included in EUROCANET, were selected for inspection.
EUROCANET is a tool for detecting high-risk taxpayers within the EU.
The participation of Member States in this scheme is voluntary.
The Czech Republic is an active participant in EUROCANET, while Germany has a passive status.
It is unsatisfactory for an active participant in the system if some Member States refuse to participate actively.
Due to the fact that the German tax administration was not involved in the exchange of data in EUROCANET, it was not possible to obtain any information on which suppliers with the German VAT ID were assessed as being at risk.
As part of the audit operation, the SAO found both cases of normal business transactions and cases with suspicion of involvement in carousel transactions or fraudulent conduct related to VAT.
Tax authorities have limited possibilities to control risky transactions, especially when it comes to so-called missing traders, and it is difficult for a mere physical examination of documents to prove any fraudulent behaviour to the taxpayer.
A similar situation arises for tax administrations when imports and exports to third countries are linked to intra-community carousel trade.
In such cases, it would be appropriate to ensure greater cooperation between customs and financial authorities in order to identify goods and inconsistencies in transport documentation, as well as to monitor their physical movement within the EU towards the final consumer.
Germany, like some other countries, is reluctant to actively participate in EUROCANET due to the lack of a sufficient legal basis.
In Germany, other tools are being used to detect risky taxpayers, which have so far proved successful for the German tax administration.
There is a need for communication and exchange of experience between EU Member States in this area.
The EU Council has reached political agreement on a proposal for a Regulation amending Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003.
Its main innovation is the creation of the EUROFISC network.
The experience gained so far in the use of EUROCANET should be the basis for the creation of this new VAT fraud network.
4. Mutual assistance for the recovery of claims
In the area of international debt recovery assistance, all EU Member States are subject to the same European legislation.
Therefore, the way in which requests for international assistance for the recovery of claims are handled is the same in the Czech Republic and Germany.
The SAO and BRH compared the statistics submitted by the two Member States to the European Commission for the years 2006-2008.
The data contained in these statistics were not consistent.
Both SAIs consider it useful to renegotiate the statistics at EU level in order to find a way to avoid persistent mismatches.
Without this, the statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, the SAIs agree that reliable statistics should contain more information on VAT.
It would probably be useful for the Commission to carry out an analysis on the basis of more detailed statistics to help Member States strengthen the effectiveness of the fight against VAT fraud.
In the view of both SAIs, this means helping Member States with low recovery rates to increase recovery rates to at least the EU average.
If a Member State so wishes, the Commission should be actively involved in this process.
5. Control of large tax entities
The Sai analysed the legal situation regarding the VAT control of large tax entities ("VDS") in both countries.
In addition, they collected information from tax administrations in the form of a questionnaire on areas considered by the SAI to be essential for the management of this issue.
It is clear from the responses received that the situation in the two countries is different.
The Czech Republic has a system in place to guide the selection of risk-prone cases, which is based on a large amount of relevant data (e.g. information from tax checks carried out, data from balance sheets and profit and loss accounts, etc.).
This ensures effective management and analysis of VAT control in general.
In 2012, it is planned to set up a specialised financial office for the management of the VDS.
A similar system does not yet exist in Germany, which makes it difficult to manage and analyse VAT controls in general.
Germany has so far focused more on the selection of the individual cases in question, mainly on the basis of data from VAT returns and recapitulative statements.
The analysis of these data is based on different components of risk management, which will be strengthened.
3. Progress of the control action
3.1 Running of the control event in the Czech Republic
The audit was carried out between May 2009 and February 2010 by the Department II - the revenue department of the state budget and the regional unions IX. Plzeň, X. České Budějovice, XIII. Brno and XV. Ostrava.
The audited persons were: The Ministry of Finance of the Czech Republic (hereinafter also referred to as the "Czech Ministry of Finance") and 25 tax authorities (hereinafter also referred to as the "FÚ"): FÚ Brno II, FÚ Brno III, FÚ Brno IV, FÚ in Břeclav, FÚ in Domažlice, FÚ in Hodonín, FÚ in Hradec Králové, FÚ in Cheb, FÚ in Jablonec nad Nisou, FÚ in Karlovy Vary, FÚ in Kralupech nad Vltavou, FÚ in Kraslice, FÚ Ostrava I, FÚ Ostrava III, FÚ in Písek, FÚ in Plzeň, FÚ in Prague 1, FÚ in Prague 4, FÚ in Prague 8, FÚ in Rakovník, FÚ in Sokolov, FÚ in Tábor, FÚ in Vysoký Mýta, FÚ in Zlín and FÚ in Žamberk.
The audit conclusion of this audit action was approved by the College of the Supreme Audit Office on 27 April 2010.
3.2 Conduct of the inspection in Germany
The audit was carried out between February 2009 and February 2010 by the audit service for indirect taxes and the staff of the designated regional audit offices in Berlin, Frankfurt am Main and Munich.
Following the selection of a sample of cases, a number of Länder were informed of the mission of the inspection.
In addition to the interviews at the Federal Ministry of Finance, the following Länder carried out the audit:
The tax files of the following tax authorities have been included: - Erlangen, Zentralfinanzamt München (Munich Central Tax Office), Hof, Schwandorf, Regensburg, Weiden in der Oberpfalz, Grafenau; - Hamburg-Nord (Hamburg-North), Hamburg-Hansa, Hamburg für Großunternehmen (Hamburg-VDS);
In addition, discussions were held with the tax authorities of Mühlacker, Reutlingen, Starnberg, Verden, Erfurt, Leipzig, Halle-Süd (Halle-jih) and with the financial directorates of Frankfurt am Main, Chemnitz and Münster.
A report on the audit findings was submitted to the Federal Ministry of Finance in April 2010.
3.3 Cooperation between the two audit institutions
As part of the preparation of the parallel control actions, a meeting of representatives of the two control institutions took place in September 2008 to discuss and define control topics.
Subsequently, in December 2008, the leaders of the two SAIs signed a cooperation agreement on the implementation of parallel controls.
At a meeting in Bonn in June 2009, the audit teams informed each other of the initial results achieved during the preparation of the audit, discussed possible audit approaches and agreed on the way forward.
The second meeting took place in Prague from 2 to 4 December 2009.
The inspection teams exchanged the findings gathered so far and agreed on a timetable for drawing up a joint report.
Both SAIs, when carrying out parallel control actions, decided to focus on: A follow-up of the implementation of the recommendations made in the previous report, a review of selected cases of intra-community transactions between tax payers from the Czech Republic and Germany, which were not resolved during the previous parallel check, a review of selected cases of intra-community transactions between tax payers from the Czech Republic and Germany, which were classified as high risk cases, a review of the procedure of tax administrations in the area of international assistance in the recovery of VAT claims, a review of the tax controls of large companies.
A report on the results of the parallel control actions was prepared during a workshop in June 2010.
4. Control of VAT administration in selected areas
4.1 Evaluation of recommendations from the previous review
4.1.1 Evaluation of the recommendations in the Czech Republic
Recommendation 1
Conditions for the registration of payers should be harmonised across the EU
On the basis of the results of the previous audit, the SAO recommended the modification of the conditions for VAT registration and the introduction of a new rule for de-registration in the Czech Republic.
The modified conditions should make it possible to reduce the risk of possible tax evasion in the collection of VAT more effectively.
In this context, it was found that in some cases the tax authorities did not make use of the right to cancel the VAT registration of taxpayers who did not comply with the obligations under Act No 235 / 2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax ("the VAT Act").
The Czech Ministry of Finance has not yet proposed an amendment to the provision to introduce an obligation for tax authorities to cancel VAT registration for taxpayers when they repeatedly fail to submit VAT returns.
Under the VAT Act, the tax authority can revoke the registration of the taxpayer "ex officio" in cases where: (A) the payer has not performed a transaction without notifying the tax authority for twelve consecutive months, (b) the payer has failed to fulfil his obligations under this Act, (c) the payer ceases to be a taxable person.
In a previous inspection, it was found that the legislation in force allowed the FÚ for Prague 1 to cancel the registration for VAT on 31 January of the following calendar year for so-called non-established taxpayers who did not incur any obligation to declare and pay tax during the current calendar year.
The FÚ pro Prahu 1 often did not cancel the VAT registration of these payers, as the relevant provision set an insufficient deadline for the cancellation of the registration.
This problem was solved by an amendment to the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2009.
The tax authority is entitled to cancel the registration of a non-established taxpayer if the taxpayer has not supplied any taxable goods or services or exempt goods or services with the right to deduct VAT in the previous calendar year.
Recommendation 2
Monthly submission of summary reports
In the framework of international cooperation, a previous control action recommended that all EU countries introduce a one-month deadline for submitting summary reports.
The Council Directive reduces the period for which summary reports on intra-EU transactions are submitted to one month. This measure has been implemented in the Czech Republic through the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2010.
There is also a new obligation to submit summary reports in electronic form.
Payers must also submit a recapitulative statement if the services for which the place of supply is determined in accordance with Section 9 (1) of the VAT Act are supplied to another Member State to a taxable person registered in another Member State and if the recipient is obliged to declare and pay the tax on those services.
This obligation is based on Council Directive 2008 / 8 / EC amending Directive 2006 / 112 / EC as regards the place of supply of services.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements in order to make VIES data more reliable This recommendation concerned the German tax administration.
The Czech administration compares data on intra-community transactions reported in VAT returns and summary reports of Czech payers automatically in the ADIS system.
Recommendation 4
Sharing the successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level
Proper collection of VAT is one of the prerequisites for the proper functioning of the EU internal market.
The fight against VAT fraud is therefore an area of priority and has received considerable attention in recent years.
The importance of this fight is evidenced, among other things, by the findings of a study published by the European Commission in October 2009, in which an external evaluator attempted to establish the difference between the amount of VAT actually collected and justified in the 25 EU Member States ("EU-25") during the period 2000-2006.
On the basis of an analysis of the available data, the author of the analysis concluded that the estimated loss of VAT not collected over this period is between EUR 90 billion and EUR 113 billion, with an average of 12% of eligible VAT not collected annually in the EU-25.
For the Czech Republic, the VAT loss for 2006 was estimated at 18%.
In the context of international cooperation, a previous control action found that an effective risk management system could not be developed by just one Member State.
The successful criteria, components and approaches of this system must be shared and implemented in each EU Member State.
As regards the risk management system, the SAO carried out an audit of the EUROCANET system, which is used for the exchange of information in the EU.
Cases of risky intra-community transactions carried out by EU taxpayers, included in EUROCANET, were selected for inspection (see Chapter 4.3).
The objectives of improving administrative cooperation and improving the effectiveness of the fight against VAT fraud should also be achieved through the establishment of the EUROFISC network, which should improve the cooperation of the responsible authorities in a way that allows fraud to be detected in the bud.
This network should later also become an important source of information in the risk assessment of intra-Community transactions.
The ECOFIN Council already approved the creation of EUROFISC on 7 October 200812, setting out the basic principles that will guide it.
The image of EUROFISC is the already functioning system of rapid and selective exchange of information EUROCANET, which was developed by the Belgian tax administration in cooperation with other Member States and with the support of the European Commission and OLAF.
The aim of this system is to detect risky commercial transactions and entities involved in organised VAT fraud.
4.1.2 Evaluation of the recommendations in Germany
The evaluation of the recommendations of the first report revealed the following findings:
Recommendation 1
Conditions for the registration of payers should be harmonised across the EU
The German tax authorities have set up a well-functioning system for registering taxpayers, which is based on a detailed questionnaire.
The Federal Ministry of Finance notified the Commission of the scheme in October 2007.
Improvements to the system shall be made on an ongoing basis.
At present, the data from the questionnaire are processed electronically and will then be used for the survey as part of risk management during registration.
The Commission presented a proposal to amend Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003, which included common standards for the registration and deregistration of taxpayers.
Member States have requested further clarification and detailed elaboration of this issue.
BRH has asked the Federal Ministry of Finance to ensure the level of standards already achieved in this area in Germany.
Recommendation 2
Monthly submission of summary reports
A law on the transposition of EU directives into national law was adopted on 8 April 2010.
This law contains provisions concerning the monthly submission of summary reports on intra-community deliveries.
Those provisions entered into force on 1 July 2010.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements to make VIES data more reliable and to consider linking the two VAT return and recapitulative statement systems
A joint working group composed of staff from the Länder and the Federal Ministry of Finance has been set up.
The group developed a strategy for automatically comparing data from VAT returns and recapitulative statements.
This strategy is still being discussed in the Länder.
The working group also looked at a tool designed to optimise the control process for transactions in the internal market.
Recommendation 4
Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level The exchange of relevant information takes place at EU level.
Germany is a participant in this exchange in the framework of the so-called risk management platform.
The European Commission supported the idea of such a platform and, following a written consultation on 18 October 2006, the establishment of a risk management platform was added to the Fiscalis 2006-2007 Action Plan.
The members of the platform are further divided into subgroups that deal with individual topics, such as:
Reports on the results of the work of these sub-groups were published in early 2010.
4.1.3 Evaluation
Registration
The issue of the conditions for VAT registration and the withdrawal of VAT registration in different countries has been addressed at EU level.
The proposal for an amendment to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003 included an extension of existing databases within the EU, including the database of VAT payers' tax identification numbers.
It also regulated common minimum standards for the registration and deregistration of taxpayers.
For the time being, the issue of registration and deregistration has been left to the national legislation of EU Member States.
Member States have requested further clarification and detailed elaboration of this issue.
The BRH has asked the Federal Ministry of Finance to ensure that the level of standards already achieved in Germany does not fall.
On 8 June 2010, the ECOFIN Council reached a political consensus on the proposed Regulation.
The idea of common minimum standards has been abandoned.
Member States are required to implement national procedures and are only required to inform the Administrative Cooperation Committee of these procedures.
Both SAIs regret that the Commission has not been able to convince Member States of the need for common standards for the registration and de-registration of payers, as both SAIs consider this measure to be an important element of prevention in the fight against VAT fraud.
They would therefore like the Commission to make further efforts in this direction.
Monthly submission of summary reports
In the framework of international cooperation, a previous control action recommended that all EU countries introduce a one-month deadline for submitting recapitulative statements, allowing for a more timely examination of the values of intra-community transactions.
Council Directive 2008 / 117 / EC amending Directive 2006 / 112 / EC on the common system of value added tax to combat tax evasion linked to intra-Community transactions reduces the reporting period for intra-EU transactions to one month.
In the Czech Republic, this measure was implemented through the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2010, and in Germany it took effect on 1 July 2010.
Germany has not introduced an obligation to submit recapitulative statements on a monthly basis according to a set calendar, while the Czech Republic has (in accordance with EU directives).
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements in Germany to make VIES data more reliable and consider linking the two systems for VAT returns and recapitulative statements
The German tax administration accepted the BRH's recommendations and set up a working group to find possible solutions.
Work is still ongoing and the BRH will closely monitor further developments.
Sharing the successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level
Germany and the Czech Republic apply different approaches to the risk management system for the purpose of identifying risk-prone traders.
The SAO carried out an audit of the EUROCANET system, which is used for the exchange of information in the EU (see Chapter 4.3).
In this area, BRH focused on German participation in the so-called risk management platform.
4.2 Follow-up of selected cases of intra-community transactions
In a previous audit operation, the execution of commercial transactions for which there were doubts about their execution or irregularities in the way in which payers from both countries reported these commercial transactions in their VAT returns or recapitulative statements was jointly examined.
The two audit institutions selected for follow-up nine cases involving the intra-Community movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany, the control of which carried out by the tax administrations of the two countries was not completed during the previous joint audit action.
(1)
In the first quarter of 2005, the Czech payer purchased goods worth €22,686 from the German payer.
This acquisition of goods was not declared by the Czech payer in his VAT return because the German payer was not assigned a VAT ID during that period, but only a tax number intended for domestic transactions in Germany.
On the basis of international administrative cooperation under Council Regulation (EC) No 798 / 2003, the Czech tax authority received information that, under the German VAT Act, a payer who supplies goods to other Member States does not have to be assigned a VAT ID in order for the intra-Community supply of goods to be exempt from VAT.
A subsequent audit by the SAO found that on the basis of an audit carried out by the Czech tax authority, the Czech payer submitted an additional VAT return in which he declared the acquisition of goods of the stated value and at the same time claimed the right to deduct VAT of the same amount in this tax return.
(2)
In the fourth quarter of 2004, the Czech payer was to purchase goods worth EUR 12,561 from the German payer.
The acquisition of these goods was denied by the Czech payer and he did not mention it in his VAT return.
The German tax authorities refused to cooperate on request under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003 because the turnover of the transactions did not exceed EUR 15 000.
As the Czech tax authority did not obtain evidence, it terminated the inspection without a finding and the tax liability remained assessed at the original amount.
A subsequent audit by the SAO found that the Czech tax authority had received two spontaneous pieces of information from Germany under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003, which showed that the German payer had invoiced the goods to Slovakia.
The Czech payer purchased the goods from the Slovak payer and stated this acquisition in the regular VAT return for the month of October 2004.
(3)
In the fourth quarter of 2004, the Czech payer was to purchase a passenger car worth EUR 48 500 from the German payer.
The acquisition of the goods in question was not declared by the Czech taxpayer.
This payer has not filed VAT returns since August 2004, so the tax authority assessed the VAT for that quarter at CZK 0.
On the basis of information obtained in the framework of the international exchange of information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003 from Germany, in March 2007 the tax authorities requested the payer to submit an additional VAT return, which was not submitted by the payer.
A subsequent check revealed that the tax authority had carried out further acts in the tax procedure in 2007, which showed that the passenger car in question had been sold by the Czech payer to a car dealership in the Czech Republic.
The Czech tax authority issued a notice of payment for the December 2004 tax year, by which it subsequently assessed VAT on the acquisition of goods from another Member State and their subsequent sale in the amount of CZK 295 379.
By order of the regional court, the Czech payer was liquidated and a liquidator was appointed.
In the absence of enforcement of the taxable assets of the tax debtor, the arrears appear to be irrecoverable.
(4)
The Czech payer was to deliver new vehicles (passenger cars) to Germany during the fourth quarter of 2004 and the first quarter of 2005 for a total value of EUR 198 167.
A reply to a request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003 revealed that the German entity was the subject of pending tax and criminal proceedings in Germany.
During a subsequent check, BRH received information that, following the conclusion of tax proceedings in Germany, it had been established that the German taxpayer had been involved in fraudulent activities.
Intra-Community acquisitions of goods were taxed at a value of EUR 182 424 (2004) and EUR 369 690 (2005).
The SAO's subsequent audit found that the Czech payer was involved in the carousel business with new means of transport.
On the basis of information from the German tax administration concerning the examination of the supply of goods, a VAT check was initiated with the Czech tax entity for the tax years April, May and June 2005.
On the basis of the inspection findings and information obtained in the context of the international exchange of information, the tax authorities subsequently assessed VAT for the period May 2005 at CZK 703 031 and for the period June 2005 at CZK 726 551.
(5)
In February 2005, Czech payer A was to purchase a machine from a German payer for a total value of EUR 58 000.
The German payer was to deliver a machine worth EUR 88 027 to the Czech payer B in the third quarter of 2004, but payer B denied this purchase of the goods.
A subsequent audit by the SAO found that payer B had purchased the machine from a German company which had an organisational unit in the Czech Republic.
The Czech payer A did not declare the acquisition of goods from the German payer in his VAT return.
A reply from the German tax authority to a request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003 showed that the German payer did not carry out an intra-community supply of machinery worth EUR 58 000, but a supply of goods within the Czech Republic.
Following a subsequent inspection, BRH found that, following a tax inspection, the intra-Community supply of the machine had been reclassified as a supply of the machine within the country and the VAT exemption had been abolished.
(6)
In the third quarter of 2004, the German taxpayer was to deliver €11,600 worth of goods to the Czech taxpayer.
The goods were purchased and then sold in Germany in 2005.
The SAO's subsequent audit found that the Czech tax administration had assessed the submitted additional VAT return, which wrongly stated the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State, including the acquisition of goods with the stated value.
BRH found that, after receiving a reply to a request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003, the German tax authority had corrected the German taxpayer's VAT return and subsequently assessed VAT worth EUR 1 600.
The further movement of goods in Germany and the application of VAT in Germany are subject to tax control.
The German payer's recapitulative statement has not yet been corrected, as corrections to recapitulative statements in Germany can only be made by the payer who submitted the recapitulative statement.
(7)
The Czech tax authority received a request from the German tax administration for information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003 as to whether the Czech taxpayer had purchased a passenger car worth EUR 47 400 from the German taxpayer in February 2005.
Following the tax procedure carried out for the February 2005 tax year, the Czech tax authority charged the Czech taxpayer a tax liability of CZK 0 and informed the German tax authority that it could not confirm the purchase of the car by the Czech taxpayer.
A subsequent audit by the SAO found that the registration of the Czech VAT payer was cancelled in 2007 for failure to fulfil obligations and the Czech tax administration sent the documents to the Police of the Czech Republic.
Following a subsequent check, BRH found that the German payer had changed his registered office and that the new local tax authority had cancelled the VAT exemption for the supply of the car in question to the Czech taxpayer following an inspection.
The German taxpayer has not yet corrected the data in the recapitulative statement and has lodged an appeal against the decision of the tax authority.
(8)
According to VIES data, the German taxpayer supplied goods worth a total of EUR 33 205 to the Czech taxpayer between the third quarter of 2004 and the first quarter of 2005.
A subsequent audit by the SAO found that the Czech tax authority was trying to determine the causes of the differences between the Czech tax payer and the purchase of goods between the third quarter of 2004 and the first quarter of 2005.
The Czech taxpayer has repeatedly submitted an additional VAT return for the first quarter of 2005.
The Czech tax authority did not clarify the difference in the value of the purchased goods in the amount of CZK 134,273 for the period from Q3 2004 to Q1 2005 because, according to the Czech tax authority, it was not possible to accurately capture the business transactions for each quarter and therefore the tax authority accepted the additional tax returns submitted.
(9)
In the third quarter of 2004, the German taxpayer delivered goods worth EUR 46 854 to the Czech taxpayer.
During the same period, the Czech payer awarded the intra-Community purchase of goods worth only EUR 14 856.
The Czech tax authority verified the amount of supplies made in the framework of the international exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003.
The reply to the request for information received from Germany was accompanied by 3 invoices with a total stated value of the supply of goods of EUR 31 998, which is the value corresponding to the difference between the acquisition declared by the Czech payer in the VAT return and the data provided in the VIES system.
A subsequent audit by the SAO found that the Czech payer filed an additional VAT return for the tax year July 2004 only in January 2007, after many urges from the tax administration.
At the same time, in that tax return, the taxpayer exercised the right to deduct VAT, which left the tax liability for that tax year unchanged.
A follow-up check verified that in selected cases of commercial transactions between payers from the Czech Republic and Germany, most of the tax procedures had been completed and that the tax authorities in both the Czech Republic and Germany had taken adequate measures (i.e. subsequently assessed VAT or prevented input tax refunds).
4.3 Checking selected cases of risky intra-community transactions
4.3.1 Results of the inspection in the Czech Republic
Eurocanet can be an important source of information for the detection of risk actors within the Member State where the goods were acquired.
In the Czech Republic, the signal information obtained from EUROCANET was compared by the relevant local tax authorities with the data of the acquirers.
Starting in the first quarter of 2008, the Czech Republic has been sending data to EUROCANET on risky transactions and on tax entities acting as suppliers.
In the framework of international cooperation, nine Czech tax entities included in the EUROCANET system were selected for the audit.
They acted either as suppliers or as purchasers of goods.
Relevant data from tax administrations from other Member States have been captured in EUROCANET.
Since the German tax authorities did not participate in the exchange of data in EUROCANET, it was not possible to obtain any information that would help to establish whether suppliers with German VAT ID were assessed by the German tax authorities as being at risk.
The audit revealed cases of normal commercial transactions as well as cases of suspected involvement in carousel transactions or VAT fraud.
Where applicable, the tax authorities have used the exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798 / 2003.
For example:
The tax authorities did not detect any suspicion of involvement in risky transactions when verifying the signal information.
The tax authorities monitor such tax entities on an ongoing basis for their inclusion in EUROCANET.
During the verification of risky transactions, the tax authorities did not show deviations from the rules applicable to the calculation of the tax base and VAT in the submitted accounts, even though they found irregularities in the transport and storage of goods or revealed business relations with suspected or non-contact companies from other Member States.
The verification of commercial transactions was complicated because some taxpayers did not cooperate with tax authorities and could not be contacted.
For the most part, the local tax authorities examined risky tax entities and risky transactions identified in the EUROCANET signal information.
Tax authorities have limited options when examining risky transactions, especially in connection with the screening of so-called missing traders, and it is difficult to prove fraudulent behaviour to a tax entity from a physical check of documents alone.
Stricter VAT registration requirements for taxpayers and more flexible deregistration would help reduce missing-trader fraud.
In the case of tax entities involved in carousel fraud and other fraudulent activities, VAT is registered in order to report fictitious supplies of goods within the EU or to issue formally correct tax documents to taxpayers who improperly draw input VAT deductions on the basis of them.
Greater cooperation between customs and financial authorities should be ensured in cases where tax entities are suspected of being involved in carousel transactions and other fraud, and goods are imported and exported from third countries.
Closer cooperation between these authorities would help to identify goods and inconsistencies in transport documentation, as well as to monitor the physical movement of goods within the EU towards the end consumer.
The participation of EU Member States in EUROCANET is voluntary.
The fact that three large Member States (Germany, Italy and the United Kingdom) did not participate in EUROCANET was assessed by the European Parliament at the end of 2008 as a weakness of EUROFISC, which should be addressed by setting up a mandatory EUROFISC network.
4.3.2 Results of the inspection in Germany
BRH analysed the information available at the Federal Central Tax Office, which contained data from EUROCANET.
That information was the criterion for the collection of the six files of German taxpayers for inspection.
Germany, like some other countries, has refused to participate actively in EUROCANET.
As a result, Germany has a passive status, which means that it does not send data to Brussels, but only receives data from EUROCANET.
The justification for this position is contained in the following statement: .In the government's view, it is not legally permissible for state (public) institutions to provide data to EUROCANET.
There is currently no legal basis for breaching the applicable rules on tax confidentiality.
In addition, the government has no reliable information on how such EUROCANET data is used by other Member States. "17 Since October 2007, the Federal Central Tax Office has carried out analyses of EUROCANET data and forwarded them to the tax authorities of the Länder in accordance with the agreed procedure.
The German tax authorities receive audit information on the direct business relations of payers (registered with specific tax authorities) with traders from other Member States who have been included in EUROCANET.
However, the German tax authorities do not receive any information as to whether such a trader from another Member State has any risky business relationships with traders from other Member States who also have business relations with the German trader in question.
4.3.3 Evaluation
The Czech Republic is an active participant in EUROCANET, while Germany has a passive status.
It is unsatisfactory for an active participant if some Member States refuse to take part.
As a result, control in the area had to be carried out in different ways.
However, the results did not reveal major differences in the detection of VAT fraud cases, as EUROCANET is not the only systemic risk management tool.
The tax administrations of both countries have a number of other tools to detect fraudulent transactions, but it is necessary to develop a comprehensive risk management system within the EU.
The Council of the EU has reached political agreement on a proposal for a regulation, the main benefit of which lies in the establishment of EUROFISC.
The experience gained from the use of EUROCANET data should also be part of the envisaged VAT fraud network.
Member States should therefore communicate their experiences at European level.
On the other hand, the cases brought before the courts at national and European level show that a discussion between Member States and the Commission on the conditions for tax exemptions in intra-Community transactions appears to be necessary.
4.4 Mutual assistance for debt recovery
4.4.1 International debt recovery assistance in the Czech Republic
In particular, the following directives are the basic rules for international cooperation in the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU:
Council Directive 76 / 308 / EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims arising from operations forming part of the system of financing the European Agricultural Guidance and Guarantee Fund, as well as agricultural levies and customs duties;
Council Directive 2001 / 44 / EC amending Directive 76 / 308 / EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims arising from operations forming part of the system of financing the European Agricultural Guidance and Guarantee Fund, agricultural levies and customs duties, value added tax and certain excise duties;
(1) Commission Directive 2002 / 94 / EC implementing certain provisions of Council Directive 76 / 308 / EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims relating to certain levies, duties, taxes and other measures.
In the Czech Republic, Council Directive 76 / 308 / EEC was implemented by Act No 252 / 2000 Coll., on International Assistance for the Recovery of Certain Financial Claims.
Following the adoption of Council Directive 2001 / 44 / EC, it was necessary to implement this directive in the Czech legal order and at the same time to amend the aforementioned Act No 252 / 2000 Coll.
In this context, a new Act No. 191 / 2004 Coll., on International Assistance for the Recovery of Certain Financial Claims, was adopted.
Commission Regulation (EC) No 1179 / 2008 of 28.11.2008 is a new regulation in the system for regulating international cooperation in the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU.
The Annex to the Regulation sets out new models of requests, which have been in use since 1.1.2009, introduces an obligation for electronic communication and an obligation for the applicant authority to confirm the conformity of the documents sent with the original document.
Guiding principles for the provision of international cooperation in debt recovery:
1. reciprocity;
2. assistance is always granted only on the basis of an application containing the prescribed particulars;
3. the assistance does not cover financial claims which are in the nature of criminal sanctions in the requested State;
4. the provision of international assistance for the recovery of claims shall be carried out in accordance with the national law of the State which has been requested to provide assistance;
5. foreign claims do not have priority in recovery;
6. assistance shall be granted only for the recovery of uncontested claims;
7. the principle of exhaustion (the requesting State has, without success, made use of all the possibilities available to it to recover the claim under its legal system).
Act No 191 / 2004 Coll. defines the three forms by which assistance takes place, namely the provision of information, the service of documents and the actual recovery of claims.
Procedure for sending recovery requests to other EU Member States
The locally competent tax office will electronically send a request for information, a request for service or a request for recovery of claims together with the relevant documents to the Czech Ministry of Finance through the financial directorates.
The Czech Ministry of Finance will arrange for the translation of the application into the relevant language, scan it, including annexes, and send it via the CCN / CSI network to the competent authority of the tax administration of the designated state.
There are two basic requirements for recovery: The claim must be more than EUR 1 500 and not more than 5 years old.
If those requirements are not met, the requested authority may refuse enforcement.
Procedure for receiving recovery requests from other EU Member States
Upon receipt of a request from another Member State, the Czech Ministry of Finance must confirm receipt of the request as soon as possible and within seven days at the latest.
If the Czech Ministry of Finance decides not to comply with the request, it will inform the requesting authority of the reasons for the rejection of the request and specify the specific provisions of the directive on which it relies.
This notification shall be sent no later than three months after the date of acknowledgement of receipt of the request.
Upon receipt of the application, the Czech Ministry of Finance will verify that the application has all the elements according to the law and should immediately forward the application through the Finance Directorate to the local tax office for processing.
If the request for recovery is accepted, the tax authorities will, among other things, examine the debtor's assets, e.g. by obtaining land registry statements, checking bank accounts, verifying the registration of vehicles at the transport inspectorate, etc.
Six months after the date on which receipt of the request was confirmed, the Czech Ministry of Finance should inform the requesting authority of the outcome of the investigation carried out in order to obtain the requested information.
In the case of non-contact tax entities, where recovery is not possible, the applicant authority should also be informed of this fact.
Any amount recovered by the tax authorities shall be transferred to the applicant authority in CZK within one month of the date on which the claim was recovered.
It is not impossible for the Czech tax authority enforcing foreign claims to allow it to wait until it has been paid or paid in instalments, if the state that requested the recovery gives its consent.
During the period of recovery, the debtor is prescribed interest or periodic penalty payments under Act No. 337 / 1992 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes and Fees.
This interest or penalty payment is due to the State that requested the recovery.
In the case of received requests for recovery, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not send requests to the local tax authorities in time, especially in 2006 and 2007.
A similar situation was found in the framework of international debt recovery assistance in the case of requests received from tax authorities in the Czech Republic.
The audit revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance did not act in accordance with Act No. 191 / 2004 Coll., because it did not inform the local competent authority of the Member State of the progress made in the recovery within six months of the date on which the receipt of the request was confirmed.
This situation has been improving since 2008.
Statistical data
