In accordance with the provisions of Section 13 (4) of Act No 191 / 2004 Coll. the Czech Ministry of Finance processes statistical data for the European Commission by 15 March each year, indicating the number of requests for information, service or recovery sent or received in the past year, indicating the amount of claims to which the requests relate.
The European Commission is preparing a report on the state of recovery on the basis of documents provided by all EU Member States, which it will submit to the EU Council and the European Parliament.
The audit found that the Czech Ministry of Finance underestimated the statistical data due to an error in the item of receivables recovered in 2008 by EUR 5 250 thousand by indicating the incorrect value of the receivable for VAT (this was a shift of the decimal point after the conversion of the receivable from Czech crowns to the value in euros).
This error was subsequently reflected in the European Commission statistics.
Information on mutual assistance, including recoveries, is provided in the table below.
4.4.2 International debt recovery assistance in Germany
The legal authorisation for international administrative assistance in tax matters is derived from European Community law, Council Directive 2008 / 55 / EC of 26 May 2008 (EC Recovery Directive) and Commission Regulation of 28 November 2008 (EC Implementing Directive).
In order to make the wording more accessible and easier to understand, the EC Recovery Directive codifies Council Directive 76 / 308 / EEC of 15 March 197621, the provisions of which have been substantially amended several times.
The provisions apply, inter alia, to the recovery of VAT, income tax and capital gains tax, including accessories.
The EC Recovery Directive was transposed into national German law by the Act (EC) on the collection of state taxes of 3 May 2003.
Enforcement procedures in Germany are governed by the German Fiscal Code.
Article 117.2 of the Code stresses that tax authorities can provide international judicial and administrative assistance on the basis of international agreements and legal instruments of the European Communities, which are valid in national jurisdiction, and on the basis of the EC Act on Administrative Assistance.
Part Six of the German Fiscal Code (Articles 249-346) enshrines the statutory provisions governing the enforcement procedure.
The administrative tasks of the tax authorities are mainly governed by instructions for execution and instructions for enforcement.
The Federal Ministry of Finance has reached an agreement with representatives of the highest tax authorities of the Länder on the principles of administrative assistance in the assessment of taxes and has transferred its own responsibility in this matter to the Federal Central Tax Office.
The general prerequisites for applying for recovery are as follows:
The legal requirements must be fulfilled (Sections 251 and 254 of the German Fiscal Code [AO]).
* All available domestic means of recovery have already been exhausted.
The claims which are the subject of requests for recovery assistance must be final.
No more than five years may elapse between the issue of the enforcement order or the date on which the claim becomes final (i.e. it is no longer subject to appeal) and the date on which the applications are submitted.
The total amount of the claim must be more than €1,500.
Procedure for sending recovery requests to other EU Member States
German requests for the recovery of outstanding tax liabilities are sent from the implementing departments of the tax authorities to the competent foreign office, such as the Czech CLO, through the intermediary office and the Federal Central Tax Office.
The Guideline on International Administrative Assistance in Tax Matters (Recovery of Claims) of 19 January 2004.25 is currently being revised by a working group of the federal and provincial governments to adapt it to the Recovery Directive.
The application, including the annexes, shall be submitted electronically by the tax office to the intermediate office.
This office will check the accuracy of the application in terms of content and form.
If the application is not correct, it is returned to the relevant tax office.
If it meets all the requirements, it is referred to the Federal Central Tax Office.
The Federal Central Tax Office will then provide the necessary communication with the relevant foreign office and will also provide a translation of the application.
Procedure for receiving recovery requests from other EU Member States
Requests for recovery received from other Member States are registered by the Federal Central Tax Office and a receipt is sent within 10 days.
In addition, the Federal Central Tax Office will check whether the formal requirements have been met.
The Federal Central Tax Office submits these requests to the intermediary office, which then forwards them to the competent tax authorities and monitors their processing.
The Federal Central Tax Office also sends preliminary or final reports.
If it takes more than six months to process the application, the intermediary authority shall request the submission of a preliminary report to be submitted pursuant to Article 16 of Commission Directive 2002 / 94 / DG.
Once the formal and factual elements of the application have been checked, the implementing services shall notify the method of recovery.
Any sums recovered must be transferred to the bank account specified in the application within one month of receipt.

4.4.3 Recovery control, case studies
In the framework of international cooperation, 21 requests for international assistance for the recovery of claims between the Czech Republic and Germany were selected for inspection.
An examination of ten selected cases revealed, among other things:
1.
On 20 October 2006, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request from Germany for the recovery of a VAT claim for 2004 and 2005 totalling EUR 3 883, or CZK 109 820, from a Czech tax entity.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send a request for recovery to the tax authorities until 26 February 2008.
In order to secure the enforced claim, the Czech tax authority established a lien on real estate owned by the Czech tax entity.
Since it was not possible to pay the entire enforced claim by mortgaging the real estate, a payment plan was agreed with the Czech tax entity with payments of at least CZK 2,000 per month.
On 31 August 2009, information on the state of recovery was sent to the German tax administration with the result that, as of 25 August 2009, the claim had been partially recovered in instalments of CZK 49 600.
This amount was sent to Germany and a further instalment of CZK 3 000 was sent to Germany on 28 August 2009.
2.
On 7 January 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request for the recovery of tax arrears from a Czech tax entity that owed EUR 180 869 in Germany, i.e. CZK 4 434 915, in VAT and in income tax and accessories.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the request to the tax authorities until 27 November 2008.
By examining the ownership of accounts with banks, securities, real estate, motor vehicles and movable property, the tax authority found that the debtor did not own any executable assets.
In addition, a local investigation found that the debtor did not stay at his permanent address for almost a year.
His whereabouts in the Czech Republic are unknown.
This communication was received by the Czech Ministry of Finance on 6 April 2009 and on 16 April 2009 the reply of the tax authorities was sent to the German tax administration.
3.
On 21 November 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request from Germany for recovery concerning tax arrears on turnover tax and accessories of the Czech tax entity amounting to EUR 3 139, or CZK 84 846.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request for recovery of this claim to the tax authorities on 6 August 2008, although on 18 February 2008 the Czech Ministry of Finance received information from Germany that the Czech tax entity had paid the claim in Germany.
On 9 December 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance notified the tax authorities that the request for recovery was being processed by the payment of a claim by a Czech tax entity in Germany.
However, the claim in question was also recovered in the Czech Republic and paid to Germany on 27 October 2008.
Due to long time periods in which the Czech Ministry of Finance informed the authorised tax authorities, in this case the claim was paid twice - by the entity itself in Germany and by the recovery of the claim by the Czech tax authorities.
In cooperation with BRH, it was found that the amount recovered from the Czech Republic should have been set off against a claim from a further request for recovery of EUR 6 649, which was due to be sent to the Czech Republic in September 2008.
The Czech Ministry of Finance only records a request for recovery of EUR 3 139 from this company, and a request for recovery of EUR 6 649 does not appear in the records of the Czech Ministry of Finance with the company in question.
4.
On 15 September 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request from Germany for the recovery of tax arrears from a Czech tax entity that owed EUR 39 957, or CZK 956 654, in income tax and VAT and accessories in Germany.
On 19 December 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request to the Czech tax authorities.
On 1 June 2009, the procedure for recovery of the claim was initiated, an execution was ordered for ordering a claim on accounts with banks in the Czech Republic and for a deduction from wages (the deduction amounted to CZK 7,000).
In a meeting with the tax authority, the debtor stated that he did not agree with the amount of the claim and considered it to be disputed.
The Czech tax authority found that in the past the tax entity was willing to pay EUR 250 per month, which was not accepted by the German tax authority.
The taxpayer has promised to discuss the application with the German tax authorities with a view to obtaining a change in the amount of its claim.
The recovery of the claim was still ongoing during the SAO audit mission.
5.
On 19 November 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request for recovery from Germany concerning a Czech tax entity which owed a total of EUR 113 444, or CZK 3 116 304, in income tax for 2005 and in turnover tax for the period 2003-2007 and accessories.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the request to the FÚ pro Prahu 1, which is responsible for administering the tax to non-established tax entities in the Czech Republic, until 14 November 2008, as it was not possible to determine the local tax authority based on the address of the tax entity.
During the investigation carried out, the FÚ received information that the debtor had an income of EUR 4 704 on 19 September 2008; however, the FÚ could no longer issue an execution order for this amount, as the Czech Ministry of Finance did not submit a request for recovery until after that date.
On 26 January 2009, the Czech tax authority initiated the recovery of the claim and issued an enforcement order ordering the claim on the debtor's funds in accounts held with banks and savings and credit cooperatives.
The recovery of the claim was still ongoing during the SAO audit mission.
6.
The Czech tax authority requested international cooperation in the recovery of VAT claims and costs totalling CZK 146,223,742 on 3 October 2006.
It was not until 13 May 2008 that the Czech Ministry of Finance sent this request for recovery to the German tax administration.
On 8 September 2008, the German tax authority transferred to the Czech authorities, through the Federal Bank, the amount obtained from the execution of funds in the debtor's account, amounting to EUR 17 700, or CZK 439 226.
An error was found in the calculation of the amount recovered during the verification of the volume of recoveries.
The recovered amount of CZK 146 223 742 was erroneously converted at the rate of EUR 1 = CZK 25,065 to EUR 583 378.
The correct recalculation of the amount recovered is EUR 5 833 781.83.
A request for recovery was therefore sent to Germany, which was reduced by EUR 5 250 404.
7.
On 1 March 2007, the Czech tax authority sent a request to the Czech Ministry of Finance to recover the tax arrears from the Czech tax entity, which owed CZK 1,970,632, or EUR 79,847, in VAT and accessories.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the application to the German tax administration until 10 November 2008.
On 4 February 2009, the German tax authorities asked the debtor to pay the arrears.
In view of the significant decrease in the company's turnover in the second half of 2008 and in particular in the first half of 2009 and the related liquidation situation of the company, the following payments were made to cover the arrears: EUR 4 600 on 8.4.2009, EUR 3 000 on 6.5.2009 and EUR 2 500 on 16.6.2009.
These payments were sent to the account of the tax authorities in the Czech Republic.
On 23 June 2009, the German tax authorities agreed with the debtor to pay a further instalment of EUR 2 500 by 30 June 2009.
8.
The request for recovery of a total amount of EUR 398 653, i.e. CZK 9 832 779, including a claim for real estate transfer tax, was received from the Czech tax authority to the Czech Ministry of Finance on 22 May 2008.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request for recovery to the German tax administration on 2 October 2008.
On 3 April 2009, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a notification from the German tax administration that the application had been returned by the German tax administration.
The German tax authorities justified the refund on the grounds that the transfer tax was not a tax within the meaning of Article 2 (e), (f), (g) or (h) of Council Directive 2008 / 55 / EC.
The German tax authorities also stated that Article 2 (g) concerns claims relating to income tax and wealth tax.
Similarly, Article 3 of Council Directive 2008 / 55 / EC applies to taxes on income and capital listed in Article 1 (3) in conjunction with Article 1 (4) of Council Directive 77 / 799 / EEC.
The Czech Ministry of Finance has proposed to prepare and submit a new request for recovery, excluding the arrears in real estate transfer tax in the amount of CZK 61,759 and indicating the arrears in VAT, corporate income tax and personal income tax, which will be sent back to the German tax administration.
The Czech Ministry of Finance has received a new request from the Czech tax authority to recover tax arrears relating to the same tax entity, which owes CZK 7,079,735 in income tax and VAT.
9.
On 6 February 2006, the Czech tax authority sent a request to the Czech Ministry of Finance concerning the recovery of tax arrears from a Czech tax entity that owed CZK 3,445,782, or EUR 123,328, in personal income tax and VAT.
Of this amount, VAT amounted to CZK 1,133,967.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the request to the German tax administration until 18 April 2007.
The Czech Ministry of Finance forwarded to the Czech tax authority the reply of the German tax administration from 9 July 2007 to 11 November 2008.
The reply stated that the German tax authority had issued an enforcement order on 11.6.2007 for a bank account with the bank, which stated, however, that it did not have any business relations with the tax entity.
In doing so, the German tax authorities considered the application to be complete.
10.
On 26 September 2005, the Czech tax authority sent a request to the Czech Ministry of Finance concerning the recovery of VAT arrears totalling CZK 1 296 845, or EUR 43 591.
The request from the Czech tax authorities was received by the Czech Ministry of Finance on 10 October 2005.
On 15 December 2005, the Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request to the German tax administration.
Before sending the request for recovery, the Czech tax authority executed the execution on the debtor's funds in bank accounts and a deduction from wages and established a lien on the immovable property.
The request for recovery was preceded by a request for information sent to the German tax authorities on 16 March 2005.
A reply to a request for information received by the Czech tax authority on 16 September 2005 showed that the Czech taxpayer was staying in Germany and had an income of EUR 8 437 from non-business activities.
The Czech Ministry of Finance received a reply to the request for recovery on 20.4.2006, but did not send it to the Czech tax authority until 12.2.2008.
The reply stated that no enforcement proceedings could be initiated in Germany due to the insolvency of the debtor - no assets were found in his possession and his non-business income was already subject to other enforcement proceedings.
In doing so, the German tax authorities considered the request for recovery to be complete.
4.4.4 Comparison and evaluation
In the area of international debt recovery assistance, all EU Member States are subject to the same European legislation.
Therefore, the way in which requests for international assistance for the recovery of claims are handled is the same in the Czech Republic and Germany.
The SAO and BRH compared the statistics submitted by the two Member States to the European Commission for the period 2006-2008.
The data contained in these statistics were not consistent.
In a 2006 report, the European Commission recommended that Member States pay particular attention to the management of their statistics.
In a 2009 report, the Commission concluded that the incidence of statistical mismatches had decreased despite an increase in the number of applications.
Both SAIs consider it important for statistical issues to be discussed again at EU level.
This discussion should focus on how to avoid persistent mismatches, otherwise the data reported by individual EU countries in the statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, both SAIs agree that reliable statistics should show the annual number of claims as well as the nature of the claims in question (i.e. whether the claims relate to VAT, income tax, etc.) as well as the amount of claims recovered by each Member State.
Both SAIs consider it important for the Commission to provide more detailed analyses of the statistics submitted by Member States, as this can help Member States to assess their own effectiveness in combating VAT fraud.
The fact that recovery rates can be calculated on a country-by-country basis is considered useful by both SAIs for Member States with lower recovery rates to step up their efforts to improve recovery rates at least to the EU average.
If a Member State so wishes, the Commission should be actively involved in this process.
In particular, in 2006 and 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not submit requests for recovery of claims to the local tax authorities in a timely manner.
A similar situation was found for requests for international assistance received from tax authorities in the Czech Republic.
The audit revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance did not act in accordance with Act No. 191 / 2004 Coll., on International Assistance for the Recovery of Claims, because it did not inform the locally competent authority of the Member State of the progress made in the recovery within six months of the date on which the receipt of the request was confirmed.
4.5 Control of large tax entities
4.5.1 Control of large tax entities in the Czech Republic
General information
The VAT audit of large tax entities is governed by the same rules as that of other tax entities.
The procedural procedure for the control of the VDS is based on Act No 337 / 1992 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes and Fees.
The Czech Ministry of Finance defined VDS as natural or legal persons who were established or established for the purpose of doing business and whose net turnover for the tax year stated in the personal / corporate income tax return amounted to CZK 2 billion or more.
The classification of the tax entity as a VDS took place after the filing of the income tax return for the relevant tax year, for the first time in 2003.
A taxpayer ceases to be referred to as a VDS if, in three consecutive tax years from the end of the period in which it filed the tax return on the basis of which it was classified as a VDS, its net turnover for the tax year has fallen below that threshold.
The taxpayer was not allowed to be removed from the VDS register without carrying out a tax audit of at least one tax per tax year.
By the end of 2009, all VDS had been checked at least five years apart.
From 2010, a written assessment of the tax entity must be carried out at least once every 2 years and the subsequent procedure chosen must eliminate the tax risks and their negative impact on the correct determination and collection of the tax.
The control of the FÚ is focused on at least one type of tax; the tax administration usually elects several tax years at once.
The VDCs were controlled by specialised inspection units, which are set up in a total of 13 FTAs, or by the staff of the control departments of the locally competent FTAs.
The specialised control unit carries out tax checks within the remit set by the Director of the Financial Directorate.
In addition to large tax entity audits, it also examines
(A) tax entities operating in unusual and specific business sectors;
(A) entities for which carrying out a tax audit is technically and time consuming;
(A) entities with a broad territorial and organisational structure;
(A) entities suspected of large-scale tax evasion;
* Entities linked in chains and networks that are suspected of widespread tax evasion and the unjustified diversion of excess deductions.
The number of tax checks carried out by the specialised inspection units of the FO and the results of these checks are shown in Table 3.
The Czech Ministry of Finance has proposed an amendment to Act No 531 / 1990 Coll., on Territorial Financial Bodies, which consists of the establishment of a specialised FÚ with a nationwide remit for selected tax entities (including for legal entities established for business purposes, which have achieved a turnover of more than CZK 2 billion).
4.5.2 Control of large tax entities in Germany
General information
VAT controls on large companies are governed by the same rules as tax controls in general, i.e. the relevant provisions are enshrined in the following regulations: The German Fiscal Code (AO), the Fiscal Administration Act (FVG), the Tax Control Regulations (BPO).
Other methodological documents are also in force.
German Fiscal Code
The statutory provisions relating to the inspection are laid down in Articles 193-203 of the German Fiscal Code in Section IV - Tax inspection on the spot. In particular, these articles lay down the rules on the admissibility of tax inspection on the spot (i.e. on the premises of the company), their scope in terms of subject matter, the rules on the allocation of responsibilities, the form and content of the inspection notice, the principles of control, the obligation of the tax entity to cooperate and the preconditions for carrying out the final discussion and communication of the inspection report.
On-the-spot tax checks are carried out by the competent tax authorities (Article 195 of the Code).
The Fiscal Administration Act According to Article 5.1 (1), in connection with Article 19 of the Act, participation in on-the-spot tax checks carried out by the tax authorities is compulsory for the Federal Central Tax Office.
The participating authorities shall agree on the spot on the nature and extent of the participation of the Federal Central Tax Office in the tax controls.
In addition, the Federal Central Tax Office has the right to require the specific undertakings it selects to be inspected at a time to be determined by it.
In such a case, it may lay down rules on the conduct and content of inspections at the premises of those companies.
Rules on tax controls According to Article 108.7 of the German Constitution, the rules on tax controls (German acronym BPO 2000) have been agreed by the Bundesrat, the upper house of the German Parliament, in which the governments of the Länder are represented.
These administrative rules apply to on-the-spot checks carried out both by the tax authorities of the Länder and by the Federal Central Tax Office.
Undertakings are classified according to size at regular intervals, in accordance with Article 3 of the BPO 2000.
Large enterprises are subject to ex post control (Article 4.2 BPO).
According to Article 33.1 of the BPO 2000, each informed tax office must keep a register of groups of companies as defined in the BPO 2000.
Methodological guidelines
In addition to the above, the additional methodology for tax administration is set out in the following guidelines:
A single manual for special VAT controls in Germany;
The USLO Manual, which sets out the methodology for the use of data on intra-community trade relations conducted in VIES;
The Zauber Manual, which sets out the methodology for the use of the Zauber database;
Work aids for various and special items.
The classification of tax entities is based on criteria such as turnover and net profit, with different limits depending on the type of business.
The data are published by the Federal Ministry of Finance.
They are evaluated every three years and fixed for the next three years.
The number of companies to be inspected - not just large companies - must be determined at regular intervals.
As a general rule, checks on large enterprises are carried out on an ongoing basis.
Checks are usually announced, including VAT checks.
This means that, in the course of the inspection, checks will be carried out definitively, mainly on income tax, excise duty and VAT - i.e. checks on all types of relevant taxes.
VAT checks may be carried out either by tax inspectors or by VAT inspectors.
Implementation varies and depends on the organisation of the Länder.
The number of tax years covered by the checks is usually between three and five years.
BPO 2000 foresees an inspection period of three years.
All taxes of the company are subject to verification.
4.5.3 Management of control of large tax entities
Both SAIs decided not to investigate individual cases of VDS checks carried out, but focused on management issues in order to gain an overview of how tax administrations manage the issue of VAT checks on VDS.
In the form of a questionnaire, they collected information from tax administrations on areas they consider essential for managing the issue.
* What statistical records and analyses are available to the management of tax administrations regarding the VAT control of the VDS?
In particular:
Are there any statistics or records of the extent to which a distinction is made between the fight against VAT fraud and VAT control in general?
Czech Republic: No, the ADIS system does not allow such a resolution in the current data version.
Germany: The tax administration makes no distinction between the control proposed to combat VAT fraud and the general control of VAT.
Are there any statistics or records on the timeliness of VAT checks (linked to the time period of the transactions checked)?
Czech Republic: Records on the timeliness of enquiries relevant to intra-Community purchases of goods for selected VAT payers are reported in the ADIS system.
In addition, the information recorded in ADIS also includes data such as how long the interview took.
Germany: No, the uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors contain only information on the average time of the last inspection (information on the year).
This figure does not provide an overview of the selected control periods with regard to individual entrepreneurs.
VAT inspectors focus on the most recent tax assessment period; they also have the right to carry out VDS checks.
However, the statistics produced at the federal level for the special VAT inspection services do not provide information on the classification of tax entities.
There are some statistics or records on the nature of the additional tax revenue generated, broken down for example according to the following criteria:
I. a net increase in the tax liability (e.g. in cases where the taxpayer has improperly applied a reduced VAT rate instead of the standard tax rate);
II. only a nominal increase in the tax liability (e.g. transfer of a fully qualified VAT case to another tax year);
III. post-clearance recovery of tax revenue (payment of additional tax due).
Czech Republic:
The Czech tax administration monitors the number of tax verifications carried out, the amounts of additional tax assessed, broken down by type of tax, the number of tax entities audited and the number of tax years audited.
Other tax procedures (local investigations, complaints) are followed in the same way.
The time data and amounts of additional taxes paid are recorded as a separate task.
General debt statistics shall also be kept, broken down by type of tax but not by the declared tax or the tax established by the tax authority.
Germany: No, the uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors and for the special VAT inspection services do not distinguish between the above criteria.
In addition, the majority of tax administrations visited do not distinguish between these differences.
Are there areas of control that generate significant additional revenue?
Czech Republic: Yes, the tax authority has the right to collect the tax payer for verification on the basis of criteria that can be linked to selected indicators in the special sections of ADIS.
Germany: There are no regulations at federal level.
It follows that uniform statistics at federal level do not provide such data for tax inspectors and for the special VAT inspection services.
However, there is one coordinated approach between the finance ministers of the Länder and the federal government.
In the Zauber database, tax inspectors or tax investigators from the Länder are required to record the increased tax (VAT) liability they have assessed if they exceed a certain amount.
In such a case, it must specify, for example, the nature of the increase in the tax liability assessed.
What are the most common findings?
Czech Republic:
- VDCs exercise an unjustified right to deduct input tax on supplies and services:
(A) which have not been used to carry out any economic activity pursuant to Section 72 (1) of the VAT Act;
(A) which have been used for representation under Section 75 (3) of the VAT Act;
On the basis of tax documents which did not meet the requirements set out in Section 73 (1) of the VAT Act;
- VDS did not declare output VAT pursuant to Section 21 (1) of the VAT Act.
Germany: It has been noted that there are no regulations at federal level.
It follows that uniform statistics at federal level do not provide such data for tax inspectors and for the special VAT inspection services.
VAT findings are not separately registered by the Länder if they result from VDS tax controls.
However, in the Zauber database, where tax inspectors or tax investigators from the Länder are required to record the increased tax (VAT) liability they have assessed if they exceed a certain amount, the Federal Central Tax Office is able to analyse this information.
Does the tax administration carry out analyses of areas of control that generate a high "return" and draw conclusions for management?
Czech Republic: Yes, for example, they are launching national audits focused on risky commodities or on the subject of economic activity.
Germany: There are no regulations at federal level.
Uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors and for special VAT inspection services do not provide data on audit areas that generate high "revenue."
There are different views on the process of analysis, as well as on case management in terms of relevance.
Some regional tax authorities provide special information, but its use is at the discretion of the tax authorities.
4.5.4 Comparison and evaluation
The differences in the replies of the two Member States show that the Czech Republic provides a system that collects a number of data from the tax checks carried out, as well as data from the financial statements - balance sheet and profit and loss accounts.
Based on a wide range of data, the Czech Republic is able to guide the selection of risk-prone cases.
The same applies to the analysis and management of VAT control in general.
In 2012, the establishment of a specialised financial office for the management of the VDS is planned in the Czech Republic.
In Germany, the tax authorities do not collect this information.
It follows that it is more difficult to carry out those tasks in a similar manner.
However, Germany's philosophy puts more emphasis on selecting individual cases based on data from submitted tax returns.
Therefore, the risk management components will be strengthened and improved.
On the basis of adequate reference notes, expert auditors must be able to assess the exact amount of VAT.
Both SAIs agree that Member States should be able to ensure adequate financial management as well as an adequate risk management system.
This will help to reduce shortfalls in VAT revenue.
As a result, the revenue from VAT collection will be increased and the level of risk detection for unreliable entrepreneurs will be improved.
5. Conclusion
The cooperation of the two SAIs on parallel audits of the VAT administration met the objectives set by the SAO and BRH.
The two SAIs got to know each other better about the systems in place in the following areas: (I) intra-community transactions, (ii) VAT risk management, in particular as regards the collection of risk-prone transactions, (iii) VAT recovery assistance and (iii) VAT control of large tax entities.
Thanks to mutual cooperation, differences in VAT fraud detection strategies as well as differences in the above-mentioned areas of VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany have been revealed.
The control findings were compared and best practices were identified.
In addition, both SAIs hope that the results achieved will provide an impetus for stakeholders to start a discussion on approaches and strategies within Member States, including at European Commission level.
The extremely valuable experience and knowledge gained from the cooperation between the two SAIs can serve as an encouragement for the implementation of future control actions in the field of VAT management.
6. Communiqué
The report was drawn up in Czech, English and German and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic and the President of the Federal Court of Auditors (Bundesrechnungshof) of the Federal Republic of Germany.
Closing date: June 2010.
